## Purpose and Scope

This document provides a comprehensive overview of the Godot Engine codebase architecture, its major subsystems, and the relationships between them. It serves as an entry point for developers who need to understand how Godot is structured at the code level.

This page covers the high-level organization of the engine. For detailed information on specific subsystems, refer to:
- Core engine initialization and main loop: [Engine Initialization and Main Loop](#2.1)
- Scene graph implementation: [Scene Tree and Node System](#2.2)
- Rendering architecture: [Rendering System](#3)
- Editor implementation: [Editor System](#4)
- GUI framework: [GUI System](#5)
- Scripting integration: [Scripting System](#6)
- Resource handling: [Resource Management](#7)
- Platform support: [Platform Abstraction Layer](#8)
- Build configuration: [Build System](#9)

## Architectural Principles

Godot Engine follows a layered architecture where higher-level systems depend on lower-level abstractions. The engine is organized into several key domains:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Application["Application Layer<br/>(main.cpp, OS implementations)"]
    Core["Core Services<br/>(ProjectSettings, Engine, ResourceLoader)"]
    Servers["Server Layer<br/>(RenderingServer, PhysicsServer, AudioServer)"]
    Scene["Scene System<br/>(SceneTree, Node, Viewport)"]
    Editor["Editor Layer<br/>(EditorNode, EditorPlugins)"]
    
    Application --> Core
    Core --> Servers
    Servers --> Scene
    Scene --> Editor
```

**Sources:** [main/main.cpp:1-3100](), [editor/editor_node.cpp:1-8800](), [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp:1-2200]()

## Engine Execution Flow

The engine follows a well-defined initialization and execution sequence:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Entry["main/main.cpp::Main::setup()"]
    InitCore["Initialize Core Singletons<br/>Engine, ProjectSettings, Input, etc."]
    InitServers["Initialize Server Singletons<br/>RenderingServer, PhysicsServer2D/3D"]
    CreateSceneTree["Create SceneTree"]
    InitEditor["Initialize EditorNode<br/>(if running editor)"]
    MainLoop["Main::iteration()<br/>Game Loop"]
    Cleanup["Main::cleanup()"]
    
    Entry --> InitCore
    InitCore --> InitServers
    InitServers --> CreateSceneTree
    CreateSceneTree --> InitEditor
    InitEditor --> MainLoop
    MainLoop --> MainLoop
    MainLoop --> Cleanup
```

The entry point is `Main::setup()` which initializes all core systems sequentially. The engine distinguishes between editor mode and game mode through flags set during startup.

**Sources:** [main/main.cpp:450-2100](), [main/main.cpp:2100-3100]()

## Scene System Architecture

The scene system is the fundamental organizational structure for all game objects in Godot. It is built around a hierarchical tree of `Node` objects managed by `SceneTree`.

### Node Hierarchy

```mermaid
graph TB
    Node["Node<br/>scene/main/node.cpp<br/>Base class for all scene objects"]
    Node2D["Node2D<br/>2D transform hierarchy"]
    Node3D["Node3D<br/>3D transform hierarchy"]
    CanvasItem["CanvasItem<br/>2D drawing interface"]
    Control["Control<br/>scene/gui/control.cpp<br/>UI base class"]
    Viewport["Viewport<br/>scene/main/viewport.cpp<br/>Rendering surface"]
    Window["Window<br/>scene/main/window.cpp<br/>OS window or embedded"]
    
    Node --> Node2D
    Node --> Node3D
    Node --> CanvasItem
    CanvasItem --> Control
    CanvasItem --> Viewport
    Viewport --> Window
```

| Class | File | Purpose |
|-------|------|---------|
| `Node` | [scene/main/node.cpp]() | Base class with tree structure, lifecycle callbacks, processing |
| `SceneTree` | [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp]() | Manages the node hierarchy, game loop, groups, and scene switching |
| `Viewport` | [scene/main/viewport.cpp]() | Rendering target, input handling, 2D/3D world container |
| `CanvasItem` | [scene/2d/canvas_item.cpp]() | 2D drawing and canvas layer integration |
| `Control` | [scene/gui/control.cpp]() | GUI element with layout anchors and theme support |

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.cpp:1-100](), [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp:1-200](), [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1-100]()

### SceneTree and Lifecycle

The `SceneTree` manages the active tree of nodes and drives the game loop:

```mermaid
graph TB
    SceneTreeInit["SceneTree::initialize()"]
    RootViewport["Create root Viewport"]
    NodeAdded["Node added via add_child()"]
    EnterTree["NOTIFICATION_ENTER_TREE<br/>Node::_enter_tree()"]
    Ready["NOTIFICATION_READY<br/>Node::_ready()"]
    Process["Every frame:<br/>NOTIFICATION_PROCESS<br/>Node::_process(delta)"]
    PhysicsProcess["Physics tick:<br/>NOTIFICATION_PHYSICS_PROCESS<br/>Node::_physics_process(delta)"]
    ExitTree["NOTIFICATION_EXIT_TREE<br/>Node::_exit_tree()"]
    
    SceneTreeInit --> RootViewport
    RootViewport --> NodeAdded
    NodeAdded --> EnterTree
    EnterTree --> Ready
    Ready --> Process
    Ready --> PhysicsProcess
    Process --> Process
    PhysicsProcess --> PhysicsProcess
    Process --> ExitTree
    PhysicsProcess --> ExitTree
```

Nodes receive notifications in a specific order:
1. **ENTER_TREE** (parent first, then children): Node enters the active scene tree
2. **READY** (children first, then parent): Called once when node and all children are ready
3. **PROCESS** (every frame): Called at frame rate for gameplay logic
4. **PHYSICS_PROCESS** (fixed rate): Called at fixed intervals for physics simulation
5. **EXIT_TREE** (children first, then parent): Node leaves the scene tree

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.cpp:68-323](), [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp:150-400]()

## Rendering System Architecture

Godot's rendering system is organized as a client-server architecture where scene nodes (clients) communicate with the `RenderingServer` to perform all graphics operations.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Scene Layer"
        Node3D["Node3D/MeshInstance3D"]
        CanvasItem["CanvasItem/Sprite2D"]
        Viewport["Viewport"]
        Camera["Camera2D/Camera3D"]
    end
    
    subgraph "RenderingServer API"
        RS["RenderingServer<br/>servers/rendering/rendering_server.h"]
        RSD["RenderingServerDefault<br/>Implementation"]
        CommandQueue["CommandQueueMT<br/>Thread-safe command queue"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Scene Management"
        RendererSceneCull["RendererSceneCull<br/>servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp<br/>Visibility determination"]
        RendererViewport["RendererViewport<br/>Viewport management"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Rendering Backends"
        RenderForwardClustered["RenderForwardClustered<br/>renderer_rd/forward_clustered/<br/>Desktop renderer"]
        RenderForwardMobile["RenderForwardMobile<br/>renderer_rd/forward_mobile/<br/>Mobile renderer"]
        GLES3["RasterizerSceneGLES3<br/>OpenGL ES 3.0 backend"]
    end
    
    subgraph "GPU Abstraction"
        RenderingDevice["RenderingDevice<br/>Vulkan/D3D12/Metal abstraction"]
        OpenGL["Direct OpenGL calls"]
    end
    
    Node3D --> RS
    CanvasItem --> RS
    Viewport --> RS
    Camera --> RS
    
    RS --> RSD
    RSD --> CommandQueue
    CommandQueue --> RendererSceneCull
    CommandQueue --> RendererViewport
    
    RendererSceneCull --> RenderForwardClustered
    RendererSceneCull --> RenderForwardMobile
    RendererSceneCull --> GLES3
    
    RenderForwardClustered --> RenderingDevice
    RenderForwardMobile --> RenderingDevice
    GLES3 --> OpenGL
```

### Rendering Pipeline Components

| Component | File | Purpose |
|-----------|------|---------|
| `RenderingServer` | [servers/rendering/rendering_server.h]() | High-level rendering API exposed to scene nodes |
| `RenderingServerDefault` | [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h]() | Default implementation with command queuing |
| `RendererSceneCull` | [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp]() | Frustum culling, LOD selection, occlusion |
| `RendererViewport` | [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp]() | Viewport rendering orchestration |
| `RenderForwardClustered` | [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp]() | Desktop forward renderer |
| `RenderForwardMobile` | [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.cpp]() | Mobile optimized renderer |
| `RenderingDevice` | [servers/rendering/rendering_device.h]() | GPU API abstraction |

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:1-200](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:1-100](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.cpp:1-100]()

### Viewport Rendering Integration

Viewports are the bridge between the scene graph and the rendering system:

```mermaid
graph LR
    Viewport["Viewport<br/>scene/main/viewport.cpp"]
    ViewportRID["viewport RID<br/>RenderingServer handle"]
    Canvas["2D Canvas<br/>current_canvas RID"]
    Scenario["3D Scenario<br/>world_3d scenario RID"]
    RS["RenderingServer"]
    
    Viewport -->|"owns"| ViewportRID
    Viewport -->|"attaches to viewport"| Canvas
    Viewport -->|"attaches to viewport"| Scenario
    ViewportRID -->|"managed by"| RS
    Canvas -->|"rendered by"| RS
    Scenario -->|"rendered by"| RS
```

Each `Viewport` creates RenderingServer resources (RIDs) for its rendering targets and manages both 2D canvas and 3D scenario rendering contexts.

**Sources:** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:588-693](), [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1100-1400]()

## Editor System Architecture

The editor is built as a specialized layer on top of the core engine, orchestrated by `EditorNode`.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Editor Core"
        EditorNode["EditorNode<br/>editor/editor_node.cpp<br/>Central singleton orchestrator"]
        EditorData["EditorData<br/>editor/editor_data.cpp<br/>Scene state, undo/redo history"]
        EditorInterface["EditorInterface<br/>editor/editor_interface.cpp<br/>Public API for plugins"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Editor Plugins"
        CanvasItemEditor["CanvasItemEditor<br/>2D scene editor"]
        Node3DEditor["Node3DEditor<br/>3D scene editor"]
        ScriptEditor["ScriptEditor<br/>Code editor"]
        EditorPlugin["EditorPlugin<br/>Base plugin class"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Editor Docks"
        SceneTreeDock["SceneTreeDock<br/>Hierarchy editor"]
        FileSystemDock["FileSystemDock<br/>Asset browser"]
        InspectorDock["InspectorDock<br/>Property editor"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Editor Services"
        EditorSettings["EditorSettings<br/>Editor configuration"]
        EditorFileSystem["EditorFileSystem<br/>Asset scanning"]
        EditorResourcePreview["EditorResourcePreview<br/>Thumbnail generation"]
    end
    
    EditorNode --> EditorData
    EditorNode --> EditorInterface
    EditorNode --> SceneTreeDock
    EditorNode --> FileSystemDock
    EditorNode --> InspectorDock
    
    EditorPlugin --> EditorInterface
    CanvasItemEditor --> EditorPlugin
    Node3DEditor --> EditorPlugin
    ScriptEditor --> EditorPlugin
    
    EditorNode --> EditorSettings
    FileSystemDock --> EditorFileSystem
    FileSystemDock --> EditorResourcePreview
```

### Editor Initialization

The editor is initialized in `Main::setup()` when the `--editor` flag is present:

```mermaid
graph TB
    MainSetup["Main::setup()<br/>main/main.cpp"]
    EditorCheck["if editor flag"]
    EditorNodeInit["EditorNode singleton created"]
    EditorSettings["EditorSettings::create()"]
    EditorTheme["EditorThemeManager::generate_theme()"]
    PluginsInit["Load and initialize EditorPlugins"]
    SceneLoad["Load last opened scene"]
    
    MainSetup --> EditorCheck
    EditorCheck -->|"true"| EditorSettings
    EditorSettings --> EditorTheme
    EditorTheme --> EditorNodeInit
    EditorNodeInit --> PluginsInit
    PluginsInit --> SceneLoad
```

**Sources:** [main/main.cpp:2100-2800](), [editor/editor_node.cpp:207-8800](), [editor/editor_interface.cpp:1-600]()

### Plugin System

Plugins extend editor functionality by inheriting from `EditorPlugin`:

| Method | Purpose |
|--------|---------|
| `_enter_tree()` | Called when plugin is activated |
| `_edit(Object*)` | Called when an object is selected for editing |
| `_handles(Object*)` | Returns true if plugin can edit this object type |
| `_make_visible(bool)` | Called when plugin's editor becomes visible/hidden |
| `_get_plugin_icon()` | Returns icon for the plugin |

**Sources:** [editor/editor_node.cpp:4000-4500](), [editor/plugins/editor_plugin.h]()

## GUI System Architecture

The GUI system is built on the `Control` class, which provides layout management, theme support, and input handling.

```mermaid
graph TB
    CanvasItem["CanvasItem<br/>Base 2D drawing class"]
    Control["Control<br/>scene/gui/control.cpp<br/>GUI base with layout"]
    Container["Container<br/>Automatic child layout"]
    Button["Button"]
    Label["Label"]
    TextEdit["TextEdit<br/>Multi-line text editor"]
    
    CanvasItem --> Control
    Control --> Container
    Control --> Button
    Control --> Label
    Control --> TextEdit
    Container --> VBoxContainer
    Container --> HBoxContainer
```

### Layout System

Controls use an anchor-based layout system:

| Layout Mode | Description |
|-------------|-------------|
| Anchors | Four anchor points (left, top, right, bottom) relative to parent, values 0.0 to 1.0 |
| Offsets | Pixel offsets from anchor positions |
| Margins | Deprecated term for offsets |
| Size Flags | Control how containers allocate space (expand, fill, shrink) |

**Sources:** [scene/gui/control.cpp:1-500](), [doc/classes/Control.xml:1-1000]()

### Theme System

The theme system provides consistent styling across the UI:

```mermaid
graph LR
    ThemeDB["ThemeDB<br/>Global theme registry"]
    Theme["Theme resource"]
    Control["Control node"]
    ThemeOwner["ThemeOwner mixin"]
    
    ThemeDB -->|"default theme"| Theme
    Theme -->|"contains"| StyleBox["StyleBox items"]
    Theme -->|"contains"| Font["Font items"]
    Theme -->|"contains"| Color["Color items"]
    Theme -->|"contains"| Constant["Constant items"]
    Control -->|"uses"| ThemeOwner
    ThemeOwner -->|"queries"| ThemeDB
    ThemeOwner -->|"queries"| Theme
```

**Sources:** [scene/gui/control.cpp:309-400](), [scene/main/window.cpp:63-165]()

## Configuration System

`ProjectSettings` provides global configuration management:

```mermaid
graph TB
    ProjectSettings["ProjectSettings<br/>core/config/project_settings.cpp<br/>Singleton"]
    ProjectGodot["project.godot<br/>Main configuration file"]
    OverrideCfg["override.cfg<br/>Local overrides"]
    FeatureTags["Feature tags<br/>Platform/config overrides"]
    
    ProjectSettings -->|"loads"| ProjectGodot
    ProjectSettings -->|"loads"| OverrideCfg
    ProjectSettings -->|"applies"| FeatureTags
```

### Key Configuration Categories

| Category | Example Settings |
|----------|------------------|
| `application/config/` | name, icon, main_scene |
| `display/window/` | size, mode, vsync |
| `rendering/` | renderer, quality settings, driver |
| `physics/` | 2d/3d physics settings |
| `input/` | Input action mappings |

**Sources:** [core/config/project_settings.cpp:1-200](), [doc/classes/ProjectSettings.xml:1-500]()

## Build System Structure

The build system uses SCons with platform-specific detection:

```mermaid
graph TB
    SConstruct["SConstruct<br/>Main build script"]
    Methods["methods.py<br/>Build utilities"]
    DetectPy["platform/*/detect.py<br/>Platform detection"]
    
    LibCore["libcore.a<br/>Core library"]
    LibScene["libscene.a<br/>Scene system"]
    LibServers["libservers.a<br/>Server implementations"]
    LibEditor["libeditor.a<br/>(optional)"]
    LibPlatform["libplatform_*.a<br/>Platform-specific"]
    
    Binary["godot executable"]
    
    SConstruct --> Methods
    SConstruct --> DetectPy
    SConstruct --> LibCore
    SConstruct --> LibScene
    SConstruct --> LibServers
    SConstruct --> LibEditor
    SConstruct --> LibPlatform
    
    LibCore --> Binary
    LibScene --> Binary
    LibServers --> Binary
    LibEditor --> Binary
    LibPlatform --> Binary
```

Platform detection scripts configure:
- Compiler flags
- Platform-specific dependencies
- Graphics API support (Vulkan, D3D12, Metal, OpenGL)
- Audio/input drivers
- Architecture-specific optimizations

**Sources:** Build system documentation in [Build System](#9)

## Key Design Patterns

### Server Architecture

Godot uses a server pattern for performance-critical subsystems:

- **RenderingServer**: All graphics operations
- **PhysicsServer2D/3D**: Physics simulation
- **AudioServer**: Audio processing
- **NavigationServer2D/3D**: Pathfinding

Servers can run in separate threads and use command queuing for thread safety.

### RID (Resource ID) System

Resources managed by servers use RIDs instead of direct pointers:
- Thread-safe
- Validated on access
- Can be passed between threads
- Prevent dangling references

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/rendering_server.h](), [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:1-200]()

### Singleton Pattern

Many core systems are singletons accessed via static methods:
```cpp
ProjectSettings::get_singleton()
RenderingServer::get_singleton()
SceneTree::get_singleton()  // When in tree
EditorNode::get_singleton()  // In editor
```

**Sources:** [core/config/project_settings.cpp:56-58](), [editor/editor_node.cpp:207]()

## Summary

The Godot Engine architecture is organized into clear layers:

1. **Application Layer**: Entry point ([main/main.cpp]()), OS abstraction
2. **Core Services**: ProjectSettings, Engine, resource management
3. **Server Layer**: RenderingServer, PhysicsServer, AudioServer
4. **Scene System**: SceneTree, Node hierarchy, Viewport
5. **Specialized Systems**: GUI (Control), Editor (EditorNode), Scripting

This layered approach allows:
- Clear separation of concerns
- Platform independence through abstraction
- Thread-safe operation via server architecture
- Extensibility through inheritance and plugin systems

For in-depth information on specific subsystems, refer to the linked wiki pages at the beginning of this document.

**Sources:** [main/main.cpp:1-3100](), [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp:1-2200](), [editor/editor_node.cpp:1-8800](), [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:1-1000]()18:T4f11,# Core Engine Architecture

- [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.cpp](servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.cpp)

- [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_render.h](servers/rendering/renderer_scene_render.h)
- [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp](servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp)
- [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.h](servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.h)
- [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h](servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document provides an architectural overview of Godot's core engine systems, covering the fundamental components that initialize the engine, manage the scene graph, and connect gameplay logic to rendering. It explains how the main entry point initializes core services, how the scene tree manages the node hierarchy and game loop, and how viewports bridge the scene system to the rendering backend.

For details on the main loop and initialization sequence, see [Engine Initialization and Main Loop](#2.1). For the scene graph implementation and node lifecycle, see [Scene Tree and Node System](#2.2). For viewport rendering integration specifics, see [Viewport and Rendering Integration](#2.3).

---

## Architectural Overview

The Godot engine architecture consists of four primary layers that work together to run games:

**Application Layer**: The `Main` class ([main/main.cpp]()) serves as the entry point, initializing all engine subsystems and running the main loop. Platform-specific implementations of the `OS` class provide abstraction for operating system services.

**Core Services**: Singleton services like `ProjectSettings`, `ResourceLoader`, and `RenderingServer` provide essential functionality that is accessible throughout the engine. These are initialized early and remain available for the lifetime of the application.

**Scene System**: The `SceneTree` manages the hierarchical organization of `Node` objects and implements the game loop via the `MainLoop` interface. `Viewport` nodes serve as rendering surfaces within this hierarchy.

**Server Layer**: Low-level servers like `RenderingServer`, `PhysicsServer2D`, `PhysicsServer3D`, and others provide the actual implementation of rendering, physics, and other engine features. The scene system communicates with these servers through their APIs.

### Core Architecture Diagram

```mermaid
graph TB
    Main["Main<br/>(main/main.cpp)"]
    OS["OS<br/>(core/os/os.h)"]
    Engine["Engine<br/>(core/config/engine.h)"]
    
    subgraph "Core Services"
        PS["ProjectSettings<br/>(core/config/project_settings.h)"]
        RL["ResourceLoader<br/>(core/io/resource_loader.h)"]
        RS["RenderingServer<br/>(servers/rendering/)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Main Loop Implementation"
        ML["MainLoop<br/>(core/os/main_loop.h)"]
        ST["SceneTree<br/>(scene/main/scene_tree.h)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Scene Graph"
        Node["Node<br/>(scene/main/node.h)"]
        VP["Viewport<br/>(scene/main/viewport.h)"]
        Control["Control<br/>(scene/gui/control.h)"]
    end
    
    Main -->|"setup()"| PS
    Main -->|"setup()"| RL
    Main -->|"setup()"| RS
    Main -->|"setup2()"| ST
    Main -->|"iteration()"| ML
    
    ML <|..|"implements"| ST
    ST -->|"manages"| Node
    Node <|--|"inherits"| VP
    Node <|--|"inherits"| Control
    
    VP -->|"rendering API"| RS
    ST -->|"uses"| Engine
    ST -->|"uses"| OS
    
    Node -->|"loads via"| RL
```

**Sources**: [main/main.cpp:163-199](), [scene/main/scene_tree.h:61-103](), [scene/main/node.h:53-237](), [scene/main/viewport.h:95-534]()

---

## Initialization Sequence

The engine initialization follows a multi-stage process coordinated by the `Main` class. This ensures that dependencies are satisfied and systems come online in the correct order.

### Initialization Flow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Platform
    participant Main
    participant OS
    participant Engine
    participant ProjectSettings
    participant RenderingServer
    participant SceneTree
    participant Node
    
    Platform->>Main: main()
    Main->>Main: setup()
    Main->>OS: initialize()
    Main->>Engine: new Engine()
    Main->>ProjectSettings: new ProjectSettings()
    Note over Main,ProjectSettings: Register core types<br/>Load project.godot
    
    Main->>Main: setup2()
    Main->>RenderingServer: create server instance
    Main->>SceneTree: new SceneTree()
    SceneTree->>Node: create root viewport
    
    Main->>Main: start()
    Note over Main,SceneTree: Main loop begins
    
    loop Each Frame
        Main->>SceneTree: iteration(delta)
        SceneTree->>Node: _process() callbacks
        SceneTree->>Node: _physics_process() callbacks
        SceneTree->>RenderingServer: flush commands
    end
```

**Sources**: [main/main.cpp:742-941](), [main/main.cpp:2435-2794](), [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp:1219-1335]()

### Initialization Stages

The initialization process is divided into distinct stages, each with specific responsibilities:

| Stage | Function | Key Responsibilities |
|-------|----------|---------------------|
| **Setup** | `Main::setup()` | Initialize OS, create Engine singleton, create ProjectSettings, register core types, load project configuration |
| **Setup2** | `Main::setup2()` | Create display server, initialize rendering server, create audio server, create physics servers, create SceneTree |
| **Start** | `Main::start()` | Load main scene, begin main loop execution |
| **Iteration** | `Main::iteration()` | Process one frame: handle input, run physics, call process callbacks, render frame |

**Sources**: [main/main.cpp:742-941](), [main/main.cpp:2435-2539](), [main/main.cpp:2794-3074](), [main/main.cpp:3092-3368]()

---

## Core Services

Core services are singleton objects that provide essential functionality throughout the engine. They are initialized during the setup phase and remain available globally.

### ProjectSettings

`ProjectSettings` ([core/config/project_settings.h]()) is a singleton that stores configuration values from `project.godot`. It provides a key-value store for project settings, supports feature tag overrides, and handles loading/saving configuration files.

Key methods:
- `get_setting()` - Retrieve a configuration value
- `set_setting()` - Set a configuration value  
- `get_setting_with_override()` - Get setting with feature tag overrides applied
- `save()` - Save settings to disk

**Sources**: [core/config/project_settings.h:56-239](), [core/config/project_settings.cpp:56-240]()

### ResourceLoader

`ResourceLoader` provides the interface for loading resources from disk. It delegates to format-specific loaders registered for different file types (`.tres`, `.res`, `.import`, etc.).

The loading process:
1. Determine file format
2. Select appropriate `ResourceFormatLoader`
3. Parse file and construct Resource object
4. Cache loaded resource to prevent duplicates
5. Return reference to caller

**Sources**: [main/main.cpp:50](), [doc/classes/ProjectSettings.xml:1-11]()

### RenderingServer

`RenderingServer` ([servers/rendering/]()) is the low-level API for all rendering operations. Scene nodes like `CanvasItem` and `Node3D` communicate with the rendering server using RIDs (Resource IDs) to create and manipulate rendering resources.

The rendering server:
- Runs on a separate thread (in most configurations)
- Accepts commands from the main thread via a command queue
- Manages rendering resources (meshes, textures, materials, etc.)
- Performs scene culling and rendering

**Sources**: [main/main.cpp:82-83](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/](), [doc/classes/RenderingServer.xml:1-16]()

---

## Scene System Architecture

The scene system consists of the `SceneTree` managing a hierarchy of `Node` objects. This provides the fundamental structure for organizing game content.

### SceneTree and MainLoop

```mermaid
graph TB
    MainLoop["MainLoop<br/>(abstract interface)"]
    SceneTree["SceneTree<br/>(concrete implementation)"]
    Root["Root Viewport"]
    
    MainLoop -->|"iteration()<br/>_process_frame()"| SceneTree
    
    SceneTree -->|"contains"| Root
    SceneTree -->|"manages"| Groups["Node Groups"]
    SceneTree -->|"tracks"| Timers["SceneTreeTimer objects"]
    
    subgraph "Frame Processing"
        Physics["_physics_process()"]
        Process["_process()"]
        Input["Input events"]
    end
    
    SceneTree -->|"dispatches"| Physics
    SceneTree -->|"dispatches"| Process
    SceneTree -->|"distributes"| Input
    
    Root -->|"root of"| NodeTree["Node Hierarchy"]
```

**Sources**: [scene/main/scene_tree.h:61-445](), [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp:1219-1335](), [core/os/main_loop.h:34-69]()

`SceneTree` implements the `MainLoop` interface, making it the game loop implementation. The `Main::iteration()` function calls `MainLoop::iteration()`, which in SceneTree's case processes the frame:

1. **Input Phase**: Distribute input events to nodes
2. **Physics Phase**: Call `_physics_process()` on all nodes with physics processing enabled
3. **Idle Phase**: Call `_process()` on all nodes with processing enabled  
4. **Render Phase**: Flush rendering commands to RenderingServer

**Sources**: [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp:474-563](), [main/main.cpp:3181-3260]()

### Node Hierarchy

Nodes form a tree structure where each node can have multiple children and one parent. The `Node` class ([scene/main/node.h]()) provides the base functionality for all scene objects.

```mermaid
graph TB
    Node["Node<br/>(scene/main/node.h)"]
    
    subgraph "Node State"
        Parent["parent: Node*"]
        Children["children: HashMap&lt;StringName, Node*&gt;"]
        Tree["tree: SceneTree*"]
        Owner["owner: Node*"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Node Lifecycle"
        EnterTree["_enter_tree()"]
        Ready["_ready()"]
        Process["_process(delta)"]
        PhysicsProcess["_physics_process(delta)"]
        ExitTree["_exit_tree()"]
    end
    
    Node --> Parent
    Node --> Children
    Node --> Tree
    Node --> Owner
    
    Tree -->|"calls"| EnterTree
    Tree -->|"calls"| Ready
    Tree -->|"calls"| Process
    Tree -->|"calls"| PhysicsProcess
    Tree -->|"calls"| ExitTree
```

**Sources**: [scene/main/node.h:197-239](), [scene/main/node.cpp:68-323](), [doc/classes/Node.xml:7-18]()

#### Node Lifecycle

When a node is added to the scene tree:

1. `_enter_tree()` - Called when node enters the tree (before children)
2. Children's `_enter_tree()` - Called recursively
3. Children's `_ready()` - Called in reverse order (children before parents)
4. `_ready()` - Called when node and all children are in tree

When processing:
- `_physics_process(delta)` - Called at fixed physics rate (default 60 Hz)
- `_process(delta)` - Called once per frame

When removed:
1. `_exit_tree()` - Called before node leaves tree
2. Children's `_exit_tree()` - Called recursively

**Sources**: [scene/main/node.cpp:343-391](), [scene/main/node.cpp:412-459](), [doc/classes/Node.xml:25-37]()

### Processing Modes

Nodes can have different processing modes that determine when they receive process callbacks:

| Process Mode | Behavior |
|--------------|----------|
| `PROCESS_MODE_INHERIT` | Use parent's mode |
| `PROCESS_MODE_PAUSABLE` | Process only when tree is not paused |
| `PROCESS_MODE_WHEN_PAUSED` | Process only when tree is paused |
| `PROCESS_MODE_ALWAYS` | Process regardless of pause state |
| `PROCESS_MODE_DISABLED` | Never process |

**Sources**: [scene/main/node.h:78-84](), [scene/main/node.cpp:671-766]()

---

## Viewport Integration

`Viewport` ([scene/main/viewport.h]()) is a special node that serves as a rendering surface. It bridges the scene graph to the rendering system by:

1. Owning a RenderingServer viewport RID
2. Receiving rendering commands from child nodes
3. Managing 2D canvas and 3D scenario
4. Processing input events
5. Handling GUI focus and mouse interaction

### Viewport Architecture

```mermaid
graph TB
    Viewport["Viewport<br/>(scene/main/viewport.h)"]
    ViewportRID["viewport: RID"]
    
    subgraph "2D Rendering"
        Canvas["canvas: RID"]
        CanvasItems["CanvasItem nodes"]
        Canvas2D["Camera2D"]
    end
    
    subgraph "3D Rendering"
        Scenario["scenario: RID"]
        Instances["Node3D instances"]
        Camera3D["Camera3D"]
    end
    
    subgraph "GUI System"
        GUIRoot["GUI input root"]
        Control["Control nodes"]
        Focus["Focus tracking"]
    end
    
    Viewport -->|"owns"| ViewportRID
    ViewportRID -->|"RS API"| RenderingServer
    
    Viewport -->|"2D world"| Canvas
    Canvas -->|"draws"| CanvasItems
    Canvas2D -->|"view for"| Canvas
    
    Viewport -->|"3D world"| Scenario
    Scenario -->|"contains"| Instances
    Camera3D -->|"view for"| Scenario
    
    Viewport -->|"processes input"| GUIRoot
    GUIRoot -->|"distributes to"| Control
    GUIRoot -->|"manages"| Focus
```

**Sources**: [scene/main/viewport.h:95-534](), [scene/main/viewport.cpp:592-776]()

### Viewport Rendering Flow

Each frame, the viewport:

1. **Update Transform**: Calculate canvas transform and update RenderingServer
2. **Process Input**: Distribute input events to GUI and 3D picking system
3. **Update 2D**: Send canvas item draw commands to RenderingServer
4. **Update 3D**: Update instance transforms in scenario
5. **Render**: RenderingServer renders viewport contents to texture or screen

**Sources**: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:779-1126](), [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp:1-76]()

### Sub-Viewports

Viewports can be nested to create sub-viewports for effects like split-screen or render-to-texture. Each sub-viewport:

- Has its own rendering surface
- Can have independent 2D/3D worlds
- Receives input only if explicitly configured
- Renders to a `ViewportTexture` that can be displayed

**Sources**: [scene/main/viewport.h:55-93](), [scene/main/viewport.cpp:87-261]()

---

## Runtime Structure

At runtime, the engine maintains the following structure:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Main["Main Loop Thread"]
    SceneTree["SceneTree instance"]
    RootVP["Root Viewport"]
    
    subgraph "Node Hierarchy"
        MainScene["Main Scene Root"]
        Node1["Node"]
        Node2["Node"]
        Viewport2["Sub-Viewport"]
        Control1["Control"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Rendering Thread"
        RSImpl["RenderingServerDefault"]
        CommandQueue["CommandQueueMT"]
        Backend["Renderer Backend"]
    end
    
    Main -->|"iteration()"| SceneTree
    SceneTree -->|"root"| RootVP
    RootVP -->|"children"| MainScene
    MainScene --> Node1
    MainScene --> Node2
    Node1 --> Viewport2
    MainScene --> Control1
    
    RootVP -->|"draw commands"| CommandQueue
    Viewport2 -->|"draw commands"| CommandQueue
    Control1 -->|"draw commands"| CommandQueue
    
    CommandQueue -->|"thread-safe queue"| RSImpl
    RSImpl -->|"executes on render thread"| Backend
```

**Sources**: [main/main.cpp:3092-3368](), [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp:474-563](), [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:1-55]()

The main thread runs the game loop, processes nodes, and enqueues rendering commands. The rendering thread (when enabled) dequeues commands and performs actual rendering operations. This separation allows the CPU and GPU to work in parallel.

---

## Key Interactions

### Node to RenderingServer Communication

Nodes communicate with RenderingServer through RIDs:

1. Node creates rendering resource: `RID mesh_rid = RS::get_singleton()->mesh_create()`
2. Node configures resource: `RS::get_singleton()->mesh_add_surface(...)`
3. Node updates resource each frame if needed
4. Node frees resource on destruction: `RS::get_singleton()->free_rid(mesh_rid)`

**Sources**: [servers/rendering/rendering_server.h](), [doc/classes/RenderingServer.xml:7-15]()

### Input Event Flow

Input events flow from the OS through the viewport hierarchy:

1. `DisplayServer` receives OS input event
2. Event sent to root `Viewport`
3. Viewport processes event for GUI system
4. If not handled, event propagates to scene nodes via groups:
   - `_vp_input` group receives `_input()` calls
   - `_vp_unhandled_input` group receives `_unhandled_input()` calls

**Sources**: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:779-1126](), [scene/main/node.cpp:107-186](), [doc/classes/Node.xml:72-81]()

### Resource Loading and Scene Instantiation

When loading a scene:

1. `ResourceLoader::load("res://scene.tscn")` loads PackedScene resource
2. `PackedScene::instantiate()` creates node hierarchy from scene data
3. Nodes added to tree with `add_child()`
4. `_enter_tree()` and `_ready()` callbacks fire
5. Nodes begin receiving process callbacks

**Sources**: [scene/resources/packed_scene.h](), [scene/main/node.cpp:343-391]()

---

## Summary

The core engine architecture consists of:

- **Main entry point** (`Main` class) that initializes subsystems and runs the main loop
- **Core services** (ProjectSettings, ResourceLoader, RenderingServer) providing global functionality
- **Scene system** (SceneTree, Node) managing the hierarchy and game loop
- **Viewport system** bridging scene nodes to rendering backend
- **Server layer** providing low-level implementations

This architecture provides a clean separation of concerns while maintaining tight integration between systems. The node hierarchy provides a flexible way to organize game content, while the server layer ensures efficient rendering and physics simulation.

For detailed information about specific subsystems, see the related pages: [Engine Initialization and Main Loop](#2.1), [Scene Tree and Node System](#2.2), and [Viewport and Rendering Integration](#2.3).19:T3d78,# Engine Initialization and Main Loop

This document explains how the Godot engine initializes its core subsystems during startup and executes the main game loop during runtime. It covers the initialization phases, singleton creation, and frame-by-frame execution flow.

**Scope**: This page focuses on engine-level initialization (`Main::setup()`, `Main::setup2()`, `Main::start()`) and the main loop execution (`Main::iteration()`). For details about the scene graph and node lifecycle, see [Scene Tree and Node System](#2.2). For viewport-specific rendering integration, see [Viewport and Rendering Integration](#2.3).

## Initialization Phases

The engine initialization occurs in three distinct phases executed sequentially by platform-specific entry points. Each phase initializes progressively higher-level subsystems.

```mermaid
graph TB
    Entry["Platform Entry Point<br/>(main(), WinMain(), etc.)"]
    Setup1["Main::setup()<br/>Phase 1: Core Systems"]
    Setup2["Main::setup2()<br/>Phase 2: Servers"]
    Start["Main::start()<br/>Phase 3: Scene Load"]
    Loop["Main::iteration()<br/>Main Loop"]
    Cleanup["Main::cleanup()<br/>Shutdown"]
    
    Entry --> Setup1
    Setup1 --> Setup2
    Setup2 --> Start
    Start --> Loop
    Loop -->|"exit=true"| Cleanup
    Loop -->|"continue"| Loop
```

**Diagram: Engine Initialization and Execution Flow**

Sources: [main/main.cpp:1-2500]()

### Phase 1: Core Setup (Main::setup)

The first initialization phase establishes the most fundamental engine systems. This phase processes command-line arguments, initializes the OS abstraction layer, and creates core singletons.

**Key Systems Initialized:**

| System | Singleton Variable | Class | Purpose |
|--------|-------------------|-------|---------|
| Engine Configuration | `engine` | `Engine` | Stores engine version, feature flags, and runtime state |
| Project Settings | `globals` | `ProjectSettings` | Manages project configuration from `project.godot` |
| Input System | `input` | `Input` | Handles raw input device state |
| Input Mapping | `input_map` | `InputMap` | Maps input events to actions |
| Localization | `translation_server` | `TranslationServer` | Manages translations and locale |
| Performance Monitoring | `performance` | `Performance` | Tracks performance metrics |
| Packed Data | `packed_data` | `PackedData` | Manages PCK/ZIP file resources |
| Message Queue | `message_queue` | `MessageQueue` | Deferred method call queue |

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Main
    participant OS
    participant ProjectSettings
    participant Engine
    participant PackedData
    
    Main->>OS: initialize()
    Main->>Engine: create singleton
    Main->>ProjectSettings: create singleton
    Main->>ProjectSettings: setup()
    ProjectSettings->>PackedData: load .pck files
    Main->>OS: parse command line
    Note over Main: Register core types
    Main->>ProjectSettings: load project.godot
```

**Diagram: Phase 1 Initialization Sequence**

The `setup()` function also registers core types (via `register_core_types()`) which makes fundamental classes like `String`, `Vector2`, `Resource` available to the reflection system.

Sources: [main/main.cpp:742-1500](), [core/config/project_settings.cpp:1-700]()

### Phase 2: Server Initialization (Main::setup2)

Phase 2 creates the high-level server singletons that provide rendering, audio, physics, and other major subsystems. This phase requires the OS and display to be initialized first.

**Server Singletons:**

| Server | Variable | Purpose |
|--------|----------|---------|
| `DisplayServer` | `display_server` | Window management and OS display integration |
| `RenderingServer` | `rendering_server` | Low-level rendering API (RenderingServerDefault) |
| `AudioServer` | `audio_server` | Audio mixing and playback |
| `PhysicsServer2D` | `physics_server_2d` | 2D physics simulation |
| `PhysicsServer3D` | `physics_server_3d` | 3D physics simulation |
| `NavigationServer2D` | Navigation in 2D space |
| `NavigationServer3D` | Navigation in 3D space |
| `XRServer` | `xr_server` | VR/AR interface (if not disabled) |
| `CameraServer` | `camera_server` | Camera device management |
| `TextServerManager` | `tsman` | Text rendering and shaping |
| `ThemeDB` | `theme_db` | UI theme management |

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Phase 2 Initialization Order"
        DisplayServer["DisplayServer::create()"]
        RenderingServer["RenderingServerDefault::create()"]
        AudioServer["AudioServer::create()"]
        PhysicsServers["Physics Server Initialization"]
        ThemeDB["ThemeDB Initialization"]
        SceneTypes["Register Scene Types"]
        
        DisplayServer --> RenderingServer
        RenderingServer --> AudioServer
        AudioServer --> PhysicsServers
        PhysicsServers --> ThemeDB
        ThemeDB --> SceneTypes
    end
```

**Diagram: Server Creation Dependencies**

The `initialize_physics()` helper function specifically handles physics server setup, checking project settings to determine which physics implementation to use and falling back to dummy servers if needed.

Sources: [main/main.cpp:1500-2100](), [main/main.cpp:358-410](), [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:47-100]()

### Phase 3: Scene Initialization (Main::start)

The final initialization phase loads the main scene or editor. For game exports, this creates a `SceneTree` instance and loads the main scene specified in project settings. For the editor, it creates `EditorNode`.

```mermaid
graph LR
    Start["Main::start()"]
    CheckEditor{"Editor Mode?"}
    CreateSceneTree["Create SceneTree"]
    CreateEditor["Create EditorNode"]
    LoadMainScene["Load Main Scene"]
    Ready["System Ready"]
    
    Start --> CheckEditor
    CheckEditor -->|"No"| CreateSceneTree
    CheckEditor -->|"Yes"| CreateEditor
    CreateSceneTree --> LoadMainScene
    CreateEditor --> Ready
    LoadMainScene --> Ready
```

**Diagram: Phase 3 Branching Logic**

The `SceneTree` instance becomes the active `MainLoop` and takes control of per-frame execution. The scene tree is stored in `OS::get_singleton()->get_main_loop()`.

Sources: [main/main.cpp:2100-2500](), [scene/main/scene_tree.h:1-200]()

## Main Loop Execution

The main loop runs continuously until the application exits, processing one frame at a time. The loop is driven by `Main::iteration()` which delegates to the active `MainLoop` implementation (typically `SceneTree`).

### MainLoop Interface

The `MainLoop` class defines the abstract interface for game loop execution:

| Method | Purpose |
|--------|---------|
| `initialize()` | Called once before first iteration |
| `physics_process(delta)` | Fixed-timestep physics update |
| `process(delta)` | Variable-timestep frame update |
| `finalize()` | Called once before destruction |

`SceneTree` implements this interface to propagate updates through the node tree.

Sources: [core/object/main_loop.h:1-100]()

### Frame Processing Flow

Each call to `Main::iteration()` executes one complete frame, handling physics, rendering, and script execution.

```mermaid
graph TB
    Start["Main::iteration()"]
    TimerSync["MainTimerSync<br/>Calculate delta time"]
    PhysicsSteps{"Physics<br/>Steps Due?"}
    PhysicsProcess["SceneTree::physics_process()"]
    ProcessStep["SceneTree::process()"]
    FlushCommands["MessageQueue::flush()"]
    RenderFrame["RenderingServer::draw()"]
    SwapBuffers["DisplayServer::swap_buffers()"]
    End["Return continue/exit"]
    
    Start --> TimerSync
    TimerSync --> PhysicsSteps
    PhysicsSteps -->|"Yes, N times"| PhysicsProcess
    PhysicsProcess --> PhysicsSteps
    PhysicsSteps -->|"Done"| ProcessStep
    ProcessStep --> FlushCommands
    FlushCommands --> RenderFrame
    RenderFrame --> SwapBuffers
    SwapBuffers --> End
```

**Diagram: Single Frame Iteration**

The `MainTimerSync` class manages frame timing, ensuring physics runs at a fixed timestep (default 60 Hz) while rendering runs as fast as possible. If the frame rate drops below the physics rate, multiple physics steps execute in a single frame to catch up.

Sources: [main/main.cpp:2700-3000](), [main/main_timer_sync.h:1-100]()

### SceneTree Frame Processing

When `SceneTree` receives frame callbacks, it propagates them through the node hierarchy:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "SceneTree::physics_process()"
        PhysEntry["SceneTree::physics_process(delta)"]
        PhysIdle["_process_physics_frame()"]
        PhysicsNode["Call _physics_process() on nodes"]
        PhysicsFlush["Flush physics queries"]
    end
    
    subgraph "SceneTree::process()"
        ProcEntry["SceneTree::process(delta)"]
        ProcIdle["_process_frame()"]
        ProcessNode["Call _process() on nodes"]
        NotifyFrame["Send NOTIFICATION_PROCESS"]
    end
    
    PhysEntry --> PhysIdle
    PhysIdle --> PhysicsNode
    PhysicsNode --> PhysicsFlush
    
    ProcEntry --> ProcIdle
    ProcIdle --> ProcessNode
    ProcessNode --> NotifyFrame
```

**Diagram: SceneTree Frame Callbacks**

Nodes receive callbacks in tree order (parent before children by default). The process priority property can modify execution order.

Sources: [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp:400-800]()

### Rendering Integration

After scene processing, the main loop triggers rendering through `RenderingServer`:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Main
    participant SceneTree
    participant Viewport
    participant RenderingServer
    participant DisplayServer
    
    Main->>SceneTree: process(delta)
    SceneTree->>Viewport: update viewport tree
    Main->>RenderingServer: sync()
    Main->>RenderingServer: draw()
    RenderingServer->>RenderingServer: render all viewports
    Main->>DisplayServer: swap_buffers()
    DisplayServer-->>Main: frame complete
```

**Diagram: Rendering Frame Synchronization**

The `RenderingServer` maintains its own command queue that can run on a separate thread (configured via project settings). The `sync()` call ensures all queued commands complete before drawing.

Sources: [main/main.cpp:2900-3000](), [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:80-100]()

## Shutdown and Cleanup

When the main loop exits (either from `SceneTree::quit()` or the OS closing the window), `Main::cleanup()` destroys all systems in reverse order of creation:

**Cleanup Sequence:**

1. Finalize and delete `SceneTree`/`MainLoop`
2. Delete scene types and server singletons
3. Delete core singletons (`ProjectSettings`, `Input`, etc.)
4. Finalize OS abstraction
5. Unload all remaining resources

The cleanup order ensures dependent systems are destroyed before their dependencies. For example, all rendering resources must be freed before `RenderingServer` is deleted.

Sources: [main/main.cpp:3000-3500]()

## Command-Line Argument Processing

The engine processes command-line arguments during `Main::setup()` to configure runtime behavior before subsystem initialization. Arguments are parsed in [main/main.cpp:900-1400]().

**Common Arguments:**

| Argument | Effect | Phase |
|----------|--------|-------|
| `--editor` | Launch editor instead of game | Phase 1 |
| `--headless` | Disable display and audio | Phase 1 |
| `--path <dir>` | Set project directory | Phase 1 |
| `--rendering-driver <driver>` | Select rendering backend | Phase 2 |
| `--audio-driver <driver>` | Select audio backend | Phase 2 |
| `--fixed-fps <n>` | Force fixed frame rate | Main loop |

These arguments set global flags that later phases check when creating subsystems. For example, `--headless` sets `display_driver = "headless"` which `DisplayServer::create()` reads during Phase 2.

Sources: [main/main.cpp:525-732](), [main/main.cpp:900-1400]()

## Threading Model

The engine can run servers on separate threads for improved parallelism:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Main Thread"
        MainLoop["Main Loop"]
        SceneTree["Scene Tree"]
        Input["Input Processing"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Render Thread (Optional)"
        RenderServer["RenderingServer"]
        DrawCommands["Draw Commands"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Audio Thread"
        AudioServer["AudioServer"]
        AudioMix["Audio Mixing"]
    end
    
    MainLoop -->|"queue commands"| RenderServer
    RenderServer -->|"sync"| MainLoop
    AudioServer -.->|"independent"| AudioMix
```

**Diagram: Multi-threaded Server Architecture**

The render thread is controlled by the `render_thread_mode` project setting (values: `unsafe`, `safe`, `separate`). In `separate` mode, `RenderingServerDefault` uses `CommandQueueMT` to marshal calls between threads safely.

Sources: [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:80-100](), [main/main.cpp:1600-1700]()

## Purpose and Scope

This document describes Godot's scene graph architecture, focusing on the `Node` class hierarchy and the `SceneTree` that manages it. The scene tree is the fundamental organizational structure for all game objects in Godot, providing a hierarchical container for nodes with lifecycle management, process callbacks, and group-based organization.

For information about the main loop and engine initialization, see [Engine Initialization and Main Loop](#2.1). For viewport-specific rendering integration, see [Viewport and Rendering Integration](#2.3).

## Overview

The scene tree system consists of two primary components:

1. **Node**: The base class for all scene objects, providing hierarchy, lifecycle, and processing capabilities
2. **SceneTree**: A `MainLoop` implementation that manages the active node hierarchy and game loop

All visible and interactive game objects inherit from `Node`. Nodes are organized in a tree structure where each node can have one parent and multiple children. The `SceneTree` singleton manages this hierarchy, coordinates lifecycle notifications, and drives the per-frame processing callbacks.

### SceneTree as MainLoop Implementation

```mermaid
graph TB
    Main["Main::iteration<br/>(main/main.cpp)"]
    MainLoop["MainLoop<br/>(core/os/main_loop.h)"]
    SceneTree["SceneTree<br/>(scene/main/scene_tree.h)"]
    
    Main -->|"calls process()"| MainLoop
    MainLoop -.->|"implements"| SceneTree
    SceneTree -->|"manages"| NodeHierarchy["Node Hierarchy"]
    SceneTree -->|"drives"| ProcessCallbacks["Process Callbacks"]
    
    subgraph "Virtual Methods"
        Init["_initialize()"]
        PhysProc["_physics_process(delta)"]
        Proc["_process(delta)"]
        Final["_finalize()"]
    end
    
    MainLoop --> Init
    MainLoop --> PhysProc
    MainLoop --> Proc
    MainLoop --> Final
```

**Sources:** [core/os/main_loop.h:36-72](), [scene/main/scene_tree.h:1-664](), [doc/classes/SceneTree.xml:1-589]()

## The Node Class

`Node` is the base class for all scene objects. It provides the foundation for the scene graph structure, lifecycle management, and processing systems.

### Node Class Hierarchy

```mermaid
graph TB
    Object["Object"]
    Node["Node<br/>(scene/main/node.h)"]
    Node2D["Node2D<br/>2D Transform"]
    Node3D["Node3D<br/>3D Transform"]
    CanvasItem["CanvasItem<br/>2D Drawing"]
    Control["Control<br/>UI Base"]
    Viewport["Viewport<br/>Rendering Surface"]
    Window["Window"]
    
    Object --> Node
    Node --> Node2D
    Node --> Node3D
    Node --> CanvasItem
    CanvasItem --> Control
    CanvasItem --> Viewport
    Viewport --> Window
    
    Node2D --> Camera2D["Camera2D"]
    Node2D --> Sprite2D["Sprite2D"]
    Node3D --> Camera3D["Camera3D"]
    Node3D --> MeshInstance3D["MeshInstance3D"]
```

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.h:53-833](), [doc/classes/Node.xml:1-1392]()

### Core Node Data Structure

The `Node` class maintains essential state through its nested `Data` struct:

| Member | Type | Purpose |
|--------|------|---------|
| `parent` | `Node*` | Parent node in hierarchy |
| `children` | `HashMap<StringName, Node*>` | Child nodes by name |
| `owner` | `Node*` | Scene owner for persistence |
| `tree` | `SceneTree*` | Active scene tree reference |
| `viewport` | `Viewport*` | Closest viewport ancestor |
| `name` | `StringName` | Unique name within parent |
| `depth` | `int32_t` | Depth in tree (-1 if not in tree) |
| `process_mode` | `ProcessMode` | Processing behavior |
| `process_owner` | `Node*` | Inherited process mode owner |

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.h:198-298]()

## SceneTree Management

The `SceneTree` class is the central manager for the active node hierarchy. It implements the `MainLoop` interface and coordinates all scene-related activities.

### SceneTree Core Responsibilities

```mermaid
graph TB
    SceneTree["SceneTree"]
    
    subgraph "Core Functions"
        NodeMgmt["Node Management<br/>add_to_group()<br/>remove_from_group()"]
        Lifecycle["Lifecycle Coordination<br/>node_added()<br/>node_removed()"]
        Processing["Process Coordination<br/>_process_nodes()<br/>_physics_process_nodes()"]
        Groups["Group Operations<br/>call_group()<br/>notify_group()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "State"
        RootNode["root: Window*"]
        CurrentScene["current_scene: Node*"]
        GroupMap["group_map: HashMap"]
        ProcessGroups["Process Thread Groups"]
    end
    
    SceneTree --> NodeMgmt
    SceneTree --> Lifecycle
    SceneTree --> Processing
    SceneTree --> Groups
    
    NodeMgmt -.-> GroupMap
    Processing -.-> ProcessGroups
    Lifecycle -.-> RootNode
```

**Sources:** [scene/main/scene_tree.h:152-664](), [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp:150-1390]()

### Key SceneTree Methods

| Method | Purpose |
|--------|---------|
| `get_root()` | Returns the root `Window` viewport |
| `get_current_scene()` | Returns the currently active scene root node |
| `change_scene_to_file()` | Loads and switches to a new scene |
| `change_scene_to_node()` | Switches to an already-instantiated scene |
| `call_group()` | Calls a method on all nodes in a group |
| `get_nodes_in_group()` | Returns all nodes belonging to a group |

**Sources:** [doc/classes/SceneTree.xml:15-589]()

## Node Lifecycle

Nodes have a well-defined lifecycle with specific notification points and virtual callbacks.

### Lifecycle Flow Diagram

```mermaid
stateDiagram-v2
    [*] --> Created: new Node()
    Created --> EnteringTree: add_child()
    
    EnteringTree --> InTree: NOTIFICATION_ENTER_TREE
    InTree --> PostEnter: NOTIFICATION_POST_ENTER_TREE
    PostEnter --> Ready: NOTIFICATION_READY
    
    Ready --> Processing: is_inside_tree() == true
    Processing --> Processing: _process() / _physics_process()
    
    Processing --> Exiting: remove_child() / queue_free()
    Exiting --> ExitingNotif: NOTIFICATION_EXIT_TREE
    ExitingNotif --> Exited: tree_exited signal
    Exited --> [*]: Object freed
```

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.cpp:68-323](), [doc/classes/Node.xml:6-16]()

### Lifecycle Methods and Notifications

The lifecycle is implemented through a series of notifications and virtual methods:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Enter Tree Phase"
        AddChild["add_child()"]
        PropEnter["_propagate_enter_tree()"]
        EnterTree["NOTIFICATION_ENTER_TREE"]
        VirtEnter["_enter_tree()"]
        TreeEntered["tree_entered signal"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Ready Phase"
        PropReady["_propagate_ready()"]
        PostEnter["NOTIFICATION_POST_ENTER_TREE"]
        Ready["NOTIFICATION_READY"]
        VirtReady["_ready()"]
        ReadySig["ready signal"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Exit Tree Phase"
        RemChild["remove_child()"]
        PropExit["_propagate_exit_tree()"]
        VirtExit["_exit_tree()"]
        Exiting["tree_exiting signal"]
        ExitTree["NOTIFICATION_EXIT_TREE"]
        Exited["tree_exited signal"]
    end
    
    AddChild --> PropEnter
    PropEnter --> EnterTree --> VirtEnter --> TreeEntered
    TreeEntered --> PropReady
    PropReady --> PostEnter --> Ready --> VirtReady --> ReadySig
    
    RemChild --> PropExit
    PropExit --> VirtExit --> Exiting --> ExitTree --> Exited
```

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.cpp:325-459](), [doc/classes/Node.xml:25-37]()

### Lifecycle Order Guarantees

When adding a node tree to the scene:

1. **Enter Tree**: Parent's `_enter_tree()` â†’ Children's `_enter_tree()` (top-down)
2. **Ready**: Children's `_ready()` â†’ Parent's `_ready()` (bottom-up)

This ensures that:
- Parent nodes can initialize before children enter the tree
- Children are fully ready before parent attempts to access them in `_ready()`

**Sources:** [doc/classes/Node.xml:9-11](), [scene/main/node.cpp:325-390]()

## Node Hierarchy Management

Nodes are organized in a parent-child tree structure with strict naming requirements and efficient lookup.

### Hierarchy Operations

| Method | Description |
|--------|-------------|
| `add_child(node, force_readable_name, internal)` | Adds a child node |
| `remove_child(node)` | Removes a child node |
| `get_child(index, include_internal)` | Gets child by index |
| `get_child_count(include_internal)` | Returns number of children |
| `get_node(path)` | Gets node by NodePath |
| `find_child(pattern, recursive, owned)` | Finds child by name pattern |
| `move_child(child, index)` | Reorders children |

**Sources:** [doc/classes/Node.xml:152-397]()

### Internal Nodes

Nodes can be added as internal nodes using the `InternalMode` enum:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Parent["Parent Node"]
    
    subgraph "Internal Front (INTERNAL_MODE_FRONT)"
        IF1["Internal Child 1"]
        IF2["Internal Child 2"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Normal Children (INTERNAL_MODE_DISABLED)"
        C1["Child 1"]
        C2["Child 2"]
        C3["Child 3"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Internal Back (INTERNAL_MODE_BACK)"
        IB1["Internal Child 3"]
    end
    
    Parent --> IF1
    Parent --> IF2
    Parent --> C1
    Parent --> C2
    Parent --> C3
    Parent --> IB1
```

Internal nodes are hidden from normal iteration (unless `include_internal = true`) and are used for implementation details that should not be exposed to users.

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.h:123-127](), [doc/classes/Node.xml:157-161]()

### Children Storage and Caching

The node hierarchy uses a two-tier storage system:

1. **Primary Storage**: `data.children` - HashMap<StringName, Node*> for O(1) name lookup
2. **Cache**: `data.children_cache` - LocalVector<Node*> for ordered iteration

The cache is marked dirty and rebuilt when:
- A child is added or removed
- A child is moved to a new position
- The first iteration is requested after becoming dirty

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.h:205-213](), [scene/main/node.cpp:1311-1367]()

## Process Callbacks

Nodes can receive per-frame callbacks for game logic and physics updates.

### Process Modes

Each node has a `ProcessMode` that determines when it processes:

| Mode | Behavior |
|------|----------|
| `PROCESS_MODE_INHERIT` | Use parent's mode (default) |
| `PROCESS_MODE_PAUSABLE` | Process when tree is not paused |
| `PROCESS_MODE_WHEN_PAUSED` | Process only when tree is paused |
| `PROCESS_MODE_ALWAYS` | Always process regardless of pause state |
| `PROCESS_MODE_DISABLED` | Never process |

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.h:78-84](), [scene/main/node.cpp:671-727]()

### Process Callback Types

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Per-Frame Processing"
        Process["_process(delta)<br/>NOTIFICATION_PROCESS<br/>Called each frame"]
        ProcessInt["_process_internal(delta)<br/>NOTIFICATION_INTERNAL_PROCESS<br/>For engine internals"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Fixed-Step Physics Processing"
        PhysProc["_physics_process(delta)<br/>NOTIFICATION_PHYSICS_PROCESS<br/>Called at physics tick rate"]
        PhysInt["_physics_process_internal(delta)<br/>NOTIFICATION_INTERNAL_PHYSICS_PROCESS<br/>For engine internals"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Input Processing"
        Input["_input(event)<br/>All input events"]
        ShortcutInput["_shortcut_input(event)<br/>Shortcuts before GUI"]
        UnhandledInput["_unhandled_input(event)<br/>Events not handled by GUI"]
        UnhandledKeyInput["_unhandled_key_input(event)<br/>Key events not handled by GUI"]
    end
    
    SceneTree["SceneTree::_process()"] --> Process
    SceneTree --> ProcessInt
    
    SceneTreePhys["SceneTree::_physics_process()"] --> PhysProc
    SceneTreePhys --> PhysInt
    
    InputSystem["Input System"] --> Input
    InputSystem --> ShortcutInput
    InputSystem --> UnhandledInput
    InputSystem --> UnhandledKeyInput
```

**Sources:** [doc/classes/Node.xml:72-150](), [scene/main/node.cpp:99-105]()

### Enabling Process Callbacks

Process callbacks must be explicitly enabled (or are auto-enabled when the corresponding virtual method is overridden):

```
set_process(bool) - Enables _process()
set_physics_process(bool) - Enables _physics_process()
set_process_input(bool) - Enables _input()
set_process_unhandled_input(bool) - Enables _unhandled_input()
```

**Sources:** [doc/classes/Node.xml:958-1043]()

### Process Priority

Nodes have priority values that determine their processing order:

- `process_priority` - Order for `_process()` callbacks
- `physics_process_priority` - Order for `_physics_process()` callbacks

Lower priority values are processed first. Nodes with the same priority are processed in tree order (pre-order traversal).

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.h:241-242](), [scene/main/node.cpp:189-195]()

## Groups

Groups provide a way to organize nodes for batch operations without requiring a specific hierarchy.

### Group Operations

```mermaid
graph TB
    SceneTree["SceneTree"]
    GroupMap["group_map<br/>HashMap&lt;StringName, SceneTreeGroup&gt;"]
    
    subgraph "SceneTreeGroup"
        Nodes["nodes: Vector&lt;Node*&gt;"]
        Changed["changed: bool"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Group Methods"
        AddGroup["add_to_group(group, persistent)"]
        RemoveGroup["remove_from_group(group)"]
        IsInGroup["is_in_group(group)"]
        GetGroups["get_groups()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Batch Operations"
        CallGroup["call_group(group, method, ...)"]
        CallGroupFlags["call_group_flags(flags, group, method, ...)"]
        NotifyGroup["notify_group(group, notification)"]
        SetGroup["set_group(group, property, value)"]
    end
    
    SceneTree --> GroupMap
    GroupMap --> Nodes
    GroupMap --> Changed
    
    Node["Node"] --> AddGroup
    Node --> RemoveGroup
    Node --> IsInGroup
    Node --> GetGroups
    
    SceneTree --> CallGroup
    SceneTree --> CallGroupFlags
    SceneTree --> NotifyGroup
    SceneTree --> SetGroup
```

**Sources:** [scene/main/scene_tree.h:152-664](), [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp:174-421]()

### Group Call Flags

When calling methods on groups, behavior can be customized with flags:

| Flag | Effect |
|------|--------|
| `GROUP_CALL_DEFAULT` | Call immediately in tree order |
| `GROUP_CALL_REVERSE` | Call in reverse tree order |
| `GROUP_CALL_DEFERRED` | Queue calls for next frame |
| `GROUP_CALL_UNIQUE` | Only one call per group (requires DEFERRED) |

**Sources:** [doc/classes/SceneTree.xml:16-40](), [scene/main/scene_tree.cpp:357-421]()

### Persistent vs Non-Persistent Groups

Groups can be marked as persistent when adding nodes:
- **Persistent groups**: Saved with the scene, restored when scene is loaded
- **Non-persistent groups**: Runtime only, not saved

**Sources:** [doc/classes/Node.xml:426-436]()

## Node Ownership and Scene Structure

The `owner` property determines which nodes are saved with a scene.

### Owner Semantics

```mermaid
graph TB
    SceneRoot["Scene Root<br/>(owner = null)"]
    
    subgraph "Owned Nodes (saved with scene)"
        Node1["Node1<br/>(owner = SceneRoot)"]
        Node2["Node2<br/>(owner = SceneRoot)"]
        Node3["Node3<br/>(owner = SceneRoot)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Not Owned (not saved)"
        Runtime1["Runtime Node<br/>(owner = null)"]
        Runtime2["Runtime Child<br/>(owner = null)"]
    end
    
    SceneRoot --> Node1
    Node1 --> Node2
    Node2 --> Node3
    Node1 --> Runtime1
    Runtime1 --> Runtime2
```

Rules:
- Scene root has `owner = null`
- Nodes with `owner` set are saved when the owner is saved
- Nodes without an owner (or owned by a different scene) are not saved
- Setting owner automatically adds the node to the owner's `owned` list

**Sources:** [doc/classes/Node.xml:6-20](), [scene/main/node.cpp:297-304](), [scene/main/node.h:228]()

## Node Paths

`NodePath` provides a string-based addressing system for navigating the node hierarchy.

### Path Syntax

| Pattern | Meaning |
|---------|---------|
| `"Node"` | Child named "Node" |
| `"Child/GrandChild"` | Descendant path |
| `"."` | Current node |
| `".."` | Parent node |
| `"../Sibling"` | Sibling node |
| `"/root/Node"` | Absolute path from tree root |
| `"%UniqueNode"` | Node with unique name in owner |

**Sources:** [doc/classes/Node.xml:599-612]()

### Unique Names

Nodes can be marked with `unique_name_in_owner = true` to enable owner-scoped lookup:

```
get_node("%PlayerController")  # Finds node anywhere under owner
```

This allows refactoring the scene hierarchy without breaking script references.

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.h:209](), [scene/main/node.cpp:1822-1880]()

## Integration with Viewport and Rendering

Nodes connect to the rendering system through their closest `Viewport` ancestor.

### Viewport Reference Caching

```mermaid
graph TB
    Root["Root Viewport"]
    NodeA["Node A<br/>(data.viewport = Root)"]
    SubVP["SubViewport<br/>(data.viewport = self)"]
    NodeB["Node B<br/>(data.viewport = SubVP)"]
    NodeC["Node C<br/>(data.viewport = SubVP)"]
    
    Root --> NodeA
    NodeA --> SubVP
    SubVP --> NodeB
    SubVP --> NodeC
```

When a node enters the tree:
1. If the node itself is a `Viewport`, `data.viewport = this`
2. Otherwise, `data.viewport = parent->data.viewport`

This cached reference allows O(1) viewport lookup instead of traversing ancestors.

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.cpp:343-356]()

### Viewport Input Groups

When nodes enter a tree, they're automatically added to viewport-specific input groups:

- `_vp_input{viewport_id}` - For nodes with `_input()` enabled
- `_vp_shortcut_input{viewport_id}` - For nodes with `_shortcut_input()` enabled  
- `_vp_unhandled_input{viewport_id}` - For nodes with `_unhandled_input()` enabled
- `_vp_unhandled_key_input{viewport_id}` - For nodes with `_unhandled_key_input()` enabled

This allows the viewport to efficiently dispatch input events only to nodes that have the corresponding handlers enabled.

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.cpp:171-182](), [scene/main/node.cpp:213-224]()

## Thread Safety and Process Thread Groups

Godot 4 introduced threaded processing capabilities for nodes.

### Process Thread Groups

Nodes can specify how they should be processed across threads:

| Mode | Behavior |
|------|----------|
| `PROCESS_THREAD_GROUP_INHERIT` | Use parent's mode |
| `PROCESS_THREAD_GROUP_MAIN_THREAD` | Process only on main thread |
| `PROCESS_THREAD_GROUP_SUB_THREAD` | Can process on worker thread |

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.h:86-90]()

### Process Group Ownership

Each node tracks its `process_thread_group_owner`:
- Nodes with `PROCESS_THREAD_GROUP_INHERIT` inherit from parent
- Nodes with `MAIN_THREAD` or `SUB_THREAD` become group owners
- Group owners manage a `process_group` data structure

Process groups coordinate multi-threaded processing of node subtrees while maintaining deterministic behavior.

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.h:230-235](), [scene/main/node.cpp:134-153]()

## Summary

The Scene Tree and Node System provides Godot's fundamental organizational structure:

1. **Node**: Base class providing hierarchy, lifecycle, processing, and groups
2. **SceneTree**: Singleton managing the active tree, driving the game loop
3. **Lifecycle**: Well-defined enter/ready/exit phases with notifications
4. **Processing**: Per-frame and physics callbacks with priority control  
5. **Groups**: Flexible organization for batch operations
6. **Ownership**: Determines persistence and scene structure
7. **Viewport Integration**: Cached references connect nodes to rendering

This system enables the composition-based architecture that Godot is known for, where complex game objects are built from hierarchies of specialized node types.

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.h:53-833](), [scene/main/scene_tree.h:152-664](), [doc/classes/Node.xml:1-1392](), [doc/classes/SceneTree.xml:1-589]()1b:T4e9f,# Viewport and Rendering Integration
