## Purpose and Scope

This document describes how the `Viewport` class bridges the scene graph to the rendering system, managing rendering surfaces, input processing, and sub-windows. A Viewport creates a rendering context that scene nodes draw into, and owns server-side resources (RIDs) for 2D and 3D rendering.

For information about the RenderingServer architecture and rendering backends, see [Rendering Server Architecture](#3.1). For scene tree and node management, see [Scene Tree and Node System](#2.2). For GUI-specific input handling, see [Input Processing and GUI Events](#5.3).

---

## Core Architecture

### Viewport as Rendering Surface Bridge

The `Viewport` class serves as the bridge between the scene graph (node hierarchy) and the rendering server. Each viewport owns a server-side rendering surface represented by a `RID` and manages the connection between scene nodes and their rendered representation.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Scene Graph Layer"
        VP[Viewport Node]
        N2D[Node2D Children]
        CI[CanvasItem Children]
        N3D[Node3D Children]
        CAM2D[Camera2D]
        CAM3D[Camera3D]
    end
    
    subgraph "Viewport State"
        VID["viewport (RID)"]
        CANVAS["current_canvas (RID)"]
        W2D["world_2d (Ref&lt;World2D&gt;)"]
        W3D["world_3d (Ref&lt;World3D&gt;)"]
        CT["canvas_transform"]
        ST["stretch_transform"]
    end
    
    subgraph "RenderingServer"
        VPSRV["Viewport (Server)"]
        CANVASSRV["Canvas (Server)"]
        SCENARIO["Scenario (Server)"]
    end
    
    VP -->|owns| VID
    VP -->|owns| CANVAS
    VP -->|has| W2D
    VP -->|has| W3D
    
    VID -->|represents| VPSRV
    CANVAS -->|represents| CANVASSRV
    W3D -->|has scenario| SCENARIO
    
    CI -->|draws to| CANVAS
    N3D -->|added to| SCENARIO
    CAM2D -->|sets viewport camera| CANVAS
    CAM3D -->|sets viewport camera| SCENARIO
    
    VP -->|manages| CT
    VP -->|manages| ST
```

**Diagram: Viewport Rendering Architecture**

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.h:238-262](), [scene/main/viewport.cpp:592-610]()

### RID-Based Server Integration

Viewports communicate with the rendering server exclusively through Resource IDs (RIDs), which are lightweight handles to server-side resources. This enables thread-safe communication and separation between scene logic and rendering implementation.

| Client-Side Object | RID Field | Server-Side Resource | Purpose |
|-------------------|-----------|---------------------|---------|
| `Viewport` | `viewport` | Viewport | Main rendering surface |
| `Viewport` | `current_canvas` | Canvas | 2D rendering context |
| `Viewport` | `subwindow_canvas` | Canvas | Embedded window layer |
| `World2D` | `canvas` | Canvas | Shared 2D world space |
| `World3D` | `scenario` | Scenario | 3D scene container |
| `ViewportTexture` | `proxy` | Texture | Render-to-texture output |

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.h:248-250](), [scene/main/viewport.cpp:602-605]()

---

## Viewport Lifecycle and Scene Tree Integration

### Initialization and Tree Entry

When a `Viewport` enters the scene tree, it initializes its rendering server resources and connects to the world systems:

```mermaid
graph LR
    ENTER["NOTIFICATION_ENTER_TREE"]
    PARENT["Get parent viewport"]
    WORLD2D["find_world_2d()"]
    WORLD3D["find_world_3d()"]
    ATTACH["Attach canvas to viewport"]
    SETSCEN["Set scenario on viewport"]
    PARENT_VP["Set parent viewport"]
    
    ENTER --> PARENT
    PARENT --> PARENT_VP
    PARENT --> WORLD2D
    WORLD2D --> ATTACH
    PARENT --> WORLD3D
    WORLD3D --> SETSCEN
```

**Diagram: Viewport Initialization Flow**

The key initialization sequence in `_notification(NOTIFICATION_ENTER_TREE)`:

1. **Parent Resolution**: Finds parent viewport via `get_parent()->get_viewport()`
2. **World Discovery**: Calls `find_world_2d()` and `find_world_3d()` to locate shared world resources
3. **Canvas Attachment**: Attaches `current_canvas` RID to viewport using `RenderingServer::viewport_attach_canvas()`
4. **Scenario Setup**: Sets 3D scenario using `RenderingServer::viewport_set_scenario()`
5. **Hierarchy Linkage**: Sets parent viewport relationship in rendering server

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:592-610]()

### World Discovery Mechanism

Viewports search up the node hierarchy to find the first valid `World2D` or `World3D`:

```mermaid
graph TD
    START["Viewport needs world"]
    CHECK_OWN["Has own world_2d/world_3d?"]
    USE_OWN["Use own world"]
    PARENT["Get parent viewport"]
    CHECK_PARENT["Parent has world?"]
    USE_PARENT["Use parent's world"]
    CREATE["Create default world"]
    
    START --> CHECK_OWN
    CHECK_OWN -->|Yes| USE_OWN
    CHECK_OWN -->|No| PARENT
    PARENT --> CHECK_PARENT
    CHECK_PARENT -->|Yes| USE_PARENT
    CHECK_PARENT -->|No| CREATE
```

**Diagram: World Discovery Algorithm**

- `find_world_2d()`: Searches `world_2d` property up viewport hierarchy, returns first found
- `find_world_3d()`: Searches `world_3d` property up viewport hierarchy, returns first found
- Allows viewports to share rendering contexts or create isolated rendering environments

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1232-1252]()

---

## Rendering Pipeline Integration

### Canvas (2D) Rendering System

2D content renders through the canvas system. Each `CanvasItem` node (base class for all 2D nodes) registers with the viewport's canvas:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Viewport Canvas Management"
        VP["Viewport"]
        CANVAS["current_canvas (RID)"]
        SUBCANVAS["subwindow_canvas (RID)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "2D Nodes"
        CI1["CanvasItem (Sprite2D, etc)"]
        CI2["CanvasItem (Control, etc)"]
        CL["CanvasLayer"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Sub-windows"
        SW["Window (embedded)"]
        SWCI["SubWindow.canvas_item"]
    end
    
    VP -->|owns| CANVAS
    VP -->|creates when needed| SUBCANVAS
    CI1 -->|draws to| CANVAS
    CI2 -->|draws to| CANVAS
    CL -->|manages layer on| CANVAS
    SW -->|parent is| SWCI
    SWCI -->|child of| SUBCANVAS
```

**Diagram: Canvas Rendering Hierarchy**

The viewport manages canvas transforms that affect all 2D rendering:
- `canvas_transform`: User-controllable 2D camera transform
- `global_canvas_transform`: Combined with parent viewports
- `stretch_transform`: Automatic scaling for resolution adaptation

Canvas attachment happens during tree entry:
```
current_canvas = find_world_2d()->get_canvas();
RenderingServer::viewport_attach_canvas(viewport, current_canvas);
RenderingServer::viewport_set_canvas_transform(viewport, current_canvas, canvas_transform);
```

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:602-605](), [scene/main/viewport.h:252-254]()

### Scenario (3D) Rendering System

3D content renders through the scenario system, which contains all 3D objects, lights, and environment settings:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Viewport 3D Management"
        VP["Viewport"]
        W3D["world_3d"]
        SCENARIO["scenario (RID from World3D)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "3D Nodes"
        N3D1["Node3D (MeshInstance3D, etc)"]
        N3D2["Node3D (Light3D, etc)"]
        CAM["Camera3D"]
        ENV["WorldEnvironment"]
    end
    
    VP -->|has| W3D
    W3D -->|provides| SCENARIO
    N3D1 -->|instances added to| SCENARIO
    N3D2 -->|instances added to| SCENARIO
    CAM -->|sets active camera for| VP
    ENV -->|configures| SCENARIO
```

**Diagram: 3D Scenario Integration**

The scenario is attached during viewport initialization:
```
RenderingServer::viewport_set_scenario(viewport, find_world_3d()->get_scenario());
```

Camera activation updates the viewport's active 3D camera:
```cpp
void Camera3D::make_current() {
    // Sets this camera as viewport's camera_3d
    get_viewport()->_camera_3d_set(this);
}
```

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:608](), [scene/main/viewport.h:470-474]()

### Transform Management

Viewports manage multiple transform hierarchies for different rendering contexts:

| Transform | Purpose | Modification |
|-----------|---------|--------------|
| `canvas_transform` | 2D camera/view transform | `set_canvas_transform()` |
| `global_canvas_transform` | Accumulated parent transforms | Auto-calculated |
| `stretch_transform` | Resolution scaling | Auto-calculated from size |
| Internal (from Window) | Window-specific transforms | Managed by Window class |

The final 2D transform chain:
```
final_transform = parent.global_canvas_transform * canvas_transform * stretch_transform
```

Methods:
- `get_canvas_transform()`: Returns user-set canvas transform
- `get_global_canvas_transform()`: Returns accumulated transform from root
- `get_final_transform()`: Returns complete transform to embedder coordinates
- `get_screen_transform()`: Returns transform to screen coordinates

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:2265-2286](), [scene/main/viewport.h:252-254]()

---

## Input Processing

### Input Event Flow

Viewports are responsible for routing input events through the scene tree. The SceneTree sends events to the root viewport, which then propagates them to appropriate nodes:

```mermaid
graph TD
    ST["SceneTree::_process_picking"]
    ROOT_VP["Root Viewport"]
    INPUT["Viewport::push_input"]
    CHECK_SW["Check sub-windows"]
    SW_INPUT["Route to sub-window"]
    PHYSICS["Physics object picking"]
    GUI["GUI input routing"]
    NODE_INPUT["Node input groups"]
    
    ST --> ROOT_VP
    ROOT_VP --> INPUT
    INPUT --> CHECK_SW
    CHECK_SW -->|Hit sub-window| SW_INPUT
    CHECK_SW -->|No sub-window| PHYSICS
    PHYSICS --> GUI
    GUI --> NODE_INPUT
    
    NODE_INPUT --> |_vp_input| INPUTGROUP["_input() handlers"]
    NODE_INPUT --> |_vp_shortcut_input| SHORTCUT["_shortcut_input() handlers"]
    NODE_INPUT --> |_vp_unhandled_input| UNHANDLED["_unhandled_input() handlers"]
```

**Diagram: Input Event Processing Flow**

Input processing groups are managed by the viewport:
- Nodes register to groups like `_vp_input{viewport_id}` when they enable input processing
- Viewport calls group methods in order: input â†’ shortcut_input â†’ GUI â†’ unhandled_input â†’ unhandled_key_input
- Any handler can call `Viewport::set_input_as_handled()` to stop propagation

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:2674-2818](), [scene/main/node.cpp:171-182]()

### Physics Object Picking

For 2D and 3D physics object interaction, viewports perform raycasting/shape queries and dispatch input events to collision objects:

```mermaid
graph LR
    VPPROC["Viewport::_process_picking()"]
    CHECK2D["2D: PhysicsDirectSpaceState2D::intersect_point"]
    CHECK3D["3D: PhysicsDirectSpaceState3D::intersect_ray"]
    COLLIDER["CollisionObject2D/3D"]
    INPUT["_input_event_call()"]
    MOUSE["_mouse_enter() / _mouse_exit()"]
    
    VPPROC --> CHECK2D
    VPPROC --> CHECK3D
    CHECK2D --> COLLIDER
    CHECK3D --> COLLIDER
    COLLIDER --> INPUT
    COLLIDER --> MOUSE
```

**Diagram: Physics Picking Flow**

Physics picking is enabled via `physics_object_picking` property and processes events from `physics_picking_events` list. The viewport maintains state for mouse-over tracking:
- `physics_2d_mouseover`: HashMap of 2D objects currently under mouse
- `physics_object_over`: ObjectID of 3D object currently under mouse
- Mouse enter/exit callbacks triggered on changes

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:779-1070](), [scene/main/viewport.h:272-282]()

---

## Sub-window Management

### Embedded Window System

Viewports can embed `Window` nodes as sub-windows, rendering them as part of the viewport's canvas hierarchy. This enables modal dialogs, popups, and multi-window UIs without requiring OS-level windows:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Viewport"
        VP["Viewport"]
        SUBCANVAS["subwindow_canvas (RID)"]
        SUBWINS["gui.sub_windows (Vector)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "SubWindow Structure"
        SW["SubWindow struct"]
        SWCI["canvas_item (RID)"]
        SWWIN["window (Window*)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Embedded Window"
        WIN["Window (embedded)"]
        WINVP["Window.viewport (RID)"]
        WINTEX["Window texture"]
    end
    
    VP -->|creates on first sub-window| SUBCANVAS
    VP -->|maintains| SUBWINS
    SUBWINS -->|contains| SW
    SW -->|has| SWCI
    SW -->|points to| SWWIN
    SWWIN -->|is| WIN
    SWCI -->|child of| SUBCANVAS
    SWCI -->|draws| WINTEX
    WIN -->|has own| WINVP
```

**Diagram: Sub-window Architecture**

### Registration and Update Flow

Sub-window lifecycle:
1. **Registration**: `_sub_window_register(Window*)` called when Window becomes child
2. **Canvas Creation**: First sub-window triggers `subwindow_canvas` creation
3. **Canvas Item**: Each sub-window gets a dedicated `canvas_item` RID for rendering
4. **Drawing**: `_sub_window_update()` renders window border and viewport texture
5. **Cleanup**: `_sub_window_remove()` on Window removal

Sub-window drawing order (z-order management):
- `_sub_window_update_order()` sorts windows by "always on top" flag and exclusivity
- Each window's `canvas_item` gets a draw index via `canvas_item_set_draw_index()`
- Higher indices draw on top

Focus management:
- `gui.subwindow_focused`: Currently focused sub-window
- `_sub_window_grab_focus()`: Changes focus, sends WINDOW_EVENT_FOCUS_IN/OUT
- Only one sub-window can have focus at a time

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:326-557](), [scene/main/viewport.h:336-374]()

---

## Viewport Textures

### ViewportTexture Resource

`ViewportTexture` is a special `Texture2D` subclass that references a viewport's rendering output, enabling render-to-texture effects:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "ViewportTexture Setup"
        VT["ViewportTexture resource"]
        PATH["viewport_path"]
        SCENE["local_scene"]
        SETUP["setup_local_to_scene()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Viewport Connection"
        VP["Target Viewport"]
        TEX_RID["viewport.texture_rid"]
        PROXY["ViewportTexture.proxy (RID)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Usage"
        MATERIAL["Material using texture"]
        SPRITE["Sprite2D using texture"]
    end
    
    VT -->|has| PATH
    VT -->|resolves via| SCENE
    SCENE --> SETUP
    SETUP -->|finds| VP
    VP -->|provides| TEX_RID
    VT -->|creates proxy to| PROXY
    PROXY -->|references| TEX_RID
    MATERIAL -->|samples| PROXY
    SPRITE -->|draws| PROXY
```

**Diagram: ViewportTexture Reference System**

### Local-to-Scene Pattern

ViewportTextures use Godot's "local to scene" pattern to resolve references:
1. **Path Storage**: `viewport_path` stores NodePath relative to local scene root
2. **Deferred Setup**: `setup_local_to_scene()` called when resource enters a scene
3. **Viewport Resolution**: `get_node_or_null(path)` finds target viewport
4. **Proxy Creation**: Creates texture proxy RID pointing to viewport's `texture_rid`
5. **Registration**: Viewport tracks all ViewportTextures referencing it in `viewport_textures` set

The proxy enables the texture to update automatically as the viewport renders, without copying pixel data.

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:87-235](), [scene/main/viewport.h:55-93]()

---

## Camera and Audio Listener Management

### Camera Selection

Viewports maintain active cameras for both 2D and 3D rendering:

| Camera Type | Viewport Field | Registration | Activation |
|-------------|---------------|--------------|------------|
| `Camera2D` | `camera_2d` | Added to `camera_2d_set` | `make_current()` |
| `Camera3D` | `camera_3d` | Added to `camera_3d_set` | `make_current()` |

Camera lifecycle:
- **Registration**: Camera registers with viewport on `NOTIFICATION_ENTER_TREE`
- **Auto-selection**: In `NOTIFICATION_READY`, viewport picks first camera if none current
- **Manual Selection**: Call `Camera2D/3D::make_current()` to activate specific camera
- **Deregistration**: Camera removes itself on `NOTIFICATION_EXIT_TREE`

Viewport methods:
- `get_camera_2d()` / `get_camera_3d()`: Returns currently active camera (may be null)
- Camera updates call viewport's internal `_camera_2d_set()` / `_camera_3d_set()`

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:636-664](), [scene/main/viewport.h:468-477]()

### Audio Listener Selection

Similar pattern for audio listeners:

| Listener Type | Viewport Field | Purpose |
|--------------|---------------|---------|
| `AudioListener2D` | `audio_listener_2d` | 2D positional audio |
| `AudioListener3D` | `audio_listener_3d` | 3D positional audio |

If no explicit listener is active, the active camera is used as the listener position for positional audio calculations.

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:606-609](), [scene/main/viewport.h:478-484]()

---

## Common Patterns and Usage

### Creating a Sub-Viewport for Render-to-Texture

```
1. Create SubViewport node (inherits Viewport)
2. Set size property (e.g., 512x512)
3. Add child nodes (3D scene, 2D elements, etc.)
4. Create ViewportTexture resource
5. Set viewport_path to point to SubViewport
6. Use ViewportTexture in Material or Sprite
```

The ViewportTexture will automatically reference the SubViewport's rendered output.

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:87-113]()

### Handling Input in Embedded Windows

Sub-windows automatically receive input when:
- Mouse position intersects window bounds
- Window is focused (for keyboard input)
- Window is not behind another window in z-order

Input routing:
1. Viewport checks `gui.sub_windows` for hit testing
2. If hit, routes input to `Window::_window_input()`
3. Window processes via its own viewport and GUI system
4. Can call `accept_event()` to prevent propagation

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:2700-2730]()

### Transform Coordinate Systems

Converting between coordinate systems:

| Method | From | To |
|--------|------|-----|
| `get_final_transform()` | Viewport | Embedder (parent viewport or window) |
| `get_screen_transform()` | Viewport | Screen pixels |
| `get_canvas_transform()` | Canvas | Viewport |
| `get_global_canvas_transform()` | Canvas | Root viewport |

For screen-space to viewport-space conversion:
```cpp
Vector2 viewport_pos = get_screen_transform().affine_inverse().xform(screen_pos);
```

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:2265-2286]()

### Multiple Viewport Rendering

Common use cases:
- **Split-screen**: Multiple viewports with different cameras in same world
- **Minimap**: Small viewport with top-down camera
- **Picture-in-picture**: SubViewport with different World3D
- **UI rendering**: Separate viewport for UI layer

Each viewport can have:
- Independent `world_2d` / `world_3d` (isolated scenes)
- Shared worlds (same scene, different views)
- Different rendering settings (MSAA, scaling, etc.)

Sources: [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1232-1252]()

- [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.h](servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.h)
- [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h](servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

The Rendering System encompasses Godot's entire graphics pipeline, from high-level scene rendering requests to low-level GPU commands. This page provides an architectural overview of how the engine processes visual content, manages render targets, and abstracts multiple graphics backends.

For details about specific subsystems:
- **RenderingServer API internals** and command queuing: see [Rendering Server Architecture](#3.1)
- **Modern rendering backends** (Vulkan/D3D12/Metal): see [Forward Clustered and Mobile Renderers](#3.2)
- **Legacy OpenGL backend**: see [OpenGL ES 3 Backend](#3.3)
- **Material resources and shader compilation**: see [Material and Shader System](#3.4)

For information about how scenes connect to the rendering system, see [Viewport and Rendering Integration](#2.3).

---

## Architecture Overview

The rendering system is organized in four major layers that progressively transform high-level scene data into GPU commands:

**Rendering System Layers**

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Client Layer"
        SceneNodes["Scene Nodes<br/>Node3D, MeshInstance3D<br/>CanvasItem, Sprite2D"]
        Materials["Material Resources<br/>BaseMaterial3D, ShaderMaterial"]
    end
    
    subgraph "RenderingServer API Layer"
        RS["RenderingServer<br/>High-level API<br/>singleton interface"]
        RSD["RenderingServerDefault<br/>Implementation"]
        CommandQ["CommandQueueMT<br/>Thread-safe command queue"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Scene Management Layer"
        RSC["RendererSceneCull<br/>Visibility culling<br/>Light/shadow management"]
        RV["RendererViewport<br/>Render target management<br/>Canvas/3D integration"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Rendering Backend Layer"
        RenderMethod["RendererSceneRenderRD<br/>Base renderer"]
        RFC["RenderForwardClustered<br/>Desktop/Console"]
        RFM["RenderForwardMobile<br/>Mobile Devices"]
        GLES3["RasterizerSceneGLES3<br/>OpenGL ES 3.0"]
    end
    
    subgraph "GPU Abstraction Layer"
        RDevice["RenderingDevice<br/>Modern API abstraction"]
        GLBackend["OpenGL Direct Calls"]
    end
    
    SceneNodes -->|"rendering requests"| RS
    Materials -->|"shader data"| RS
    RS --> RSD
    RSD --> CommandQ
    CommandQ -->|"culling requests"| RSC
    CommandQ -->|"viewport config"| RV
    
    RSC -->|"visible instances"| RenderMethod
    RV -->|"render targets"| RenderMethod
    
    RenderMethod -->|"implements"| RFC
    RenderMethod -->|"implements"| RFM
    RenderMethod -.->|"alternative"| GLES3
    
    RFC --> RDevice
    RFM --> RDevice
    GLES3 --> GLBackend
    
    RDevice -->|"Vulkan/D3D12/Metal"| GPU["GPU Hardware"]
    GLBackend -->|"OpenGL commands"| GPU
```

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_render_rd.h:1-500](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.h:1-200](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.h:1-200](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:1-150]()

The system architecture ensures:
- **Thread Safety**: `CommandQueueMT` enables main thread to submit rendering work without blocking
- **Backend Flexibility**: Multiple rendering implementations can coexist based on platform capabilities
- **Performance Isolation**: Scene culling and management occur independently of backend-specific rendering

---

## RenderingServer API

`RenderingServer` is the singleton interface exposed to the engine for all visual operations. It abstracts the entire rendering pipeline behind a unified API.

**RenderingServer Core Components**

```mermaid
graph TB
    Client["Client Code<br/>Scene System"]
    
    subgraph "RenderingServer Singleton"
        API["RenderingServer Interface<br/>servers/rendering/rendering_server.h"]
        Impl["RenderingServerDefault<br/>servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h"]
        CmdQ["CommandQueueMT<br/>command_queue_mt.h"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Server Thread Operations"
        SceneOps["Scene Operations<br/>instance_create()<br/>instance_set_base()<br/>instance_set_scenario()"]
        ViewportOps["Viewport Operations<br/>viewport_create()<br/>viewport_set_scenario()<br/>viewport_attach_canvas()"]
        ResourceOps["Resource Operations<br/>mesh_create()<br/>material_set_shader()<br/>texture_create()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Execution Layer"
        Cull["RendererSceneCull<br/>renderer_scene_cull.cpp"]
        Viewport["RendererViewport<br/>renderer_viewport.cpp"]
    end
    
    Client -->|"RS::get_singleton()->"| API
    API --> Impl
    Impl -->|"if MT"| CmdQ
    Impl -->|"if single"| SceneOps
    CmdQ -->|"on render thread"| SceneOps
    
    SceneOps --> Cull
    ViewportOps --> Viewport
    ResourceOps --> Cull
    ViewportOps --> Cull
```

Sources: [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:47-100](), [main/main.cpp:180-185]()

### Key API Categories

The `RenderingServer` exposes several major functional groups:

| Category | Purpose | Example Methods |
|----------|---------|----------------|
| **Scenario** | 3D world container | `scenario_create()`, `scenario_set_environment()` |
| **Instance** | Visual object instances | `instance_create()`, `instance_set_base()`, `instance_set_transform()` |
| **Viewport** | Render targets | `viewport_create()`, `viewport_set_scenario()`, `viewport_set_update_mode()` |
| **Canvas** | 2D rendering | `canvas_create()`, `canvas_item_create()`, `canvas_item_add_rect()` |
| **Camera** | View configuration | `camera_create()`, `camera_set_perspective()`, `camera_set_transform()` |
| **Light** | Lighting | `directional_light_create()`, `omni_light_create()`, `spot_light_create()` |
| **Mesh** | Geometry | `mesh_create()`, `mesh_add_surface()` |
| **Material** | Appearance | `material_create()`, `material_set_shader()` |

Sources: [doc/classes/RenderingServer.xml:1-100]()

### Thread Safety Model

`RenderingServerDefault` wraps all API calls through `CommandQueueMT` when running in multi-threaded mode (default for most platforms):

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant MainThread as Main Thread
    participant CmdQueue as CommandQueueMT
    participant RenderThread as Render Thread
    participant Renderer as Scene Renderer
    
    MainThread->>CmdQueue: instance_set_transform(rid, xform)
    Note over CmdQueue: Enqueue command
    MainThread->>CmdQueue: material_set_shader(rid, shader)
    Note over CmdQueue: Enqueue command
    
    Note over MainThread: Frame continues...
    
    RenderThread->>CmdQueue: flush() - start of frame
    CmdQueue->>Renderer: Execute: instance_set_transform()
    CmdQueue->>Renderer: Execute: material_set_shader()
    Note over Renderer: Process commands
    RenderThread->>Renderer: render_frame()
```

Sources: [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:47-70](), [core/templates/command_queue_mt.h:1-50]()

This design allows the main thread (game logic, scripts) to continue executing while the render thread processes the previous frame's commands and renders geometry.

---

## Scene Management Layer

The scene management layer sits between `RenderingServer` API calls and the actual rendering backends. It handles visibility culling, light/shadow setup, and viewport management.

**Scene Management Data Flow**

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Input"
        Instances["Instance RIDs<br/>Transforms<br/>Visibility layers"]
        Lights["Light RIDs<br/>Positions<br/>Parameters"]
        Camera["Camera<br/>Transform<br/>Projection"]
    end
    
    subgraph "RendererSceneCull"
        Frustum["Frustum Culling<br/>_render_scene()"]
        Occlusion["Occlusion Culling<br/>RendererSceneOcclusionCull"]
        Sorting["Instance Sorting<br/>By material/distance"]
        LightCull["Light Culling<br/>_light_instance_update_shadow()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "RendererViewport"
        VPSetup["Viewport Setup<br/>viewport_draw()"]
        Canvas2D["2D Canvas Rendering<br/>_draw_2d()"]
        Scene3D["3D Scene Rendering<br/>_draw_3d()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Output to Backend"
        RenderList["PagedArray of<br/>RenderGeometryInstance*"]
        LightList["PagedArray of<br/>Light RIDs"]
        RenderData["RenderData struct<br/>Camera, Viewport, Lists"]
    end
    
    Instances --> Frustum
    Camera --> Frustum
    Frustum --> Occlusion
    Occlusion --> Sorting
    Lights --> LightCull
    
    Sorting --> RenderList
    LightCull --> LightList
    Camera --> RenderData
    RenderList --> RenderData
    LightList --> RenderData
    
    VPSetup --> Canvas2D
    VPSetup --> Scene3D
    RenderData --> Scene3D
```

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:1-200](), [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp:1-200]()

### RendererSceneCull

`RendererSceneCull` [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:31-100]() is responsible for determining which objects are visible and need to be rendered. Key operations:

- **Frustum Culling**: Checks instance AABBs against camera frustum planes
- **Occlusion Culling**: Uses GPU-based occlusion queries to skip hidden geometry
- **Light Assignment**: Associates lights with visible geometry based on bounds overlap
- **Shadow Caster Culling**: Determines which objects cast shadows for each light
- **Instance Sorting**: Orders instances by material, depth, or other criteria for efficient rendering

The `_render_scene()` method [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:3500-3700]() orchestrates the culling process and produces `PagedArray<RenderGeometryInstance*>` for the backend.

### RendererViewport

`RendererViewport` [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp:31-100]() manages render targets and coordinates 2D/3D rendering:

- Maintains viewport state (size, clear mode, MSAA, HDR)
- Handles canvas layer management for 2D rendering
- Invokes `RendererSceneCull` for 3D culling
- Calls backend `render_scene()` with culled data
- Manages post-processing effects (tonemapping, FXAA, etc.)

The `draw_viewports()` method [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp:600-800]() is called each frame to render all active viewports.

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp:30-200](), [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:30-300]()

---

## Rendering Backend Architecture

Godot supports three rendering backend implementations, each optimized for different platforms and capabilities:

**Backend Selection and Capabilities**

| Backend | API | Platforms | Class | Lighting Model |
|---------|-----|-----------|-------|----------------|
| **Forward Clustered** | Vulkan/D3D12/Metal | Desktop, Console | `RenderForwardClustered` | Clustered forward with many lights |
| **Forward Mobile** | Vulkan/D3D12/Metal | Mobile, Low-end Desktop | `RenderForwardMobile` | Forward with per-object light limits |
| **GL Compatibility** | OpenGL ES 3.0 / GL 3.3 | Legacy, Web, Some Mobile | `RasterizerSceneGLES3` | Forward with vertex lighting option |

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.h:1-100](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.h:1-100](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:1-100]()

### Backend Selection at Runtime

The rendering backend is selected during engine initialization based on project settings and platform capabilities:

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["Engine Init<br/>main.cpp::Main::setup2()"]
    
    CheckSetting["Check ProjectSettings:<br/>rendering/renderer/rendering_method"]
    
    ForwardPlus["'forward_plus'<br/>RenderForwardClustered"]
    Mobile["'mobile'<br/>RenderForwardMobile"]
    GLCompat["'gl_compatibility'<br/>RasterizerSceneGLES3"]
    
    CreateRD["Create RenderingDevice<br/>Vulkan/D3D12/Metal"]
    CreateGL["Direct OpenGL Context"]
    
    InitRenderer["Initialize Scene Renderer<br/>setup_render_buffer_data()"]
    
    Start --> CheckSetting
    CheckSetting -->|"forward_plus"| ForwardPlus
    CheckSetting -->|"mobile"| Mobile
    CheckSetting -->|"gl_compatibility"| GLCompat
    
    ForwardPlus --> CreateRD
    Mobile --> CreateRD
    GLCompat --> CreateGL
    
    CreateRD --> InitRenderer
    CreateGL --> InitRenderer
```

Sources: [main/main.cpp:2000-2200](), [doc/classes/ProjectSettings.xml:1-100]()

### RenderingDevice Abstraction

Modern backends (Forward Clustered and Forward Mobile) use `RenderingDevice` as an abstraction over Vulkan, Direct3D 12, and Metal:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Renderer Implementation"
        Renderer["RenderForwardClustered<br/>or RenderForwardMobile"]
        ShaderCreation["Shader Creation<br/>_create_shader_versions()"]
        Pipeline["Pipeline Management<br/>_setup_pipeline()"]
        DrawCalls["Draw Commands<br/>_render_list()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "RenderingDevice API"
        RD["RenderingDevice<br/>servers/rendering/rendering_device.h"]
        Shaders["shader_create_from_bytecode()"]
        Pipelines["render_pipeline_create()"]
        Drawing["draw_list_begin()<br/>draw_list_bind_pipeline()<br/>draw_list_draw()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Backend Drivers"
        RD_Vulkan["RenderingDeviceVulkan<br/>drivers/vulkan/"]
        RD_D3D12["RenderingDeviceD3D12<br/>drivers/d3d12/"]
        RD_Metal["RenderingDeviceMetal<br/>drivers/metal/"]
    end
    
    Renderer --> ShaderCreation
    ShaderCreation --> Shaders
    Pipeline --> Pipelines
    DrawCalls --> Drawing
    
    Shaders --> RD
    Pipelines --> RD
    Drawing --> RD
    
    RD -->|"Vulkan"| RD_Vulkan
    RD -->|"D3D12"| RD_D3D12
    RD -->|"Metal"| RD_Metal
```

Sources: [servers/rendering/rendering_device.h:1-200](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:1-300]()

The `RenderingDevice` provides a unified API for:
- **Shader compilation**: Compiles GLSL to SPIR-V, then to native formats
- **Pipeline state**: Manages render passes, framebuffers, and graphics pipelines
- **Resource binding**: Uniforms, textures, buffers via uniform sets
- **Command recording**: Draw commands, compute dispatches, barriers

### OpenGL Backend

The OpenGL ES 3 backend (`RasterizerSceneGLES3`) does not use `RenderingDevice`, instead making direct OpenGL calls:

```mermaid
graph LR
    GLES3["RasterizerSceneGLES3<br/>drivers/gles3/"]
    
    ShaderGLES["GLES3_ShaderData<br/>Compile GLSL directly"]
    StateGLES["OpenGL State Cache<br/>Track bound textures/buffers"]
    DrawGLES["Direct GL Calls<br/>glDrawElements()<br/>glBindTexture()"]
    
    GLES3 --> ShaderGLES
    GLES3 --> StateGLES
    GLES3 --> DrawGLES
    
    ShaderGLES -->|"glCompileShader()"| OpenGL["OpenGL Driver"]
    StateGLES -->|"glBindX()"| OpenGL
    DrawGLES -->|"glDraw*()"| OpenGL
```

Sources: [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:31-300](), [drivers/gles3/shaders/scene.glsl:1-100]()

This backend is optimized for:
- **Compatibility**: Works on older hardware and WebGL
- **Simplicity**: No intermediate abstraction layer
- **Performance on GL**: Direct state management without translation overhead

---

## Rendering Pass Pipeline

All backends follow a similar multi-pass rendering pipeline, though implementation details differ:

**Typical Frame Rendering Sequence**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant VP as RendererViewport
    participant Cull as RendererSceneCull
    participant Backend as Scene Renderer
    participant RD as RenderingDevice/GL
    
    VP->>Cull: render_camera()
    Cull->>Cull: Frustum culling
    Cull->>Cull: Light culling
    Cull->>Backend: render_scene(render_data)
    
    Note over Backend: Depth Pre-pass
    Backend->>RD: Begin depth framebuffer
    Backend->>RD: Draw opaque geometry (depth only)
    
    Note over Backend: Shadow Pass (per light)
    loop For each shadow-casting light
        Backend->>RD: Begin shadow framebuffer
        Backend->>RD: Draw shadow casters
    end
    
    Note over Backend: Opaque Pass
    Backend->>RD: Begin color framebuffer
    Backend->>RD: Draw opaque surfaces
    Backend->>RD: Apply SSAO/SSR/other effects
    
    Note over Backend: Sky/Environment
    Backend->>RD: Draw sky if visible
    
    Note over Backend: Transparent Pass
    Backend->>RD: Draw transparent surfaces (sorted back-to-front)
    
    Note over Backend: Post-Processing
    Backend->>RD: Apply glow, tonemapping, etc.
    
    Backend->>VP: Frame complete
```

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:2000-2500](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:1500-2000]()

### Render Pass Types

Each backend organizes rendering into distinct passes:

| Pass | Purpose | Framebuffer Attachments | Shader Defines |
|------|---------|------------------------|----------------|
| **Depth Pre-pass** | Early Z rejection, establish depth buffer | Depth only | `MODE_RENDER_DEPTH` |
| **Shadow** | Render depth from light's view | Depth (or VSM) | `RENDER_SHADOWS` |
| **Opaque** | Render solid geometry with full lighting | Color + Depth | `BASE_PASS` |
| **Transparent** | Render alpha-blended surfaces | Color + Depth (read-only) | `BASE_PASS`, `ALPHA_PASS` |
| **Post-Process** | Screen-space effects | Color | Various effect flags |

Sources: [drivers/gles3/shaders/scene.glsl:1-100](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:1000-1500]()

---

## Material and Shader Integration

Materials define the visual appearance of surfaces and integrate tightly with the rendering backends through shader compilation and uniform management.

**Material to Shader Pipeline**

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Resource Layer"
        Material["Material Resource<br/>scene/resources/material.cpp"]
        BaseMat["BaseMaterial3D<br/>Built-in PBR material"]
        ShaderMat["ShaderMaterial<br/>Custom shader"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Shader Resources"
        Shader["Shader Resource<br/>scene/resources/shader.cpp"]
        ShaderCode["Shader Code String<br/>GLSL/Godot shader language"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Backend Shader Data"
        SceneShader["SceneShaderData<br/>Backend-specific compiled shader"]
        Variants["Shader Variants<br/>Different feature combinations"]
        Pipelines["Graphics Pipelines<br/>Compiled for draw states"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Rendering"
        MaterialData["MaterialData<br/>Uniform values<br/>Textures"]
        Drawing["Draw Call<br/>Bind pipeline + uniforms<br/>Draw geometry"]
    end
    
    Material -->|"has"| Shader
    BaseMat -.->|"generates"| ShaderCode
    ShaderMat -->|"references"| Shader
    Shader -->|"contains"| ShaderCode
    
    Shader -->|"compiles to"| SceneShader
    SceneShader -->|"generates"| Variants
    Variants -->|"compile to"| Pipelines
    
    Material -->|"creates"| MaterialData
    MaterialData -->|"binds to"| Drawing
    Pipelines -->|"binds to"| Drawing
```

Sources: [scene/resources/material.cpp:1-200](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:3000-3500]()

### Shader Compilation Process

The shader system compiles high-level shader code into backend-specific formats:

1. **Parse**: Godot shader language parsed into AST
2. **Generate**: Convert to GLSL with engine-specific defines and functions
3. **Compile**: 
   - **RD backends**: GLSL â†’ SPIR-V â†’ native (via `RenderingDevice`)
   - **GL backend**: GLSL â†’ GL driver compilation
4. **Cache**: Store compiled shaders to avoid recompilation

For `BaseMaterial3D`, the engine generates shader code based on enabled features (normal maps, emission, transparency, etc.), creating hundreds of potential variants [scene/resources/material.cpp:1000-2000]().

### Material Parameters

Materials expose parameters (uniforms) to the shader:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Material Properties"
        Props["albedo_color<br/>metallic<br/>roughness<br/>normal_texture<br/>..."]
    end
    
    subgraph "Shader Uniforms"
        Uniforms["uniform vec4 albedo<br/>uniform float metallic<br/>uniform sampler2D normal_map"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Backend Binding"
        UBO["Uniform Buffer Object<br/>MaterialUniforms"]
        Samplers["Texture Samplers<br/>Bound to shader slots"]
    end
    
    Props -->|"Material::set_shader_parameter()"| Uniforms
    Uniforms -->|"RenderingServer"| UBO
    Uniforms -->|"RenderingServer"| Samplers
    
    UBO -->|"Per-draw binding"| GPU["GPU Shader"]
    Samplers -->|"Per-draw binding"| GPU
```

Sources: [scene/resources/material.cpp:450-520](), [drivers/gles3/shaders/scene.glsl:540-600]()

The parameter system supports:
- **Scalar types**: `float`, `int`, `bool`
- **Vector types**: `vec2`, `vec3`, `vec4`, `Color`
- **Textures**: `Texture2D`, `Texture3D`, `TextureCube`
- **Arrays**: For vertex skinning, particle data, etc.

---

## Initialization and Configuration

The rendering system is initialized during engine startup and configured through project settings.

### Engine Startup Sequence

The rendering server and backends are created in `Main::setup2()`:

```mermaid
graph TD
    Setup["Main::setup2()<br/>main.cpp"]
    
    CreateRS["Create RenderingServer<br/>RenderingServerDefault::create()"]
    
    InitDisplay["Initialize DisplayServer<br/>Platform-specific window creation"]
    
    CheckRenderer{"Check rendering/<br/>renderer/<br/>rendering_method"}
    
    CreateRD["Create RenderingDevice<br/>Based on driver preference"]
    CreateGL["Create GL Context"]
    
    CreateBackend["Create Scene Renderer:<br/>RenderForwardClustered<br/>RenderForwardMobile<br/>RasterizerSceneGLES3"]
    
    InitBackend["Initialize backend<br/>Load shaders<br/>Create pipelines<br/>Setup render buffers"]
    
    Setup --> CreateRS
    CreateRS --> InitDisplay
    InitDisplay --> CheckRenderer
    
    CheckRenderer -->|"forward_plus/mobile"| CreateRD
    CheckRenderer -->|"gl_compatibility"| CreateGL
    
    CreateRD --> CreateBackend
    CreateGL --> CreateBackend
    
    CreateBackend --> InitBackend
```

Sources: [main/main.cpp:1800-2300](), [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:47-100]()

### Project Settings

Key project settings affect rendering behavior:

| Setting | Values | Effect |
|---------|--------|--------|
| `rendering/renderer/rendering_method` | `forward_plus`, `mobile`, `gl_compatibility` | Selects rendering backend [doc/classes/ProjectSettings.xml:1-100]() |
| `rendering/anti_aliasing/quality/msaa_3d` | `disabled`, `2x`, `4x`, `8x` | Multi-sample anti-aliasing level |
| `rendering/lights_and_shadows/directional_shadow/size` | 512-16384 | Resolution of directional light shadow maps |
| `rendering/global_illumination/voxel_gi/quality` | `low`, `high` | VoxelGI octree detail level (Forward+ only) |
| `rendering/scaling_3d/mode` | `bilinear`, `fsr`, `fsr2` | Upscaling method for internal resolution |

These settings are read during initialization and affect which shader variants are compiled and which rendering features are enabled.

Sources: [doc/classes/ProjectSettings.xml:1-500](), [core/config/project_settings.cpp:1-300]()

---

## Summary

The Godot rendering system is a sophisticated multi-layered architecture:

1. **RenderingServer** provides a thread-safe API abstracting all visual operations
2. **RendererSceneCull** performs visibility determination and light management
3. **RendererViewport** coordinates 2D and 3D rendering to render targets
4. **Multiple backends** support different platforms:
   - Forward Clustered (high-end, many lights)
   - Forward Mobile (mobile/low-end, optimized for fewer lights)
   - OpenGL ES 3 (compatibility, legacy hardware)
5. **Material system** bridges resources to backend-compiled shaders

This architecture allows Godot to render efficiently across desktop, console, mobile, and web platforms while providing a consistent API to game developers.

Sources: [servers/rendering/rendering_server.h:1-200](), [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:1-200](), [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp:1-200](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.h:1-200](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.h:1-200](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:1-200]()1d:T58f7,# Rendering Server Architecture

## Purpose and Scope

This page documents the architecture of the RenderingServer, Godot's low-level graphics API. The RenderingServer provides the interface between the scene system and the rendering backends, managing resource creation, scene culling, viewport rendering, and command queuing for thread safety.

This page focuses on the server architecture itselfâ€”the API design, command queuing, scene culling, and viewport management. For information about specific rendering backends (Forward Clustered, Mobile, OpenGL), see [Forward Clustered and Mobile Renderers](#3.2) and [OpenGL ES 3 Backend](#3.3). For details on how scene nodes integrate with rendering, see [Viewport and Rendering Integration](#2.3).

## Architecture Overview

The RenderingServer architecture consists of several layers that separate the public API from the rendering implementation:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Client Layer"
        Scene["Scene Nodes<br/>(Node3D, CanvasItem)"]
        Camera["Camera Nodes<br/>(Camera3D, Camera2D)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Public API Layer"
        RS["RenderingServer<br/>(Abstract Interface)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Implementation Layer"
        RSD["RenderingServerDefault<br/>(Concrete Implementation)"]
        CQ["CommandQueueMT<br/>(Thread-Safe Queue)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Management Layer"
        RSC["RendererSceneCull<br/>(Visibility & Culling)"]
        RV["RendererViewport<br/>(Viewport Management)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Backend Interface"
        RSR["RendererSceneRender<br/>(Backend Interface)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Backend Implementations"
        RSRRD["RendererSceneRenderRD<br/>(RenderingDevice Base)"]
        RFC["RenderForwardClustered"]
        RFM["RenderForwardMobile"]
        GLES3["RasterizerSceneGLES3"]
    end
    
    Scene --> RS
    Camera --> RS
    RS --> RSD
    RSD --> CQ
    CQ --> RSC
    CQ --> RV
    RSC --> RSR
    RV --> RSR
    RSR --> RSRRD
    RSR --> GLES3
    RSRRD --> RFC
    RSRRD --> RFM
    
```

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/rendering_server.h](), [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h](), [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.h](), [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.h](), [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_render.h]()

## RenderingServer API Design

The `RenderingServer` class provides the public API for all rendering operations in Godot. It uses a **Resource ID (RID)** based design where resources are created and manipulated through opaque handles.

### RID-Based Resource Management

All rendering resources (textures, meshes, materials, lights, etc.) are represented by RIDs. The server provides `*_create()` methods to allocate resources and `*_set_*()` methods to configure them:

| Resource Type | Creation Method | Example Configuration Methods |
|---------------|----------------|-------------------------------|
| Texture | `texture_2d_create()` | `texture_2d_update()` |
| Mesh | `mesh_create()` | `mesh_add_surface()`, `mesh_surface_set_material()` |
| Material | `material_create()` | `material_set_shader()`, `material_set_param()` |
| Light | `light_create()` | `light_set_color()`, `light_set_param()` |
| Camera | `camera_create()` | `camera_set_transform()`, `camera_set_perspective()` |
| Viewport | `viewport_create()` | `viewport_set_size()`, `viewport_attach_camera()` |
| Scenario | `scenario_create()` | `scenario_set_environment()` |
| Canvas | `canvas_create()` | N/A |

The RID design allows the server implementation to be completely opaqueâ€”clients never directly access rendering resource data structures.

**Sources:** [doc/classes/RenderingServer.xml:1-30](), [servers/rendering/rendering_server.h]()

### Key Subsystems

The RenderingServer API is organized into several subsystems:

```mermaid
graph LR
    RS["RenderingServer"]
    
    RS --> Texture["Texture API<br/>texture_*"]
    RS --> Mesh["Mesh API<br/>mesh_*"]
    RS --> Material["Material/Shader API<br/>material_*, shader_*"]
    RS --> Light["Light API<br/>light_*"]
    RS --> Camera["Camera API<br/>camera_*"]
    RS --> Viewport["Viewport API<br/>viewport_*"]
    RS --> Scenario["3D Scene API<br/>scenario_*, instance_*"]
    RS --> Canvas["2D Canvas API<br/>canvas_*, canvas_item_*"]
```

**Sources:** [doc/classes/RenderingServer.xml]()

## RenderingServerDefault Implementation

The `RenderingServerDefault` class provides the concrete implementation of the `RenderingServer` interface. Its primary responsibility is to manage thread safety and dispatch commands to the appropriate subsystems.

### Thread Safety Architecture

The rendering server can operate in two modes:

1. **Single-threaded mode**: Commands execute immediately on the calling thread
2. **Multi-threaded mode**: Commands are queued and executed on a dedicated render thread

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Main Thread"
        Client["Client Code<br/>(Scene System)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "RenderingServerDefault"
        API["API Methods<br/>(texture_create, etc.)"]
        Check{{"Thread Check<br/>server_thread?"}}
        Direct["Direct Execution"]
        Queue["CommandQueueMT<br/>command_queue.push()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Render Thread"
        Loop["_thread_loop()"]
        Execute["Execute Commands"]
        Subsystems["Rendering Subsystems<br/>(RendererSceneCull, etc.)"]
    end
    
    Client --> API
    API --> Check
    Check -->|"Same Thread"| Direct
    Check -->|"Different Thread"| Queue
    Direct --> Subsystems
    Queue --> Loop
    Loop --> Execute
    Execute --> Subsystems
```

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:80-98](), [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:117-119]()

### Command Queue Pattern

The implementation uses macros to determine whether to execute immediately or queue commands:

- `ASYNC_COND_PUSH`: True if calling from a different thread than the render thread
- `WRITE_ACTION`: Marks that the rendering state has changed (calls `redraw_request()`)

For resource creation, the pattern looks like:

```
virtual RID texture_2d_create(...) override {
    RID ret = RSG::texture_storage->texture_allocate();
    if (Thread::get_caller_id() == server_thread || can_create_async()) {
        RSG::texture_storage->texture_2d_initialize(ret, ...);
    } else {
        command_queue.push(RSG::texture_storage, &RendererTextureStorage::texture_2d_initialize, ret, ...);
    }
    return ret;
}
```

This allows resources to be created immediately on the render thread or asynchronously on other threads.

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:136-167](), [core/templates/command_queue_mt.h]()

### Initialization

The rendering server is initialized early in the engine startup sequence:

1. `Main::setup2()` creates the rendering server instance
2. Platform-specific display server is initialized
3. `rendering_server->init()` is called to initialize subsystems
4. Scene rendering systems are set up (RendererSceneCull, RendererViewport)

**Sources:** [main/main.cpp:2000-2100]()

## Scene Culling with RendererSceneCull

The `RendererSceneCull` class is responsible for managing 3D scenes, performing visibility culling, and preparing render lists for the rendering backend.

### Scene and Instance Management

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Scene Hierarchy"
        Scenario["Scenario<br/>(3D World Container)"]
        Instance["Instance<br/>(Geometry, Lights, etc.)"]
        Camera["Camera<br/>(View Parameters)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Spatial Indexing"
        BVH["DynamicBVH<br/>(Broad Phase)"]
        Octree["Octree<br/>(Optional, Legacy)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Culling Process"
        Frustum["Frustum Culling"]
        Occlusion["Occlusion Culling<br/>(Optional)"]
        Distance["Distance Culling<br/>(LOD)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Output"
        RenderList["Render Lists<br/>(Opaque, Alpha, Shadow)"]
        LightList["Light Cull Lists"]
    end
    
    Scenario --> Instance
    Instance --> BVH
    BVH --> Frustum
    Frustum --> Occlusion
    Occlusion --> Distance
    Distance --> RenderList
    Instance --> LightList
    Camera --> Frustum
```

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.h:52-66](), [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:1-50]()

### Instance Data and Pairing

Each instance in a scenario has associated data structures:

- **Instance**: Core instance data with transform, AABB, layer mask
- **InstanceData**: Cached instance data for efficient rendering
- **InstanceGeometryData**: Geometry-specific data including paired lights, reflection probes, decals

The `_instance_pair()` and `_instance_unpair()` methods manage relationships between instances. For example, when a light instance overlaps with a geometry instance, they are paired so the light affects the geometry.

| Pair Type | Description |
|-----------|-------------|
| Light â†” Geometry | Light affects geometry for lighting calculations |
| ReflectionProbe â†” Geometry | Probe provides reflections for geometry |
| Decal â†” Geometry | Decal projects onto geometry surface |
| Lightmap â†” Geometry | Baked lightmap applied to geometry |
| GI Probe â†” Geometry | GI probe provides indirect lighting |

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:176-270](), [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.h:300-450]()

### Visibility Culling Process

The main culling method is `RendererSceneCull::_render_scene()`, which performs several culling passes:

1. **Frustum Culling**: Test instance AABBs against camera frustum
2. **Occlusion Culling**: Test against occlusion buffers (if enabled)
3. **Distance Culling**: Apply LOD and distance-based culling
4. **Layer Mask Filtering**: Check instance layers against camera cull mask
5. **Shadow Culling**: Separate pass for shadow-casting instances

The culling results are stored in `PagedArray` structures that are passed to the rendering backend.

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:2500-3500]()

### Render List Generation

After culling, instances are sorted into render lists based on their properties:

```mermaid
graph LR
    Instances["Culled Instances"]
    
    Instances --> Opaque["Opaque List<br/>(Front-to-back)"]
    Instances --> Alpha["Alpha List<br/>(Back-to-front)"]
    Instances --> Shadow["Shadow List<br/>(Optimized)"]
    Instances --> Reflection["Reflection Probe List"]
    
    Opaque --> Backend["Rendering Backend"]
    Alpha --> Backend
    Shadow --> Backend
    Reflection --> Backend
```

The render lists are optimized for each use case:
- **Opaque**: Sorted front-to-back for early Z rejection
- **Alpha**: Sorted back-to-front for correct blending
- **Shadow**: Optimized for minimal state changes

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:3500-4000]()

## Viewport Management with RendererViewport

The `RendererViewport` class manages viewport resources, coordinates rendering passes, and handles viewport hierarchies for sub-viewports.

### Viewport Structure

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Viewport Components"
        VP["Viewport<br/>(RID)"]
        RT["RenderTarget<br/>(Output Texture)"]
        Camera["Camera<br/>(View)"]
        Scenario["Scenario<br/>(3D Content)"]
        Canvas["Canvas Layers<br/>(2D Content)"]
        RB["RenderBuffers<br/>(Internal Buffers)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Viewport Settings"
        Size["Size"]
        MSAA["MSAA Level"]
        HDR["HDR Mode"]
        DebugDraw["Debug Draw Mode"]
        Scaling["3D Scaling"]
    end
    
    VP --> RT
    VP --> Camera
    VP --> Scenario
    VP --> Canvas
    VP --> RB
    VP --> Size
    VP --> MSAA
    VP --> HDR
    VP --> DebugDraw
    VP --> Scaling
```

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.h:50-150]()

### Viewport Rendering Pipeline

The main rendering entry point is `RendererViewport::draw_viewports()`, which processes all active viewports in the correct order:

1. **Sort viewports**: Children before parents (topological sort)
2. **For each viewport**:
   - Update viewport size and settings
   - Configure render buffers (3D rendering targets)
   - Render 3D scene (if scenario attached)
   - Render 2D canvas layers
   - Apply post-processing effects
   - Copy to output texture

```mermaid
graph TB
    Start["draw_viewports()"]
    Sort["_sort_active_viewports()"]
    Loop{{"For Each Viewport"}}
    
    Update["Update Size & Settings"]
    Config3D["_configure_3d_render_buffers()"]
    Render3D["_draw_3d()<br/>(RendererSceneCull)"]
    Render2D["_draw_2d()<br/>(RendererCanvasCull)"]
    PostFX["Post-Processing"]
    Output["Copy to RenderTarget"]
    
    Next{{"More Viewports?"}}
    End["Complete"]
    
    Start --> Sort
    Sort --> Loop
    Loop -->|"Yes"| Update
    Update --> Config3D
    Config3D --> Render3D
    Render3D --> Render2D
    Render2D --> PostFX
    PostFX --> Output
    Output --> Next
    Next -->|"Yes"| Loop
    Next -->|"No"| End
```

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp:500-800](), [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp:98-134]()

### 3D Render Buffers Configuration

For 3D rendering, viewports create and manage `RenderSceneBuffers` which contain:

- **Color Buffers**: HDR/LDR color output
- **Depth Buffer**: Depth/stencil buffer
- **MSAA Buffers**: Multi-sample anti-aliasing (if enabled)
- **Motion Vectors**: For TAA and motion blur
- **Effect Buffers**: For screen-space effects (SSAO, SSR, etc.)

The `_configure_3d_render_buffers()` method handles:
- Scaling/resolution changes
- MSAA configuration
- FSR/TAA upscaling setup
- VRS (Variable Rate Shading) setup

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp:136-200]()

### 2D Canvas Rendering

Viewports can have multiple canvas layers for 2D rendering. Each canvas has:

- **Transform**: 2D transformation matrix
- **Layer**: Sorting layer
- **Follow Viewport**: Whether to follow 3D viewport camera
- **Canvas Items**: The 2D drawable elements

The rendering order is:
1. Render background canvases (layer < 0)
2. Render 3D scene
3. Render foreground canvases (layer >= 0)

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.cpp:800-1000]()

## Backend Interface: RendererSceneRender

The `RendererSceneRender` class provides the abstract interface that rendering backends must implement. This separates the scene management (culling, viewports) from the actual rendering implementation.

### Key Backend Methods

| Method | Purpose |
|--------|---------|
| `render_scene()` | Main entry point to render a scene |
| `render_shadow()` | Render shadow map for a light |
| `render_material()` | Render material preview |
| `render_sdfgi()` | Render SDFGI voxel data |
| `render_particle_collider_heightfield()` | Render heightfield for particle collision |

### RenderData Structure

Rendering backends receive a `RenderData` structure containing:

- **Render Buffers**: Target buffers for rendering
- **Camera Data**: View/projection matrices, frustum
- **Scene Data**: Environment, lights, reflections
- **Cull Data**: Culled instance lists
- **Viewport**: The viewport being rendered
- **Shadow Atlas**: Shadow map atlas (if rendering shadows)

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_render.h:50-150](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/storage_rd/render_data_rd.h]()

### Backend Selection

During initialization, the appropriate backend is selected based on:

1. Project settings (`rendering/renderer/rendering_method`)
2. Platform capabilities
3. Available drivers (Vulkan, D3D12, Metal, OpenGL)

The backends are:
- **RenderForwardClustered**: Desktop/console, clustered lighting
- **RenderForwardMobile**: Mobile devices, simplified lighting
- **RasterizerSceneGLES3**: OpenGL ES 3.0 fallback

**Sources:** [main/main.cpp:2000-2100](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/renderer_scene_render_rd.h]()

## Command Queue and Thread Safety

The `CommandQueueMT` provides thread-safe command queuing with several important features:

### Command Execution Model

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Producer Threads"
        T1["Main Thread"]
        T2["Script Thread"]
        T3["Physics Thread"]
    end
    
    subgraph "CommandQueueMT"
        Buffer["Circular Buffer"]
        Lock["Mutex"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Consumer Thread"
        RT["Render Thread"]
        Exec["Execute Commands"]
    end
    
    T1 -->|"Push Commands"| Buffer
    T2 -->|"Push Commands"| Buffer
    T3 -->|"Push Commands"| Buffer
    Buffer --> RT
    RT --> Exec
    Lock -.->|"Protects"| Buffer
```

### Synchronization Points

The command queue provides synchronization through:

1. **Flush**: Wait for all queued commands to execute
2. **Sync**: Execute a command and wait for completion
3. **Frame Boundary**: Commands are batched per frame

The `RenderingServerDefault::sync()` method forces synchronization, ensuring all pending commands complete before returning. This is used when the main thread needs to read rendering results.

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:80-130](), [core/templates/command_queue_mt.h]()

## Resource Management and Lifetime

### RID Allocation

RIDs are allocated from RID owners which manage resource lifetime:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Create["Resource Creation<br/>(e.g., texture_create)"]
    Allocate["RID Owner Allocates"]
    Initialize["Resource Initialized"]
    Usage["Resource Used in Rendering"]
    Free["free_rid() Called"]
    Cleanup["Resource Destroyed"]
    
    Create --> Allocate
    Allocate --> Initialize
    Initialize --> Usage
    Usage --> Free
    Free --> Cleanup
```

Each resource type has its own RID owner that tracks all instances. When `free_rid()` is called, the server determines the resource type and delegates to the appropriate storage system for cleanup.

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:1000-1100]()

### Frame Markers

The rendering server tracks frame boundaries for resource management:

- `frame_pre_draw()`: Called before rendering starts
- `frame_post_draw()`: Called after rendering completes
- Frame numbers used for resource reference counting

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/rendering_server.h]()

## Initialization Sequence

The complete initialization sequence from engine startup:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Main["Main::setup2()"]
    CreateRS["Create RenderingServerDefault"]

    Ready["Ready to Render"]
    
    Main --> CreateRS
    CreateRS --> CreateDS
    CreateDS --> InitRS
    InitRS --> InitSubsystems
    InitSubsystems --> CreateCull
    InitSubsystems --> CreateVP
    InitSubsystems --> CreateBackend
    InitSubsystems --> RegisterTypes
    RegisterTypes --> Ready
```

**Sources:** [main/main.cpp:1800-2100]()

## Performance Considerations

### Culling Optimizations

The culling system employs several optimizations:

- **BVH Spatial Indexing**: O(log n) broad-phase culling
- **SIMD Frustum Tests**: Vectorized frustum plane tests
- **Dirty Flags**: Only recalculate changed instances
- **Occlusion Culling**: CPU-based occlusion buffer (optional)

### Command Queue Overhead

The command queue adds minimal overhead:
- Lock-free reads when possible
- Batched command execution
- Commands inlined for small arguments
- Pointer-based arguments for large data

### Multi-threaded Rendering

When using multi-threaded rendering:
- Main thread continues while render thread executes
- Synchronization only at frame boundaries
- Resources can be created asynchronously

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.cpp:100-300](), [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h:80-120]()

---

**Key Takeaways:**

1. **RenderingServer** provides the public API using RID-based resource management
2. **RenderingServerDefault** implements thread safety through **CommandQueueMT**
3. **RendererSceneCull** handles visibility culling and render list generation
4. **RendererViewport** manages viewport rendering and coordinates 2D/3D rendering
5. **RendererSceneRender** defines the backend interface for actual rendering
6. The architecture separates concerns: API â†’ Implementation â†’ Management â†’ Backend

**Sources:** [servers/rendering/rendering_server.h](), [servers/rendering/rendering_server_default.h](), [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_cull.h](), [servers/rendering/renderer_viewport.h](), [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_render.h]()1e:T7757,# Forward Clustered and Mobile Renderers

## Purpose and Scope

This document describes the modern 3D rendering backends in Godot Engine that use the `RenderingDevice` abstraction layer. These renderers support Vulkan, Direct3D 12, and Metal graphics APIs and provide high-quality rendering features for desktop, console, and mobile platforms.

The two primary implementations covered are:
- **RenderForwardClustered**: High-performance renderer for desktop and console platforms with advanced lighting capabilities
- **RenderForwardMobile**: Optimized renderer for mobile devices with reduced memory footprint and simplified rendering paths

For information about the OpenGL ES 3.0 compatibility renderer, see [OpenGL ES 3 Backend](#3.3). For the higher-level rendering server API, see [Rendering Server Architecture](#3.1).

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.h:1-100](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.h:1-100]()

## Architecture Overview

Both forward renderers inherit from `RendererSceneRenderRD`, which provides common infrastructure for RenderingDevice-based rendering. The class hierarchy establishes shared functionality while allowing platform-specific optimizations.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Rendering Server Layer"
        RS["RenderingServer"]
        RSD["RenderingServerDefault"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Scene Culling Layer"
        RSC["RendererSceneCull"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Base Renderer"
        RSRRD["RendererSceneRenderRD<br/>(Base Class)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Forward Renderer Implementations"
        RFC["RenderForwardClustered<br/>Desktop/Console"]
        RFM["RenderForwardMobile<br/>Mobile Devices"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Graphics API Abstraction"
        RD["RenderingDevice"]
        Vulkan["Vulkan"]
        D3D12["Direct3D 12"]
        Metal["Metal"]
    end
    
    RS --> RSD
    RSD --> RSC
    RSC --> RSRRD
    
    RSRRD <|-- RFC
    RSRRD <|-- RFM
    
    RFC --> RD
    RFM --> RD
    
    RD --> Vulkan
    RD --> D3D12
    RD --> Metal
    
    style RFC fill:#e8f4f8
    style RFM fill:#e8f4f8
    style RSRRD fill:#f0f0f0
```

**Selection Logic**: The engine selects between renderers based on project settings and platform capabilities. The rendering method is configured via `rendering/renderer/rendering_method` in `ProjectSettings`.

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/renderer_scene_render_rd.h:57-100](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.h:60-90](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.h:42-75]()

## RenderForwardClustered Implementation

### Key Features

`RenderForwardClustered` provides advanced rendering capabilities optimized for desktop and console hardware:

| Feature | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| **Clustered Lighting** | Uses `ClusterBuilderRD` to organize lights into 3D grid clusters for efficient lighting evaluation |
| **Advanced Post-Processing** | Supports SSAO, SSIL, SSR, temporal anti-aliasing (TAA) |
| **Upscaling Technologies** | FSR 2.2 and MetalFX Temporal upscaling support |
| **Motion Vectors** | Per-object motion vectors for temporal effects |
| **High-Quality Shadows** | PCSS (Percentage-Closer Soft Shadows) for realistic soft shadows |

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "RenderForwardClustered Components"
        RFC["RenderForwardClustered"]
        RBDFC["RenderBufferDataForwardClustered"]
        ClusterBuilder["ClusterBuilderRD"]
        SceneShader["SceneShaderForwardClustered"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Advanced Effects"
        SSEffects["SS Effects<br/>(SSAO, SSIL, SSR)"]
        TAA["Temporal Anti-Aliasing"]
        FSR2["FSR 2.2 Context"]
        MFXTemporal["MetalFX Temporal"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Render Targets"
        ColorBuffer["Color Buffer"]
        SpecularBuffer["Specular Buffer<br/>(Separate Specular)"]
        DepthBuffer["Depth Buffer"]
        NormalRoughness["Normal/Roughness Buffer"]
        VelocityBuffer["Motion Vectors"]
        VoxelGI["Voxel GI Buffer"]
    end
    
    RFC --> RBDFC
    RFC --> SceneShader
    
    RBDFC --> ClusterBuilder
    RBDFC --> SSEffects
    RBDFC --> TAA
    RBDFC --> FSR2
    RBDFC --> MFXTemporal
    
    RBDFC --> ColorBuffer
    RBDFC --> SpecularBuffer
    RBDFC --> DepthBuffer
    RBDFC --> NormalRoughness
    RBDFC --> VelocityBuffer
    RBDFC --> VoxelGI
```

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.h:60-150](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:50-160]()

### Render Buffer Structure

The `RenderBufferDataForwardClustered` class manages all render targets and intermediate buffers for the clustered renderer:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Texture Creation On-Demand"
```

**Buffer Format Details**:

| Buffer | Format | Purpose |
|--------|--------|---------|
| Specular | `RD::DATA_FORMAT_R16G16B16A16_SFLOAT` | Separate specular reflections for advanced compositing |
| Normal/Roughness | `RD::DATA_FORMAT_R8G8B8A8_UNORM` | Surface normal and roughness for screen-space effects |
| Voxel GI | `RD::DATA_FORMAT_R8G8_UINT` | Voxel global illumination probe indices |

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:50-276]()

### Clustered Light Management

The forward clustered renderer uses `ClusterBuilderRD` to organize scene lights into a 3D grid structure. This enables efficient evaluation of many lights per pixel:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Cluster Building"
        CB["ClusterBuilderRD"]
        SharedData["ClusterBuilderSharedDataRD<br/>(Shared across viewports)"]
        Setup["setup()<br/>Configure cluster dimensions"]
        Begin["begin()<br/>Start cluster collection"]
        Bake["bake_cluster()<br/>Finalize cluster data"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Light Types"
        OmniLights["Omni Lights"]
        SpotLights["Spot Lights"]
        Decals["Decals"]
        ReflectionProbes["Reflection Probes"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Cluster Output"
        ClusterBuffer["Cluster Index Buffer"]
        ElementBuffer["Light/Decal Element Data"]
    end
    
    CB --> SharedData
    CB --> Setup
    CB --> Begin
    CB --> Bake
    
    Begin --> OmniLights
    Begin --> SpotLights
    Begin --> Decals
    Begin --> ReflectionProbes
    
    Bake --> ClusterBuffer
    Bake --> ElementBuffer
```

The cluster builder divides the view frustum into a 3D grid (typically 16Ã—8Ã—24 clusters) and assigns lights to each cluster based on their influence volume.

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:143-159](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/cluster_builder_rd.h]()

### Rendering Pipeline Stages

The main rendering flow in `RenderForwardClustered` consists of multiple passes:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Start["_render_scene()"]

    ClusterBuild["Build Light Clusters"]
    
    subgraph "Depth Pre-Pass"
        DepthPass["Render Depth<br/>(Opaque Only)"]

    end
    
    subgraph "Screen-Space Effects"
        SSAO["SSAO Pass"]
        SSIL["SSIL Pass"]
        SSR["SSR Pass"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Main Color Pass"
        OpaquePass["Render Opaque Geometry"]
        SkyPass["Render Sky"]
        TransparentPass["Render Transparent Geometry"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Post-Processing"
        Resolve["Resolve MSAA"]
        TAA["Temporal AA"]
        Upscale["FSR2/MetalFX Upscaling"]
        Tonemap["Tonemapping"]
    end
    
    Start --> Setup
    Setup --> ClusterBuild
    ClusterBuild --> DepthPass
    DepthPass --> DepthNormalRoughness
    
    DepthNormalRoughness --> SSAO
    SSAO --> SSIL
    SSIL --> SSR
    
    SSR --> OpaquePass
    OpaquePass --> SkyPass
    SkyPass --> TransparentPass
    
    TransparentPass --> Resolve
    Resolve --> TAA
    TAA --> Upscale
    Upscale --> Tonemap
```

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:300-600]()

## RenderForwardMobile Implementation

### Mobile-Specific Optimizations

`RenderForwardMobile` is designed for mobile GPUs with limited bandwidth and compute resources. Key differences from the clustered renderer:

| Optimization | Implementation |
|--------------|----------------|
| **Simplified Lighting** | Forward ID system instead of clusters (max 8 lights per object) |
| **Single-Pass Rendering** | Combines opaque and post-processing in subpasses where possible |
| **Reduced Buffer Count** | No separate specular buffer, simplified G-buffer |
| **Tile-Based Rendering** | Optimized for mobile tile-based deferred rendering (TBDR) architectures |

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Mobile Renderer Components"
        RFM["RenderForwardMobile"]
        RBDM["RenderBufferDataForwardMobile"]
        FwdIDStorage["ForwardIDStorageMobile"]
        SceneShaderMobile["SceneShaderForwardMobile"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Light Management"
        AllocID["allocate_forward_id()"]
        MapID["map_forward_id()"]
        FillIndices["fill_push_constant_instance_indices()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Framebuffer Configs"
        SinglePass["FB_CONFIG_RENDER_PASS<br/>(Single render pass)"]
        MultiPass["FB_CONFIG_RENDER_AND_POST_PASS<br/>(Render + Blit)"]
    end
    
    RFM --> RBDM
    RFM --> FwdIDStorage
    RFM --> SceneShaderMobile
    
    FwdIDStorage --> AllocID
    FwdIDStorage --> MapID
    FwdIDStorage --> FillIndices
    
    RBDM --> SinglePass
    RBDM --> MultiPass
```

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.h:42-150](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.cpp:52-154]()

### Forward ID System

Instead of clusters, the mobile renderer uses a simpler forward ID system that limits each geometry instance to a maximum of 8 lights, 8 decals, and 8 reflection probes:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Per-Instance Light Assignment"
        GeomInstance["Geometry Instance"]
        OmniArray["omni_lights[8]"]
        SpotArray["spot_lights[8]"]
        DecalArray["decals[8]"]
        ProbeArray["reflection_probes[8]"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Forward ID Allocators"
        OmniAllocator["FORWARD_ID_TYPE_OMNI_LIGHT"]
        SpotAllocator["FORWARD_ID_TYPE_SPOT_LIGHT"]
        DecalAllocator["FORWARD_ID_TYPE_DECAL"]
        ProbeAllocator["FORWARD_ID_TYPE_REFLECTION_PROBE"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Push Constants"
        PC["Push Constant"]
        PackedIndices["Packed 8-bit Indices<br/>(4 indices per uint32)"]
    end
    
    GeomInstance --> OmniArray
    GeomInstance --> SpotArray
    GeomInstance --> DecalArray
    GeomInstance --> ProbeArray
    
    OmniArray --> OmniAllocator
    SpotArray --> SpotAllocator
    DecalArray --> DecalAllocator
    ProbeArray --> ProbeAllocator
    
    OmniAllocator --> PC
    SpotAllocator --> PC
    DecalAllocator --> PC
    ProbeAllocator --> PC
    
    PC --> PackedIndices
```

The system packs up to 8 light indices (8-bit each) into two uint32 values, allowing efficient light lookup in the shader without cluster traversal.

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.cpp:52-154]()

### Subpass Optimization

Mobile renderer uses framebuffer subpasses to optimize tile-based architectures:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Single Pass Config (FB_CONFIG_RENDER_PASS)"
        SP_Color["Color Attachment 0"]
        SP_Depth["Depth Attachment"]
        SP_Resolve["Resolve Color<br/>(if MSAA)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Dual Pass Config (FB_CONFIG_RENDER_AND_POST_PASS)"
        MP_Pass1["Subpass 0: Main Render"]
        MP_Pass2["Subpass 1: Blit to Target"]
        MP_Input["Input Attachment"]
        MP_Output["Output to Render Target"]
    end
    
    SP_Color --> SP_Resolve
    
    MP_Pass1 --> MP_Input
    MP_Input --> MP_Pass2
    MP_Pass2 --> MP_Output
```

The dual-pass configuration enables efficient on-tile post-processing without round-tripping to main memory on TBDR GPUs.

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.cpp:203-323]()

## Common Infrastructure (RendererSceneRenderRD)

### Shared Systems

`RendererSceneRenderRD` provides infrastructure used by both forward renderers:

| System | Class | Purpose |
|--------|-------|---------|
| **Sky Rendering** | `RendererRD::SkyRD` | Procedural and image-based sky rendering |
| **Global Illumination** | `RendererRD::GI` | Voxel GI and SDFGI systems |
| **Fog** | `RendererRD::Fog` | Volumetric fog simulation |
| **Post-Processing** | `RendererRD::CopyEffects`, `RendererRD::ToneMapper` | Screen-space effects and HDR tonemapping |
| **Shadow Rendering** | Managed in base class | Directional, omni, and spot shadow maps |
| **Forward ID Storage** | `RendererRD::ForwardIDStorage` | Light/decal ID management (override in mobile) |

### Texture Scope System

Render buffers use a scope-based texture management system to organize renderer-specific textures:

| Scope | Renderer | Textures |
|-------|----------|----------|
| `RB_SCOPE_FORWARD_CLUSTERED` | Clustered | `RB_TEX_SPECULAR`, `RB_TEX_SPECULAR_MSAA`, `RB_TEX_NORMAL_ROUGHNESS`, `RB_TEX_NORMAL_ROUGHNESS_MSAA`, `RB_TEX_VOXEL_GI`, `RB_TEX_VOXEL_GI_MSAA` |
| `RB_SCOPE_MOBILE` | Mobile | Minimal additional textures |
| `RB_SCOPE_BUFFERS` | Common | `RB_TEX_COLOR`, `RB_TEX_COLOR_MSAA`, `RB_TEX_DEPTH`, `RB_TEX_DEPTH_MSAA` |
| `RB_SCOPE_VRS` | Common | `RB_TEXTURE` (VRS texture) |
| `RB_SCOPE_SSAO` | Clustered | SSAO intermediate buffers |
| `RB_SCOPE_SSIL` | Clustered | SSIL intermediate buffers |
| `RB_SCOPE_SSR` | Clustered | SSR intermediate buffers |

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:303-537](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.cpp:600-900]()

### Draw List Template System

Both renderers use templated `_render_list_template` methods to minimize branching during draw call submission:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Start["_render_list_template<br/>&lt;PassMode, ColorPassFlags&gt;"]
    
    BindGlobalSets["Bind Global Uniform Sets<br/>(SCENE_UNIFORM_SET, RENDER_PASS_UNIFORM_SET)"]
    
    LoopStart["For each element in render list"]
    
    CheckInstance["Check instance count > 0"]
    
    GetPipeline["Get or compile pipeline<br/>(shader->pipeline_hash_map.get_pipeline)"]
    
    BindMaterial["Bind material uniform set"]
    BindTransforms["Bind transforms uniform set"]
    BindVertexArray["Bind vertex array"]
    BindIndexArray["Bind index array if not emulating points"]
    
    DrawCall["RD::draw_list_draw()"]
    
    LoopEnd["Next element"]
    
    Start --> BindGlobalSets
    BindGlobalSets --> LoopStart
    LoopStart --> CheckInstance
    CheckInstance -->|Skip if 0| LoopEnd
    CheckInstance -->|Valid| GetPipeline
    GetPipeline --> BindMaterial
    BindMaterial --> BindTransforms
    BindTransforms --> BindVertexArray
    BindVertexArray --> BindIndexArray
    BindIndexArray --> DrawCall
    DrawCall --> LoopEnd
    LoopEnd -->|More elements| CheckInstance
```

The template parameters eliminate runtime conditionals for pass-specific behavior, improving draw call throughput.

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:303-600](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/render_forward_mobile.cpp:350-700]()

## Material and Shader Integration

### Scene Shader Classes

Each renderer has a corresponding scene shader class that manages shader variants:

| Renderer | Shader Class | Shader Stages |
|----------|--------------|---------------|
| Forward Clustered | `SceneShaderForwardClustered` | Vertex, Fragment, Depth-only variants |
| Forward Mobile | `SceneShaderForwardMobile` | Vertex, Fragment, Depth-only variants |

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Material to Shader Flow"
        Material["Material Resource"]
        ShaderRID["Shader RID"]
        ShaderData["ShaderData<br/>(per-shader instance)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Pipeline Compilation"
        VertexFormat["Vertex Format ID"]
        FramebufferFormat["Framebuffer Format ID"]
        PipelineKey["PipelineKey<br/>(format + specialization)"]
        PipelineHashMap["Pipeline Hash Map"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Runtime Binding"
        MaterialUniforms["Material Uniform Set"]
        PushConstants["Push Constants"]
        Pipeline["Graphics Pipeline RID"]
    end
    
    Material --> ShaderRID
    ShaderRID --> ShaderData
    
    ShaderData --> VertexFormat
    ShaderData --> FramebufferFormat
    VertexFormat --> PipelineKey
    FramebufferFormat --> PipelineKey
    
    PipelineKey --> PipelineHashMap
    PipelineHashMap --> Pipeline
```
