```mermaid
    PushConstants --> Runtime
```

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/scene_shader_forward_clustered.h](), [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_mobile/scene_shader_forward_mobile.h]()

### Shader Specialization Constants

Both renderers use shader specialization constants for compile-time optimization:

| Specialization | Purpose |
|----------------|---------|
| `multimesh` | Enable multimesh instance data fetching |
| `multimesh_format_2d` | 2D transform format for multimesh |
| `multimesh_has_color` | Include per-instance color data |
| `multimesh_has_custom_data` | Include custom data in instance buffer |
| `use_light_soft_shadows` | Enable PCSS for soft shadows (clustered) |
| `use_light_projector` | Enable light projector textures |
| `use_forward_gi` | Enable voxel GI in forward pass (clustered) |

The specialization system generates optimized shader code that avoids dynamic branching for features not used by a particular material or geometry instance.

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:420-456]()

### Ubershader Fallback System

When a specialized pipeline is not yet compiled, the renderers fall back to an ubershader:

```mermaid
graph TB
    RequestPipeline["Request Pipeline with Specialization"]
    
    CheckCache["Check Pipeline Hash Map"]
    
    Found{"Pipeline<br/>Exists?"}
    
    UseSpecialized["Use Specialized Pipeline"]
    
    TryUbershader["Set ubershader flag"]
    
    CheckUbershader{"Ubershader<br/>Pipeline Exists?"}
    
    UseUbershader["Use Ubershader"]
    
    CompileBackground["Queue Background Compilation"]
    
    Skip["Skip Draw Call"]
    
    RequestPipeline --> CheckCache
    CheckCache --> Found
    
    Found -->|Yes| UseSpecialized
    Found -->|No| TryUbershader
    
    TryUbershader --> CheckUbershader
    CheckUbershader -->|Yes| UseUbershader
    CheckUbershader -->|No| Skip
    
    UseUbershader --> CompileBackground
```

Ubershaders contain all possible code paths with dynamic branching, ensuring no visual glitches while specialized pipelines compile in the background.

Sources: [servers/rendering/renderer_rd/forward_clustered/render_forward_clustered.cpp:495-537]()

### Performance Settings

Key project settings affecting forward renderer behavior:

| Setting | Default | Impact |
|---------|---------|--------|
| `rendering/anti_aliasing/quality/msaa_3d` | Disabled | MSAA sample count for 3D rendering |
| `rendering/scaling_3d/mode` | Bilinear | Upscaling method (FSR, FSR2, MetalFX) |
| `rendering/scaling_3d/scale` | 1.0 | Internal render resolution scale |
| `rendering/lights_and_shadows/directional_shadow/size` | 4096 | Directional shadow map resolution |
| `rendering/global_illumination/voxel_gi/quality` | High | Voxel GI cone trace quality |
| `rendering/environment/ssao/quality` | Medium | SSAO sampling quality (clustered only) |
| `rendering/environment/ssil/quality` | Medium | SSIL sampling quality (clustered only) |

Sources: [doc/classes/ProjectSettings.xml:1-500]()1f:T5d3a,# OpenGL ES 3 Backend

## Purpose and Scope

The OpenGL ES 3 backend provides a legacy rendering implementation for Godot that uses direct OpenGL ES 3.0 API calls. This backend serves as a compatibility option for platforms and hardware that do not support modern graphics APIs (Vulkan, Direct3D 12, Metal). Unlike the modern rendering backends that use the RenderingDevice abstraction (see [Forward Clustered and Mobile Renderers](#3.2)), the GLES3 backend makes direct OpenGL calls to implement scene rendering, lighting, shadows, and post-processing.

This document covers the GLES3 rendering implementation including scene rendering, geometry management, material processing, lighting, and shadow systems. For information about the general rendering server architecture, see [Rendering Server Architecture](#3.1). For material resource definitions, see [Material and Shader System](#3.4).

---

## Architecture Overview

### Integration with Rendering System

The GLES3 backend implements the `RendererSceneRender` interface as an alternative to the RenderingDevice-based renderers.

```mermaid
graph TB
    RS["RenderingServer API"]
    RSD["RenderingServerDefault"]
    RSR["RendererSceneRender<br/>(Interface)"]
    
    GLES3["RasterizerSceneGLES3<br/>(GLES3 Implementation)"]
    RFC["RenderForwardClustered<br/>(Modern Desktop)"]
    RFM["RenderForwardMobile<br/>(Modern Mobile)"]
    
    RDevice["RenderingDevice<br/>(Vulkan/D3D12/Metal)"]
    GL["OpenGL ES 3.0<br/>Direct Calls"]
    
    RS --> RSD
    RSD --> RSR
    RSR -.implements.-> GLES3
    RSR -.implements.-> RFC
    RSR -.implements.-> RFM
    
    GLES3 --> GL
    RFC --> RDevice
    RFM --> RDevice
    
    MS["MaterialStorage"]
    LS["LightStorage"]
    MeshS["MeshStorage"]
    
    GLES3 --> MS
    GLES3 --> LS
    GLES3 --> MeshS
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:149](), [servers/rendering/renderer_scene_render.h]()

### Conditional Compilation

The GLES3 backend is conditionally compiled using the `GLES3_ENABLED` preprocessor directive. All GLES3 code is wrapped in `#ifdef GLES3_ENABLED` blocks to allow builds without OpenGL support.

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:33](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:33]()

## Core Components

### RasterizerSceneGLES3 Class

The `RasterizerSceneGLES3` class is the main entry point for 3D scene rendering in the GLES3 backend. It implements the `RendererSceneRender` interface.

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "RasterizerSceneGLES3"

    end
    
    subgraph "Scene State"
        ubo["UBO data<br/>(scene uniforms)"]
        lights["Light buffers<br/>(omni/spot/directional)"]
        shadows["Shadow buffers"]
        render_lists["render_list[3]<br/>(opaque/alpha/secondary)"]
    end
    
    scene_state --> ubo
    scene_state --> lights
    scene_state --> shadows
    scene_state --> render_lists
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:149-151](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:392-648]()

### Scene State Structure

The `SceneState` structure maintains all OpenGL state and uniform buffer data for scene rendering.

| Component | Type | Purpose |
|-----------|------|---------|
| `UBO data` | Uniform buffer | Scene-wide parameters (projection, view matrices, fog, etc.) |
| `MultiviewUBO multiview_data` | Uniform buffer | Stereo/XR view matrices |
| `omni_lights` / `spot_lights` | `LightData*` | Light parameter arrays |
| `directional_lights` | `DirectionalLightData*` | Directional light parameters |
| `positional_shadows` / `directional_shadows` | Shadow data | Shadow matrices and configuration |
| `current_blend_mode` / `cull_mode` | GL state cache | Cached OpenGL state to minimize state changes |

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:392-648]()

### Geometry Instance Management

Geometry instances represent renderable objects in the scene. The GLES3 backend uses paged allocators for efficient memory management.

```mermaid

    surfaces["surface_caches<br/>(linked list)"]
    lights["paired_omni_lights<br/>paired_spot_lights"]
    probes["paired_reflection_probes"]
    
    GI --> base
    GI --> surfaces
    GI --> lights
    GI --> probes
    
    surfaces --> GIS
    
    shader["shader<br/>(SceneShaderData*)"]
    material["material<br/>(SceneMaterialData*)"]
    mesh_surface["surface<br/>(Mesh::Surface*)"]
    flags["flags<br/>(pass/feature flags)"]
    
    GIS --> shader
    GIS --> material
    GIS --> mesh_surface
    GIS --> flags
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:236-357](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:56-72]()

## Rendering Pipeline

### Main Rendering Flow

The rendering process follows a structured pipeline from scene setup through final output.

```mermaid
graph TD
    render_scene["render_scene()<br/>(entry point)"]
    
    setup_env["_setup_environment()<br/>(configure fog, ambient)"]
    setup_lights["_setup_lights()<br/>(collect and sort lights)"]
    fill_list["_fill_render_list()<br/>(cull and sort geometry)"]
    
    render_shadows["_render_shadows()<br/>(shadow passes)"]
    
    depth_prepass["depth pre-pass<br/>(if needed)"]
    opaque_pass["opaque pass<br/>(RENDER_LIST_OPAQUE)"]
    sky_pass["_draw_sky()<br/>(sky rendering)"]
    alpha_pass["alpha pass<br/>(RENDER_LIST_ALPHA)"]
    
    post["_render_post_processing()<br/>(post effects)"]
    
    render_scene --> setup_env
    setup_env --> setup_lights
    setup_lights --> fill_list
    fill_list --> render_shadows
    
    render_shadows --> depth_prepass
    depth_prepass --> opaque_pass
    opaque_pass --> sky_pass
    sky_pass --> alpha_pass
    alpha_pass --> post
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:1300-1600]()

### Render List Organization

Geometry is organized into three render lists for different passes:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Render Lists"
        OPAQUE["RENDER_LIST_OPAQUE<br/>(solid geometry)"]
        ALPHA["RENDER_LIST_ALPHA<br/>(transparent geometry)"]
        SECONDARY["RENDER_LIST_SECONDARY<br/>(shadows, depth-only)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Pass Modes"
        COLOR["PASS_MODE_COLOR"]
        TRANS["PASS_MODE_COLOR_TRANSPARENT"]
        SHADOW["PASS_MODE_SHADOW"]
        DEPTH["PASS_MODE_DEPTH"]
    end
    
    OPAQUE -.rendered in.-> COLOR
    ALPHA -.rendered in.-> TRANS
    SECONDARY -.rendered in.-> SHADOW
    SECONDARY -.rendered in.-> DEPTH
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:47-61](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:722]()

### Surface Sorting

Surfaces are sorted using a 128-bit sort key for optimal rendering order:

| Bits | Field | Purpose |
|------|-------|---------|
| 0-7 | `lod_index` | Level of detail |
| 8-15 | `surface_index` | Surface within mesh |
| 16-47 | `geometry_id` | Mesh identifier |
| 48-63 | `material_id_low` | Material ID (low bits) |
| 64-79 | `material_id_hi` | Material ID (high bits) |
| 80-111 | `shader_id` | Shader identifier |
| 112-119 | `priority` | Material render priority |

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:253-273](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:311-321]()

## Material and Shader System

### Material Processing

Materials in GLES3 are processed through the `SceneMaterialData` and `SceneShaderData` classes from the MaterialStorage system.

```mermaid
graph TB
    Material["Material Resource"]
    SMD["SceneMaterialData<br/>(GLES3::SceneMaterialData)"]
    SSD["SceneShaderData<br/>(GLES3::SceneShaderData)"]

    SMD --> SSD

        depth["depth_draw/depth_test<br/>(depth configuration)"]
        blend["blend_mode<br/>(alpha blending)"]
    end
    
    SSD --> version
    SSD --> uses
    SSD --> depth
    SSD --> blend
    
    subgraph "Material Data"
        uniforms["uniform cache"]
        next_pass["next_pass<br/>(multi-pass)"]
        priority["priority<br/>(render order)"]
    end
    
    SMD --> uniforms
    SMD --> next_pass
    SMD --> priority
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/storage/material_storage.h](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:216-329]()

### Shader Specialization

The GLES3 scene shader uses specialization constants to enable/disable features at compile time:

| Specialization | Purpose |
|----------------|---------|
| `DISABLE_LIGHTMAP` | Remove lightmap support |
| `DISABLE_LIGHT_DIRECTIONAL/OMNI/SPOT` | Remove specific light types |
| `USE_RADIANCE_MAP` | Enable environment reflections |
| `RENDER_SHADOWS` | Shadow rendering pass |
| `SHADOW_MODE_PCF_5/PCF_13` | Shadow filtering quality |
| `LIGHT_USE_PSSM2/PSSM4` | Directional shadow splits |
| `USE_ADDITIVE_LIGHTING` | Additive light pass |
| `ADDITIVE_OMNI/ADDITIVE_SPOT` | Specific light in additive pass |

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/shaders/scene.glsl:9-42]()

### Surface Flag System

Each `GeometryInstanceSurface` has flags determining which passes it participates in:

```cpp
enum {
    FLAG_PASS_DEPTH = 1,
    FLAG_PASS_OPAQUE = 2,
    FLAG_PASS_ALPHA = 4,
    FLAG_PASS_SHADOW = 8,
    FLAG_USES_SHARED_SHADOW_MATERIAL = 128,
    FLAG_USES_SCREEN_TEXTURE = 2048,
    FLAG_USES_DEPTH_TEXTURE = 4096,
    FLAG_USES_NORMAL_TEXTURE = 8192,
    FLAG_USES_DOUBLE_SIDED_SHADOWS = 16384,
    FLAG_USES_STENCIL = 32768,
};
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:240-251](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:224-268]()

```mermaid
graph LR

        position["position[3]<br/>inv_radius"]
        direction["direction[3]<br/>size"]
        color["color[3]<br/>attenuation"]
```

```mermaid
graph LR

    end
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:177-210]()

### Light Collection and Sorting

The `_setup_lights()` function collects lights from the scene and sorts them by distance for optimal quality:

```mermaid
graph TD
    setup["_setup_lights()"]
    
    collect_dir["Collect directional lights<br/>(max 8)"]
    collect_omni["Collect omni lights<br/>(sort by distance)"]
    collect_spot["Collect spot lights<br/>(sort by distance)"]
    
    upload_dir["Upload to directional_light_buffer"]
    upload_omni["Upload to omni_light_buffer"]
    upload_spot["Upload to spot_light_buffer"]

    setup --> collect_omni
    setup --> collect_spot

    collect_omni --> upload_omni
    collect_spot --> upload_spot
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:1900-2100]()

### Light Pairing

Geometry instances are paired with nearby lights during culling. The pairing information is stored per-instance:

| Field | Type | Purpose |
|-------|------|---------|
| `paired_omni_lights` | `LocalVector<RID>` | Omni lights affecting this instance |
| `paired_spot_lights` | `LocalVector<RID>` | Spot lights affecting this instance |
| `omni_light_gl_cache` | `LocalVector<uint32_t>` | Indices into uniform buffer |
| `spot_light_gl_cache` | `LocalVector<uint32_t>` | Indices into uniform buffer |

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:323-328](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:93-117]()

## Shadow Rendering

### Shadow Atlas and Maps

The GLES3 backend supports both positional (omni/spot) and directional shadows.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Positional Shadows"
        atlas["Shadow Atlas<br/>(2D texture array)"]
        omni_cube["Omni: 6 faces<br/>(cubemap)"]
        spot_single["Spot: 1 face<br/>(2D projection)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Directional Shadows"
        dir_atlas["Directional Atlas<br/>(separate texture)"]
        pssm["PSSM splits<br/>(2 or 4 cascades)"]
    end
    
    atlas --> omni_cube
    atlas --> spot_single
    dir_atlas --> pssm
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:212-234]()

### Shadow Data Structures

**Positional Shadow Data:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `shadow_matrix[16]` | float | View-projection matrix for shadow |
| `light_position[3]` | float | Light world position |
| `shadow_normal_bias` | float | Normal offset to reduce acne |
| `shadow_atlas_pixel_size` | float | Texel size for PCF |

**Directional Shadow Data:**

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `shadow_matrices[4][16]` | float | Matrices for up to 4 PSSM splits |
| `shadow_split_offsets[4]` | float | Distance ranges for each split |
| `shadow_normal_bias[4]` | float | Per-split normal bias |
| `fade_from` / `fade_to` | float | Shadow fade distances |

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:212-234]()

### Shadow Rendering Pass

The shadow rendering process uses a specialized render path:

```mermaid
graph TD
    render_shadows["_render_shadows()"]
    
    iter_lights["Iterate shadow-casting lights"]
    setup_fb["Bind shadow framebuffer"]
    clear["Clear depth buffer"]
    
    fill_list["_fill_render_list()<br/>(PASS_MODE_SHADOW)"]
    render["_render_list_template()<br/>(shadow geometry)"]
    
    render_shadows --> iter_lights
    iter_lights --> setup_fb
    setup_fb --> clear
    clear --> fill_list
    fill_list --> render
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:2400-2600]()

### Shadow Shader Specializations

Shadow passes use specialized shader variants:

- `RENDER_SHADOWS`: Standard depth-only rendering
- `RENDER_SHADOWS_LINEAR`: Linear depth for omni lights (distance from light)
- Shadow-specific vertex transformations to handle normal bias in vertex shader

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/shaders/scene.glsl:57-61](), [drivers/gles3/shaders/scene.glsl:756-798]()

### Sky Rendering Pipeline

Sky rendering occurs after the opaque pass but before transparent objects:

```mermaid
graph TD
    setup_sky["_setup_sky()<br/>(prepare uniforms)"]
    
    check_dirty["Check if radiance needs update"]
    update_radiance["_update_sky_radiance()<br/>(render to cubemap faces)"]

    check_dirty --> draw_sky
    update_radiance --> draw_sky
    
    draw_sky --> bind_shader
    bind_shader --> set_uniforms
    set_uniforms --> bind_radiance

```

### Sky Uniform Locations

The sky shader uses a separate set of uniform binding locations to avoid conflicts with scene rendering:

| Uniform Location | Purpose |
|------------------|---------|
| `SKY_TONEMAP_UNIFORM_LOCATION` | Tonemapping parameters |
| `SKY_GLOBALS_UNIFORM_LOCATION` | Global shader uniforms |
| `SKY_MATERIAL_UNIFORM_LOCATION` | Sky material parameters |
| `SKY_DIRECTIONAL_LIGHT_UNIFORM_LOCATION` | Directional lights for sky |
| `SKY_MULTIVIEW_UNIFORM_LOCATION` | Stereo/XR projection matrices |

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:81-96]()

## Vertex and Fragment Shader Processing

### Vertex Shader Inputs

The GLES3 scene shader receives vertex data in a packed format to minimize bandwidth:

| Location | Attribute | Format | Contents |
|----------|-----------|--------|----------|
| 0 | `vertex_angle_attrib` | vec4 | Position (xyz) + tangent angle (w) |
| 1 | `axis_tangent_attrib` | vec4 | Normal/axis (xy octahedral) + tangent (zw) |
| 3 | `color_attrib` | vec4 | Vertex color (RGBA) |
| 4 | `uv_attrib` | vec2 | UV coordinates |
| 5 | `uv2_attrib` | vec2 | UV2 for lightmaps |

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/shaders/scene.glsl:78-116]()

### Octahedral Normal Compression

Normals and tangents use octahedral compression to save memory:

```mermaid
graph LR
    compressed["Octahedral vec2<br/>(RG16)"]
    decode["oct_to_vec3()"]
    normal["Normal vec3<br/>(normalized)"]
    
    compressed --> decode
    decode --> normal
```

The `oct_to_vec3()` function reconstructs a unit vector from a 2D octahedral encoding:

```glsl
vec3 oct_to_vec3(vec2 e) {
    vec3 v = vec3(e.xy, 1.0 - abs(e.x) - abs(e.y));
    float t = max(-v.z, 0.0);
    v.xy += t * -sign(v.xy);
    return normalize(v);
}
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/shaders/scene.glsl:142-147]()

### Fragment Shader Lighting

The fragment shader implements a full PBR lighting model with support for multiple light types:

```mermaid
graph TD
    fragment["Fragment Shader Entry"]
    
    material["Calculate material properties<br/>(albedo, metallic, roughness)"]
    
    ambient["Apply ambient lighting<br/>(ambient_light, IBL)"]
    
    dir_lights["Process directional lights<br/>(loop over directional_lights)"]
    omni_lights["Process omni lights<br/>(loop over omni_light_indices)"]
    spot_lights["Process spot lights<br/>(loop over spot_light_indices)"]
    
    shadows["Apply shadows<br/>(sample shadow maps)"]
    
    fog["Apply fog<br/>(depth and height fog)"]
    
    output["Output final color"]
    
    fragment --> material
    material --> ambient
    ambient --> dir_lights
    dir_lights --> omni_lights
    omni_lights --> spot_lights
    spot_lights --> shadows
    shadows --> fog
    fog --> output
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/shaders/scene.glsl:1000-2000]()

---

## OpenGL State Management

### State Caching

To minimize expensive OpenGL state changes, `SceneState` maintains cached state values:

| Cached State | GL Function | Cache Variable |
|--------------|-------------|----------------|
| Blend enabled | `glEnable(GL_BLEND)` | `current_blend_enabled` |
| Depth write | `glDepthMask()` | `current_depth_draw_enabled` |
| Depth test | `glEnable(GL_DEPTH_TEST)` | `current_depth_test_enabled` |
| Depth function | `glDepthFunc()` | `current_depth_function` |
| Cull mode | `glCullFace()` | `cull_mode` |
| Scissor test | `glEnable(GL_SCISSOR_TEST)` | `current_scissor_test_enabled` |
| Stencil test | `glEnable(GL_STENCIL_TEST)` | `current_stencil_test_enabled` |

State is only changed when necessary by comparing against cached values:

```cpp
void enable_gl_blend(bool p_enabled) {
    if (current_blend_enabled != p_enabled) {
        if (p_enabled) {
            glEnable(GL_BLEND);
        } else {
            glDisable(GL_BLEND);
        }
        current_blend_enabled = p_enabled;
    }
}
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:488-622]()

### Uniform Buffer Management

Uniform buffers are updated using a helper function that avoids redundant uploads:

```mermaid
graph LR
    update["_update_scene_ubo()"]
    
    check["Compare with<br/>previous data"]
    upload["glBufferData()<br/>(upload to GPU)"]
    cache["Update cache"]
    
    update --> check
    check -->|changed| upload
    upload --> cache
    check -->|unchanged| cache
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:1700-1750]()

---

## Performance Optimizations

### Shared Shadow Materials

To reduce draw calls and state changes, opaque geometry can use a shared shadow material when its vertex shader doesn't modify positions:

Conditions for shared shadow material:
- No particle trails (`!uses_particle_trails`)
- No vertex shader position modification (`!writes_modelview_or_projection`)
- No vertex displacement (`!uses_vertex`)
- No alpha discard (`!uses_discard && !uses_alpha_clip`)
- No world coordinate usage (`!uses_world_coordinates`)
- Not wireframe (`!wireframe`)

When these conditions are met, `FLAG_USES_SHARED_SHADOW_MATERIAL` is set.

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:270-284]()

### Instance Data Flags

Instance data is packed with flags to enable efficient shader branching:

| Flag | Value | Purpose |
|------|-------|---------|
| `INSTANCE_DATA_FLAG_MULTIMESH` | 1 << 12 | MultiMesh instance |
| `INSTANCE_DATA_FLAG_MULTIMESH_FORMAT_2D` | 1 << 13 | 2D transform format |
| `INSTANCE_DATA_FLAG_MULTIMESH_HAS_COLOR` | 1 << 14 | Has per-instance color |
| `INSTANCE_DATA_FLAG_MULTIMESH_HAS_CUSTOM_DATA` | 1 << 15 | Has custom data |
| `INSTANCE_DATA_FLAG_PARTICLES` | 1 << 11 | Particle system |
| `INSTANCE_DATA_FLAG_USE_LIGHTMAP` | 1 << 8 | Uses lightmap |

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:362-375](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:469-502]()

### Geometry Instance Dirty List

Geometry instances that need updating are added to a dirty list to batch updates efficiently:

```mermaid
graph LR
    modify["Modify instance<br/>(material, transform, etc)"]
    mark["_mark_dirty()"]
    add["Add to dirty_list"]
    
    update["_update_dirty_geometry_instances()"]
    process["Process all dirty instances"]
    clear["Clear dirty list"]
    
    modify --> mark
    mark --> add
    
    update --> process
    process --> clear
```

**Sources:** [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:341](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:140-157](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:183-187]()20:T5fa0,# Material and Shader System

## Purpose and Scope

The Material and Shader System defines how surface appearance properties are represented, compiled, and applied during rendering. This system encompasses material resource classes, shader compilation, material data structures used by rendering backends, and the integration of materials into the rendering pipeline.

This page focuses on the material resource layer and shader generation. For information about the rendering pipeline that consumes materials, see [Rendering Server Architecture](#3.1). For shader language parsing and compilation in custom shaders, see [Scripting System](#6).

---

## System Architecture Overview

The material system operates at three distinct levels: **Resource Layer** (user-facing material and shader resources), **Compilation Layer** (shader code generation), and **Backend Layer** (rendering-backend-specific material data).

**Material System Architecture**

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Resource Layer"
        Material["Material<br/>(base class)"]
        ShaderMaterial["ShaderMaterial"]
        BaseMaterial3D["BaseMaterial3D"]
        StandardMaterial3D["StandardMaterial3D"]
        ORMMaterial3D["ORMMaterial3D"]
        Shader["Shader<br/>(resource)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Compilation Layer"
        ShaderGen["BaseMaterial3D::_update_shader()"]
        ShaderMap["BaseMaterial3D::shader_map"]
        MaterialKey["BaseMaterial3D::MaterialKey"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Backend Layer - GLES3"
        SceneMaterialData["GLES3::SceneMaterialData"]
        SceneShaderData["GLES3::SceneShaderData"]
        MaterialStorage["GLES3::MaterialStorage"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Rendering Integration"
        GeometryInstance["GeometryInstanceGLES3"]
        GeometrySurface["GeometryInstanceSurface"]
        RenderList["RenderList"]
    end
    
    Material -->|"get_rid()"| RenderingServer["RenderingServer (RID)"]
    ShaderMaterial -->|extends| Material
    BaseMaterial3D -->|extends| Material
    StandardMaterial3D -->|extends| BaseMaterial3D
    ORMMaterial3D -->|extends| BaseMaterial3D
    
    ShaderMaterial -->|references| Shader
    
    BaseMaterial3D -->|"_update_shader()"| ShaderGen
    ShaderGen -->|"_compute_key()"| MaterialKey
    MaterialKey -->|"shader_map lookup"| ShaderMap
    ShaderGen -->|"generates code"| Shader
    
    Material -->|"material RID"| MaterialStorage
    MaterialStorage -->|creates| SceneMaterialData
    SceneMaterialData -->|references| SceneShaderData
    
    GeometrySurface -->|material| SceneMaterialData
    GeometrySurface -->|shader| SceneShaderData
    GeometrySurface -->|added to| RenderList
```

Sources: [scene/resources/material.h:38-93](), [scene/resources/material.cpp:183-192](), [scene/resources/material.h:140-888](), [drivers/gles3/storage/material_storage.h](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:236-293]()

## Material Resource Hierarchy

### Base Material Class

The `Material` class serves as the abstract base for all materials. Each material owns a `RID` that references the material in the `RenderingServer`.

**Material Base Class Structure**

```mermaid
classDiagram
    class Material {
        -RID material
        -Ref~Material~ next_pass
        -int render_priority
        -int init_state
        +set_next_pass()
        +get_rid()
        +_mark_initialized()
    }
    
    class ShaderMaterial {
        -Ref~Shader~ shader
        -HashMap param_cache
        -HashMap remap_cache
        +set_shader()
        +set_shader_parameter()
        +get_shader_parameter()
        -_check_material_rid()
    }
    
    class BaseMaterial3D {
        -MaterialKey current_key
        -RID shader_rid
        -HashMap~MaterialKey, ShaderData~ shader_map
        -Color albedo
        -float metallic
        -float roughness
        -Ref~Texture2D~ textures[]
        +_update_shader()
        +_compute_key()
    }
    
    class StandardMaterial3D {
    }
    
    class ORMMaterial3D {
    }
    
    Material <|-- ShaderMaterial
    Material <|-- BaseMaterial3D
    BaseMaterial3D <|-- StandardMaterial3D
    BaseMaterial3D <|-- ORMMaterial3D
```

**Key Properties:**
- `material`: RID identifying the material in RenderingServer
- `next_pass`: Allows chaining materials for multi-pass rendering
- `render_priority`: Controls rendering order (range: -128 to 127)
- `init_state`: Tracks initialization state during resource loading

Sources: [scene/resources/material.h:38-93](), [scene/resources/material.cpp:44-192]()

### ShaderMaterial

`ShaderMaterial` provides direct access to custom shaders. It stores shader parameters in a cache and supports dynamic shader assignment.

**Parameter Management:**

| Mechanism | Purpose |
|-----------|---------|
| `param_cache` | Stores parameter name â†’ value mappings |
| `remap_cache` | Maps property names to parameter names |
| `_check_material_rid()` | Lazy initialization of material RID |
| `set_shader_parameter()` | Updates parameter via RenderingServer |

The material RID is created lazily on first access to support efficient resource loading:

```
ShaderMaterial::get_rid()
  â””â”€> _check_material_rid()
      â””â”€> RS::material_create_from_shader() [if not created]
          â””â”€> For each param in param_cache:
              â””â”€> RS::material_set_param()
```

Sources: [scene/resources/material.h:95-136](), [scene/resources/material.cpp:196-583]()

### BaseMaterial3D

`BaseMaterial3D` is the foundation for `StandardMaterial3D` and `ORMMaterial3D`. It automatically generates shader code based on enabled features and property values.

**Material Features:**

| Feature | Enum | Description |
|---------|------|-------------|
| Emission | `FEATURE_EMISSION` | Emissive lighting |
| Normal Mapping | `FEATURE_NORMAL_MAPPING` | Per-pixel normals |
| Rim | `FEATURE_RIM` | Edge lighting effect |
| Clearcoat | `FEATURE_CLEARCOAT` | Dual-layer specular |
| Anisotropy | `FEATURE_ANISOTROPY` | Directional reflections |
| Ambient Occlusion | `FEATURE_AMBIENT_OCCLUSION` | Occlusion darkening |
| Height Mapping | `FEATURE_HEIGHT_MAPPING` | Parallax/displacement |
| Subsurface Scattering | `FEATURE_SUBSURFACE_SCATTERING` | Light penetration |
| Refraction | `FEATURE_REFRACTION` | Transparency distortion |
| Detail | `FEATURE_DETAIL` | Secondary texture layer |

Sources: [scene/resources/material.h:140-888](), [doc/classes/BaseMaterial3D.xml:1-58]()

---

## Shader Code Generation

### MaterialKey System

`BaseMaterial3D` uses a `MaterialKey` to uniquely identify shader variants. The key encodes all material properties that affect shader compilation.

**MaterialKey Structure**

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "MaterialKey (128 bits)"
        Enums["Enums<br/>texture_filter<br/>transparency<br/>blend_mode<br/>cull_mode<br/>etc."]
        Booleans["Booleans<br/>deep_parallax<br/>grow<br/>proximity_fade<br/>orm"]
        FeatureMask["feature_mask<br/>(32 bits)"]
        FlagMask["flags<br/>(32 bits)"]
    end
    
    MaterialKey["MaterialKey"] --> Enums
    MaterialKey --> Booleans
    MaterialKey --> FeatureMask
    MaterialKey --> FlagMask
    
    ComputeKey["_compute_key()"] -->|generates| MaterialKey
    MaterialKey -->|"hash()"| ShaderMapLookup["shader_map lookup"]
```

The `MaterialKey` is computed from material properties and used to deduplicate shaders across materials with identical configurations.

Sources: [scene/resources/material.h:358-408](), [scene/resources/material.h:420-462]()

### Shader Generation Process

When a material's properties change, `_update_shader()` generates GLSL code based on the enabled features.

**Shader Generation Flow**

```mermaid
graph TD
    PropertyChange["Material Property Changed"] --> QueueShaderChange["_queue_shader_change()"]
    QueueShaderChange --> AddToDirtyList["Add to dirty_materials list"]
    
    FlushChanges["BaseMaterial3D::flush_changes()"] --> UpdateLoop["For each dirty material"]
    UpdateLoop --> UpdateShader["_update_shader()"]
    
    UpdateShader --> ComputeKey["_compute_key()"]
    ComputeKey --> CheckMap["Check shader_map"]
    
    CheckMap -->|found| ReuseShader["Reuse existing shader<br/>Increment users count"]
    CheckMap -->|not found| GenerateCode["Generate shader code"]
    
    GenerateCode --> BuildCode["Build GLSL string<br/>- Add render_mode<br/>- Add texture samplers<br/>- Add uniforms<br/>- Add vertex/fragment logic"]
    
    BuildCode --> CreateShader["RS::shader_create()"]
    CreateShader --> StoreInMap["Store in shader_map"]
    StoreInMap --> SetMaterial["RS::material_set_shader()"]
    
    ReuseShader --> SetMaterial
```

**Code Generation Example (Simplified):**

The shader code starts with type and render modes:
```glsl
shader_type spatial;
render_mode blend_mix, depth_draw_opaque, cull_back, diffuse_burley, specular_schlick_ggx;
```

Then adds texture samplers based on enabled features:
```glsl
uniform sampler2D texture_albedo : hint_default_white, filter_linear_mipmap, repeat_enable;
uniform sampler2D texture_normal : hint_roughness_normal, filter_linear_mipmap, repeat_enable;
```

Sources: [scene/resources/material.cpp:689-1724](), [scene/resources/material.h:529-531]()

### Shader Map and Deduplication

The `shader_map` is a static hash map shared across all `BaseMaterial3D` instances. It maps `MaterialKey` to `ShaderData`.

**ShaderData Structure:**

| Field | Type | Purpose |
|-------|------|---------|
| `shader` | RID | Shader resource identifier |
| `users` | int | Reference count |

When a material's key changes, the old shader's user count is decremented. If it reaches zero, the shader is freed. The new shader (or existing matching shader) has its user count incremented.

```
Material A (key=K1) â”€â”€â”
Material B (key=K1) â”€â”€â”¼â”€â”€> shader_map[K1] = {shader: RID_X, users: 3}
Material C (key=K1) â”€â”€â”˜

Material D (key=K2) â”€â”€â”€â”€> shader_map[K2] = {shader: RID_Y, users: 1}
```

Sources: [scene/resources/material.h:410-418](), [scene/resources/material.cpp:699-725]()

---

## Material Data in Rendering Backends

### Backend Material Data Classes

Each rendering backend (RenderingDevice-based, GLES3) defines material data classes that store compiled shader information and runtime state.

**GLES3 Material Data Structure**

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "GLES3 Backend"
        SceneMaterialData["GLES3::SceneMaterialData"]
        SceneShaderData["GLES3::SceneShaderData"]
        SkyMaterialData["GLES3::SkyMaterialData"]
        SkyShaderData["GLES3::SkyShaderData"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Material Storage"
        MaterialStorage["GLES3::MaterialStorage"]
        ShaderMap["material_shader_data_cache"]
    end
    
    MaterialRID["Material RID"] --> MaterialStorage
    MaterialStorage -->|"material_get_data()"| SceneMaterialData
    SceneMaterialData -->|references| SceneShaderData
    
    SceneShaderData -->|contains| ShaderVersion["Shader version RID"]
    SceneShaderData -->|contains| ShaderFlags["Feature flags<br/>uses_alpha<br/>uses_screen_texture<br/>uses_vertex<br/>etc."]
    
    ShaderMap -->|caches| SceneShaderData
```

**SceneMaterialData fields:**

| Field | Purpose |
|-------|---------|
| `shader_data` | Pointer to compiled shader data |
| `next_pass` | RID of next-pass material |
| `priority` | Render priority value |
| `uniform_set_updated` | Tracks parameter changes |

**SceneShaderData fields:**

| Field | Purpose |
|-------|---------|
| `version` | Shader program version |
| `valid` | Compilation success flag |
| `uses_alpha` | Requires alpha blending |
| `uses_screen_texture` | Needs screen copy |
| `uses_vertex` | Has vertex shader code |
| `depth_draw` | Depth write mode |
| `depth_test` | Depth test mode |
| `stencil_enabled` | Uses stencil buffer |

Sources: [drivers/gles3/storage/material_storage.h](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:216-329]()

### Material Assignment to Geometry

Materials are assigned to geometry instances through `GeometryInstanceSurface` structures.

**Material to Geometry Flow**

```mermaid
graph TB
    MeshResource["Mesh Resource"] -->|"has surfaces"| SurfaceMaterials["Surface materials array"]
    GeometryInstance["GeometryInstanceGLES3"] -->|"material_override"| MaterialOverride
    GeometryInstance -->|"material_overlay"| MaterialOverlay
    
    UpdateGeometry["_geometry_instance_update()"] -->|"for each surface"| AddSurface["_geometry_instance_add_surface()"]
    
    AddSurface --> SelectMaterial["Select material:<br/>1. material_override<br/>2. surface material<br/>3. default_material"]
    
    SelectMaterial --> GetMaterialData["MaterialStorage::material_get_data()"]
    GetMaterialData --> CreateSurfaceCache["Create GeometryInstanceSurface"]
    
    CreateSurfaceCache --> SetSurfaceFields["Set fields:<br/>- shader<br/>- material<br/>- surface (mesh data)<br/>- flags<br/>- sort key"]
    
    SetSurfaceFields --> HandleNextPass["Handle next_pass chain"]
    HandleNextPass --> HandleOverlay["Handle material_overlay"]
    
    HandleOverlay --> LinkToInstance["Link to instance:<br/>surface->next = instance->surface_caches"]
```

Each `GeometryInstanceSurface` contains:
- `shader`: Pointer to `SceneShaderData`
- `material`: Pointer to `SceneMaterialData`
- `surface`: Pointer to mesh surface data
- `flags`: Rendering flags (pass type, features used)
- `sort`: 128-bit sort key for render ordering

Sources: [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:216-390](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:236-293]()

---

## Material Rendering Pipeline

### Surface Flags and Pass Assignment

The material system determines which rendering passes a surface participates in based on shader properties.

**Pass Determination Logic**

```mermaid
graph TD
    CheckAlpha["has_alpha = uses_alpha || uses_blend_alpha"]
    CheckDepthDisabled["depth_draw == DISABLED || depth_test != ENABLED"]
    
    Start["Analyze material shader data"] --> CheckAlpha
    CheckAlpha --> CheckDepthDisabled
    
    CheckDepthDisabled -->|"alpha || depth disabled"| AlphaPass["FLAG_PASS_ALPHA"]
    CheckDepthDisabled -->|else| OpaquePass["FLAG_PASS_OPAQUE<br/>FLAG_PASS_DEPTH<br/>FLAG_PASS_SHADOW"]
    
    AlphaPass --> CheckDepthPrepass["uses_depth_prepass_alpha?"]
    CheckDepthPrepass -->|yes| AddDepthShadow["Add FLAG_PASS_DEPTH<br/>Add FLAG_PASS_SHADOW"]
    CheckDepthPrepass -->|no| SkipDepth["Skip depth/shadow passes"]
    
    AddDepthShadow --> CheckScreenTextures["Check screen texture usage"]
    SkipDepth --> CheckScreenTextures
    OpaquePass --> CheckScreenTextures
    
    CheckScreenTextures --> SetFlags["Set additional flags:<br/>FLAG_USES_SCREEN_TEXTURE<br/>FLAG_USES_DEPTH_TEXTURE<br/>FLAG_USES_NORMAL_TEXTURE<br/>FLAG_USES_STENCIL"]
```

The flags control which render lists receive the surface:
- `FLAG_PASS_OPAQUE` â†’ `RENDER_LIST_OPAQUE`
- `FLAG_PASS_ALPHA` â†’ `RENDER_LIST_ALPHA`
- `FLAG_PASS_SHADOW` â†’ `RENDER_LIST_SECONDARY` (during shadow passes)

Sources: [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:219-268]()

### Sort Key Generation

Each surface receives a 128-bit sort key for efficient rendering order.

**Sort Key Fields:**

| Bits | Field | Purpose |
|------|-------|---------|
| 0-7 | `lod_index` | Level of detail |
| 8-15 | `surface_index` | Surface index within mesh |
| 16-47 | `geometry_id` | Mesh RID local index |
| 48-63 | `material_id_low` | Material RID low bits |
| 0-15 | `material_id_hi` | Material RID high bits |
| 16-47 | `shader_id` | Shader RID local index |
| 56-63 | `priority` | Material render priority |

Opaque surfaces sort by shader/material to minimize state changes. Alpha surfaces sort by depth for correct blending.

Sources: [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:311-322](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:252-273]()

---

## Advanced Material Features

### Next Pass Materials

Materials support chaining via the `next_pass` property, enabling multi-pass effects like outlines or special rendering modes.

**Next Pass Chain Structure**

```mermaid
graph LR
    Surface["Geometry Surface"] --> Material1["Primary Material<br/>(e.g., standard PBR)"]
    Material1 -->|next_pass| Material2["Secondary Material<br/>(e.g., outline)"]
    Material2 -->|next_pass| Material3["Tertiary Material<br/>(optional)"]
    
    Material1 -.->|creates| Surface1["GeometryInstanceSurface #1"]
    Material2 -.->|creates| Surface2["GeometryInstanceSurface #2"]
    Material3 -.->|creates| Surface3["GeometryInstanceSurface #3"]
    
    Surface1 --> RenderList["Render Lists"]
    Surface2 --> RenderList
    Surface3 --> RenderList
```

The `_geometry_instance_add_surface_with_material_chain()` function iterates through the chain, creating a separate `GeometryInstanceSurface` for each pass.

**Typical next_pass use case:**
1. Base material renders object normally
2. Next-pass material with `cull_mode = CULL_FRONT` and vertex grow renders outline

Sources: [scene/resources/material.cpp:44-63](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:331-348]()

### Material Override and Overlay

`GeometryInstance` supports material override and overlay:

| Property | Priority | Behavior |
|----------|----------|----------|
| `material_override` | Highest | Replaces all surface materials |
| Surface materials | Default | Per-surface assignment |
| `material_overlay` | Additive | Rendered after surface material |

The override uses the `next_pass` chain from the override material. The overlay adds its `next_pass` chain after processing the base material.

```
Override exists?
  Yes: Use override (+ its next_pass chain)
  No:  Use surface material (+ its next_pass chain)

Overlay exists?
  Yes: Add overlay (+ its next_pass chain) after above
```

Sources: [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:350-389]()

### Render Priority

Materials can specify a render priority in the range [-128, 127]. Higher priority values render later (on top).

**Priority Sorting:**

Opaque objects primarily sort by shader/material for efficiency, but priority acts as a tie-breaker. Alpha objects sort by depth first, then priority, allowing depth-correct transparency with manual ordering when needed.

The priority is stored in the sort key's highest 8 bits for alpha surfaces and affects the `SortByReverseDepthAndPriority` comparator.

Sources: [scene/resources/material.cpp:69-82](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.h:705-715]()

### Shadow Material Optimization

Materials automatically use a simplified shadow-only material when possible to reduce rendering overhead during shadow passes.

**Shadow Material Selection:**

```mermaid
graph TD
    CheckFeatures["Check shader features:<br/>- particle_trails<br/>- writes_modelview_or_projection<br/>- uses_vertex<br/>- uses_discard<br/>- uses_depth_prepass_alpha<br/>- uses_alpha_clip<br/>- uses_world_coordinates<br/>- wireframe"]
    
    CheckFeatures -->|"All false"| UseShared["Use shared shadow material:<br/>scene_globals.default_material"]
    CheckFeatures -->|"Any true"| UseOriginal["Use original material"]
    
    UseShared --> GetShadowMesh["Get shadow mesh variant<br/>(if available)"]
    GetShadowMesh --> SetShadowFields["Set shadow fields:<br/>shader_shadow<br/>material_shadow<br/>surface_shadow"]
    
    UseOriginal --> SetShadowSame["shadow fields = original fields"]
```

This optimization allows the majority of materials to share a single compiled shadow shader, reducing GPU state changes during shadow rendering.

Sources: [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:270-284](), [drivers/gles3/rasterizer_scene_gles3.cpp:300-304]()

---

## Material Property System

### BaseMaterial3D Properties

`BaseMaterial3D` exposes over 100 properties organized by feature. The property system uses `_material_set_param()` to communicate with the `RenderingServer`.

**Property to Shader Parameter Mapping:**

```mermaid
graph LR
    UserProperty["User sets property<br/>(e.g., set_albedo())"] --> QueueChange["_queue_shader_change()"]
    QueueChange --> SetParam["_material_set_param()"]
    
    SetParam --> CheckCache["Check pending_params"]
    CheckCache --> StoreParam["Store in pending_params<br/>if material not initialized"]
    
    CheckCache --> SendNow["Send immediately if initialized:<br/>RS::material_set_param()"]
    
    MaterialInit["Material initialization"] --> FlushPending["For each pending_params:<br/>RS::material_set_param()"]
```

**Texture Properties:**

Textures are handled specially through the `set_texture()` method, which uses a `TextureParam` enum to identify slots.

| TextureParam | Shader Uniform |
|--------------|----------------|
| `TEXTURE_ALBEDO` | `texture_albedo` |
| `TEXTURE_METALLIC` | `texture_metallic` |
| `TEXTURE_ROUGHNESS` | `texture_roughness` |
| `TEXTURE_NORMAL` | `texture_normal` |
| `TEXTURE_EMISSION` | `texture_emission` |
| `TEXTURE_ORM` | `texture_orm` |
| ... | ... |

Sources: [scene/resources/material.h:464-521](), [scene/resources/material.cpp:593-676]()

### ShaderMaterial Property System

`ShaderMaterial` uses a dynamic property system that adapts to the assigned shader's uniforms.

**Dynamic Property Discovery:**

```mermaid
graph TD
    GetPropertyList["_get_property_list()"] --> CheckShader["shader.is_valid()?"]
    CheckShader -->|no| ReturnEmpty["Return empty list"]
    CheckShader -->|yes| GetUniforms["shader->get_shader_uniform_list()"]
    
    GetUniforms --> ParseGroups["Parse group/subgroup hints"]
    ParseGroups --> BuildHierarchy["Build property hierarchy:<br/>- Groups (::)<br/>- Subgroups<br/>- Individual properties"]
    
    BuildHierarchy --> AddPrefix["Add 'shader_parameter/' prefix"]
    AddPrefix --> CheckCache["Check param_cache for value"]
    CheckCache --> ReturnList["Return property list"]
    
    UserSet["User sets property"] --> RemapCheck["Check remap_cache"]
    RemapCheck --> UpdateCache["Update param_cache"]
    UpdateCache --> SendToServer["RS::material_set_param()"]
```

This allows `ShaderMaterial` to expose any uniform defined in the shader as an editable property in the Inspector.

Sources: [scene/resources/material.cpp:246-389](), [scene/resources/material.cpp:452-492]()

## Shader Compilation Specialization

### GLES3 Scene Shader Specializations

The GLES3 scene shader uses specialization constants to generate shader variants efficiently.

**Specialization Constants:**

| Constant | Purpose |
|----------|---------|
| `DISABLE_LIGHTMAP` | Exclude lightmap code |
| `DISABLE_LIGHT_DIRECTIONAL` | Exclude directional lights |
| `DISABLE_LIGHT_OMNI` | Exclude omni lights |
| `DISABLE_LIGHT_SPOT` | Exclude spot lights |
| `USE_RADIANCE_MAP` | Include radiance cubemap |
| `RENDER_SHADOWS` | Shadow rendering mode |
| `BASE_PASS` | First geometry pass |
| `USE_ADDITIVE_LIGHTING` | Additive light pass |
| `ADDITIVE_OMNI` | Omni light type |
| `ADDITIVE_SPOT` | Spot light type |

These constants are set at draw time based on the rendering configuration, allowing a single shader to serve multiple purposes.

Sources: [drivers/gles3/shaders/scene.glsl:11-41]()

### Material Modes

The scene shader defines multiple rendering modes:

**Scene Shader Modes:**

```mermaid
graph LR
    SceneShader["scene.glsl"] --> ColorMode["mode_color<br/>(standard rendering)"]
    SceneShader --> ColorInstancing["mode_color_instancing<br/>(+ USE_INSTANCING)"]
    SceneShader --> DepthMode["mode_depth<br/>(MODE_RENDER_DEPTH)"]
    SceneShader --> DepthInstancing["mode_depth_instancing<br/>(depth + USE_INSTANCING)"]
    
    ColorMode --> BasePass["BASE_PASS variants"]
    ColorMode --> AdditivePass["USE_ADDITIVE_LIGHTING variants"]
    
    AdditivePass --> DirectionalAdditive["Directional light"]
    AdditivePass --> OmniAdditive["ADDITIVE_OMNI"]
    AdditivePass --> SpotAdditive["ADDITIVE_SPOT"]
```

Each mode represents a different shader compilation target used in specific rendering contexts.

Sources: [drivers/gles3/shaders/scene.glsl:1-8]()21:T5197,# Editor System

## Purpose and Scope

The Editor System encompasses the core infrastructure that implements the Godot editor application. This includes the central orchestration layer (`EditorNode`), plugin architecture (`EditorPlugin`), state management (`EditorData`), and public API (`EditorInterface`). The system coordinates all editor functionality including scene editing, asset management, inspector panels, and viewport editors.

For information about specific editor subsystems, see:
- Editor Core and State Management: [#4.1](#4.1)
- Editor Viewport Plugins (2D/3D editors): [#4.2](#4.2)
- Editor Docks (Scene Tree, File System): [#4.3](#4.3)
- Editor Settings and Debugging: [#4.4](#4.4)

## Core Architecture

### EditorNode: The Central Orchestrator

`EditorNode` is the singleton class that serves as the primary entry point and coordinator for all editor functionality. It inherits from `Node` and is added to the scene tree when the editor is running.

**Key Responsibilities:**

| Responsibility | Implementation |
|---------------|----------------|
| Scene management | Manages opened scenes via `EditorData`, scene tabs, save/load operations |
| Plugin coordination | Owns and delegates to `EditorPluginList`, manages plugin lifecycle |
| UI orchestration | Creates and manages docks, bottom panel, main screens, menu bars |
| Undo/redo system | Coordinates with `EditorUndoRedoManager` for history management |
| Resource operations | Handles resource saving, loading, and preview generation |
| Theme management | Generates and applies editor theme via `EditorThemeManager` |

**Singleton Access:**

```cpp
EditorNode *EditorNode::get_singleton()
```

The singleton is accessible throughout the editor codebase and provides access to all major subsystems.

**EditorNode Architecture**

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "EditorNode Singleton"
        EN[EditorNode<br/>editor_node.cpp:207]
        
        subgraph "Core State"
            ED[EditorData<br/>editor_data]
            EF[EditorFolding<br/>editor_folding]
            EH[EditorSelectionHistory<br/>editor_history]
        end
        
        subgraph "UI Components"
            GUI[gui_base<br/>Control]
            VBOX[main_vbox<br/>VBoxContainer]
            SPLIT[DockSplitContainer]
            TABS[EditorSceneTabs<br/>scene_tabs]
        end
        
        subgraph "Managers"
            EURM[EditorUndoRedoManager]
            EDM[EditorDockManager<br/>editor_dock_manager]
            EMS[EditorMainScreen<br/>editor_main_screen]
            EBP[EditorBottomPanel<br/>bottom_panel]
        end
        
        subgraph "Plugins"
            EPL[EditorPluginList]
            PLUGINS[Vector_EditorPlugin_<br/>editor_plugins]
            ADDON[HashMap addon_name_to_plugin]
        end
    end
    
    EN --> ED
    EN --> EF
    EN --> EH
    EN --> GUI
    EN --> EURM
    EN --> EDM
    EN --> EMS
    EN --> EBP
    EN --> EPL
    EN --> PLUGINS
    EN --> ADDON
    
    GUI --> VBOX
    VBOX --> SPLIT
    VBOX --> TABS
```

Sources: [editor/editor_node.h:120-877](), [editor/editor_node.cpp:1-3500]()

### EditorData: State Management

`EditorData` manages the state of all opened scenes, edited resources, editor plugins, and custom types. It maintains the authoritative record of what is currently being edited.

**Core Data Structures:**

| Structure | Purpose |
|-----------|---------|
| `Vector<EditedScene> edited_scene` | All currently opened scenes with their state |
| `int current_edited_scene` | Index of the active scene tab |
| `Vector<EditorPlugin*> editor_plugins` | All registered editor plugins |
| `HashMap<String, Vector<CustomType>> custom_types` | User-defined node types |
| `List<PropertyData> clipboard` | Property clipboard for copy/paste |

**EditedScene Structure:**

```cpp
struct EditedScene {
    Node *root;                    // Root node of the scene
    String path;                   // File path
    uint64_t file_modified_time;   // Last modification timestamp
    Dictionary editor_states;      // Plugin-specific editor state
    List<Node*> selection;         // Currently selected nodes
    int history_id;                // Undo/redo history identifier
    NodePath live_edit_root;       // Root for live editing
    // ...
}
```

**Scene and Plugin State Flow**

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "EditorData"
        ES[EditedScene<br/>edited_scene Vector]
        CUR[current_edited_scene<br/>int index]
        PLUG[editor_plugins<br/>Vector]
    end
    
    subgraph "Scene State"
        ROOT[Node* root]
        PATH[String path]
        SEL[List selection]
        STATES[Dictionary<br/>editor_states]
        HID[int history_id]
    end
    
    subgraph "Plugin System"
        EP1[EditorPlugin 1]
        EP2[EditorPlugin 2]
        EP3[EditorPlugin N]
    end
    
    ES --> ROOT
    ES --> PATH
    ES --> SEL
    ES --> STATES
    ES --> HID
    
    PLUG --> EP1
    PLUG --> EP2
    PLUG --> EP3
    
    EP1 -.get_state.-> STATES
    EP2 -.get_state.-> STATES
    EP3 -.get_state.-> STATES
    
    HID --> EURM[EditorUndoRedoManager]
```

Sources: [editor/editor_data.h:105-267](), [editor/editor_data.cpp:31-1200]()

### EditorInterface: Public API

`EditorInterface` provides a stable, controlled API for plugins and scripts to interact with the editor. It acts as a facade over `EditorNode` and other editor internals.

**Key API Categories:**

| Category | Methods | Purpose |
|----------|---------|---------|
| Scene Operations | `get_edited_scene_root()`, `edit_node()`, `open_scene_from_path()` | Access and modify current scene |
| Resource Operations | `edit_resource()`, `edit_script()`, `save_scene()` | Edit and save resources |
| Selection | `get_selection()`, `inspect_object()` | Query and modify selection |
| Editor Services | `get_resource_filesystem()`, `get_resource_previewer()` | Access editor subsystems |
| UI Access | `get_editor_main_screen()`, `get_base_control()`, `get_inspector()` | Access editor UI elements |
| Playback | `play_main_scene()`, `stop_playing_scene()`, `is_playing_scene()` | Control scene playback |

**EditorInterface as Facade**

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Public API"
        EI[EditorInterface<br/>Singleton]
    end
    
    subgraph "Editor Internals"
        EN[EditorNode::get_singleton]
        ED[EditorData]
        EFS[EditorFileSystem]
        ERP[EditorResourcePreview]
        ESEL[EditorSelection]
        ESET[EditorSettings]
        EURM[EditorUndoRedoManager]
    end
    
    subgraph "Clients"
        PLUGIN[EditorPlugin]
        SCRIPT[EditorScript]
        TOOL[Tool Scripts]
    end
    
    PLUGIN --> EI
    SCRIPT --> EI
    TOOL --> EI
    
    EI --> EN
    EI --> EFS
    EI --> ERP
    EI --> ESEL
    EI --> ESET
    EI --> EURM
    
    EN --> ED
```

Sources: [editor/editor_interface.h:61-213](), [editor/editor_interface.cpp:71-800]()

## Plugin System

The plugin system allows extending the editor with custom functionality. All editor features, including the built-in 2D and 3D editors, are implemented as plugins.

### EditorPlugin Base Class

`EditorPlugin` is the abstract base class for all editor plugins. Plugins can extend the editor in multiple ways:

**Plugin Extension Points:**

| Extension Point | Virtual Method | Purpose |
|----------------|----------------|---------|
| Main Screen | `_has_main_screen()`, `_make_visible()` | Add custom main screen tabs |
| Object Editing | `_handles()`, `_edit()` | Handle specific object types |
| Viewport Overlay | `_forward_3d_draw_over_viewport()`, `_forward_canvas_draw_over_viewport()` | Draw custom overlays |
| Input Handling | `_forward_3d_gui_input()`, `_forward_canvas_gui_input()` | Process viewport input |
| State Persistence | `_get_state()`, `_set_state()` | Save/restore plugin state |
| Lifecycle | `_enable_plugin()`, `_disable_plugin()` | Initialize/cleanup |

**Plugin Lifecycle**

```mermaid
graph TD
    START[Plugin Loaded] --> CONSTRUCT[Constructor Called]
    CONSTRUCT --> ENTER[_enter_tree called]
    ENTER --> ENABLE[_enable_plugin called]
    ENABLE --> READY[Plugin Ready]
    
    READY --> EDIT{Object to Edit?}
    EDIT -->|Yes| HANDLES[_handles called]
    HANDLES -->|true| EDITCALL[_edit called]
    HANDLES -->|false| READY
    EDITCALL --> VISIBLE[_make_visible called]
    VISIBLE --> READY
    
    READY --> SAVE{Scene/Project<br/>Saving?}
    SAVE -->|Yes| GETSTATE[_get_state called]
    GETSTATE --> APPLY[_apply_changes called]
    APPLY --> SAVEEXT[_save_external_data called]
    SAVEEXT --> READY
    SAVE -->|No| READY
    
    READY --> DISABLE{Disable<br/>Plugin?}
    DISABLE -->|Yes| DISABLECALL[_disable_plugin called]
    DISABLECALL --> EXIT[_exit_tree called]
    EXIT --> END[Plugin Unloaded]
    DISABLE -->|No| READY
```

Sources: [doc/classes/EditorPlugin.xml:1-800]()

### Plugin Registration and Management

Plugins are registered through `EditorNode` and managed by `EditorData`:

**Built-in Plugin Registration:**

[editor/editor_node.cpp:7800-8200]() shows how built-in plugins like `CanvasItemEditorPlugin` and `Node3DEditorPlugin` are registered during editor initialization.

**Addon Plugin Registration:**

Addons are registered via the project settings and loaded dynamically:

```cpp
// EditorNode manages addon loading
void EditorNode::set_addon_plugin_enabled(const String &p_addon, bool p_enabled, bool p_config_changed)
```

**Plugin State Storage:**

Each plugin's state is stored per-scene in `EditedScene::editor_states`:

```cpp
Dictionary EditorData::get_editor_plugin_states() const {
    Dictionary metadata;
    for (int i = 0; i < editor_plugins.size(); i++) {
        Dictionary state = editor_plugins[i]->get_state();
        if (state.is_empty()) continue;
        metadata[editor_plugins[i]->get_plugin_name()] = state;
    }
    return metadata;
}
```

Sources: [editor/editor_data.cpp:316-358](), [editor/editor_node.cpp:7800-8500]()


Sources: [editor/editor_node.h:268-287](), [editor/editor_data.h:129-176]()

## Editor Components

### Main Screen Editors

Main screen editors are plugins that appear in the top toolbar (2D, 3D, Script, etc.). They implement `_has_main_screen()` to return `true`.

**Main Screen Selection:**

```cpp
// EditorMainScreen manages visibility
class EditorMainScreen : public VBoxContainer {
    void select(int p_index);  // Switch active screen
    void select_next();        // Cycle to next screen
    void select_prev();        // Cycle to previous screen
}
```

When a main screen is selected:
1. Previous screen's `_make_visible(false)` is called
2. New screen's `_make_visible(true)` is called
3. The screen's UI control is shown in the editor main area

Sources: [editor/editor_main_screen.h:1-100]()

### Editor Docks

Docks are UI panels that appear around the viewport. Major docks include:

| Dock | Class | Purpose |
|------|-------|---------|
| Scene Tree | `SceneTreeDock` | Hierarchy editor, node operations |
| File System | `FileSystemDock` | Asset browser and file operations |
| Inspector | `InspectorDock` | Property editor for selected objects |
| Import | `ImportDock` | Import settings for assets |
| Node | `NodeDock` | Node-specific panels (signals, groups) |

**Dock Management:**

```cpp
class EditorDockManager {
    void add_dock(EditorDock *p_dock);
    void remove_dock(EditorDock *p_dock);
    void update_tab_styles();
    // Handles dock floating, layout saving/loading
}
```

**Dock Communication Pattern**

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "User Action"
        USER[User clicks node]
    end
    
    subgraph "Selection System"
        ESEL[EditorSelection]
        SIG[selection_changed<br/>signal]
    end
    
    subgraph "Responding Docks"
        STD[SceneTreeDock<br/>Updates tree highlight]
        INSP[InspectorDock<br/>Displays properties]
        NODE[NodeDock<br/>Shows signals/groups]
    end
    
    USER --> ESEL
    ESEL --> SIG
    SIG --> STD
    SIG --> INSP
    SIG --> NODE
```

Sources: [editor/docks/editor_dock_manager.h:1-150](), [editor/editor_node.cpp:58-64]()

### Editor Services

Services are singleton subsystems that provide specialized functionality:

**EditorFileSystem:**
- Scans project directory for assets
- Manages import metadata (`.import` files)
- Triggers resource reimport when source files change
- Provides file change notifications

**EditorResourcePreview:**
- Generates thumbnail previews for resources
- Caches previews for performance
- Extensible via `EditorResourcePreviewGenerator` plugins

**EditorSettings:**
- Stores editor preferences and configuration
- Per-project and global settings
- Used for editor behavior customization

**Editor Services Architecture**

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "EditorFileSystem"
        EFS[EditorFileSystem<br/>Singleton]
        SCAN[scan called<br/>on startup]
        FSCHANGED[sources_changed<br/>signal]
        REIMPORT[resources_reimported<br/>signal]
    end
    
    subgraph "EditorResourcePreview"
        ERP[EditorResourcePreview<br/>Singleton]
        QUEUE[queue_resource_preview]
        GEN[EditorResourcePreviewGenerator<br/>plugins]
        PREVIEW[preview_invalidated<br/>signal]
    end
    
    subgraph "EditorSettings"
        ESET[EditorSettings<br/>Singleton]
        PROPS[PropertyInfo list]
        NOTIFY[settings_changed<br/>signal]
    end
    
    subgraph "Consumers"
        FSD[FileSystemDock]
        EN[EditorNode]
        PLUGINS[EditorPlugins]
    end
    
    EFS --> SCAN
    SCAN --> FSCHANGED

    ERP --> QUEUE
```

Sources: [editor/file_system/editor_file_system.h:1-400](), [editor/inspector/editor_resource_preview.h:1-200](), [editor/settings/editor_settings.h:1-300]()

## State Management and Persistence

### Scene State Persistence

Each opened scene maintains its own state including:
- Editor plugin states (viewport camera position, grid settings, etc.)
- Node selection
- Undo/redo history
- Custom plugin data

**State Save Flow:**

```mermaid
graph TD
    TRIGGER[Scene tab change<br/>or save] --> SAVESTATE[_save_editor_states]
    SAVESTATE --> GETPLUGIN[get_editor_plugin_states]
    
    GETPLUGIN --> LOOP{For each plugin}
    LOOP --> GETSTATE[plugin.get_state]
    GETSTATE --> DICT[Add to Dictionary]
    DICT --> LOOP
    
    LOOP --> SAVEFILE[Save to .godot/editor/<br/>scene_file.editstate]
    
    SAVEFILE --> DONE[State Saved]
```

**State Restore Flow:**

When a scene tab is switched or reopened:
1. `_load_editor_plugin_states_from_config()` is called
2. Each plugin's `set_state(Dictionary)` is invoked
3. Plugin restores its viewport, selection, etc.

Sources: [editor/editor_node.cpp:5571-5620](), [editor/editor_data.cpp:316-383]()

### Global Editor Layout

The editor's dock layout, window positions, and open scenes are stored in:
- `editor_layout.cfg` - Dock positions, split sizes
- Recent scenes list
- Last opened project

**Layout Save/Load:**

```cpp
void EditorNode::_save_editor_layout() {
    Ref<ConfigFile> config;
    config.instantiate();
    
    // Save dock positions
    editor_dock_manager->save_layout(config);
    
    // Save plugin window layouts
    _get_window_layout(config);
    
    // Save open scenes
    _save_open_scenes_to_config(config);
    
    config->save(editor_layout_path);
}
```

Sources: [editor/editor_node.cpp:5660-5750]()

## Initialization Sequence

The editor initialization follows a specific sequence to ensure all systems are ready:

**Editor Startup Flow**

```mermaid
graph TD
    START[Main Entry Point<br/>main.cpp] --> OSSETUP[OS Setup]
    OSSETUP --> ENGINEINIT[Engine::setup]
    ENGINEINIT --> CREATEEDITOR[EditorNode created]
    
    CREATEEDITOR --> ENTREE[_enter_tree called]
    ENTREE --> BUILDUI[Build UI structure<br/>docks splits menus]
    BUILDUI --> REGISTERSERVICES[Register singletons<br/>FileSystem Settings Preview]
    
    REGISTERSERVICES --> REGPLUGINS[Register built-in plugins<br/>CanvasItemEditor Node3DEditor]
    REGPLUGINS --> LOADADDONS[Load addon plugins<br/>from project.godot]
    
    LOADADDONS --> ENABLEPLUGINS[Call _enable_plugin<br/>on all plugins]
    ENABLEPLUGINS --> FIRSTSCAN[Request first filesystem scan]
    
    FIRSTSCAN --> WAITINGSCAN{Waiting for<br/>scan complete?}
    WAITINGSCAN -->|Yes| SCANPROGRESS[Show progress dialog]
    SCANPROGRESS --> SCANDONE[Scan complete]
    SCANDONE --> LOADLAYOUT[Load editor_layout.cfg]
    
    LOADLAYOUT --> LOADSCENES[Restore open scenes]
    LOADSCENES --> RESTORESTATE[Restore plugin states]
    RESTORESTATE --> READY[Editor Ready]
    
    WAITINGSCAN -->|No| LOADLAYOUT
```

**Key Initialization Points:**

1. **`EditorNode::_enter_tree()`** [editor/editor_node.cpp:7600-7900]()
   - Creates UI hierarchy
   - Registers core services
   
2. **`EditorNode::_ready()`** [editor/editor_node.cpp:7900-8100]()
   - Builds main menu
   - Initializes theme
   
3. **`EditorNode::init_plugins()`** [editor/editor_node.cpp:8100-8300]()
   - Registers all built-in plugins
   - Loads addon plugins
   
4. **`EditorNode::_begin_first_scan()`** [editor/editor_node.cpp:3400-3450]()
   - Triggers initial file system scan
   - Shows progress UI if needed

Sources: [editor/editor_node.cpp:7600-8500](), [main/main.cpp:2500-2800]()

## Integration with Engine Core

The editor runs as a specialized mode of the Godot engine. Key integration points:

**Editor Detection:**

```cpp
bool Engine::is_editor_hint() const  // Returns true when editor is running
```

Scripts can check this to execute editor-only code paths.

**Scene Tree Integration:**

When the editor is running:
- `SceneTree::get_edited_scene_root()` returns the scene being edited
- The editor's UI is the main scene tree root
- The edited scene is placed in a `SubViewport` (`EditorNode::scene_root`)

**Display Server Integration:**

- Editor uses native windowing for multi-window support
- Custom title bar on some platforms
- Editor-specific mouse cursors and icons

**Editor-Specific Servers:**

Some servers have editor-specific features:
- `RenderingServer`: Editor-only debug draw modes
- `PhysicsServer`: Editor collision visualization
- `NavigationServer`: Editor navigation mesh visualization

Sources: [editor/editor_node.h:460](), [scene/main/scene_tree.h:100-150]()

---

This completes the overview of the Editor System. The modular plugin architecture allows the editor to be extended while maintaining a stable core. For implementation details of specific editor subsystems, refer to the child pages in this section.22:T5bee,# Editor Core: EditorNode and State Management

## Purpose and Scope

This document describes the core editor architecture centered around `EditorNode`, the singleton orchestrator that manages the entire editor lifecycle. It covers state management through `EditorData`, the public plugin API via `EditorInterface`, and selection tracking systems. For information about specific editor plugins (2D/3D editors, docks), see [4.2](#4.2) and [4.3](#4.3). For editor settings and configuration, see [4.4](#4.4).

---

## Core Architecture

`EditorNode` is the central singleton that initializes and coordinates all editor subsystems. It owns the state management layer (`EditorData`), provides a stable public API (`EditorInterface`), and manages the plugin system, selection state, and undo/redo operations.

### EditorNode as Central Orchestrator

## EditorNode: The Singleton Orchestrator

`EditorNode` inherits from `Node` and acts as the root of the editor scene tree. It is initialized once at editor startup and remains active throughout the editor session.

### Key Responsibilities

| Responsibility | Implementation |
|----------------|----------------|
| **Scene Management** | Manages `EditorData::edited_scene` vector, handles scene loading/saving/switching |
| **Plugin Orchestration** | Maintains `editor_plugins` vector, forwards callbacks to all registered plugins |
| **Selection Tracking** | Owns `EditorSelection` singleton, syncs with `EditorData::selection` per scene |
| **Undo/Redo Coordination** | Integrates with `EditorUndoRedoManager`, manages per-scene history IDs |
| **UI Coordination** | Owns docks, main screen, bottom panel, and coordinates their visibility |
| **State Persistence** | Saves/loads editor layout, window positions, and plugin states |

### Singleton Access Pattern

```mermaid
graph LR
    Client["Any Editor Code"]
    EN["EditorNode::singleton"]
    GetSingleton["EditorNode::get_singleton()"]
    
    Client -->|calls| GetSingleton
    GetSingleton -->|returns| EN
```

The singleton is set in [editor/editor_node.cpp:207]() and accessed via `EditorNode::get_singleton()` throughout the codebase. It is never deleted during the editor session.

Sources: [editor/editor_node.h:120-121](), [editor/editor_node.cpp:207]()

### EditorNode Core Members

```mermaid
graph TB
    EN[EditorNode]
    
    subgraph "State"
        ED[EditorData editor_data]
        EF[EditorFolding editor_folding]
        EH[EditorSelectionHistory editor_history]
    end
    
    subgraph "Services"
        ES[EditorSelection* editor_selection]
        EE[EditorExport* editor_export]
        ERP[EditorResourcePreview* resource_preview]
        LOG[EditorLog* log]
    end
    
    subgraph "Plugins"
        EP[Vector&lt;EditorPlugin*&gt; editor_plugins]
        EPFI[EditorPluginList* force_input_forwarding]
        EPFO[EditorPluginList* force_over]
        EPO[EditorPluginList* over]
    end
    
    EN --> ED
    EN --> EF
    EN --> EH
    EN --> ES
    EN --> EE
    EN --> ERP
    EN --> LOG
    EN --> EP
    EN --> EPFI
    EN --> EPFO
    EN --> EPO
```

Sources: [editor/editor_node.h:259-276]()

## EditorData: Scene and Plugin State

`EditorData` manages the state of all open scenes, tracks the current edited scene, and stores plugin states. It does not own the scene nodes directly but maintains metadata about them.

### EditedScene Structure

Each open scene tab corresponds to one `EditedScene` entry in the `edited_scene` vector:

```mermaid
graph TB
    ES[EditedScene struct]
    
    Root[Node* root<br/>Scene root node]
    Path[String path<br/>File path]
    States[Dictionary editor_states<br/>Plugin states]
    Selection[List&lt;Node*&gt; selection<br/>Selected nodes]
    HistoryID[int history_id<br/>Undo/redo history]
    LiveEdit[NodePath live_edit_root]
    TimeOpened[uint64_t time_opened]
    
    ES --> Root
    ES --> Path
    ES --> States
    ES --> Selection
    ES --> HistoryID
    ES --> LiveEdit
    ES --> TimeOpened
```

Sources: [editor/editor_data.h:113-126]()

### Scene State Lifecycle

```mermaid
graph TB
    Add[add_edited_scene]
    Set[set_edited_scene_root]
    Switch[set_edited_scene]
    Save[save_editor_external_data]
    Remove[remove_scene]
    
    Add -->|creates EditedScene| ES[edited_scene vector]
    Set -->|assigns root node| ES
    Switch -->|changes current_edited_scene| ES
    Save -->|persists editor_states| ES
    Remove -->|deletes EditedScene| ES
    
    ES -->|notifies| Plugins[editor_plugins]
```

The `current_edited_scene` index tracks which scene is currently being edited. Each scene has a unique `history_id` for undo/redo operations managed by `EditorUndoRedoManager`.

Sources: [editor/editor_data.cpp:613-672](), [editor/editor_data.h:143-145]()

### Plugin State Management

`EditorData` stores and retrieves plugin states via `Dictionary` objects:

| Method | Purpose |
|--------|---------|
| `get_editor_plugin_states()` | Calls `get_state()` on all plugins, returns combined Dictionary |
| `set_editor_plugin_states()` | Calls `set_state()` on matching plugins with saved Dictionary |
| `get_scene_editor_states()` | Returns per-scene plugin states for a specific scene index |
| `notify_edited_scene_changed()` | Calls `edited_scene_changed()` on all plugins when scene switches |

Sources: [editor/editor_data.cpp:316-365]()

---

## EditorInterface: Public API for Plugins

`EditorInterface` is a singleton that provides a stable, versioned API for editor plugins. It acts as a facade to `EditorNode` and `EditorData`, hiding implementation details and reducing coupling.

### API Design Pattern

```mermaid
graph LR
    Plugin[EditorPlugin]
    EI[EditorInterface::singleton]
    EN[EditorNode::singleton]
    ED[EditorData]
    
    Plugin -->|calls| EI
    EI -->|delegates| EN
    EI -->|accesses| ED
    
    Plugin -.->|does not access directly| EN
    Plugin -.->|does not access directly| ED
```

Plugins should only access editor functionality through `EditorInterface` methods. Direct access to `EditorNode` is discouraged and may break in future versions.

Sources: [editor/editor_interface.h:61-64](), [doc/classes/EditorInterface.xml:1-10]()

### Core EditorInterface Methods

```mermaid
graph TB
    EI[EditorInterface]
    
    subgraph "Scene Access"
        GER[get_edited_scene_root]
        GOS[get_open_scenes]
        OSP[open_scene_from_path]
        SS[save_scene]
    end
    
    subgraph "Selection"
        GSel[get_selection]
        EN[edit_node]
        ER[edit_resource]
    end
    
    subgraph "Editor Tools"
        GFS[get_resource_filesystem]
        GRP[get_resource_previewer]
        GU[get_editor_undo_redo]
        GS[get_editor_settings]
    end
    
    subgraph "UI Access"
        GBC[get_base_control]
        GMS[get_editor_main_screen]
        GI[get_inspector]
    end
    
    EI --> GER
    EI --> GOS
    EI --> OSP
    EI --> SS
    EI --> GSel
    EI --> EN
    EI --> ER
    EI --> GFS
    EI --> GRP
    EI --> GU
    EI --> GS
    EI --> GBC
    EI --> GMS
    EI --> GI
```

Sources: [editor/editor_interface.h:95-210](), [doc/classes/EditorInterface.xml:21-386]()

### Example: Plugin Scene Access

When a plugin needs to access the current scene:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Plugin
    participant EditorInterface
    participant EditorNode
    participant EditorData
    
    Plugin->>EditorInterface: get_edited_scene_root()
    EditorInterface->>EditorNode: get_edited_scene()
    EditorNode->>EditorData: get_edited_scene_root()
    EditorData-->>EditorNode: Node* root
    EditorNode-->>EditorInterface: Node* root
    EditorInterface-->>Plugin: Node* root
```

Sources: [editor/editor_interface.cpp:423-424](), [editor/editor_node.h:864](), [editor/editor_data.cpp:784-792]()

## Selection Management

The editor maintains two systems for tracking user selections: `EditorSelection` for the current selection set, and `EditorSelectionHistory` for navigation history.

### EditorSelection: Current Selection Set

`EditorSelection` is a singleton that maintains a `HashMap<ObjectID, Object*>` of currently selected nodes and their editor metadata.

```mermaid
graph TB
    ESel[EditorSelection]
    
    subgraph "Selection Storage"
        Map[HashMap&lt;ObjectID, Object*&gt; selection]
        NodeID[ObjectID: node instance ID]
        Meta[Object*: editor metadata]
    end
    
    subgraph "Methods"
        Add[add_node]
        Remove[remove_node]
        Clear[clear]
        GetNodes[get_selected_nodes]
        GetTop[get_top_selected_node_list]
    end
    
    subgraph "Signals"
        Changed[selection_changed]
    end
    
    ESel --> Map
    Map --> NodeID
    Map --> Meta
    
    ESel --> Add
    ESel --> Remove
    ESel --> Clear
    ESel --> GetNodes
    ESel --> GetTop
    
    Add -.->|emits| Changed
    Remove -.->|emits| Changed
    Clear -.->|emits| Changed
```

The metadata (`Object*`) is obtained by calling `_get_editor_data(node)` on each registered editor plugin, allowing plugins to attach custom data to selected nodes.

Sources: [editor/editor_data.h:275-337](), [editor/editor_data.cpp:not shown in excerpt but referenced]()

### EditorSelectionHistory: Navigation History

`EditorSelectionHistory` maintains a vector of `HistoryElement` entries representing the objects that have been inspected in the editor.

```mermaid
graph TB
    EH[EditorSelectionHistory]
    
    subgraph "History Storage"
        HV[Vector&lt;HistoryElement&gt; history]
        HE[HistoryElement]
        Path[Vector&lt;_Object&gt; path]
        Level[int level]
    end
    
    subgraph "Navigation"
        Prev[previous]
        Next[next]
        AddObj[add_object]
        GetCurr[get_current]
    end
    
    subgraph "_Object"
        RefC[Ref&lt;RefCounted&gt; ref]
        OID[ObjectID object]
        Prop[String property]
        InspOnly[bool inspector_only]
    end
    
    EH --> HV
    HV --> HE
    HE --> Path
    HE --> Level
    
    Path --> RefC
    Path --> OID
    Path --> Prop
    Path --> InspOnly
    
    EH --> Prev
    EH --> Next
    EH --> AddObj
    EH --> GetCurr
```

Each `HistoryElement` represents a selection event. The `path` vector contains the object and any sub-resources that were navigated to (e.g., Node â†’ Resource â†’ nested Resource). The `level` indicates the depth of the current focus within that path.

Sources: [editor/editor_data.h:47-101](), [editor/editor_data.cpp:49-252]()

### Selection Workflow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant User
    participant EditorNode
    participant EditorSelection
    participant EditorSelectionHistory
    participant Plugins
    
    User->>EditorNode: clicks node in tree
    EditorNode->>EditorSelection: add_node(node)
    EditorSelection->>Plugins: _get_editor_data(node)
    Plugins-->>EditorSelection: metadata object
    EditorSelection->>EditorSelection: store in HashMap
    EditorSelection->>EditorSelection: emit selection_changed
    
    EditorNode->>EditorSelectionHistory: add_object(node_id)
    EditorSelectionHistory->>EditorSelectionHistory: create HistoryElement
    EditorSelectionHistory->>EditorSelectionHistory: append to history vector
    
    EditorSelection-->>Plugins: selection_changed signal
    Plugins->>EditorSelection: get_selected_nodes()
    EditorSelection-->>Plugins: selected nodes
```

Sources: [editor/editor_data.cpp:110-145](), [editor/editor_node.cpp:not shown in excerpt]()
