## Input Processing Flow

GUI input events flow from the operating system through the viewport to specific controls:

```mermaid
graph TB
    OS["Operating System<br/>Mouse/Keyboard Events"]
    DisplayServer["DisplayServer<br/>servers/display/display_server.h"]
    Input["Input Singleton<br/>core/input/input.h"]
    
    SceneTree["SceneTree<br/>_process_picking()"]
    Viewport["Viewport<br/>viewport.h:95"]
    
    SubWindowCheck{"Subwindow<br/>Active?"}
    GUIInputCheck{"Control<br/>Under Mouse?"}
    
    gui_mouse_focus["gui.mouse_focus<br/>viewport.h"]
    gui_key_focus["gui.key_focus<br/>viewport.h"]
    
    Control_gui_input["Control::_gui_input()<br/>control.cpp"]
    Control_virtual["Control::gui_input()<br/>Virtual Override"]
    
    OS --> DisplayServer
    DisplayServer --> Input
    Input --> SceneTree
    SceneTree --> Viewport
    
    Viewport --> SubWindowCheck
    SubWindowCheck -->|Yes| gui_mouse_focus
    SubWindowCheck -->|No| GUIInputCheck
    
    GUIInputCheck -->|Yes| gui_mouse_focus
    GUIInputCheck -->|No| gui_key_focus
    
    gui_mouse_focus --> Control_gui_input
    gui_key_focus --> Control_gui_input
    
    Control_gui_input --> Control_virtual
```

### Input Event Routing in Viewport

The `Viewport` class manages GUI input state in the `gui` struct [scene/main/viewport.h:1]():

| Member | Purpose | File Reference |
|--------|---------|----------------|
| `gui.mouse_focus` | Control currently under mouse | [scene/main/viewport.h:1]() |
| `gui.key_focus` | Control with keyboard focus | [scene/main/viewport.h:1]() |
| `gui.mouse_over` | ObjectID of hovered control | [scene/main/viewport.h:1]() |
| `gui.subwindow_focused` | Active embedded window | [scene/main/viewport.h:1]() |
| `gui.dragging` | Drag operation active | [scene/main/viewport.h:1]() |

**Mouse Input Processing:**
1. `_gui_input_event()` [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1]() receives input events
2. Determines target control via `_gui_find_control()` using position and z-order
3. Checks `mouse_filter` property:
   - `MOUSE_FILTER_STOP`: Consumes event [scene/gui/control.h:1]()
   - `MOUSE_FILTER_PASS`: Passes to parent [scene/gui/control.h:1]()
   - `MOUSE_FILTER_IGNORE`: Ignores completely [scene/gui/control.h:1]()
4. Calls `_gui_input()` then virtual `gui_input()` [scene/gui/control.cpp:1]()

**Keyboard Input Processing:**
1. Events sent to `gui.key_focus` control
2. Focus managed via `grab_focus()` [scene/gui/control.cpp:1]()
3. Focus visibility controlled by `gui.hide_focus` [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1]()

**Sources:** [scene/main/viewport.h:95](), [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1](), [scene/gui/control.cpp:1]()

---

## Theme System

Controls obtain visual styling from the theme system:

```mermaid
graph TB
    ThemeDB["ThemeDB Singleton<br/>scene/theme/theme_db.h<br/>Global Theme Registry"]
    Theme["Theme Resource<br/>scene/theme/theme.h"]
    
    Control["Control Node"]
    
    theme_override["Theme Overrides<br/>control.h<br/>theme_*_override maps"]
    theme_property["theme Property<br/>Explicit Theme"]
    theme_type_variation["theme_type_variation<br/>Alternate Style"]
    
    ThemeOwner["ThemeOwner Mixin<br/>scene/theme/theme_owner.h<br/>Theme Propagation"]
    
    default_theme["Default Theme<br/>ThemeDB::get_default_theme()"]
    
    ThemeDB --> Theme
    ThemeDB --> default_theme
    
    Control --> theme_override
    Control --> theme_property
    Control --> theme_type_variation
    Control -.uses.-> ThemeOwner
    
    theme_override -.priority 1.-> Control
    theme_property -.priority 2.-> Control
    ThemeOwner -.priority 3.-> Control
    default_theme -.priority 4.-> Control
```

### Theme Resolution Order

When a `Control` requests a theme item (e.g., font, color, stylebox):

1. **Theme Overrides**: Check `theme_*_override` maps [scene/gui/control.cpp:309-379]()
   - `theme_icon_override`
   - `theme_style_override`  
   - `theme_font_override`
   - `theme_font_size_override`
   - `theme_color_override`
   - `theme_constant_override`

2. **Explicit Theme**: If `theme` property is set [scene/gui/control.h:1]()

3. **Parent Propagation**: Walk up node tree via `ThemeOwner` [scene/theme/theme_owner.h:1]()

4. **Default Theme**: `ThemeDB::get_singleton()->get_default_theme()` [scene/theme/theme_db.h:1]()

### Theme Cache

Controls cache theme lookups in `theme_cache` struct:
- Populated in `_update_theme_item_cache()` [scene/gui/control.cpp:1]()
- Called on `NOTIFICATION_THEME_CHANGED` [scene/gui/control.cpp:1]()
- Invalidated when theme changes via `_notify_theme_override_changed()` [scene/gui/control.cpp:324]()

**Example from Label:**
```
struct ThemeCache {
    Ref<Font> font;
    int font_size = 0;
    Color font_color;
    Color font_shadow_color;
    Color font_outline_color;
    int outline_size = 0;
    // ...
}
```
[scene/gui/label.h:1]()

**Sources:** [scene/gui/control.h:1](), [scene/gui/control.cpp:309-379](), [scene/theme/theme_db.h:1](), [scene/theme/theme_owner.h:1]()

## Rendering Integration

Controls inherit from `CanvasItem` and render via the `RenderingServer`:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Control["Control Node"]
    CanvasItem["CanvasItem<br/>scene/2d/canvas_item.h<br/>Drawing Interface"]
    
    notification_draw["NOTIFICATION_DRAW<br/>control.cpp"]
    draw_methods["draw_*() methods<br/>draw_rect(), draw_texture()"]
    
    canvas_item_ci["canvas_item RID<br/>CanvasItem handle"]
    RenderingServer["RenderingServer<br/>servers/rendering/rendering_server.h"]
    
    viewport["Viewport<br/>Rendering Root"]
    canvas["Canvas RID<br/>2D render target"]
    
    Control -.inherits.-> CanvasItem
    Control --> notification_draw
    notification_draw --> draw_methods
    
    CanvasItem --> canvas_item_ci
    draw_methods --> RenderingServer
    canvas_item_ci --> RenderingServer
    
    RenderingServer --> canvas
    viewport --> canvas
```

### Drawing Process

1. **Draw Notification**: Controls receive `NOTIFICATION_DRAW` [scene/gui/control.cpp:1]()
2. **Canvas Item Commands**: Use inherited drawing methods:
   - `draw_rect()` [scene/2d/canvas_item.cpp:1]()
   - `draw_texture()` [scene/2d/canvas_item.cpp:1]()
   - `draw_string()` [scene/2d/canvas_item.cpp:1]()
   - `draw_style_box()` [scene/2d/canvas_item.cpp:1]()
3. **RenderingServer API**: Commands sent to `RenderingServer` via `canvas_item` RID
4. **Canvas Rendering**: Viewport's canvas collects all items for rendering

### Text Rendering via TextServer

Text components use `TextServer` for complex text layout:

**TextEdit Example:**
```
_notification(NOTIFICATION_DRAW):
    - Iterate visible lines
    - For each line:
        - Get TextParagraph: text.get_line_data(line)
        - Draw shaped text: text_buf->draw(...)
```
[scene/gui/text_edit.cpp:914-2130]()

**TextServer Integration:**
- Text shaped into glyphs: `TS->shaped_text_*()` methods
- BiDi (bidirectional text) support
- Font fallback handling
- Inline objects (images in text)

**Sources:** [scene/gui/control.cpp:1](), [scene/2d/canvas_item.h:1](), [scene/gui/text_edit.cpp:914-2130](), [servers/text/text_server.h:1]()

---

## Focus System

The GUI focus system determines which control receives keyboard input:

```mermaid
graph LR
    viewport_key_focus["viewport.gui.key_focus<br/>Current Focused Control"]
    
    grab_focus["Control::grab_focus()<br/>control.cpp"]
    release_focus["Control::release_focus()<br/>control.cpp"]
    
    NOTIFICATION_FOCUS_ENTER["NOTIFICATION_FOCUS_ENTER"]
    NOTIFICATION_FOCUS_EXIT["NOTIFICATION_FOCUS_EXIT"]
    
    focus_changed["emit focus_entered/exited"]
    
    grab_focus --> viewport_key_focus
    viewport_key_focus --> NOTIFICATION_FOCUS_ENTER
    viewport_key_focus --> NOTIFICATION_FOCUS_EXIT
    
    NOTIFICATION_FOCUS_ENTER --> focus_changed
    NOTIFICATION_FOCUS_EXIT --> focus_changed
    
    release_focus --> viewport_key_focus
```

**Focus Management:**
- Only one control has focus per viewport
- `grab_focus()` requests focus [scene/gui/control.cpp:1]()
- Focus mode controlled by `focus_mode` enum [scene/gui/control.h:1]():
  - `FOCUS_NONE`: Cannot receive focus
  - `FOCUS_CLICK`: Focus on mouse click
  - `FOCUS_ALL`: Focus via mouse or keyboard navigation
- Focus neighbor navigation via `focus_next`, `focus_previous` [scene/gui/control.h:1]()

**Sources:** [scene/gui/control.h:1](), [scene/gui/control.cpp:1](), [scene/main/viewport.h:1]()

---

## Accessibility Integration

Controls integrate with the `AccessibilityServer` for screen reader support:

**Accessibility Element Creation:**
- Each `Control` creates an accessibility element RID [scene/gui/control.cpp:1]()
- Updated on `NOTIFICATION_ACCESSIBILITY_UPDATE` [scene/gui/control.cpp:1]()
- Elements form a hierarchy matching the scene tree

**TextEdit Accessibility:**
`TextEdit` creates sub-elements for each visible line [scene/gui/text_edit.cpp:775-818]():
- Line elements stored in `text[i].accessibility_text_root_element` [scene/gui/text_edit.h:155]()
- Positioned based on visible layout
- Support selection ranges via `AccessibilityServer::update_set_text_selection()`

**Sources:** [scene/gui/control.cpp:1](), [scene/gui/text_edit.cpp:775-818](), [servers/display/accessibility_server.h:1]()27:T45df,# Control Nodes and Layout System

## Purpose and Scope

This document describes the Control node system in Godot, which provides the foundation for all GUI elements. It covers the layout system (anchors, offsets, and containers), size management, theming, and input handling for UI nodes. For information about specific text editing components, see [Text Editing Components](#5.2). For details on input event propagation, see [Input Processing and GUI Events](#5.3).

## Control Class Overview

The `Control` class ([scene/gui/control.h:45](), [scene/gui/control.cpp:31]()) is the base class for all UI nodes in Godot. It inherits from `CanvasItem`, which provides 2D rendering capabilities, and adds layout management, theming, and input handling specific to user interfaces.

### Class Hierarchy

```mermaid
graph TB
    Object["Object<br/>Base class"]
    Node["Node<br/>Scene tree node"]
    CanvasItem["CanvasItem<br/>2D rendering"]
    Control["Control<br/>UI base class"]
    Button["Button"]
    Label["Label"]
    Container["Container"]
    Panel["Panel"]
    
    Object --> Node
    Node --> CanvasItem
    CanvasItem --> Control
    Control --> Button
    Control --> Label
    Control --> Container
    Control --> Panel
    
    style Control fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Control Class Responsibilities**

```mermaid
graph LR
    Control["Control Node"]
    Layout["Layout Management<br/>Anchors, Offsets, Size"]
    Theme["Theme System<br/>Visual Properties"]
    Input["Input Handling<br/>Mouse, Focus, Drag"]
    MinSize["Minimum Size<br/>Calculation"]
    
    Control --> Layout
    Control --> Theme
    Control --> Input
    Control --> MinSize
```

Sources: [scene/gui/control.h:45-178](), [doc/classes/Control.xml:1-10]()

## Layout Modes

Control nodes support four distinct layout modes that determine how their position and size are managed. The layout mode is automatically determined based on the node's parent and properties.

### Layout Mode Types

| Mode | Enum Value | Description | Use Case |
|------|------------|-------------|----------|
| Position | `LAYOUT_MODE_POSITION` | Direct position/size control | Root controls, manual positioning |
| Anchors | `LAYOUT_MODE_ANCHORS` | Anchor-based responsive layout | Responsive UIs, relative positioning |
| Container | `LAYOUT_MODE_CONTAINER` | Managed by parent Container | Child of Container nodes |
| Uncontrolled | `LAYOUT_MODE_UNCONTROLLED` | No automatic layout | Advanced custom layouts |

```mermaid
graph TB
    Root["Control Node"]
    CheckParent{"Parent is<br/>Container?"}
    CheckAnchors{"Using<br/>anchors?"}
    
    ModeContainer["LAYOUT_MODE_CONTAINER<br/>Parent controls layout"]
    ModeAnchors["LAYOUT_MODE_ANCHORS<br/>Anchor-based positioning"]
    ModePosition["LAYOUT_MODE_POSITION<br/>Direct positioning"]
    
    Root --> CheckParent
    CheckParent -->|Yes| ModeContainer
    CheckParent -->|No| CheckAnchors
    CheckAnchors -->|Yes| ModeAnchors
    CheckAnchors -->|No| ModePosition
```

Sources: [scene/gui/control.h:149-154](), [scene/gui/control.cpp:76-122]()

## Anchor and Offset System

The anchor system provides responsive layouts by defining positions relative to the parent's edges. Each control has four anchor values (left, top, right, bottom) and four offset values.

### Anchor Coordinates

Anchors are normalized values from 0.0 to 1.0 representing positions along the parent's width/height:
- `0.0` = beginning edge (left/top)
- `0.5` = center
- `1.0` = ending edge (right/bottom)

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Parent Control"
        TL["anchor_left = 0.0<br/>anchor_top = 0.0"]
        TR["anchor_right = 1.0<br/>anchor_top = 0.0"]
        BL["anchor_left = 0.0<br/>anchor_bottom = 1.0"]
        BR["anchor_right = 1.0<br/>anchor_bottom = 1.0"]
        C["anchor_left = 0.5<br/>anchor_top = 0.5"]
        
        TL -.-> TR
        TL -.-> BL
        BL -.-> BR
        TR -.-> BR
        TL -.-> C
        C -.-> BR
    end
```

### Position Calculation

The final position of a control is calculated using anchors and offsets:

```
left_pixel = parent_width * anchor_left + offset_left
top_pixel = parent_height * anchor_top + offset_top
right_pixel = parent_width * anchor_right + offset_right
bottom_pixel = parent_height * anchor_bottom + offset_bottom

position = (left_pixel, top_pixel)
size = (right_pixel - left_pixel, bottom_pixel - top_pixel)
```

**Core Data Structure** ([scene/gui/control.h:426-430]()):
```cpp
struct Data {
    real_t anchor[4];      // SIDE_LEFT, SIDE_TOP, SIDE_RIGHT, SIDE_BOTTOM
    real_t offset[4];      // Pixel offsets from anchor positions
    Size2 size;           // Calculated size
    Point2 position;      // Calculated position
    // ...
}
```

Sources: [scene/gui/control.cpp:1494-1577](), [scene/gui/control.h:426-430]()

### Layout Presets

Common anchor configurations are available as presets ([scene/gui/control.h:123-140]()):

| Preset | Anchors | Description |
|--------|---------|-------------|
| `PRESET_TOP_LEFT` | (0,0)-(0,0) | Fixed to top-left corner |
| `PRESET_CENTER` | (0.5,0.5)-(0.5,0.5) | Centered in parent |
| `PRESET_FULL_RECT` | (0,0)-(1,1) | Fills entire parent |
| `PRESET_LEFT_WIDE` | (0,0)-(0,1) | Full height, anchored left |
| `PRESET_VCENTER_WIDE` | (0,0.5)-(1,0.5) | Centered vertically, full width |

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Common Presets"
        A["PRESET_TOP_LEFT<br/>(0,0)-(0,0)"]
        B["PRESET_CENTER<br/>(0.5,0.5)-(0.5,0.5)"]
        C["PRESET_FULL_RECT<br/>(0,0)-(1,1)"]
    end
```

Sources: [scene/gui/control.cpp:1738-1875](), [scene/gui/control.h:123-140]()

## Container System

Container nodes automatically manage the layout of their children. When a Control is a child of a Container, its layout mode becomes `LAYOUT_MODE_CONTAINER`, and the parent controls its position and size.

### Container-Child Communication

```mermaid
graph TB
    Container["Container Node"]
    Child1["Child Control 1<br/>size_flags_horizontal<br/>size_flags_vertical"]
    Child2["Child Control 2<br/>size_flags_horizontal<br/>size_flags_vertical"]
    
    Container -->|"Queries minimum size"| Child1
    Container -->|"Queries minimum size"| Child2
    Child1 -->|"Returns min size + flags"| Container
    Child2 -->|"Returns min size + flags"| Container
    Container -->|"Sets final rect"| Child1
    Container -->|"Sets final rect"| Child2
    
    MinSize1["get_combined_minimum_size()"]
    MinSize2["get_combined_minimum_size()"]
    
    Child1 -.-> MinSize1
    Child2 -.-> MinSize2
```

### Size Flags

Children communicate layout preferences to their parent Container through size flags ([scene/gui/control.h:79-87]()):

| Flag | Value | Behavior |
|------|-------|----------|
| `SIZE_FILL` | 1 | Fill available space in container |
| `SIZE_EXPAND` | 2 | Request more space than minimum |
| `SIZE_SHRINK_CENTER` | 4 | Center when smaller than allocation |
| `SIZE_SHRINK_END` | 8 | Align to end when smaller |
| `SIZE_EXPAND_FILL` | 3 | Combine EXPAND and FILL |

**Properties Managed by Containers** ([scene/gui/control.cpp:294-307]()):
```
offset_left, offset_top, offset_right, offset_bottom
anchor_left, anchor_top, anchor_right, anchor_bottom
position, rotation, scale, size
```

When a Control is a child of a Container, these properties become read-only and are managed by the parent ([scene/gui/control.cpp:557-607]()).

Sources: [scene/gui/control.cpp:294-307](), [scene/gui/control.cpp:557-607](), [scene/gui/control.h:79-87]()

### Minimum Size System

Every Control calculates a minimum size based on its content and theming:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Control["Control Node"]
    GetMinSize["get_combined_minimum_size()"]
    CustomMinSize["custom_minimum_size<br/>property"]
    ContentMinSize["_get_minimum_size()<br/>virtual method"]
    ThemeMinSize["Theme item sizes<br/>fonts, styleboxes"]
    
    Control --> GetMinSize
    GetMinSize --> CustomMinSize
    GetMinSize --> ContentMinSize
    GetMinSize --> ThemeMinSize
    
    Result["max(custom, content, theme)"]
    
    CustomMinSize --> Result
    ContentMinSize --> Result
    ThemeMinSize --> Result
```

The minimum size is calculated in [scene/gui/control.cpp:771-808]() and cached until invalidated by layout changes.

Sources: [scene/gui/control.cpp:771-808](), [scene/gui/control.cpp:810-838]()

## Theme System

The theme system provides visual styling for Control nodes through a hierarchical property resolution chain. Each Control can override specific theme properties or inherit them from parent controls or a global theme.

### Theme Property Types

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Theme Property Types"
        Color["Color<br/>text_color, font_color"]
        Constant["Constant<br/>separation, margin"]
        Font["Font<br/>font"]
        FontSize["Font Size<br/>font_size"]
        Icon["Icon/Texture2D<br/>icons"]
        StyleBox["StyleBox<br/>panel, border"]
    end
```

### Theme Resolution Chain

```mermaid
graph TB
    Request["Theme Property Request<br/>get_theme_color('font_color')"]
    
    LocalOverride{"Local Override<br/>add_theme_*_override()"}
    ControlTheme{"Control.theme<br/>property"}
    ParentChain{"Parent Control<br/>theme chain"}
    ProjectTheme{"ThemeDB<br/>project theme"}
    DefaultTheme{"ThemeDB<br/>default theme"}
    
    Request --> LocalOverride
    LocalOverride -->|Found| Return["Return Value"]
    LocalOverride -->|Not found| ControlTheme
    ControlTheme -->|Found| Return
    ControlTheme -->|Not found| ParentChain
    ParentChain -->|Found| Return
    ParentChain -->|Not found| ProjectTheme
    ProjectTheme -->|Found| Return
    ProjectTheme -->|Not found| DefaultTheme
    DefaultTheme --> Return
```

### Theme Override System

Controls can override individual theme properties using dedicated methods ([scene/gui/control.cpp:309-379]()):

**Override Methods**:
- `add_theme_icon_override(name, texture)`
- `add_theme_stylebox_override(name, stylebox)`
- `add_theme_font_override(name, font)`
- `add_theme_font_size_override(name, size)`
- `add_theme_color_override(name, color)`
- `add_theme_constant_override(name, value)`

**Retrieval Methods**:
- `get_theme_icon(name)` - Returns Texture2D
- `get_theme_stylebox(name)` - Returns StyleBox
- `get_theme_font(name)` - Returns Font
- `get_theme_font_size(name)` - Returns int
- `get_theme_color(name)` - Returns Color
- `get_theme_constant(name)` - Returns int

**Theme Override Storage** ([scene/gui/control.h:435-441]()):
```cpp
HashMap<StringName, Ref<Texture2D>> theme_icon_override;
HashMap<StringName, Ref<StyleBox>> theme_style_override;
HashMap<StringName, Ref<Font>> theme_font_override;
HashMap<StringName, int> theme_font_size_override;
HashMap<StringName, Color> theme_color_override;
HashMap<StringName, int> theme_constant_override;
```

Sources: [scene/gui/control.cpp:309-379](), [scene/gui/control.cpp:414-476](), [scene/gui/control.h:435-441]()

### Theme Context and Owner

The theme system uses a `ThemeOwner` and `ThemeContext` to manage property resolution ([scene/gui/control.h:443-445]()):

```mermaid
graph TB
    Control1["Control Node"]
    ThemeOwner["ThemeOwner<br/>Tracks theme hierarchy"]
    ThemeContext["ThemeContext<br/>Caches resolved properties"]
    ThemeDB["ThemeDB<br/>Global theme registry"]
    
    Control1 --> ThemeOwner
    ThemeOwner --> ThemeContext
    ThemeContext --> ThemeDB
    
    Notification["NOTIFICATION_THEME_CHANGED"]
    
    ThemeDB -.->|Invalidates| ThemeContext
    ThemeContext -.->|Triggers| Notification
    Notification -.->|Redraws| Control1
```

When theme properties change, controls receive `NOTIFICATION_THEME_CHANGED` ([scene/gui/control.cpp:415]()) and update their appearance.

Sources: [scene/gui/control.h:443-445](), [scene/gui/control.cpp:2645-2811]()

## Input and Focus Management

Control nodes handle mouse and keyboard input through a filtering and focus system integrated with the Viewport.

### Mouse Filter Modes

Controls can filter mouse input using three modes ([scene/gui/control.h:89-93]()):

| Mode | Enum | Behavior |
|------|------|----------|
| Stop | `MOUSE_FILTER_STOP` | Consume mouse events, don't pass to nodes behind |
| Pass | `MOUSE_FILTER_PASS` | Process events but pass through to nodes behind |
| Ignore | `MOUSE_FILTER_IGNORE` | Completely ignore mouse events |

```mermaid
graph TB
    MouseEvent["Mouse Input Event"]
    
    Control1["Control 1<br/>MOUSE_FILTER_STOP"]
    Control2["Control 2<br/>MOUSE_FILTER_PASS"]
    Control3["Control 3<br/>MOUSE_FILTER_IGNORE"]
    
    Background["Background Node"]
    
    MouseEvent --> Control1
    Control1 -->|Consumed| End1["Event Handled"]
    
    MouseEvent --> Control2
    Control2 -->|Processes & Passes| Background
    
    MouseEvent --> Control3
    Control3 -->|Ignored| Background
```

Sources: [scene/gui/control.h:89-93](), [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1442-1599]()

### Focus System

Controls can receive keyboard focus through four focus modes ([scene/gui/control.h:66-71]()):

| Mode | Description |
|------|-------------|
| `FOCUS_NONE` | Cannot receive focus |
| `FOCUS_CLICK` | Focus on mouse click |
| `FOCUS_ALL` | Focus via click or keyboard navigation |
| `FOCUS_ACCESSIBILITY` | Focus for accessibility tools only |

**Focus Management in Viewport** ([scene/main/viewport.h:341-366]()):
```cpp
struct {
    Control *key_focus = nullptr;           // Currently focused control
    Control *mouse_focus = nullptr;         // Control under mouse
    Control *mouse_click_grabber = nullptr; // Control that grabbed click
    // ...
} gui;
```

The Viewport manages focus state and routes input events to the focused control ([scene/main/viewport.cpp:1442-1599]()).

Sources: [scene/gui/control.h:66-71](), [scene/main/viewport.h:341-366](), [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1442-1599]()

```mermaid
    Start --> GetDragData
    GetDragData --> SetPreview

```

This page documents the text editing and display components in Godot's GUI system, including multiline editors, single-line inputs, and rich text display controls. These components handle user text input, editing operations, text rendering, and integration with the TextServer for complex text shaping and layout.

For information about the base Control class and layout system, see [Control Nodes and Layout System](#5.1). For input event handling in GUI controls, see [Input Processing and GUI Events](#5.3).

## Component Overview

Godot provides several text-related Control nodes, each serving different use cases:

| Component | Purpose | Key Features |
|-----------|---------|--------------|
| **TextEdit** | Multiline text editor | Multiple carets, undo/redo, syntax highlighting, line wrapping, gutters |
| **CodeEdit** | Code-specific editor | Extends TextEdit with code completion, folding, auto-indent, brace matching |
| **LineEdit** | Single-line input field | IME support, context menu, virtual keyboard, password masking |
| **RichTextLabel** | Rich text display | BBCode parsing, custom effects, images, tables, links |
| **Label** | Simple text display | Basic text rendering with alignment and wrapping |

**Class Hierarchy:**

```mermaid
graph TB
    Control["Control"]
    TextEdit["TextEdit"]
    CodeEdit["CodeEdit"]
    LineEdit["LineEdit"]
    RichTextLabel["RichTextLabel"]
    Label["Label"]
    
    Control --> TextEdit
    Control --> LineEdit
    Control --> RichTextLabel
    Control --> Label
    TextEdit --> CodeEdit
```

Sources: [scene/gui/text_edit.h:40](), [scene/gui/code_edit.h:36](), [scene/gui/line_edit.h:36](), [scene/gui/rich_text_label.h:50](), [scene/gui/label.h:38]()

## TextEdit - Core Multiline Editor

`TextEdit` is the foundational multiline text editing control, providing comprehensive text manipulation capabilities with support for multiple carets, undo/redo, syntax highlighting, and custom gutters.

**Internal Architecture:**

```mermaid
graph TB
    TextEdit["TextEdit<br/>(scene/gui/text_edit.h)"]
    TextClass["Text<br/>(Internal Class)"]
    Line["Line Structure"]
    TextParagraph["TextParagraph<br/>(TextServer Integration)"]
    Caret["Caret System"]
    UndoRedo["Undo/Redo Stack"]
    Gutter["Gutter System"]
    SyntaxHighlighter["SyntaxHighlighter"]
    
    TextEdit --> TextClass
    TextEdit --> Caret
    TextEdit --> UndoRedo
    TextEdit --> Gutter
    TextEdit --> SyntaxHighlighter
    
    TextClass --> Line
    Line --> TextParagraph
    
    subgraph "Text Storage"
        TextClass
        Line
        TextParagraph
    end
    
    subgraph "Editing Features"
        Caret
        UndoRedo
    end
    
    subgraph "Visual Features"
        Gutter
        SyntaxHighlighter
    end
```

Sources: [scene/gui/text_edit.h:136-287](), [scene/gui/text_edit.cpp:54-652]()

### Text Storage and Line Management

The internal `TextEdit::Text` class manages the document as a vector of `Line` structures. Each line contains:

- Raw text data (`String data`)
- BiDi override information (`Array bidi_override`)
- Shaped text buffer (`Ref<TextParagraph> data_buf`)
- IME composition text (`String ime_data`)
- Visual properties (hidden state, background color)
- Gutter metadata per line

**Line Structure:**

```mermaid
graph LR
    Line["Line Structure"]
    data["data: String<br/>(raw text)"]
    data_buf["data_buf: TextParagraph<br/>(shaped text)"]
    gutters["gutters: Vector&lt;Gutter&gt;<br/>(gutter data per line)"]
    ime["ime_data: String<br/>(IME composition)"]
    visual["hidden: bool<br/>background_color: Color<br/>line_count: int<br/>height: int<br/>width: int"]
    
    Line --> data
    Line --> data_buf
    Line --> gutters
    Line --> ime
    Line --> visual
```

Sources: [scene/gui/text_edit.h:149-170](), [scene/gui/text_edit.cpp:58-226]()

When text changes, the cache is invalidated per line using `invalidate_cache()`, which updates the TextParagraph shaping, recalculates dimensions, and handles line wrapping based on the configured width and break flags.

**Cache Invalidation Flow:**

The `Text::invalidate_cache()` method at [scene/gui/text_edit.cpp:272-398]() performs:
1. Clears accessibility elements
2. Configures TextParagraph with font, direction, break flags
3. Processes inline objects via `inline_object_parser` callable
4. Updates font spans for all text segments
5. Applies tab alignment
6. Recalculates line count after wrapping
7. Updates line height and width metrics

Sources: [scene/gui/text_edit.cpp:272-398]()

### Multiple Caret Support

TextEdit supports multiple simultaneous carets (cursors), stored in a `Vector<Caret>` where index 0 is the main caret. Each `Caret` structure contains:

- Position (`int line`, `int column`)
- Selection state (`Selection selection` with origin and end positions)
- Visual state (`Point2 draw_pos`, `bool visible`)
- Last horizontal fit position (`int last_fit_x`)

**Multicaret Edit Pattern:**

```mermaid
graph TB
    begin["begin_multicaret_edit()"]
    edit["Edit operations<br/>for each caret"]
    ignore["Check multicaret_edit_ignore_caret()"]
    end["end_multicaret_edit()"]
    merge["Merge overlapping carets"]
    
    begin --> edit
    edit --> ignore
    ignore -->|not ignored| edit
    ignore -->|done| end
    end --> merge
```

Sources: [scene/gui/text_edit.h:445-464](), [doc/classes/TextEdit.xml:127-142]()

Operations between `begin_multicaret_edit()` and `end_multicaret_edit()` delay caret merging until complete. The `multicaret_edit_ignore_caret()` helper prevents operating on carets that have already been removed or merged during the operation.

Sources: [scene/gui/text_edit.h:455-464](), [doc/classes/TextEdit.xml:127-142]()

### Undo/Redo System

TextEdit maintains an undo stack using `TextOperation` objects that record:
- Operation type (TYPE_INSERT, TYPE_REMOVE)
- Text range affected (from_line, from_column, to_line, to_column)
- The text content
- Caret states before and after (start_carets, end_carets)
- Chain flags for merging consecutive operations

**Undo Stack Structure:**

```mermaid
graph LR
    TextEdit --> current_op["current_op<br/>(TextOperation)"]
    TextEdit --> undo_stack["undo_stack<br/>(List&lt;TextOperation&gt;)"]
    TextEdit --> undo_stack_pos["undo_stack_pos<br/>(List::Element*)"]
    
    TextOperation["TextOperation"]
    TextOperation --> type["type: Type<br/>(INSERT/REMOVE)"]
    TextOperation --> range["from_line, from_column<br/>to_line, to_column"]
    TextOperation --> text["text: String"]
    TextOperation --> carets["start_carets, end_carets<br/>(Vector&lt;Caret&gt;)"]
    TextOperation --> chain["chain_forward<br/>chain_backward"]
```

Sources: [scene/gui/text_edit.h:369-389](), [scene/gui/text_edit.h:391-413]()

Complex operations (multiple related edits) can be grouped using `begin_complex_operation()` / `end_complex_operation()`, which treats all intermediate edits as a single undo/redo action.

Sources: [doc/classes/TextEdit.xml:121-126]()

### Gutter System

Gutters are vertical strips to the left of the text area displaying supplementary information. Each gutter has a type:

- `GUTTER_TYPE_STRING` - Text display
- `GUTTER_TYPE_ICON` - Icon/texture display  
- `GUTTER_TYPE_CUSTOM` - Custom drawing via callable

**Gutter Architecture:**

```mermaid
graph TB
    TextEdit --> gutters["gutters: Vector&lt;GutterInfo&gt;"]
    
    GutterInfo["GutterInfo"]
    GutterInfo --> type["type: GutterType"]
    GutterInfo --> name["name: String"]
    GutterInfo --> width["width: int"]
    GutterInfo --> draw["draw: bool"]
    GutterInfo --> clickable["clickable: bool"]
    GutterInfo --> callback["custom_draw_callback"]
    
    Text --> LineGutters["Line::gutters<br/>(per-line data)"]
    
    LineGutters --> metadata["metadata: Variant"]
    LineGutters --> icon["icon: Texture2D"]
    LineGutters --> text_data["text: String"]
    LineGutters --> color["color: Color"]
    
    gutters --> GutterInfo
```

Sources: [scene/gui/text_edit.h:73-78](), [scene/gui/text_edit.h:125-134](), [scene/gui/text_edit.h:138-145]()

Gutters are added with `add_gutter()` and can be queried/modified per line using methods like `set_line_gutter_text()`, `set_line_gutter_icon()`, etc.

## CodeEdit - Specialized Code Editor

`CodeEdit` extends `TextEdit` with programming-specific features including code completion, symbol lookup, auto-indentation, code folding, and delimiter matching.

**CodeEdit Extensions:**

```mermaid
graph TB
    TextEdit["TextEdit"]
    CodeEdit["CodeEdit"]
    
    TextEdit --> CodeEdit
    
    CodeEdit --> completion["Code Completion<br/>code_completion_options<br/>code_completion_prefixes"]
    CodeEdit --> hints["Code Hints<br/>code_hint<br/>symbol_lookup"]
    CodeEdit --> indent["Auto Indent<br/>auto_indent_prefixes<br/>indent_size"]
    CodeEdit --> fold["Code Folding<br/>can_fold_line()<br/>fold_line()"]
    CodeEdit --> delim["Delimiter Matching<br/>auto_brace_completion_pairs<br/>has_auto_brace_completion_open_key()"]
    CodeEdit --> comment["Comment Delimiters<br/>add_comment_delimiter()"]
    CodeEdit --> string["String Delimiters<br/>add_string_delimiter()"]
```

Sources: [scene/gui/code_edit.h:36-37](), [scene/gui/code_edit.cpp:47-285]()

### Code Completion System

Code completion displays a popup with suggestions based on the current context. The completion flow involves:

1. **Request**: Call `request_code_completion()` or override `_request_code_completion()`
2. **Populate**: Add options with `add_code_completion_option()`
3. **Filter**: Optionally override `_filter_code_completion_candidates()`
4. **Display**: Automatically shown when `update_code_completion_options()` is called
5. **Confirm**: User selects option, triggers `_confirm_code_completion()`

**Code Completion Data Flow:**

```mermaid
graph TB
    request["request_code_completion()"]
    add["add_code_completion_option()<br/>(display_text, insert_text, etc.)"]
    update["update_code_completion_options()"]
    filter["_filter_code_completion_candidates()"]
    display["Display popup"]
    confirm["_confirm_code_completion()"]
    insert["Insert text"]
    
    request --> add
    add --> update
    update --> filter
    filter --> display
    display --> confirm
    confirm --> insert
```

Sources: [scene/gui/code_edit.cpp:1593-1690](), [doc/classes/CodeEdit.xml:12-33]()

Each completion option is a `Dictionary` containing:
- `kind`: Icon/type identifier (CodeEdit.KIND_CLASS, KIND_FUNCTION, etc.)
- `display_text`: What's shown in the popup
- `insert_text`: What gets inserted when selected
- `font_color`: Optional text color
- `icon`: Optional custom icon
- `default_value`: For parameters, the default value to show

Sources: [scene/gui/code_edit.cpp:1593-1690]()

### Auto-Indentation

CodeEdit automatically adjusts indentation based on:
- `indent_size` and `indent_using_spaces` settings
- Auto-indent prefixes registered with `add_auto_indent_prefix()`
- Current line context

The `do_indent()` method at [scene/gui/code_edit.cpp:2078-2179]() handles inserting the appropriate whitespace when Enter is pressed.

Sources: [scene/gui/code_edit.cpp:2078-2179]()

### Code Folding

Code folding allows collapsing/expanding code blocks. The folding system:
- Identifies foldable regions via `can_fold_line()`
- Folds/unfolds with `fold_line()` / `unfold_line()`
- Uses `set_line_as_hidden()` on TextEdit to hide folded lines
- Draws fold gutter icons to indicate foldable regions

Sources: [scene/gui/code_edit.cpp:2923-3206]()

## LineEdit - Single Line Input

`LineEdit` provides a single-line text input field with selection, IME support, password masking, and virtual keyboard integration.

**LineEdit Architecture:**

```mermaid
graph TB
    LineEdit["LineEdit"]
    
    LineEdit --> text_rid["text_rid: RID<br/>(TextServer shaped text)"]
    LineEdit --> text["text: String<br/>(content)"]
    LineEdit --> ime["ime_text: String<br/>(IME composition)"]
    LineEdit --> caret["caret_column: int"]
    LineEdit --> selection["Selection<br/>(begin, end, enabled)"]
    LineEdit --> undo["undo_text: String"]
    LineEdit --> menu["PopupMenu<br/>(context menu)"]
    LineEdit --> alt["Alt Input<br/>(Unicode/OEM/Windows)"]
    
    subgraph "IME Support"
        ime
        ime_window["_update_ime_window_position()"]
        ime_text["_update_ime_text()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Text Input"
        text
        caret
        alt
    end
    
    subgraph "Selection & Editing"
        selection
        undo
    end
```

Sources: [scene/gui/line_edit.h:93-153](), [scene/gui/line_edit.cpp:56-890]()

### IME (Input Method Editor) Integration

IME support enables entering complex characters (e.g., CJK) using composition windows. The IME lifecycle:

1. **Activate**: `_update_ime_window_position()` positions the OS IME window
2. **Compose**: User types in IME, updates `ime_text` and `ime_selection`
3. **Complete**: Either `apply_ime()` inserts text or `cancel_ime()` discards it

The IME text is displayed merged with the main text during composition but stored separately until confirmed.

Sources: [scene/gui/line_edit.cpp:124-184](), [scene/gui/line_edit.h:309-310]()

### Alt Code Input

LineEdit supports special character entry via Alt codes:
- **ALT_INPUT_UNICODE**: Alt + hexadecimal (e.g., Alt+E1 for Ã¡)
- **ALT_INPUT_OEM**: Alt + decimal OEM code
- **ALT_INPUT_WIN**: Alt + 4-digit Windows code (leading zero required)

The mode is determined by the key combination when Alt is pressed, and digits are accumulated in `alt_code`. On Alt release, `apply_ime()` converts the code to a character.

Sources: [scene/gui/line_edit.cpp:724-849](), [doc/classes/LineEdit.xml:12-15]()

### Password Masking

When `secret` mode is enabled:
- Display uses `secret_character` (default "â€¢") instead of actual text
- A separate shaped text RID is created for rendering
- Actual text remains accessible via `get_text()` for processing

Sources: [scene/gui/line_edit.cpp:1088-1114]()

## RichTextLabel - Rich Text Display

`RichTextLabel` displays formatted text with support for BBCode tags, custom fonts, colors, images, tables, and interactive elements like links.

**RichTextLabel Internal Structure:**

```mermaid
graph TB
    RichTextLabel["RichTextLabel"]
    
    RichTextLabel --> main["main: ItemFrame<br/>(root container)"]
    RichTextLabel --> items["items: RID_Owner&lt;Item&gt;<br/>(item registry)"]
    RichTextLabel --> current["current: Item<br/>(current tag scope)"]
    RichTextLabel --> current_frame["current_frame: ItemFrame<br/>(current paragraph container)"]
    
    ItemFrame --> lines["lines: LocalVector&lt;Line&gt;"]
    
    Line["Line (Paragraph)"]
    Line --> from["from: Item*<br/>(first item)"]
    Line --> text_buf["text_buf: TextParagraph"]
    Line --> text_prefix["text_prefix: TextLine<br/>(for list markers)"]
    
    Item["Item (Tag)"]
    Item --> ItemText
    Item --> ItemImage
    Item --> ItemFont
    Item --> ItemColor
    Item --> ItemTable
    Item --> ItemMeta
    
    subgraph "Item Types"
        ItemText["ItemText<br/>(plain text)"]
        ItemImage["ItemImage<br/>(embedded image)"]
        ItemFont["ItemFont<br/>(font change)"]
        ItemColor["ItemColor<br/>(color change)"]
        ItemTable["ItemTable<br/>(table structure)"]
        ItemMeta["ItemMeta<br/>(clickable link)"]
    end
```

Sources: [scene/gui/rich_text_label.h:160-224](), [scene/gui/rich_text_label.h:225-249](), [scene/gui/rich_text_label.h:251-394]()

### Item Tag Stack

RichTextLabel maintains content as a tree of `Item` objects, where each item represents either:
- Text content (`ItemText`)
- Formatting tag (font, color, size, etc.)
- Structural element (paragraph, list, table)
- Interactive element (meta/link, hint/tooltip)

Items form a linked list via `subitems` and have a `parent` pointer. The tag stack determines the active formatting for text rendering.

**Tag Stack Example:**

```mermaid
graph TB
    main["ItemFrame (main)"]
    
    font["ItemFont<br/>(bold font)"]
    color["ItemColor<br/>(red)"]
    text1["ItemText<br/>('Hello ')"]
    
    color2["ItemColor<br/>(blue)"]
    text2["ItemText<br/>('World')"]
    
    main --> font
    font --> color
    color --> text1
    color --> color2
    color2 --> text2
    
    style text1 fill:#f9f9f9
    style text2 fill:#f9f9f9
```

Sources: [scene/gui/rich_text_label.h:197-223]()

### Line (Paragraph) Structure

Each `Line` in a `Frame` represents a paragraph and contains:
- `from`: Pointer to the first Item in this paragraph
- `text_buf`: TextParagraph for the shaped paragraph text
- `text_buf_disp`: Optional alternate buffer for `visible_characters` mode
- `text_prefix`: List marker text (for numbered/bulleted lists)
- `offset`, `indent`: Layout positioning

The `_shape_line()` method at [scene/gui/rich_text_label.cpp:647-852]() walks the item tree, builds the paragraph text, and shapes it with TextServer.

Sources: [scene/gui/rich_text_label.h:163-195](), [scene/gui/rich_text_label.cpp:647-852]()

### BBCode Parsing

When `bbcode_enabled` is true, the `text` property is parsed into the item tree:
1. `_process_line()` scans for BBCode tags (e.g., `[b]`, `[color=#ff0000]`)
2. For each tag, creates corresponding Item subclass (ItemFont, ItemColor, etc.)
3. Pushes/pops items on the tag stack
4. Creates ItemText for literal text between tags

The `append_text()` method allows incremental BBCode appending without rebuilding the entire tree.

Sources: [scene/gui/rich_text_label.cpp:3272-3977]()

### Table Support

`ItemTable` creates a table with cells as `ItemFrame` children. Table layout:
- Columns defined with width constraints
- Each cell is a separate ItemFrame with its own line/item tree
- `_update_table_column_width()` computes column sizes based on content
- `_update_table_size()` positions cells and calculates total table dimensions

Sources: [scene/gui/rich_text_label.h:370-393](), [scene/gui/rich_text_label.cpp:556-644]()

### Custom Effects

RichTextLabel supports custom text effects via `ItemCustomFX` and `RichTextEffect` classes:
- Effects update per frame via `_process_custom_fx()`
- `CharFXTransform` provides glyph data to effect processing
- Built-in effects: wave, tornado, rainbow, shake, pulse, fade

Sources: [scene/gui/rich_text_label.h:96-105]()

## Label - Simple Text Display

`Label` is a lightweight text display control optimized for static or infrequently-updated text. It supports alignment, wrapping, and text overflow modes.

**Label Text Rendering:**

```mermaid
graph TB
    Label["Label"]
    
    Label --> xl_text["xl_text: String<br/>(translated text)"]
    Label --> paragraphs["paragraphs: Vector&lt;Paragraph&gt;"]
    
    Paragraph["Paragraph"]
    Paragraph --> text_rid["text_rid: RID<br/>(TextServer)"]
    Paragraph --> lines_rid["lines_rid: Vector&lt;RID&gt;<br/>(wrapped lines)"]
    Paragraph --> text["text: String"]
    Paragraph --> start["start: int<br/>(char offset)"]
    Paragraph --> dirty["dirty, lines_dirty: bool"]
    
    Label --> settings["settings: LabelSettings<br/>(optional override)"]
    
    paragraphs --> Paragraph
    
    Label --> _shape["_shape()<br/>(text shaping)"]
    _shape --> TextServer["TextServer::shaped_text_*"]
```

Sources: [scene/gui/label.h:38-131](), [scene/gui/label.cpp:143-241]()

Label splits text into paragraphs at newline boundaries (or custom `paragraph_separator`), shapes each paragraph with TextServer, then breaks into wrapped lines based on `autowrap_mode`.

### LabelSettings Resource

`LabelSettings` is a shareable Resource that defines text appearance:
- Font and font size
- Font color
- Outline size and color
- Shadow offset, size, and color
- Line spacing

When assigned to a Label's `settings` property, these override the theme values.

Sources: [scene/resources/label_settings.h:34-75](), [scene/gui/label.cpp:116-141]()

## Text Rendering Pipeline

All text components ultimately rely on the **TextServer** API for text shaping, layout, and rendering. TextServer handles:
- BiDi (bidirectional) text resolution
- Complex script shaping (Arabic, Devanagari, etc.)
- Line breaking and wrapping
- Font glyph rendering
- OpenType feature application

**TextServer Integration Flow:**

```mermaid
graph TB
    Component["Text Component<br/>(TextEdit/LineEdit/Label/etc.)"]
    
    TextParagraph["TextParagraph<br/>(scene/resources/text_paragraph.h)"]
    TextLine["TextLine<br/>(scene/resources/text_line.h)"]
    
    TextServer["TextServer<br/>(servers/text/text_server.h)"]
    
    shaped_rid["Shaped Text RID"]
    
    Font["Font Resource"]
    FontRID["Font RID"]
    
    RenderingServer["RenderingServer<br/>(glyph drawing)"]
    
    Component -->|"add_string()"| TextParagraph
    Component -->|"add_string()"| TextLine
    
    TextParagraph -->|"TS->shaped_text_*"| TextServer
    TextLine -->|"TS->shaped_text_*"| TextServer
    
    TextServer --> shaped_rid
    
    Font --> FontRID
    TextServer -->|"uses"| FontRID
    
    TextParagraph -->|"draw*()"| RenderingServer
    TextLine -->|"draw*()"| RenderingServer
    
    shaped_rid -->|"draw commands"| RenderingServer
```

Sources: [scene/gui/text_edit.cpp:58-448](), [scene/gui/line_edit.cpp:852-1114](), [scene/gui/label.cpp:143-241](), [scene/gui/rich_text_label.cpp:647-852]()

### TextParagraph and TextLine

These are wrapper classes around TextServer's shaped text functionality:

- **TextParagraph**: Handles multi-line text with wrapping, tabs, and alignment
  - Used by TextEdit, RichTextLabel, Label
  - Methods: `add_string()`, `add_object()` (inline images), `tab_align()`, `get_line_count()`, `draw_line()`

- **TextLine**: Handles single-line text
  - Used by LineEdit, gutter text, list prefixes
  - Methods: `add_string()`, `get_size()`, `draw()`

Both create RIDs via TextServer (`TS->create_shaped_text()`) and configure shaping parameters (direction, break flags, fonts).

Sources: [scene/resources/text_paragraph.h](), [scene/resources/text_line.h]()

### Font and Glyph Rendering

Fonts are loaded as `Font` resources which generate RIDs for TextServer. When drawing text:
1. TextParagraph/TextLine calls `TS->shaped_text_draw()` or `TS->shaped_text_draw_outline()`
2. TextServer iterates glyphs in the shaped text
3. For each glyph, retrieves texture from font cache
4. Issues draw commands to RenderingServer (textured quads)

The font system supports:
- Multiple font variations (bold, italic, mono)
- OpenType features (ligatures, kerning, etc.)
- Spacing adjustments (glyph, space, top, bottom)
- Fallback fonts for missing glyphs

Sources: [scene/gui/text_edit.cpp:422-448](), [servers/text/text_server.cpp]()

### Accessibility Integration

All text components integrate with `AccessibilityServer` to expose text content to screen readers:

- **TextEdit**: Creates accessibility elements per wrapped line via `text.update_accessibility()`
- **LineEdit**: Single accessibility element for the text field
- **RichTextLabel**: Accessibility elements per line with metadata
- **Label**: Accessibility element with full text content

The accessibility elements receive text selection updates and support text navigation actions.

Sources: [scene/gui/text_edit.cpp:242-260](), [scene/gui/text_edit.cpp:752-833](), [scene/gui/rich_text_label.cpp:112-118]()29:T4da7,# Input Processing and GUI Events

## Purpose and Scope

This page describes how input events (mouse, keyboard, touch, gamepad) flow through Godot's scene tree to reach GUI controls and scene nodes. It covers the multi-stage input processing pipeline, the role of `Viewport` in distributing events, and how `Control` nodes intercept GUI-specific input.

For information about Control layout and theming, see [Control Nodes and Layout System](#5.1). For details about the scene tree structure, see [Scene Tree and Node System](#2.2).

---

## Input Event Pipeline Overview

Input events in Godot follow a well-defined processing order through the scene tree. The `Viewport` acts as the entry point, dispatching events to nodes that have registered for different input processing stages.

```mermaid
graph TB
    OS["Operating System<br/>Input Event"]
    
    VP["Viewport<br/>_push_input()"]
    
    InputGroup["_input() Nodes<br/>Group: _vp_input"]
    GUIProc["GUI Input Processing<br/>_gui_call_input()"]
    ShortcutGroup["_shortcut_input() Nodes<br/>Group: _vp_shortcut_input"]
    UnhandledKeyGroup["_unhandled_key_input() Nodes<br/>Group: _vp_unhandled_key_input"]
    UnhandledGroup["_unhandled_input() Nodes<br/>Group: _vp_unhandled_input"]
    
    Handled{{"Input Handled?"}}
    
    OS --> VP
    VP --> InputGroup
    InputGroup --> Handled
    Handled -->|No| GUIProc
    GUIProc --> Handled
    Handled -->|No| ShortcutGroup
    ShortcutGroup --> Handled
    Handled -->|No| UnhandledKeyGroup
    UnhandledKeyGroup --> Handled
    Handled -->|No| UnhandledGroup
    Handled -->|Yes| Done["Event Consumed"]
    UnhandledGroup --> Done
    
    style VP fill:#f9f9f9
    style GUIProc fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Input Processing Stages**

| Stage | Group Name | Purpose | Typical Use Case |
|-------|-----------|---------|------------------|
| `_input()` | `_vp_input{viewport_id}` | First to receive all events | Raw input monitoring, debugging |
| GUI Processing | N/A | Control nodes handle GUI events | Button clicks, text input |
| `_shortcut_input()` | `_vp_shortcut_input{viewport_id}` | Shortcuts before GUI | Global hotkeys, accessibility shortcuts |
| `_unhandled_key_input()` | `_vp_unhandled_key_input{viewport_id}` | Unhandled keyboard events | Character input, text shortcuts |
| `_unhandled_input()` | `_vp_unhandled_input{viewport_id}` | Final catch-all | Gameplay input, camera control |

**Sources:** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1111-1279](), [scene/main/node.cpp:171-182](), [doc/classes/Node.xml:72-150]()

---

## Viewport Input Distribution

The `Viewport` class is responsible for receiving input events from the operating system and distributing them to the appropriate nodes.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph Viewport["Viewport"]
        PushInput["_push_input(InputEvent)"]
        CallInput["_gui_call_input(Control, InputEvent)"]
        FindControl["_gui_find_control(Point2)"]
        ProcessPicking["_process_picking()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "GUI State"
        MouseOver["gui.mouse_over<br/>(Control under cursor)"]
        KeyFocus["gui.key_focus<br/>(Focused control)"]
        MouseFocus["gui.mouse_focus<br/>(Drag/scroll control)"]
        TooltipPopup["gui.tooltip_popup"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Physics Picking"
        Physics2D["physics_2d_mouseover<br/>HashMap<ObjectID, frame>"]
        Physics3D["physics_object_over<br/>ObjectID"]
    end
    
    PushInput --> CallInput
    PushInput --> ProcessPicking
    CallInput --> FindControl
    FindControl --> MouseOver
    CallInput --> KeyFocus
    CallInput --> MouseFocus
    
    ProcessPicking --> Physics2D
    ProcessPicking --> Physics3D
    
    style Viewport fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Key Methods**

- **`Viewport::_push_input(InputEvent)`** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1111-1279](): Main entry point for input events. Calls groups in order and handles the `local_input_handled` flag.

- **`Viewport::_gui_call_input(Control, InputEvent)`** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1653-1761](): Distributes GUI events to the appropriate control, handling focus and mouse-over state.

- **`Viewport::_gui_find_control(Point2)`** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1507-1544](): Performs a hit test to find the topmost control at a given position, respecting `mouse_filter` settings.

- **`Viewport::_process_picking()`** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:779-1109](): Handles physics object picking for both 2D and 3D scenes, generating input events for `CollisionObject2D` and `CollisionObject3D` nodes.

**Sources:** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:779-1279](), [scene/main/viewport.h:335-427]()

---

## GUI Input Processing in Viewports

The viewport maintains several state variables to track GUI interactions:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "GUI State Structure (viewport.h)"
        MousePos["mouse_pos: Point2"]
        MouseOver["mouse_over: ObjectID"]
        KeyFocus["key_focus: Control*"]
        MouseFocus["mouse_focus: Control*"]
        MouseClick["mouse_click_grabber: Control*"]
        TooltipControl["tooltip_control: Control*"]
        DragPreview["drag_preview_id: ObjectID"]
    end
    
    subgraph "State Transitions"
        MouseMove["Mouse Motion"] --> MouseOver
        MouseButton["Mouse Button"] --> MouseClick
        FocusGrab["grab_focus()"] --> KeyFocus
        DragStart["Drag Start"] --> DragPreview
        Hover["Hover Timeout"] --> TooltipControl
    end
    
    style MouseOver fill:#f9f9f9
    style KeyFocus fill:#f9f9f9
    style MouseFocus fill:#f9f9f9
```

**GUI Processing Flow**

1. **Mouse Motion Events** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1763-1890]():
   - Find control under cursor via `_gui_find_control()`
   - Update `gui.mouse_over` if control changed
   - Send `NOTIFICATION_MOUSE_ENTER` and `NOTIFICATION_MOUSE_EXIT` to controls
   - Call `_gui_input()` on the control under cursor

2. **Mouse Button Events** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1892-2063]():
   - On press: Set `gui.mouse_click_grabber` for drag operations
   - Check for double-click by comparing with `gui.mouse_click_pos` and timing
   - Call `_gui_input()` on focused control or control under cursor
   - Handle focus changes if control has `FOCUS_CLICK` mode

3. **Keyboard Events** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:2065-2157]():
   - Send to `gui.key_focus` if set
   - Process navigation keys (arrows, tab) for focus traversal
   - Handle shortcut matching

**Sources:** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1507-2157](), [scene/main/viewport.h:335-427]()

---

## Control Input Handling

`Control` nodes provide GUI-specific input handling through the `_gui_input()` virtual method and mouse filter settings.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph Control["Control Node"]
        GuiInput["_gui_input(InputEvent)"]
        MouseFilter["mouse_filter"]
        FocusMode["focus_mode"]
        AcceptEvent["accept_event()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Mouse Filter Modes"
        Stop["MOUSE_FILTER_STOP<br/>Intercepts all events"]
        Pass["MOUSE_FILTER_PASS<br/>Receives but doesn't block"]
        Ignore["MOUSE_FILTER_IGNORE<br/>Completely transparent"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Focus Modes"
        FocusNone["FOCUS_NONE<br/>Cannot receive focus"]
        FocusClick["FOCUS_CLICK<br/>Focus on mouse click"]
        FocusAll["FOCUS_ALL<br/>Click or keyboard nav"]
    end
    
    MouseFilter -.-> Stop
    MouseFilter -.-> Pass
    MouseFilter -.-> Ignore
    
    FocusMode -.-> FocusNone
    FocusMode -.-> FocusClick
    FocusMode -.-> FocusAll
    
    GuiInput --> AcceptEvent
    
    style Control fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Mouse Filter Implementation**

The mouse filter determines how controls respond to mouse events during the `_gui_find_control()` hit test:

| Mode | Behavior | Use Case |
|------|----------|----------|
| `MOUSE_FILTER_STOP` | Blocks event propagation to controls behind it | Buttons, clickable panels |
| `MOUSE_FILTER_PASS` | Receives events but allows pass-through | Overlays that monitor but don't block |
| `MOUSE_FILTER_IGNORE` | Completely transparent to mouse events | Decorative elements, labels |

**Implementation** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1507-1544]():
```
Control *_gui_find_control(Point2 p_global) {
    // Checks mouse_filter and visibility
    // MOUSE_FILTER_IGNORE nodes are skipped
    // MOUSE_FILTER_STOP blocks further search
    // MOUSE_FILTER_PASS allows checking children
}
```

**Sources:** [scene/gui/control.cpp:2684-2745](), [scene/gui/control.h:89-93](), [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1507-1544]()

---

## Node Input Method Registration

Nodes that override input methods are automatically registered to viewport-specific groups for efficient event distribution.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Node NOTIFICATION_ENTER_TREE"
        CheckInput["Check if _input() overridden"]
        CheckShortcut["Check if _shortcut_input() overridden"]
        CheckUnhandled["Check if _unhandled_input() overridden"]
        CheckUnhandledKey["Check if _unhandled_key_input() overridden"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Viewport Groups"
        InputGroup["add_to_group('_vp_input' + viewport_id)"]
        ShortcutGroup["add_to_group('_vp_shortcut_input' + viewport_id)"]
        UnhandledGroup["add_to_group('_vp_unhandled_input' + viewport_id)"]
        UnhandledKeyGroup["add_to_group('_vp_unhandled_key_input' + viewport_id)"]
    end
    
    CheckInput -->|Yes| InputGroup
    CheckShortcut -->|Yes| ShortcutGroup
    CheckUnhandled -->|Yes| UnhandledGroup
    CheckUnhandledKey -->|Yes| UnhandledKeyGroup
    
    style InputGroup fill:#f9f9f9
    style ShortcutGroup fill:#f9f9f9
    style UnhandledGroup fill:#f9f9f9
    style UnhandledKeyGroup fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Automatic Registration** [scene/main/node.cpp:171-182]():

When a node enters the tree, it checks if it has overridden any input virtual methods. If so, it adds itself to the corresponding viewport group. The groups are named with the viewport instance ID to ensure each viewport maintains its own input processing lists.

**Manual Control** [scene/main/node.cpp:258-272]():

Nodes can also manually enable/disable input processing:
- `set_process_input(bool)` - Enable/disable `_input()` processing
- `set_process_shortcut_input(bool)` - Enable/disable `_shortcut_input()` processing
- `set_process_unhandled_input(bool)` - Enable/disable `_unhandled_input()` processing
- `set_process_unhandled_key_input(bool)` - Enable/disable `_unhandled_key_input()` processing

**Sources:** [scene/main/node.cpp:171-182](), [scene/main/node.cpp:258-272](), [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1111-1279]()

## Focus Management System

The focus system determines which control receives keyboard input and how focus is represented visually.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Focus State (Viewport)"
        KeyFocus["gui.key_focus: Control*<br/>Current focused control"]
        FocusOwner["gui_get_focus_owner()"]
        HideFocus["gui.hide_focus<br/>Hide visual focus indicator"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Focus Actions"
        GrabFocus["Control::grab_focus()"]
        ReleaseFocus["Control::release_focus()"]
        FindNext["_gui_find_next_focusable()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Focus Events"
        FocusEntered["NOTIFICATION_FOCUS_ENTERED"]
        FocusExited["NOTIFICATION_FOCUS_EXITED"]
    end
    
    GrabFocus --> KeyFocus
    GrabFocus --> FocusEntered
    ReleaseFocus --> FocusExited
    KeyFocus --> FocusOwner
    
    TabKey["Tab Key"] --> FindNext
    FindNext --> GrabFocus
    
    MouseClick["Mouse Click on FOCUS_CLICK"] --> HideFocus
    KeyboardInput["Keyboard/Gamepad Input"] -.->|Shows| HideFocus
    
    style KeyFocus fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Focus Behavior**

- **Focus Modes** [scene/gui/control.h:66-71]():
  - `FOCUS_NONE` (0): Control cannot receive keyboard focus
  - `FOCUS_CLICK` (1): Focus on mouse click only
  - `FOCUS_ALL` (2): Focus via mouse or keyboard navigation
  - `FOCUS_ACCESSIBILITY` (3): Focus for accessibility, not shown visually

- **Visual Focus Hiding** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:572-586]():
  The `gui.hide_focus` flag automatically hides focus rectangles when using mouse input and shows them for keyboard/gamepad input. This improves accessibility while keeping the UI clean for mouse users.

- **Focus Navigation** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:2065-2157]():
  Tab, Shift+Tab, and arrow keys trigger focus traversal using `_gui_find_next_focusable()`, which searches the control tree for the next focusable control in tree order.

**Sources:** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:572-586](), [scene/main/viewport.cpp:2065-2157](), [scene/gui/control.cpp:2586-2636](), [scene/gui/control.h:66-71]()

## Physics Object Picking

Viewports support picking of physics objects (2D and 3D) alongside GUI controls, enabling interaction with non-GUI scene elements.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Physics Picking Process"
        ProcessPicking["Viewport::_process_picking()"]
        PickEvents["physics_picking_events<br/>List<InputEvent>"]
        
        subgraph "2D Picking"
            SS2D["PhysicsDirectSpaceState2D"]
            IntersectPoint["intersect_point()"]
            CO2D["CollisionObject2D"]
            MouseEnter2D["_mouse_enter()"]
            InputEvent2D["_input_event_call()"]
        end
        
        subgraph "3D Picking"
            SS3D["PhysicsDirectSpaceState3D"]
            IntersectRay["intersect_ray()"]
            CO3D["CollisionObject3D"]
            MouseEnter3D["_mouse_enter()"]
            InputEvent3D["_collision_object_3d_input_event()"]
        end
    end
    
    ProcessPicking --> PickEvents
    PickEvents --> SS2D
    PickEvents --> SS3D
    
    SS2D --> IntersectPoint
    IntersectPoint --> CO2D
    CO2D --> MouseEnter2D
    CO2D --> InputEvent2D
    
    SS3D --> IntersectRay
    IntersectRay --> CO3D
    CO3D --> MouseEnter3D
    CO3D --> InputEvent3D
    
    style ProcessPicking fill:#f9f9f9
```

**2D Physics Picking** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:899-991]():

For each canvas layer, the viewport:
1. Converts mouse position to canvas space
2. Calls `PhysicsDirectSpaceState2D::intersect_point()` with `pick_point = true`
3. Sorts results by Z-index if `physics_object_picking_sort` is enabled
4. Sends `_input_event_call()` to `CollisionObject2D` instances
5. Tracks mouse enter/exit per object and per shape

**3D Physics Picking** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:994-1109]():

1. Projects ray from camera through mouse position
2. Calls `PhysicsDirectSpaceState3D::intersect_ray()` with `pick_ray = true`
3. Sends `_collision_object_3d_input_event()` to `CollisionObject3D`
4. Supports object capture via `get_capture_input_on_drag()`
5. Maintains `physics_object_over` for mouse enter/exit tracking

**Configuration** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:783-806]():
- `physics_object_picking`: Enable/disable physics picking
- `physics_object_picking_sort`: Sort 2D results by Z-index
- `physics_object_picking_first_only`: Stop after first hit

**Sources:** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:779-1109](), [scene/main/viewport.h:272-282]()

## Drag and Drop System

Controls support drag and drop operations through three virtual methods: `_get_drag_data()`, `_can_drop_data()`, and `_drop_data()`.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Drag Source"
        GetDragData["_get_drag_data(pos)<br/>Returns drag data"]
        SetPreview["set_drag_preview(Control)<br/>Visual feedback"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Viewport Drag State"
        DragData["gui.drag_data: Variant"]
        DragPreview["gui.drag_preview_id: ObjectID"]
        DragMouse["gui.drag_mouse_over: Control*"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Drop Target"
        CanDrop["_can_drop_data(pos, data)<br/>Returns bool"]
        DoDrop["_drop_data(pos, data)<br/>Consumes data"]
    end
    
    MouseDrag["Mouse Drag Detected"] --> GetDragData
    GetDragData --> DragData
    SetPreview --> DragPreview
    
    DragData --> CanDrop
    CanDrop -->|true| Highlight["Visual highlight"]
    
    MouseRelease["Mouse Release"] --> CanDrop
    CanDrop -->|true| DoDrop
    
    style DragData fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Drag Initiation** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1892-2063]():

When mouse movement exceeds `GLOBAL_GET("gui/common/default_drag_threshold")` during a button press:
1. Viewport calls `_get_drag_data()` on the control
2. If non-null data returned, drag starts
3. Optional: Call `set_drag_preview()` to show visual feedback
4. `gui.drag_data` stores the dragged data

**Drop Validation** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1653-1761]():

During drag, for each control under the cursor:
1. Call `_can_drop_data(pos, data)` to check if drop is allowed
2. If true, control can receive visual highlight
3. On mouse release, call `_drop_data(pos, data)` to complete the operation

**Keyboard/Accessibility Drag** [doc/classes/Control.xml:95-101]():

When drag is initiated via keyboard or `accessibility_drag()`, the `pos` parameter is set to `Vector2.INF`, indicating the control should use the current selected item position.

**Sources:** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1892-2063](), [scene/gui/control.cpp:2684-2745](), [doc/classes/Control.xml:33-86]()

## Input Handling and Event Propagation

Input events can be marked as "handled" to prevent further propagation through the input pipeline.

```mermaid
graph TB
    Event["InputEvent"]
    
    AcceptEvent["Viewport::accept_event()"]
    SetHandled["Viewport::set_input_as_handled()"]
    
    IsHandled["Viewport::is_input_handled()"]
    LocalHandled["local_input_handled flag"]
    
    Event --> Stage1["_input() nodes"]
    Stage1 --> AcceptEvent
    AcceptEvent --> LocalHandled
    SetHandled --> LocalHandled
    
    LocalHandled -->|true| Stop["Stop propagation"]
    LocalHandled -->|false| Stage2["GUI processing"]
    
    Stage2 --> AcceptEvent
    Stage2 --> Stage3["_shortcut_input() nodes"]
    Stage3 --> Stage4["_unhandled_key_input() nodes"]
    Stage4 --> Stage5["_unhandled_input() nodes"]
    
    IsHandled -.-> LocalHandled
    
    style LocalHandled fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Handling Methods**

- **`Viewport::accept_event()`** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1279-1282](): Marks the current event as handled. This is the preferred method for nodes to indicate they've consumed an event.

- **`Viewport::set_input_as_handled()`** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1279-1282](): Explicitly sets the handled flag. Used internally by GUI processing.

- **`Viewport::is_input_handled()`** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1284-1295](): Checks if the current event has been marked as handled. Subsequent processing stages can skip handled events.

**Handle Input Locally** [scene/main/viewport.h:284-286]():

The `handle_input_locally` property controls whether a viewport processes input itself or delegates to its parent. When `false`, input is forwarded to the parent window's viewport, enabling embedded viewports to optionally pass input up the hierarchy.

**Sources:** [scene/main/viewport.cpp:1279-1295](), [scene/main/viewport.h:284-286](), [doc/classes/Viewport.xml:82-87]()2a:T572a,# Scripting System
