## Resource Saving System

### ResourceSaver Singleton

The `ResourceSaver` singleton manages resource serialization to disk through registered `ResourceFormatSaver` instances.

```mermaid
graph LR
    Client["Client Code"]
    RS["ResourceSaver<br/>(singleton)"]
    Savers["ResourceFormatSaver[]<br/>saver[MAX_SAVERS]"]
    
    TextSaver["ResourceSaverText<br/>(.tres, .tscn)"]
    BinarySaver["ResourceSaverBinary<br/>(.res, .scn)"]
    
    Client -->|"save(resource, path)"| RS
    RS -->|queries| Savers
    Savers -->|contains| TextSaver
    Savers -->|contains| BinarySaver
    
    RS -->|"save()"| Selected["Selected Saver"]
    Selected -->|writes| File["File on disk"]
```

**Save Function:**
- `ResourceSaver::save(resource, path, flags)` - Main save API
- Iterates through registered savers to find one that recognizes the resource
- Savers check resource type and file extension

Sources: [core/io/resource_saver.h:59-100](), [core/io/resource_saver.cpp:102-161]()

### ResourceFormatSaver Interface

Custom resource savers implement the `ResourceFormatSaver` interface:

| Virtual Method | Purpose |
|----------------|---------|
| `_save()` | Serialize resource to file at given path |
| `_recognize()` | Return true if this saver handles the resource type |
| `_get_recognized_extensions()` | Return list of supported file extensions |
| `_set_uid()` | Update UID in resource file |

Sources: [core/io/resource_saver.h:36-56](), [core/io/resource_saver.cpp:46-100]()

### Save Flags

| Flag | Purpose |
|------|---------|
| `FLAG_NONE` | Default behavior |
| `FLAG_RELATIVE_PATHS` | Save paths relative to scene |
| `FLAG_BUNDLE_RESOURCES` | Bundle sub-resources into main file |
| `FLAG_CHANGE_PATH` | Update resource's path to saved path |
| `FLAG_OMIT_EDITOR_PROPERTIES` | Skip editor-only properties |
| `FLAG_SAVE_BIG_ENDIAN` | Use big-endian byte order |
| `FLAG_COMPRESS` | Compress resource data |
| `FLAG_REPLACE_SUBRESOURCE_PATHS` | Replace sub-resource paths |

Sources: [core/io/resource_saver.h:62-71]()

---

## Resource Formats

### Text Format (.tres, .tscn)

The text format uses human-readable syntax based on `VariantParser`. Files are structured with sections:

```
[gd_resource type="ResourceType" format=4]

[ext_resource type="Texture2D" path="res://texture.png" id="1"]

[sub_resource type="Material" id="material_1"]
property = value

[resource]
property = value
external_property = ExtResource("1")
```

**Text Format Components:**
- `ResourceLoaderText` - Text format loader
- `ResourceSaverText` - Text format saver
- Section headers: `[gd_resource]`, `[ext_resource]`, `[sub_resource]`, `[resource]`
- External resources referenced by ID
- Sub-resources embedded in the file

Sources: [scene/resources/resource_format_text.h:40-143](), [scene/resources/resource_format_text.cpp:452-909]()

### Binary Format (.res, .scn)

The binary format provides faster loading and smaller file sizes:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Header["File Header<br/>Magic: 'RSRC'<br/>Version<br/>Flags"]
    Strings["String Table<br/>StringName pool"]
    ExtRes["External Resources<br/>Path, Type, UID"]
    IntRes["Internal Resources<br/>Offsets to resource data"]
    ResData["Resource Data<br/>Type, Properties, Values"]
    
    Header --> Strings
    Strings --> ExtRes
    ExtRes --> IntRes
    IntRes --> ResData
```

**Binary Format Components:**
- `ResourceLoaderBinary` - Binary format loader
- `ResourceFormatSaverBinary` - Binary format saver
- String table for efficient string storage
- Resource references stored as indices
- Properties stored as type-tagged variants

Sources: [core/io/resource_format_binary.h:38-107](), [core/io/resource_format_binary.cpp:682-912]()

### Format Variant Encoding

Both formats use custom variant encoding defined in the loader/saver implementations. The binary format uses integer type tags (e.g., `VARIANT_INT = 3`, `VARIANT_STRING = 5`) while text format uses `VariantParser`.

Sources: [core/io/resource_format_binary.cpp:46-102](), [core/io/resource_format_binary.cpp:174-676]()

---

## Resource Import Pipeline

### Import System Overview

Imported assets (images, audio, models, etc.) use a two-file system:
1. Source file (e.g., `texture.png`)
2. Metadata file (e.g., `texture.png.import`)

The `.import` file contains import settings and points to the processed resource in `.godot/imported/`.

```mermaid
graph TB
    Source["Source File<br/>texture.png"]
    Import["Metadata File<br/>texture.png.import"]
    Imported["Imported Resource<br/>.godot/imported/texture.png-[hash].ctex"]
    
    Source -.->|"processed by"| Importer["ResourceImporter<br/>(plugin)"]
    Importer -->|generates| Import
    Importer -->|generates| Imported
    
    Import -->|"path=..."| Imported
    Import -->|"type=CompressedTexture2D"| ImportType
    Import -->|"importer=texture"| ImporterName
    
    Client["Client Code"] -->|"load('texture.png')"| RFI["ResourceFormatImporter"]
    RFI -->|reads| Import
    RFI -->|loads| Imported
    RFI -->|returns| Resource["Ref&lt;Resource&gt;"]
```

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.h:41-107](), [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:44-201]()

### ResourceFormatImporter

The `ResourceFormatImporter` loader reads `.import` metadata files and delegates to the actual resource loader for the imported file:

**Import Metadata Structure:**
```ini
[remap]
path="res://.godot/imported/texture.png-abc123.ctex"
type="CompressedTexture2D"
importer="texture"
uid="uid://abc123"

[params]
compress/mode=0
mipmaps/generate=true
```

**Loading Flow:**
1. Client calls `ResourceLoader::load("res://texture.png")`
2. `ResourceFormatImporter::recognize_path()` returns true if `.import` file exists
3. `ResourceFormatImporter::_get_path_and_type()` parses `.import` file
4. Extracted path loaded via `ResourceLoader::_load()`
5. Result returned to client

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:44-156](), [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:158-201]()

### ResourceImporter Interface

Importers implement the `ResourceImporter` interface to process source assets:

| Virtual Method | Purpose |
|----------------|---------|
| `get_importer_name()` | Return unique importer identifier |
| `get_recognized_extensions()` | Return list of source file extensions |
| `get_save_extension()` | Return extension for imported resource |
| `get_resource_type()` | Return resource class name for imports |
| `get_import_options()` | Return list of configurable import options |
| `import()` | Process source file and generate imported resource |

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.h:109-183]()

### Editor File System Integration

In the editor, `EditorFileSystem` scans for assets and triggers imports when needed. It maintains the import metadata and handles reimporting when source files or settings change.

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:158-201]()

---

## External Resource Dependencies

Resources can reference other resources as dependencies. The loader systems track these dependencies for proper loading order and dependency analysis.

### Dependency Formats

Dependencies are returned as strings in specific formats:

**With UID:**
```
uid://abc123::ResourceType::res://fallback/path.res
```

**Without UID:**
```
res://path/to/resource.res::ResourceType
res://path/to/resource.res
```

The loader systems parse these strings to load dependent resources, preferring UID-based lookup when available.

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:184-203](), [scene/resources/resource_format_text.cpp:926-996]()

### External Resource Loading

For text format resources, external resources are loaded asynchronously during the main resource load:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Loader as ResourceLoaderText
    participant RL as ResourceLoader
    participant ExtRes as External Resource
    
    Loader->>Loader: Parse [ext_resource] sections
    loop For each ext_resource
        Loader->>RL: _load_start(ext_path, type)
        RL-->>Loader: LoadToken
        Loader->>Loader: Store in ext_resources map
    end
    
    Loader->>Loader: Parse main resource
    Loader->>Loader: Parse property with ExtResource("id")
    Loader->>RL: _load_complete(load_token)
    RL-->>Loader: Ref<Resource>
    Loader->>Loader: Set property value
```

Sources: [scene/resources/resource_format_text.cpp:452-538](), [scene/resources/resource_format_text.cpp:126-182]()

---

## Thread Safety and Synchronization

The resource loading system uses several synchronization mechanisms to ensure thread safety:

| Mechanism | Purpose |
|-----------|---------|
| `thread_load_mutex` | Protects thread load task registry |
| `ResourceCache::lock` | Protects resource cache access |
| `LoadToken` reference counting | Ensures task lifetime during load |
| `ConditionVariable` | Allows threads to wait for load completion |

**Key Thread-Safe Operations:**
- `ResourceLoader::load()` can be called from any thread
- Cache lookups use mutex protection
- Load tasks use atomic status updates
- Worker thread pool distributes load operations

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.h:219](), [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:226-273](), [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:812-947]()2e:T59a6,# Resource Loading and Caching

**Purpose**: This document describes the resource loading system in Godot, which manages loading, caching, and lifetime of `Resource` objects from disk. It covers the `ResourceLoader` singleton, the global `ResourceCache`, format-specific loaders, and the threaded loading infrastructure.

For information about the resource import pipeline that processes assets before they can be loaded, see [Resource Import Pipeline](#7.2). For information about the `Resource` base class itself, see the class documentation.

---

## Overview

The resource loading system provides a unified interface for loading resources from various file formats while maintaining a global cache to prevent duplicate loads and enable resource sharing across the engine.

```mermaid
graph TB
    User["User Code<br/>(load, preload)"]
    RL["ResourceLoader<br/>Singleton"]
    Cache["ResourceCache<br/>Global Registry"]
    
    subgraph "Format Loaders"
        Text["ResourceLoaderText<br/>.tres, .tscn"]
        Binary["ResourceLoaderBinary<br/>.res, .scn"]
        Importer["ResourceFormatImporter<br/>.import files"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Loaded Resources"
        Res["Resource Instances"]
    end
    
    User -->|"load(path)"| RL
    RL -->|"check cache"| Cache
    Cache -->|"cache hit"| Res
    RL -->|"cache miss"| Text
    RL --> Binary
    RL --> Importer
    Text -->|"instantiate"| Res
    Binary --> Res
    Importer --> Res
    Res -->|"register"| Cache
```

**Key Components**:
- **ResourceLoader**: Singleton managing all resource loading
- **ResourceCache**: Global path-to-resource mapping
- **ResourceFormatLoader**: Interface for format-specific loaders
- **LoadToken**: Handle for threaded load operations
- **ThreadLoadTask**: Internal state for in-progress loads

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.h:105-311](), [core/io/resource.h:197-215]()

---

## ResourceLoader Singleton

The `ResourceLoader` class provides the main API for loading resources. It maintains a registry of format loaders and coordinates loading, caching, and threading.

### Core Loading API

| Method | Description |
|--------|-------------|
| `load(path, type_hint, cache_mode)` | Synchronous load, blocks until complete |
| `load_threaded_request(path, type_hint, use_sub_threads, cache_mode)` | Initiate async load |
| `load_threaded_get_status(path, progress)` | Check async load status |
| `load_threaded_get(path)` | Retrieve completed async resource |
| `exists(path, type_hint)` | Check if resource can be loaded |

```mermaid
graph LR
    load["ResourceLoader::load()"]
    start["_load_start()"]
    complete["_load_complete()"]
    internal["_load()"]
    format["ResourceFormatLoader::load()"]
    
    load --> start
    start --> internal
    internal --> format
    format --> complete
    complete --> Resource
```

The `load()` method is the primary synchronous entry point. It calls `_load_start()` to begin the load, which may execute immediately or spawn a thread depending on the context.

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.h:233-244](), [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:513-536]()

### Format Loader Registration

ResourceLoader maintains an array of up to `MAX_LOADERS` (64) format loaders. When loading, it queries each loader's `recognize_path()` method to find a compatible handler.

```cpp
// Simplified loading logic from resource_loader.cpp:275-293
bool found = false;
Ref<Resource> res;
for (int i = 0; i < loader_count; i++) {
    if (!loader[i]->recognize_path(p_path, p_type_hint)) {
        continue;
    }
    found = true;
    res = loader[i]->load(p_path, original_path, r_error, 
                          p_use_sub_threads, r_progress, p_cache_mode);
    if (res.is_valid()) {
        break;
    }
}
```

**Built-in Format Loaders**:
- `ResourceLoaderText`: `.tres` (text resources), `.tscn` (text scenes)
- `ResourceLoaderBinary`: `.res` (binary resources), `.scn` (binary scenes)  
- `ResourceFormatImporter`: Resources with `.import` metadata

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:275-333](), [core/io/resource_loader.h:151-152]()

---

## ResourceCache

The `ResourceCache` is a global registry that maps file paths to loaded `Resource` instances. It prevents duplicate loading and enables resource sharing.

### Cache Structure

```mermaid
graph TB
    Cache["ResourceCache<br/>(static class)"]
    Lock["Mutex lock"]
    Map["HashMap&lt;String, Resource*&gt;<br/>resources"]
    
    Cache --> Lock
    Cache --> Map
    
    Map --> R1["res://textures/player.png<br/>â†’ Texture2D*"]
    Map --> R2["res://scenes/enemy.tscn<br/>â†’ PackedScene*"]
    Map --> R3["res://materials/metal.tres<br/>â†’ Material*"]
```

**Key Operations**:

| Method | Purpose |
|--------|---------|
| `has(path)` | Check if path is cached |
| `get_ref(path)` | Get cached resource as `Ref<Resource>` |
| `get_cached_resources(list)` | Retrieve all cached resources |
| `clear()` | Clear entire cache (shutdown only) |

When a resource is loaded with cache mode `CACHE_MODE_REUSE` or `CACHE_MODE_REPLACE`, it's registered in the cache. The resource's path is set via `set_path()`, which handles cache registration:

```cpp
// From resource.cpp:79-116
void Resource::set_path(const String &p_path, bool p_take_over) {
    MutexLock lock(ResourceCache::lock);
    
    if (!path_cache.is_empty()) {
        ResourceCache::resources.erase(path_cache);
    }
    
    path_cache = "";
    
    Ref<Resource> existing = ResourceCache::get_ref(p_path);
    if (existing.is_valid()) {
        if (p_take_over) {
            existing->path_cache = String();
            ResourceCache::resources.erase(p_path);
        } else {
            ERR_FAIL_MSG("Another resource is loaded from path...");
        }
    }
    
    path_cache = p_path;
    if (!path_cache.is_empty()) {
        ResourceCache::resources[path_cache] = this;
    }
}
```

**Thread Safety**: All cache operations are protected by `ResourceCache::lock` to allow concurrent access from multiple threads.

Sources: [core/io/resource.h:197-215](), [core/io/resource.cpp:79-116]()

---

## Cache Modes

Cache modes control how the loader interacts with the cache during loading. They determine whether to reuse, ignore, or replace cached resources.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Cache Modes"
        I["CACHE_MODE_IGNORE<br/>Don't use cache for main resource"]
        R["CACHE_MODE_REUSE<br/>Use cached if available"]
        Rep["CACHE_MODE_REPLACE<br/>Replace cached with new data"]
        ID["CACHE_MODE_IGNORE_DEEP<br/>Ignore for all resources"]
        RD["CACHE_MODE_REPLACE_DEEP<br/>Replace all resources"]
    end
    
    I --> Sub["Sub-resources use REUSE"]
    R --> Check["Check cache first"]
    Rep --> Check2["Check cache, copy data"]
    ID --> NoCache["No caching at any level"]
    RD --> ReplaceAll["Replace at all levels"]
```

### Mode Descriptions

| Mode | Main Resource | Sub-Resources | Dependencies |
|------|---------------|---------------|--------------|
| `CACHE_MODE_IGNORE` | Not cached | `REUSE` | `REUSE` |
| `CACHE_MODE_REUSE` | Cached/reused | `REUSE` | `REUSE` |
| `CACHE_MODE_REPLACE` | Replace if exists | `REUSE` | `REUSE` |
| `CACHE_MODE_IGNORE_DEEP` | Not cached | `IGNORE` | `REUSE` |
| `CACHE_MODE_REPLACE_DEEP` | Replace if exists | `REPLACE` | `REUSE` |

**CACHE_MODE_REPLACE Behavior**: When a resource is loaded with `CACHE_MODE_REPLACE` and an instance already exists in the cache, the existing instance's data is updated via `copy_from()` rather than creating a new instance. This preserves references.

```cpp
// From resource_loader.cpp:402-426
if (!ignoring) {
    ResourceCache::lock.lock();
    Ref<Resource> old_res = ResourceCache::get_ref(load_task.local_path);
    if (old_res.is_valid()) {
        if (old_res != load_task.resource) {
            ResourceCache::lock.unlock();
            if (replacing) {
                old_res->copy_from(load_task.resource);
            }
            load_task.resource = old_res;
        }
    } else {
        load_task.resource->set_path(load_task.local_path);
    }
}
```

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.h:51-57](), [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:391-426]()

---

## Threaded Loading

The threaded loading system allows resources to be loaded asynchronously without blocking the main thread. It uses `WorkerThreadPool` for execution and maintains state through `ThreadLoadTask` structures.

### Threading Architecture

```mermaid
graph TB
    Request["load_threaded_request()"]
    Token["LoadToken<br/>(user-facing)"]
    Task["ThreadLoadTask<br/>(internal)"]
    Pool["WorkerThreadPool"]
    Run["_run_load_task()"]
    Complete["_load_complete()"]
    Get["load_threaded_get()"]
    
    Request --> Token
    Token --> Task
    Task --> Pool
    Pool --> Run
    Run --> Complete
    Get --> Complete
    Complete --> Resource
```

### LoadToken

`LoadToken` is a reference-counted handle for threaded loads. Users receive tokens from `load_threaded_request()` and poll status via `load_threaded_get_status()`.

**Structure**:
```cpp
// From resource_loader.h:129-138
struct LoadToken : public RefCounted {
    String local_path;        // Normalized resource path
    String user_path;         // Original user-provided path
    uint32_t user_rc = 0;     // User reference count
    ThreadLoadTask *task_if_unregistered = nullptr;  // For CACHE_MODE_IGNORE
    
    void clear();
    virtual ~LoadToken();
};
```

### ThreadLoadTask

`ThreadLoadTask` holds the complete state of an in-progress load operation.

**Key Fields**:
```cpp
// From resource_loader.h:176-211
struct ThreadLoadTask {
    WorkerThreadPool::TaskID task_id;  // Pool task (if threaded)
    Thread::ID thread_id;              // Thread ID (if non-pool)
    LoadToken *load_token;             // Associated token
    String local_path;                 // Resource path
    float progress;                    // Load progress [0.0-1.0]
    ThreadLoadStatus status;           // Current status
    ResourceFormatLoader::CacheMode cache_mode;
    Error error;                       // Error code if failed
    Ref<Resource> resource;            // Loaded resource
    ThreadLoadTask *parent_task;       // Parent in dependency tree
    HashSet<String> sub_tasks;         // Child dependencies
    bool awaited;                      // Whether task has been awaited
    bool need_wait;                    // Whether awaiting is needed
    bool use_sub_threads;              // Use pool for dependencies
    // ...
};
```

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.h:129-211](), [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:226-273]()

### Load Status Flow

```mermaid
stateDiagram-v2
    [*] --> THREAD_LOAD_IN_PROGRESS: load_threaded_request()
    THREAD_LOAD_IN_PROGRESS --> THREAD_LOAD_LOADED: Success
    THREAD_LOAD_IN_PROGRESS --> THREAD_LOAD_FAILED: Error
    THREAD_LOAD_LOADED --> [*]: load_threaded_get()
    THREAD_LOAD_FAILED --> [*]: load_threaded_get()
    
    note right of THREAD_LOAD_IN_PROGRESS
        Task executing in WorkerThreadPool
        Progress updated periodically
    end note
```

**Status Values**:
- `THREAD_LOAD_INVALID_RESOURCE`: No request made for this path
- `THREAD_LOAD_IN_PROGRESS`: Loading in progress
- `THREAD_LOAD_FAILED`: Load encountered error
- `THREAD_LOAD_LOADED`: Resource ready to retrieve

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.h:116-121](), [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:675-718]()

### Dependency Handling

When a resource being loaded references other resources (dependencies), the loader creates child tasks. The dependency tree is tracked to handle cyclic dependencies and compute accurate progress.

```cpp
// From resource_loader.cpp:601-606
// Task hierarchy setup
if (curr_load_task) {
    load_task.parent_task = curr_load_task;
    curr_load_task->sub_tasks.insert(load_task.local_path);
}
```

**Cyclic Dependency Detection**: If a thread attempts to await a task that is loading in the current call stack, the loader detects this as a cyclic dependency and returns `ERR_BUSY`:

```cpp
// From resource_loader.cpp:830-841
if ((load_task.task_id != 0 && load_task.task_id == WorkerThreadPool::get_singleton()->get_caller_task_id()) ||
    (load_task.thread_id != 0 && load_task.thread_id == Thread::get_caller_id())) {
    // Load is in progress, but it's precisely this thread in charge.
    // That means this is a cyclic load.
    if (r_error) {
        *r_error = ERR_BUSY;
    }
    return Ref<Resource>();
}
```

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:601-606](), [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:830-892]()

---

## Format-Specific Loaders

Godot includes three primary format loaders for handling different resource file types.

### ResourceLoaderText

Loads text-based resources (`.tres`) and scenes (`.tscn`) using `VariantParser` to read human-readable serialized data.

**Key Components**:
```mermaid
graph LR
    File[".tres/.tscn file"]
    Parser["VariantParser"]
    ExtRes["External Resources<br/>[ext_resource]"]
    SubRes["Sub-Resources<br/>[sub_resource]"]
    Main["Main Resource<br/>[resource] or [node]"]
    
    File --> Parser
    Parser --> ExtRes
    Parser --> SubRes
    Parser --> Main
    
    ExtRes --> LoadToken["Load tokens<br/>for dependencies"]
    SubRes --> Instantiate["Instantiate objects"]
    Main --> Final["Final Resource"]
```

**Loading Process** (simplified from [scene/resources/resource_format_text.cpp:452-909]()):

1. **Parse external resources**: Read `[ext_resource]` tags, initiate threaded loads for dependencies
2. **Parse sub-resources**: Read `[sub_resource]` tags, instantiate and populate objects
3. **Parse main resource**: Read `[resource]` tag or `[node]` tags for scenes
4. **Complete external loads**: Retrieve loaded dependencies
5. **Set resource path**: Register in cache if appropriate

**File Format Example**:
```
[gd_resource type="Material" format=3]

[ext_resource type="Texture2D" path="res://textures/metal.png" id="1"]

[sub_resource type="Shader" id="shader_1"]
code = "..."

[resource]
shader = SubResource("shader_1")
albedo_texture = ExtResource("1")
```

Sources: [scene/resources/resource_format_text.cpp:452-909](), [scene/resources/resource_format_text.h:40-100]()

### ResourceLoaderBinary

Loads binary-format resources (`.res`) and scenes (`.scn`) for faster loading and smaller file sizes.

**Binary Structure**:
```mermaid
graph TB
    Header["Header<br/>Magic, version, type"]
    StrTable["String Table<br/>Reusable strings"]
    ExtTable["External Resource Table<br/>Paths and types"]
    IntTable["Internal Resource Table<br/>Offsets"]
    ResData["Resource Data<br/>Properties as binary"]
    
    Header --> StrTable
    StrTable --> ExtTable
    ExtTable --> IntTable
    IntTable --> ResData
```

**Key Differences from Text Format**:
- Uses binary encoding for variants (more compact)
- Pre-scans external resources and initiates loads before parsing main resource
- Uses offset table to jump to internal resource definitions
- Faster parsing, smaller file size

Sources: [core/io/resource_format_binary.cpp:682-917](), [core/io/resource_format_binary.h:38-107]()

### ResourceFormatImporter

Handles imported resources by reading `.import` metadata files and delegating to the actual imported resource.

**Import Redirection Flow**:
```mermaid
graph LR
    User["load('res://icon.png')"]
    Import[".import file<br/>metadata"]
    Path["path='.godot/imported/icon-xxx.ctex'"]
    Binary["ResourceLoaderBinary"]
    Resource["CompressedTexture2D"]
    
    User --> Import
    Import --> Path
    Path --> Binary
    Binary --> Resource
```

When loading a resource with an associated `.import` file, `ResourceFormatImporter` reads the import metadata to determine the actual imported resource path (usually in `.godot/imported/`), then uses `ResourceLoader::_load()` to load it.

**Import Metadata Example** (`.import` file):
```ini
[remap]
importer="texture"
type="CompressedTexture2D"
uid="uid://fqgvuwrkuixh"
path="res://.godot/imported/icon.svg-218a8f2b3041327d8a5756f3a245f83b.ctex"

[deps]
source_file="res://icon.svg"
dest_files=["res://.godot/imported/icon.svg-218a8f2b3041327d8a5756f3a245f83b.ctex"]
```

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:44-201](), [core/io/resource_importer.h:41-107]()

## Load Path Validation and Remapping

Before loading, paths are validated and potentially remapped for localization or UID resolution.

### Path Validation

The `_validate_local_path()` function normalizes paths to the `res://` format:

```cpp
// From resource_loader.cpp:477-486
String ResourceLoader::_validate_local_path(const String &p_path) {
    ResourceUID::ID uid = ResourceUID::get_singleton()->text_to_id(p_path);
    if (uid != ResourceUID::INVALID_ID) {
        return ResourceUID::get_singleton()->get_id_path(uid);
    } else if (p_path.is_relative_path()) {
        return ("res://" + p_path).simplify_path();
    } else {
        return ProjectSettings::get_singleton()->localize_path(p_path);
    }
}
```

**UID Support**: Resources can be referenced by UID (e.g., `uid://fqgvuwrkuixh`) instead of path. The loader resolves UIDs to paths using `ResourceUID`.

### Translation Remapping

For localization, `_path_remap()` checks if a path has a locale-specific alternative:

```cpp
// Translation remaps stored in:
static HashMap<String, Vector<String>> translation_remaps;

// Example: "res://text.txt" -> "res://text.es.txt" for Spanish locale
```

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:477-486](), [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:1195-1247]()

## Complete Loading Flow

This diagram shows the complete flow from user API call through format loader to cached resource:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant User
    participant ResourceLoader
    participant Cache as ResourceCache
    participant Loader as ResourceFormatLoader
    participant Resource
    
    User->>ResourceLoader: load(path)
    ResourceLoader->>ResourceLoader: _validate_local_path()
    ResourceLoader->>ResourceLoader: _path_remap()
    ResourceLoader->>ResourceLoader: _load_start()
    
    alt Cache Mode = REUSE
        ResourceLoader->>Cache: get_ref(path)
        alt Found in cache
            Cache-->>ResourceLoader: Existing Resource
            ResourceLoader-->>User: Return cached
        end
    end
    
    ResourceLoader->>Loader: recognize_path(path)
    Loader-->>ResourceLoader: true
    
    ResourceLoader->>Loader: load(path, cache_mode)
    Loader->>Resource: Instantiate
    Loader->>Resource: Set properties
    Loader-->>ResourceLoader: New Resource
    
    alt Cache Mode != IGNORE
        ResourceLoader->>Resource: set_path(path)
        Resource->>Cache: Register self
    end
    
    ResourceLoader-->>User: Return Resource
```

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:513-642](), [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:275-333]()

## Advanced Features

### Resource Changed Signals During Loading

When loading resources from non-main threads, signal connections must be deferred. The loader tracks connections in `ThreadLoadTask::resource_changed_connections` and migrates them to the main thread after loading completes.

```cpp
// From resource_loader.cpp:960-976
void ResourceLoader::resource_changed_connect(Resource *p_source, 
                                               const Callable &p_callable, 
                                               uint32_t p_flags) {
    MutexLock lock(thread_load_mutex);
    
    ThreadLoadTask::ResourceChangedConnection rcc;
    rcc.source = p_source;
    rcc.callable = p_callable;
    rcc.flags = p_flags;
    curr_load_task->resource_changed_connections.push_back(rcc);
}
```

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:960-1002]()

### Progress Reporting

For long-running loads, the loader supports progress callbacks. For dependency trees, progress is computed recursively:

```cpp
// From resource_loader.cpp:644-673
float ResourceLoader::_dependency_get_progress(const String &p_path) {
    if (thread_load_tasks.has(p_path)) {
        ThreadLoadTask &load_task = thread_load_tasks[p_path];
        
        float current_progress = 0.0;
        int dep_count = load_task.sub_tasks.size();
        if (dep_count > 0) {
            for (const String &E : load_task.sub_tasks) {
                current_progress += _dependency_get_progress(E);
            }
            current_progress /= float(dep_count);
            current_progress *= 0.5;
            current_progress += load_task.progress * 0.5;
        } else {
            current_progress = load_task.progress;
        }
        return current_progress;
    }
    return 1.0;  // Assume finished if not in task list
}
```

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:644-673]()

### Resource Reference Overrides

The loader supports temporary resource overrides during loading, used internally for scene instantiation:

```cpp
// From resource_loader.cpp:1004-1022
Ref<Resource> ResourceLoader::ensure_resource_ref_override_for_outer_load(
    const String &p_path, const String &p_res_type) {
    
    const String &local_path = _validate_local_path(p_path);
    HashMap<String, Ref<Resource>> &overrides = res_ref_overrides[load_nesting - 1];
    
    if (overrides.has(local_path)) {
        return overrides[local_path];
    } else {
        Object *obj = ClassDB::instantiate(p_res_type);
        Ref<Resource> res(obj);
        overrides[local_path] = res;
        return res;
    }
}
```

This mechanism allows parent resources to pre-create instances for their sub-resources, useful for `PackedScene` where all nodes must be created before properties are set.

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:1004-1030]()2f:T3c6b,# Resource Import Pipeline

**Purpose and Scope**: This document describes the asset import system in Godot, which processes external file formats (images, audio, 3D models, etc.) into engine-optimized formats. For information about resource loading and caching in general, see [Resource Loading and Caching](#7.1).

## Overview

The import pipeline converts source assets into optimized runtime formats. When a `.png` file is added to a project, the texture importer processes it and converts it to `.ctex` format stored in `.godot/imported/`. The original file remains unchanged, and a `.import` metadata file tracks the import settings and output location.

**Key principle**: Source assets are never modified. All processing outputs go to `.godot/imported/`, with `.import` metadata files acting as the bridge between source files and processed resources.

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:44-156](), [core/io/resource_importer.h:41-107]()

## Core Components

### ResourceFormatImporter

The main `ResourceFormatLoader` implementation that handles loading imported resources. It reads `.import` metadata files to locate and load the processed resources.

**Primary responsibilities:**
- Parse `.import` metadata files via `_get_path_and_type()`
- Locate processed resources in `.godot/imported/`
- Delegate actual resource loading to format-specific loaders
- Handle UID-based resource paths
- Support platform-specific import variants (e.g., `path.s3tc`, `path.etc2`)

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:44-156](), [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:158-201]()

### ResourceImporter

Abstract base class for all asset importers (textures, audio, meshes, etc.). Each concrete importer implements:

| Required Method | Purpose |
|----------------|---------|
| `get_importer_name()` | Unique identifier (e.g., "texture") |
| `get_visible_name()` | Human-readable name for UI |
| `get_recognized_extensions()` | File extensions handled |
| `get_save_extension()` | Output file extension (e.g., "ctex") |
| `get_resource_type()` | Resource class name (e.g., "CompressedTexture2D") |
| `import()` | Main processing function |
| `get_import_options()` | Available import settings |

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.h:109-159]()

### .import Metadata Files

Text files created alongside source assets containing:
- `path`: Location of processed resource(s)
- `type`: Resource type name
- `importer`: Importer plugin name
- `uid`: Unique resource identifier
- `metadata`: Optional importer-specific data
- `valid`: Whether import settings are current
- `group_file`: For grouped imports (e.g., 3D scenes)

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.h:44-51]()

## Import Process Flow

```mermaid
graph TD
    SourceFile["Source Asset<br/>'icon.png'"]
    EdFS["EditorFileSystem<br/>scan()"]
    FindImp["ResourceFormatImporter<br/>get_importer_by_file()"]
    Importer["ResourceImporter<br/>e.g., ResourceImporterTexture"]
    Process["import() method"]
    Output["Processed Resource<br/>'.godot/imported/icon.png-hash.ctex'"]
    Metadata["Metadata File<br/>'icon.png.import'"]
    
    SourceFile -->|"File system event"| EdFS
    EdFS -->|"Find by extension"| FindImp
    FindImp -->|"Returns importer"| Importer
    Importer -->|"Process with settings"| Process
    Process -->|"Write optimized format"| Output
    Process -->|"Write metadata"| Metadata
    
    Metadata -.->|"path field"| Output
    Metadata -.->|"importer field"| Importer
```

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:158-201](), [core/io/resource_importer.h:41-107]()

## Loading Imported Resources

**Loading flow diagram:**

```mermaid
graph TD
    LoadReq["ResourceLoader::load()<br/>'res://icon.png'"]
    CheckExt["ResourceFormatImporter<br/>recognize_path()"]
    ReadImport["_get_path_and_type()<br/>Parse icon.png.import"]
    ExtractPath["Extract path field<br/>'.godot/imported/...'"]
    LoadActual["ResourceLoader::_load()<br/>Load processed resource"]
    Resource["Loaded Resource<br/>CompressedTexture2D"]
    
    LoadReq --> CheckExt
    CheckExt -->|"Has .import file"| ReadImport
    ReadImport -->|"VariantParser"| ExtractPath
    ExtractPath -->|"Internal path"| LoadActual
    LoadActual -->|"Binary/text loader"| Resource
```

The `ResourceFormatImporter::load()` method first reads the `.import` file to determine the actual resource path, then delegates to `ResourceLoader::_load()` to load the processed resource.

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:158-201](), [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:44-156]()

## .import File Format

**Example .import file structure:**

```
[remap]

importer="texture"
type="CompressedTexture2D"
uid="uid://fqgvuwrkuixh"
path="res://.godot/imported/icon.png-487276ed1e3a0c39cad0279d744ee560.ctex"

[deps]

source_file="res://icon.png"
dest_files=["res://.godot/imported/icon.png-487276ed1e3a0c39cad0279d744ee560.ctex"]

[params]

compress/mode=0
compress/high_quality=false
compress/lossy_quality=0.7
```

**Parsing implementation:**

The `_get_path_and_type()` method uses `VariantParser::parse_tag_assign_eof()` to read key-value pairs from the `[remap]` section. Fields are stored in the `PathAndType` struct.

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:44-156](), [core/io/resource_importer.h:44-51]()

## Platform-Specific Import Variants

**Variant selection diagram:**

```mermaid
graph TD
    ImportFile[".import file<br/>multiple path fields"]
    CheckOS["OS::has_feature()"]
    PathS3TC["path.s3tc"]
    PathETC2["path.etc2"]
    PathBPTC["path.bptc"]
    Fallback["path"]
    Selected["Selected variant"]
    
    ImportFile --> CheckOS
    CheckOS -->|"Desktop GPU"| PathS3TC
    CheckOS -->|"Mobile GPU"| PathETC2
    CheckOS -->|"High-end GPU"| PathBPTC
    CheckOS -->|"No match"| Fallback
    
    PathS3TC --> Selected
    PathETC2 --> Selected
    PathBPTC --> Selected
    Fallback --> Selected
```

The `_get_path_and_type()` method at [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:90-99]() checks fields like `path.s3tc`, `path.etc2` based on `OS::get_singleton()->has_feature()`. First match wins; falls back to plain `path` field.

For decompressable formats (when native support unavailable), the method at [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:96-98]() checks `Image::can_decompress()` and uses the first decompressable variant.

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:90-99]()

## Importer Registration and Selection

**Importer registry structure:**

```mermaid
graph LR
    Init["Engine initialization"]
    Imp1["ResourceImporterTexture"]
    Imp2["ResourceImporterOggVorbis"]
    Imp3["ResourceImporterScene"]
    Registry["ResourceFormatImporter<br/>singleton"]
    Sorted["importers vector<br/>sorted by name"]
    Lookup["get_importer_by_file()"]
    
    Init --> Imp1
    Init --> Imp2
    Init --> Imp3
    
    Imp1 -->|"add_importer()"| Registry
    Imp2 -->|"add_importer()"| Registry
    Imp3 -->|"add_importer()"| Registry
    
    Registry --> Sorted
    Sorted --> Lookup
```

Importers register via `ResourceFormatImporter::add_importer()` at [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:335-344](). They're stored in a sorted vector (by `SortImporterByName` comparator at [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:40-42]()) for deterministic settings hash calculation.

**Selection process:**

`get_importer_by_file()` at [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:289-323]() iterates importers, checking:
1. `get_recognized_extensions()` matches file extension
2. `get_priority()` if multiple matches (higher wins)

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:289-344]()

## Import Order and Dependencies

**Import order enumeration:**

| Constant | Value | Use Case |
|----------|-------|----------|
| `IMPORT_ORDER_DEFAULT` | 0 | Most resources |
| `IMPORT_ORDER_SCENE` | 100 | Scenes (depend on textures/materials) |

Scene importers have higher order values so they import after their dependencies (textures, materials) are already processed.

**Build dependencies:**

The `get_build_dependencies()` method at [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:325-333]() tracks source files needed for import (e.g., import scripts). This differs from `get_dependencies()` which tracks external resources referenced by the imported resource.

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.h:140-143](), [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:325-333]()

## EditorFileSystem Integration

**Import trigger flow:**

```mermaid
graph TD
    Scan["EditorFileSystem::scan()"]
    DetectNew["Detect new/modified files"]
    ReadImport["Check .import validity"]
    NeedsImport{"Needs<br/>reimport?"}
    QueueImport["Add to import queue"]
    ImportFile["ResourceImporter::import()"]
    UpdateImport["Update .import metadata"]
    Complete["Import complete"]
    
    Scan --> DetectNew
    DetectNew --> ReadImport
    ReadImport --> NeedsImport
    NeedsImport -->|"Yes"| QueueImport
    NeedsImport -->|"No"| Complete
    QueueImport --> ImportFile
    ImportFile --> UpdateImport
    UpdateImport --> Complete
```

**Reimport triggers:**
- Source file modified (timestamp check)
- `.import` file missing
- `.import` file marked invalid (`valid=false`)
- Import settings changed
- Importer version changed (`get_format_version()`)
- Global import settings hash changed (engine update)

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:420-428](), [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:356-374]()

## Import Settings Hash

**Purpose:** Global hash of all registered importers and their default settings. Used to detect when engine updates require reimport.

**Calculation:** The `get_import_settings_hash()` method at [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:403-418]() computes:
```
MD5(importer1_name + version + options + importer2_name + version + options + ...)
```

When this hash changes (stored in project metadata), resources are marked for reimport.

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:403-418]()

## Grouped Imports

Some importers process multiple output resources from a single source file:

**Example:** 3D scene importer produces:
- Main scene file
- Mesh resources
- Material resources
- Animation resources

**Mechanism:**
- Main resource gets standard `.import` file
- Sub-resources tracked via `group_file` field at [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:148]()
- All resources in group share import settings
- Changing settings reimports entire group

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:148](), [core/io/resource_importer.h:48]()

## UID Integration

**UID in import metadata:**

```mermaid
graph LR
    Import[".import file<br/>uid field"]
    UIDReg["ResourceUID<br/>registry"]
    PathMap["UID to path<br/>mapping"]
    LoadUID["ResourceLoader::load()<br/>'uid://abc123'"]
    Resolve["Resolve to file path"]
    LoadNormal["Normal import load"]
    
    Import -->|"Register"| UIDReg
    UIDReg --> PathMap
    LoadUID --> PathMap
    PathMap --> Resolve
    Resolve --> LoadNormal
```

The `_get_path_and_type()` method at [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:109]() extracts the `uid` field and stores it in `PathAndType::uid`. External resource references can use UIDs instead of paths for stability across file moves.

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:109](), [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:491-507]()

## Runtime vs. Editor Behavior

**Editor mode:**

```cpp
#ifdef TOOLS_ENABLED
if (ResourceImporter::load_on_startup != nullptr) {
    return ResourceImporter::load_on_startup(this, p_path, r_error, ...);
}
#endif
```

At [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:164-166](), the editor can intercept loading to trigger reimport if the resource isn't imported yet.

**Exported game behavior:**
- `.import` files not exported
- Only processed resources included in export
- Platform-specific variants selected during export
- UID references baked into exported resources
- Source files excluded (unless explicitly marked for inclusion)

**Key differences:**

| Aspect | Editor | Exported Game |
|--------|--------|---------------|
| .import files | Read at load time | Not included |
| Reimport | Automatic on changes | Not possible |
| Platform variants | Selected at load | Selected at export |
| Source files | Present in project | Excluded |

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:158-170]()

## Import Validation

**Validation method:**

`ResourceFormatImporter::is_import_valid()` at [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:356-374]() checks:
1. `.import` file exists and is parseable
2. `valid` field is `true`
3. Importer still exists
4. Format version matches
5. Processed resource file exists

Returns `false` to trigger reimport.

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:356-374]()

## Error Handling

**Common error scenarios:**

| Condition | Behavior | Code Reference |
|-----------|----------|----------------|
| .import missing | Triggers reimport in editor | [resource_importer.cpp:46-52]() |
| Processed file missing | Triggers reimport in editor | [resource_importer.cpp:186-188]() |
| Importer not found | Error logged, load fails | [resource_importer.cpp:150-153]() |
| Parse error | Returns ERR_FILE_CORRUPT | [resource_importer.cpp:86-87]() |

The `load_internal()` method at [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:172-201]() has a `p_silence_errors` parameter for graceful degradation during editor startup.

Sources: [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:172-201]()

## Import Cache

**Cache interaction:**

```mermaid
graph TD
    Load["ResourceLoader::load()<br/>'res://texture.png'"]
    CheckCache["ResourceCache::has()<br/>source path"]
    InCache{"Cached?"}
    Return["Return cached<br/>resource"]
    LoadImport["Load via import<br/>pipeline"]
    AddCache["ResourceCache::add()<br/>source path as key"]
    
    Load --> CheckCache
    CheckCache --> InCache
    InCache -->|"Yes"| Return
    InCache -->|"No"| LoadImport
    LoadImport --> AddCache
    AddCache --> Return
```

**Important:** Cache key is the source file path (`res://icon.png`), not the processed path (`.godot/imported/...`). This ensures requesting the same source file returns the same resource instance.

The resource path is set at [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:191]() using the source path, not the internal processed path.

Sources: [core/io/resource_loader.cpp:588-599](), [core/io/resource_importer.cpp:191]()30:T49d6,# Platform Abstraction Layer

## Purpose and Scope

The Platform Abstraction Layer provides a unified interface for interacting with operating system functionality across Windows, Linux, macOS, BSD, Web, and other supported platforms. This layer enables Godot to run on diverse operating systems while maintaining a consistent API for the rest of the engine.

This page covers the `OS` class hierarchy and platform-specific implementations. For information about the build system that compiles platform-specific code, see [Build System](#9). For display and window management, see [Viewport and Rendering Integration](#2.3).

## Architecture Overview

The platform abstraction layer follows an abstract base class pattern where `OS` defines the interface and platform-specific classes implement the concrete functionality.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Abstract Interface"
        OS["OS<br/>(core/os/os.h)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Platform Implementations"
        OSWindows["OS_Windows<br/>(platform/windows/os_windows.cpp)"]
        OSUnix["OS_Unix<br/>(drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp)"]
        OSMacOS["OS_macOS<br/>(inherits OS_Unix)"]
        OSWeb["OS_Web"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Platform Services"
        FileAccess["FileAccess<br/>File I/O"]
        DirAccess["DirAccess<br/>Directory Operations"]
        NetSocket["NetSocket<br/>Networking"]
        ThreadImpl["Thread Implementation"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Script Exposure"
        CoreBindOS["CoreBind::OS<br/>(core/core_bind.h)"]
        GDScript["GDScript Access"]
    end
    
    OS -->|implements| OSWindows
    OS -->|implements| OSUnix
    OSUnix -->|specializes| OSMacOS
    OS -->|implements| OSWeb
    
    OSWindows -->|initializes| FileAccess
    OSWindows -->|initializes| DirAccess
    OSWindows -->|initializes| NetSocket
    OSWindows -->|initializes| ThreadImpl
    
    OSUnix -->|initializes| FileAccess
    OSUnix -->|initializes| DirAccess
    OSUnix -->|initializes| NetSocket
    OSUnix -->|initializes| ThreadImpl
    
    OS -->|wrapped by| CoreBindOS
    CoreBindOS -->|exposes to| GDScript
```

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:46-418](), [platform/windows/os_windows.h:98-286](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.h:53-144](), [core/core_bind.h:146-322]()

## The OS Base Class

The `OS` class is an abstract singleton that provides the interface for all operating system operations. It is defined in [core/os/os.h:46-418]() and implemented in [core/os/os.cpp]().

### Core Responsibilities

| Category | Methods | Description |
|----------|---------|-------------|
| **System Information** | `get_name()`, `get_version()`, `get_distribution_name()`, `get_processor_count()`, `get_processor_name()` | Platform identification and hardware info |
| **File System** | `get_user_data_dir()`, `get_cache_path()`, `get_config_path()`, `get_temp_path()` | Standard directory paths |
| **Process Management** | `execute()`, `create_process()`, `kill()`, `is_process_running()` | External process control |
| **Dynamic Libraries** | `open_dynamic_library()`, `close_dynamic_library()`, `get_dynamic_library_symbol_handle()` | GDExtension support |
| **Time and Date** | `get_ticks_usec()`, `get_unix_time()`, `get_datetime()`, `delay_usec()` | Timing functions |
| **Environment** | `has_environment()`, `get_environment()`, `set_environment()` | Environment variables |
| **Memory** | `get_memory_info()`, `get_static_memory_usage()` | Memory statistics |

### Initialization Flow

```mermaid
graph LR
    Main["Main::setup()<br/>(main/main.cpp)"] -->|creates| OSInstance["OS Instance<br/>(platform-specific)"]
    OSInstance -->|calls| Initialize["OS::initialize()"]
    Initialize -->|sets up| CoreServices["Core Services"]
    
    CoreServices -->|initializes| FileAccess["FileAccess<br/>make_default()"]
    CoreServices -->|initializes| DirAccess["DirAccess<br/>make_default()"]
    CoreServices -->|initializes| NetSocket["NetSocket<br/>make_default()"]
    CoreServices -->|initializes| Threading["Thread System"]
    
    Initialize -->|calls| InitJoypads["initialize_joypads()"]
    Main -->|calls| SetMainLoop["set_main_loop()"]
```

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:130-139](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:270-346](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:163-183]()

## Platform Implementations

### OS_Windows

The Windows implementation is in [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp]() and [platform/windows/os_windows.h](). It handles Windows-specific APIs including Win32, DirectX, and Windows-specific features.

#### Key Features

**Initialization** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:270-346]()):
- Initializes crash handler
- Sets up file and directory access classes (`FileAccessWindows`, `DirAccessWindows`)
- Configures network sockets (`NetSocketWinSock`)
- Initializes high-precision performance counter for timing
- Sets up DirectWrite factory for font rendering
- Configures minimum timer resolution

**Dynamic Library Loading** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:479-602]()):
- Supports temporary library copies to avoid file locking
- Handles PDB debugging symbol renaming
- Uses `LoadLibraryExW` with search path management
- Implements dependency checking in debug builds

**Process Management** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1232-1508]()):
- Creates processes using `CreateProcessW`
- Supports pipe redirection for subprocess I/O
- Tracks process state in `process_map`
- Implements console window control via `p_open_console` parameter

**Text Encoding** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1054-1192]()):
- Maintains encoding table for multibyte conversions
- Supports various code pages (CP_ACP, UTF-8, Shift-JIS, etc.)
- Provides `multibyte_to_string()` and `string_to_multibyte()`

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:270-346](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:479-602](), [platform/windows/os_windows.h:98-286]()

### OS_Unix

The Unix implementation in [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp]() and [drivers/unix/os_unix.h]() provides support for Linux, BSD variants, and macOS (which extends `OS_Unix` with macOS-specific functionality).

#### Key Features

**Initialization** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:163-183]()):
- Initializes POSIX threads
- Sets up `FileAccessUnix` and `DirAccessUnix`
- Configures Unix domain sockets (`NetSocketUnix`)
- Initializes high-precision clock (CLOCK_MONOTONIC or CLOCK_MONOTONIC_RAW)

**Entropy/Random Numbers** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:279-303]()):
- Uses `getentropy()` on supported platforms
- Falls back to `/dev/urandom` on older systems
- Generates cryptographically secure random bytes

**Process Management** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:814-1063]()):
- Uses `fork()` and `execvp()` for process creation
- Implements pipe-based I/O redirection
- Tracks child processes with `waitpid()`
- Supports non-blocking process status checks

**Memory Information** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:403-590]()):
Platform-specific implementations:
- **macOS**: Uses `sysctlbyname()` and `vm_statistics64`
- **FreeBSD**: Uses `sysctl()` and `kvm_getswapinfo()`
- **OpenBSD**: Uses `sysctl()` and `swapctl()`
- **Linux**: Parses `/proc/meminfo`

**Text Encoding** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:592-722]()):
- Dynamically loads `iconv` library if not using glibc
- Provides character set conversion between encodings
- Detects locale charset automatically

**Sources:** [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:163-183](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:279-303](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:403-590]()

## Platform Services

### File and Directory Access

Each platform initializes its file access implementation during `OS::initialize()`:

```mermaid
graph TB
    OSInit["OS::initialize()"] -->|Windows| FAWin["FileAccess::make_default&lt;FileAccessWindows&gt;()"]
    OSInit -->|Unix/Linux| FAUnix["FileAccess::make_default&lt;FileAccessUnix&gt;()"]
    
    FAWin -->|registers for| Resources["ACCESS_RESOURCES"]
    FAWin -->|registers for| UserData["ACCESS_USERDATA"]
    FAWin -->|registers for| FileSystem["ACCESS_FILESYSTEM"]
    
    FAUnix -->|registers for| Resources
    FAUnix -->|registers for| UserData
    FAUnix -->|registers for| FileSystem
    
    OSInit -->|both platforms| PipeAccess["FileAccessPipe<br/>(ACCESS_PIPE)"]
```

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:283-289](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:168-174]()

### Process Management

The OS layer provides comprehensive process control:

**Process Creation Methods:**

| Method | Purpose | Return Value |
|--------|---------|--------------|
| `execute()` | Blocking execution with output capture | Exit code (blocks until completion) |
| `execute_with_pipe()` | Non-blocking with pipe handles | Dictionary with `stdio`, `stderr`, `pid` |
| `create_process()` | Detached process creation | Process ID |
| `create_instance()` | Create new Godot instance | Process ID |

**Process Tracking:**

Both Windows and Unix maintain a `process_map` (HashMap<ProcessID, ProcessInfo>) to track spawned processes:
- Windows: Stores `PROCESS_INFORMATION` with handle
- Unix: Stores running state and exit code

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:215-223](), [platform/windows/os_windows.h:166-173](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.h:54-59]()

### Dynamic Library Loading

Critical for GDExtension support, the OS layer handles platform-specific library loading:

#### Windows Implementation

[platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:479-602]():
- Creates temporary copies of DLLs to avoid locking source files
- Prefix: `~` added to filename
- Renames PDB files to match temporary DLL name
- Uses `AddDllDirectory()` for dependency resolution
- Debug builds check dependencies and report missing DLLs
- Cleanup on library close removes temporary files

#### Unix Implementation

[drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:724-760]():
- Uses `dlopen()` with `RTLD_NOW | RTLD_DEEPBIND`
- Direct loading without temporary copies
- Uses `dlsym()` for symbol resolution
- `dlclose()` for cleanup

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:479-602](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:724-760]()

### Time and Date Functions

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "High-Precision Timing"
        GetTicks["get_ticks_usec()"]
        QPCWin["QueryPerformanceCounter<br/>(Windows)"]
        ClockGettimeUnix["clock_gettime()<br/>(Unix/Linux)"]
        MachTimeApple["mach_absolute_time()<br/>(macOS)"]
        
        GetTicks -->|Windows| QPCWin
        GetTicks -->|Unix| ClockGettimeUnix
        GetTicks -->|macOS| MachTimeApple
    end
    
    subgraph "Calendar Time"
        GetDateTime["get_datetime()"]
        GetLocalTime["GetLocalTime()<br/>(Windows)"]
        LocaltimeR["localtime_r()<br/>(Unix)"]
        
        GetDateTime -->|Windows| GetLocalTime
        GetDateTime -->|Unix| LocaltimeR
    end
    
    subgraph "Unix Time"
        GetUnixTime["get_unix_time()"]
        SystemTimeToFileTime["SystemTimeToFileTime<br/>(Windows)"]
        Gettimeofday["gettimeofday()<br/>(Unix)"]
        
        GetUnixTime -->|Windows| SystemTimeToFileTime
        GetUnixTime -->|Unix| Gettimeofday
    end
```

**Clock Initialization:**
- **Windows** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:294-295]()): Uses `QueryPerformanceFrequency()` to determine ticks per second
- **Unix** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:127-132]()): Uses `CLOCK_MONOTONIC_RAW` (Linux) or `CLOCK_MONOTONIC` (other Unix)
- **macOS** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:114-120]()): Uses `mach_timebase_info()` for conversion scale

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:989-1017](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:388-401](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:964-979]()

### Environment Variables

All platforms implement environment variable access:

| Method | Windows | Unix/Linux |
|--------|---------|------------|
| `has_environment()` | `GetEnvironmentVariableW()` with zero buffer | `getenv() != nullptr` |
| `get_environment()` | `GetEnvironmentVariableW()` with allocated buffer | `getenv()` |
| `set_environment()` | `SetEnvironmentVariableW()` | `setenv()` |
| `unset_environment()` | `SetEnvironmentVariableW(name, nullptr)` | `unsetenv()` |

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1510-1557](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:1065-1087]()

### Memory Information

The `get_memory_info()` method returns a Dictionary with keys: `physical`, `free`, `available`, `stack`.

**Platform-Specific Implementations:**

```mermaid
graph TB
    GetMemInfo["get_memory_info()"]
    
    GetMemInfo -->|Windows| WinAPI["GlobalMemoryStatusEx()"]
    GetMemInfo -->|macOS| MacAPI["sysctlbyname('hw.memsize')<br/>host_statistics64()"]
    GetMemInfo -->|FreeBSD| FreeBSDAPI["sysctlbyname('vm.stats...')<br/>kvm_getswapinfo()"]
    GetMemInfo -->|OpenBSD| OpenBSDAPI["sysctl(VM_UVMEXP)<br/>swapctl()"]
    GetMemInfo -->|Linux| LinuxProc["/proc/meminfo parsing"]
    
    WinAPI -->|returns| MemDict["Dictionary:<br/>physical, free,<br/>available, stack"]
    MacAPI -->|returns| MemDict
    FreeBSDAPI -->|returns| MemDict
    OpenBSDAPI -->|returns| MemDict
    LinuxProc -->|returns| MemDict
```

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1797-1828](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:403-590]()

## Script Bindings (CoreBind::OS)

The OS functionality is exposed to GDScript and other scripting languages through `CoreBind::OS` defined in [core/core_bind.h:146-322]() and [core/core_bind.cpp:241-846]().

### Binding Architecture

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Native OS Layer"
        OSNative["::OS<br/>(Singleton)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "CoreBind Wrapper"
        OSBind["CoreBind::OS"]
        Methods["Wrapper Methods:<br/>get_name()<br/>execute()<br/>has_environment()<br/>..."]
    end
    
    subgraph "Script Access"
        GDScript["GDScript:<br/>OS.get_name()<br/>OS.execute(...)"]
        CSharp["C#:<br/>OS.GetName()<br/>OS.Execute(...)"]
    end
    
    OSNative -->|wrapped by| OSBind
    OSBind -->|contains| Methods
    Methods -->|calls| OSNative
    
    OSBind -->|bound to| GDScript
    OSBind -->|bound to| CSharp
```

### Method Wrapping Pattern

The CoreBind wrapper follows a consistent pattern:

```
// Native OS method
String OS::get_name() const;

// CoreBind wrapper (core/core_bind.cpp:493-495)
String OS::get_name() const {
    return ::OS::get_singleton()->get_name();
}
```

**Type Conversions:**

| Native Type | Script Type | Conversion |
|-------------|-------------|------------|
| `List<String>` | `Vector<String>` | Manual iteration and copying |
| `ProcessID` | `int` | Direct cast |
| `String *r_pipe` | `Array r_output` | String wrapped in array |
| `Mutex *` | (internal) | Not exposed to scripts |

**Sources:** [core/core_bind.h:146-322](), [core/core_bind.cpp:287-554]()

### Key Script-Accessible Methods

From [doc/classes/OS.xml]():

**System Information:**
- `get_name()` - Platform name ("Windows", "Linux", etc.)
- `get_version()` - OS version string
- `get_processor_count()` - Logical CPU count
- `get_processor_name()` - CPU model name

**Process Management:**
- `execute(path, arguments, output, read_stderr, open_console)` - Blocking execution
- `create_process(path, arguments, open_console)` - Non-blocking process creation
- `kill(pid)` - Terminate process

**File System:**
- `get_user_data_dir()` - User data directory for current project
- `get_cache_dir()` - System cache directory
- `get_system_dir(dir_type, shared_storage)` - System directories (Desktop, Documents, etc.)

**Environment:**
- `has_environment(variable)` - Check if environment variable exists
- `get_environment(variable)` - Get environment variable value
- `set_environment(variable, value)` - Set environment variable

**Sources:** [doc/classes/OS.xml:1-700](), [core/core_bind.cpp:287-846]()

```mermaid
    ArchCheck -->|true| Bits64["'64'"]

```

**Common Feature Tags:**
- Platform: `windows`, `linux`, `macos`, `android`, `ios`, `web`
- Architecture: `x86_64`, `arm64`, `x86_32`, `arm32`, `64`, `32`
- Build: `debug`, `editor`, `template`, `template_debug`, `template_release`
- Precision: `double`, `single` (floating-point precision)

## Lifecycle Integration

```mermaid
graph TB
    Start["Program Start"] -->|"main()"| MainSetup["Main::setup()"]
    
    MainSetup -->|creates| OSInstance["Platform-Specific OS Instance"]
    OSInstance -->|"OS_Windows::initialize()"| WinInit
    OSInstance -->|"OS_Unix::initialize_core()"| UnixInit
    
    subgraph "Initialization"
        WinInit["Initialize Windows Services"]
        UnixInit["Initialize Unix Services"]
    end
    
    WinInit -->|registers| FileAccess["FileAccess Implementations"]
    UnixInit -->|registers| FileAccess
    
    WinInit -->|sets up| Timing["Timing System"]
    UnixInit -->|sets up| Timing
    
    MainSetup -->|calls| SetMainLoop["OS::set_main_loop()"]
    SetMainLoop -->|stores| MainLoopPtr["main_loop pointer"]
    
    MainLoopPtr -->|used by| MainLoop["Main Loop Execution"]
    
    MainLoop -->|on exit| Finalize["OS::finalize()"]
    Finalize -->|cleanup| FinalizeCore["OS::finalize_core()"]
    FinalizeCore -->|shuts down| Services["Platform Services"]
```

**Initialization Order** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:270-346](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:163-183]()):
1. Crash handler setup
2. Thread system initialization
3. File/Directory access registration
4. Network socket initialization
5. High-precision timer setup
6. Platform-specific services (fonts, audio, etc.)

**Finalization Order** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:359-404](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:185-190]()):
1. Delete main loop
2. Clean up temporary libraries
3. Release platform resources
4. Shut down network sockets
5. Clean up process map

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:270-404](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:163-190]()31:T546a,# OS Interface and Implementations

This document describes Godot's operating system abstraction layer, which provides a uniform interface to platform-specific functionality. For information about platform services (file I/O, networking, etc.), see [Platform Services](#8.2).

The OS layer enables Godot to run on multiple platforms (Windows, Linux, macOS, BSD, Web) while maintaining a consistent API for the rest of the engine. It handles system information queries, process management, timing, dynamic library loading, and environment access.

## Architecture Overview

Godot uses an abstract base class pattern to define the OS interface, with platform-specific implementations that override virtual methods. The singleton `OS` instance is initialized at engine startup based on the target platform.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Core Interface"
        OSBase["OS (core/os/os.h)<br/>Abstract Base Class<br/>Singleton"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Platform Implementations"
        OSWindows["OS_Windows<br/>platform/windows/os_windows.cpp"]
        OSUnix["OS_Unix<br/>drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Specialized Unix"
        OSLinux["Linux Implementation<br/>Uses OS_Unix"]
        OSMacOS["macOS Implementation<br/>Uses OS_Unix + Apple APIs"]
        OSBSD["BSD Implementation<br/>Uses OS_Unix"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Script Binding"
        CoreBindOS["CoreBind::OS<br/>core/core_bind.h<br/>Exposed to GDScript/C#"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Engine Systems"
        Main["Main<br/>Initialization"]
        Engine["Engine Core"]
        Scripts["User Scripts"]
    end
    
    OSBase -.implements.-> OSWindows
    OSBase -.implements.-> OSUnix
    OSUnix --> OSLinux
    OSUnix --> OSMacOS
    OSUnix --> OSBSD
    
    Main -->|"initializes"| OSWindows
    Main -->|"initializes"| OSUnix
    Main -->|"calls initialize()"| OSBase
    
    Engine -->|"OS::get_singleton()"| OSBase
    CoreBindOS -->|"delegates to"| OSBase
    Scripts -->|"OS.get_name()"| CoreBindOS
```

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:46-418](), [platform/windows/os_windows.h:98-286](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.h:53-144](), [core/core_bind.h:146-322]()

## The OS Base Class

The `OS` class ([core/os/os.h:46-418]()) defines the abstract interface that all platform implementations must provide. It is a singleton initialized by the `Main` class during engine startup.

### Key Responsibilities

| Category | Methods | Purpose |
|----------|---------|---------|
| **System Info** | `get_name()`, `get_version()`, `get_distribution_name()` | Platform identification |
| **Process Management** | `execute()`, `create_process()`, `kill()`, `is_process_running()` | External process control |
| **Dynamic Libraries** | `open_dynamic_library()`, `close_dynamic_library()`, `get_dynamic_library_symbol_handle()` | GDExtension loading |
| **Time/Timing** | `get_ticks_usec()`, `get_unix_time()`, `delay_usec()` | High-precision timing |
| **Environment** | `has_environment()`, `get_environment()`, `set_environment()` | Environment variables |
| **Standard I/O** | `get_stdin_string()`, `get_stdin_type()`, `alert()` | Console interaction |
| **Memory** | `get_memory_info()`, `get_static_memory_usage()` | Memory statistics |
| **Paths** | `get_user_data_dir()`, `get_config_path()`, `get_cache_path()` | Platform-specific directories |

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:46-418]()

### Virtual Method Categories

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Pure Virtual - Must Override"
        PV1["initialize()"]
        PV2["get_name()"]
        PV3["get_ticks_usec()"]
        PV4["delay_usec()"]
        PV5["execute()"]
        PV6["create_process()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Virtual - Optional Override"
        V1["get_entropy()"]
        V2["open_dynamic_library()"]

        V4["get_video_adapter_driver_info()"]
        V5["shell_open()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Non-Virtual - Common Implementation"
        NV1["get_singleton()"]
        NV2["has_feature()"]
        NV3["get_locale_language()"]
        NV4["set_exit_code()"]
    end
```

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:132-139](), [core/os/os.h:215-228](), [core/os/os.h:360-365]()

## Platform Implementations

### OS_Windows

`OS_Windows` ([platform/windows/os_windows.h:98-286](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:31-2395]()) provides the Windows-specific implementation using Win32 APIs.

**Key Features:**

- **Initialization** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:270-346]()):
  - Sets up DirectWrite for font rendering
  - Initializes file access providers (`FileAccessWindows`, `DirAccessWindows`)
  - Configures networking (`NetSocketWinSock`, `IPWindows`)
  - Sets up performance counter for high-resolution timing
  - Initializes process map for tracking child processes

- **Process Management** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1153-1462]()):
  - Uses `CreateProcessW` with Unicode support
  - Handles pipe redirection for `execute_with_pipe()`
  - Manages console window creation with `CREATE_NO_WINDOW` flag
  - Tracks running processes via `ProcessInfo` structure

- **Dynamic Library Loading** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:479-602]()):
  - Uses `LoadLibraryExW` with `LOAD_LIBRARY_SEARCH_DEFAULT_DIRS`
  - Creates temporary copies of DLLs to avoid file locking during development
  - Debug builds check for missing dependencies using `ImageDirectoryEntryToData`
  - Handles PDB file copying for debugging support

- **System Information** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:612-663]()):
  - Uses `RtlGetVersion` from ntdll.dll for accurate version info
  - Detects Windows 10, 11, Server versions based on build number
  - Queries registry for video driver information
  - Uses WMI (`IWbemServices`) as fallback for hardware info

**Example: Windows Process Creation**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Script
    participant CoreBind
    participant OS_Windows
    participant Win32API
    
    Script->>CoreBind: OS.create_process(path, args)
    CoreBind->>OS_Windows: create_process(path, args, &pid)
    OS_Windows->>OS_Windows: _quote_command_line_argument()
    OS_Windows->>Win32API: CreateProcessW()
    Win32API-->>OS_Windows: PROCESS_INFORMATION
    OS_Windows->>OS_Windows: process_map->insert(pid, ProcessInfo)
    OS_Windows-->>CoreBind: OK, pid
    CoreBind-->>Script: pid
```

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:270-346](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1153-1462](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:479-602]()

### OS_Unix

`OS_Unix` ([drivers/unix/os_unix.h:53-144](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:31-1314]()) serves as the base for Linux, macOS, BSD, and other POSIX-compliant systems.

**Key Features:**

- **Initialization** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:163-183]()):
  - Sets up POSIX threading (`init_thread_posix`)
  - Configures Unix file/directory access providers
  - Initializes Unix sockets (`NetSocketUnix`, `IPUnix`)
  - Sets up high-resolution clock (`CLOCK_MONOTONIC` or `CLOCK_MONOTONIC_RAW`)

- **Process Management** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:733-1018]()):
  - Uses `fork()` and `execvp()` for process creation
  - Implements `execute()` with pipe redirection using `pipe()` and `dup2()`
  - Uses `waitpid()` with `WNOHANG` to check process status
  - Handles `SIGCHLD` for child process termination

- **Dynamic Library Loading** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:653-731]()):
  - Uses `dlopen()` with `RTLD_NOW | RTLD_DEEPBIND`
  - ASAN builds use `RTLD_NOW` only to avoid conflicts
  - Supports `.so`, `.dylib` (macOS), and `.bundle` extensions
  - Uses `dlsym()` for symbol resolution

- **Platform-Specific Variants**:
  - **macOS** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:411-445]()): Uses `mach_absolute_time()` and `vm_statistics64` for timing/memory
  - **Linux** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:544-580]()): Reads `/proc/meminfo` for memory statistics
  - **FreeBSD** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:447-489]()): Uses `sysctl` and `kvm_getswapinfo()`
  - **OpenBSD/NetBSD** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:490-542]()): Uses `uvmexp` for memory info

**Example: Unix Clock Setup**

```mermaid
graph TB
    Start["_setup_clock()"]
    CheckPlatform{"Platform?"}
    
    Start --> CheckPlatform
    
    CheckPlatform -->|macOS| MacOS["mach_timebase_info()<br/>Calculate nanosecond scale<br/>_clock_start = mach_absolute_time()"]
    CheckPlatform -->|Linux/BSD| Unix["clock_gettime(CLOCK_MONOTONIC_RAW)<br/>_clock_start = tv_nsec/1000 + tv_sec*1000000"]
    
    MacOS --> Done["Ready for get_ticks_usec()"]
    Unix --> Done
```

**Sources:** [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:110-132](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:388-401]()

### Encoding Support

Windows and non-glibc Unix systems include multibyte encoding support ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1054-1104](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:592-652]()):

| Platform | Implementation | Encoding Database |
|----------|----------------|-------------------|
| **Windows** | `MultiByteToWideChar()` / `WideCharToMultiByte()` | 140+ Windows code pages ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1054-1104]()) |
| **Unix (glibc)** | `iconv()` (direct) | System iconv database |
| **Unix (non-glibc)** | `dlopen("libiconv")` | Dynamically loaded iconv |

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:2231-2350](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:1108-1224]()

## Initialization and Lifecycle

The OS singleton is initialized during engine startup by the `Main` class. The lifecycle follows this sequence:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Main
    participant OS_Platform
    participant FileAccess
    participant NetSocket
    participant Timing
    
    Note over Main: Engine Startup
    Main->>OS_Platform: new OS_Windows() / OS_Unix()
    Main->>OS_Platform: initialize()
    
    OS_Platform->>FileAccess: make_default<FileAccessWindows>()
    OS_Platform->>NetSocket: NetSocketWinSock::make_default()
    OS_Platform->>Timing: QueryPerformanceFrequency() / clock_gettime()
    OS_Platform->>OS_Platform: Initialize process_map
    
    Note over Main: Engine Running
    Main->>OS_Platform: Main loop calls get_ticks_usec()
    
    Note over Main: Engine Shutdown
    Main->>OS_Platform: finalize()
    OS_Platform->>OS_Platform: Clean up process_map
    OS_Platform->>NetSocket: cleanup()
    Main->>OS_Platform: finalize_core()
```

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:270-346](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:163-183](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:387-404]()

### Platform-Specific Initialization Details

**Windows Initialization** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:270-346]()):
```
1. Crash handler setup
2. Thread initialization (init_thread_win)
3. File/Directory access providers
4. Network socket initialization
5. Performance counter setup (ticks_per_second, ticks_start)
6. Set timer resolution (timeBeginPeriod)
7. Process map creation
8. DirectWrite factory initialization (font support)
```

**Unix Initialization** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:163-183]()):
```
1. Thread initialization (init_thread_posix)
2. File/Directory access providers
3. Network socket initialization
4. Process map creation
5. Clock setup (_setup_clock)
```

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:270-346](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:163-183]()

## Core Functionality

### System Information

The OS layer provides platform identification and system details:

| Method | Windows Implementation | Unix Implementation |
|--------|----------------------|-------------------|
| `get_name()` | Returns `"Windows"` | Returns `"Unix"` (overridden by platform) |
| `get_version()` | `RtlGetVersion()` â†’ `"major.minor.build"` | Varies by platform (uname, sysctl) |
| `get_version_alias()` | Maps build numbers to names like `"11"`, `"Server 2022"` | Platform-specific |
| `get_processor_name()` | Registry query `HARDWARE\DESCRIPTION\System\CentralProcessor\0` | `/proc/cpuinfo` or sysctl |
| `get_processor_count()` | `GetSystemInfo()` | `sysconf(_SC_NPROCESSORS_ONLN)` or `std::thread::hardware_concurrency()` |

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:604-663](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:305-316](), [core/os/os.cpp:456-462]()

### Time and Timing

High-resolution timing is critical for frame timing and profiling:

**Windows** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:989-1017]()):
- Uses `QueryPerformanceCounter()` with frequency from `QueryPerformanceFrequency()`
- Microsecond precision: `(ticks - ticks_start) * 1000000 / ticks_per_second`
- `delay_usec()` uses `Sleep(usec / 1000)` (millisecond precision)

**Unix** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:388-401]()):
- macOS: `mach_absolute_time()` with timebase conversion
- Linux/BSD: `clock_gettime(CLOCK_MONOTONIC_RAW)` or `CLOCK_MONOTONIC`
- Nanosecond precision converted to microseconds
- `delay_usec()` uses `nanosleep()` for accurate sub-millisecond delays

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:989-1017](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:388-401](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:379-386]()

### Process Management

Both platforms support creating, monitoring, and terminating external processes:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Process Creation API"
        CreateProcess["create_process(path, args)"]
        Execute["execute(path, args, output)"]
        ExecutePipe["execute_with_pipe(path, args)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Process Monitoring"
        IsRunning["is_process_running(pid)"]
        GetExitCode["get_process_exit_code(pid)"]
        Kill["kill(pid)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Windows Implementation"
        WinCreate["CreateProcessW()"]
        WinWait["WaitForSingleObject(WNOHAIT)"]
        WinTerm["TerminateProcess()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Unix Implementation"
        UnixFork["fork() + execvp()"]
        UnixWait["waitpid(WNOHANG)"]
        UnixKill["kill(SIGKILL)"]
    end
    
    CreateProcess --> WinCreate
    CreateProcess --> UnixFork
    IsRunning --> WinWait
    IsRunning --> UnixWait
    Kill --> WinTerm
    Kill --> UnixKill
```

**Process Tracking:**
- Both implementations maintain a `process_map` (HashMap) to track spawned processes
- `ProcessInfo` structure stores running state and exit code
- Mutex-protected for thread safety

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1153-1462](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:733-1018]()

### Dynamic Library Loading

GDExtensions rely on dynamic library loading with platform-specific considerations:

**Windows** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:479-602]()):
```
Flow:
1. Check if library exists
2. If generate_temp_files: Create "~" prefixed copy (avoid file lock)
3. Copy associated PDB file for debugging
4. AddDllDirectory() for dependency resolution
5. LoadLibraryExW() with LOAD_LIBRARY_SEARCH_DEFAULT_DIRS
6. On failure: Check dependencies with ImageDirectoryEntryToData (debug only)
7. Store in temp_libraries map for cleanup
```

**Unix** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:653-731]()):
```
Flow:
1. Check if library exists
2. Determine correct extension (.so, .dylib, .bundle)
3. dlopen() with RTLD_NOW | RTLD_DEEPBIND (or just RTLD_NOW for ASAN)
4. On failure: Return error with dlerror() message
5. No temporary copy needed (Unix handles file locks differently)
```

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:479-602](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:653-731]()

### Standard I/O Handling

The OS layer detects and manages standard I/O streams:

**Handle Types** ([core/os/os.h:57-63]()):
```cpp
enum StdHandleType {
    STD_HANDLE_INVALID,   // Handle doesn't exist
    STD_HANDLE_CONSOLE,   // Connected to terminal/console
    STD_HANDLE_FILE,      // Redirected to file
    STD_HANDLE_PIPE,      // Redirected to pipe
    STD_HANDLE_UNKNOWN    // Type cannot be determined
};
```

**Windows Detection** ([platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:2066-2127]()):
- Uses `GetFileType()` on `GetStdHandle(STD_INPUT_HANDLE)`
- `FILE_TYPE_CHAR` â†’ `STD_HANDLE_CONSOLE`
- `FILE_TYPE_DISK` â†’ `STD_HANDLE_FILE`
- `FILE_TYPE_PIPE` â†’ `STD_HANDLE_PIPE`

**Unix Detection** ([drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:216-277]()):
- Uses `isatty(fileno(stdin))` to detect terminal
- Uses `fstat()` with `S_ISFIFO()`, `S_ISREG()`, `S_ISLNK()` for type

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:2066-2127](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:216-277]()

### Environment Variables

Platform-specific implementations for environment variable access:

| Operation | Windows | Unix |
|-----------|---------|------|
| **Check Existence** | `GetEnvironmentVariableW()` with NULL buffer | `getenv() != nullptr` |
| **Get Value** | `GetEnvironmentVariableW()` with buffer | `getenv()` |
| **Set Value** | `SetEnvironmentVariableW()` | `setenv()` |
| **Unset** | `SetEnvironmentVariableW(var, nullptr)` | `unsetenv()` |

**Note:** Environment variable names are case-sensitive on Unix but case-insensitive on Windows.

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1838-1887](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:1264-1287]()

## Script Binding Layer

The `CoreBind::OS` class ([core/core_bind.h:146-322](), [core/core_bind.cpp:241-867]()) exposes OS functionality to GDScript and C#:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Script Layer"
        GDScript["GDScript<br/>OS.get_name()"]

    end
    
    subgraph "Binding Layer (CoreBind::OS)"

    Methods --> Delegates
    Delegates --> OSCore
    OSCore --> Platform
```

**Key Bindings:**

```cpp
// Process execution
int OS::execute(const String &p_path, const Vector<String> &p_arguments, 
                Array r_output, bool p_read_stderr, bool p_open_console);

// System info
String get_name() const;
String get_version() const;

// Environment

void set_environment(const String &p_var, const String &p_value) const;

// Process management

                   bool p_open_console = false);
```
