```cpp
Error kill(int p_pid);
```

**Logger Integration:**
The binding layer includes `LoggerBind` ([core/core_bind.cpp:243-285]()) to intercept log messages and forward them to custom GDScript/C# logger implementations.

**Sources:** [core/core_bind.h:146-322](), [core/core_bind.cpp:241-867]()

## Platform Detection and Features

The `has_feature()` method ([core/os/os.cpp:468-634]()) allows runtime platform detection:

### Feature Tag Categories

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Platform Tags"
        P1["windows"]
        P2["linux"]
        P3["macos"]
        P4["android"]
        P5["ios"]
        P6["web"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Architecture Tags"
        A1["x86_64"]
        A2["x86_32"]
        A3["arm64"]
        A4["arm32"]
        A5["riscv"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Build Tags"
        B1["debug"]
        B2["release"]
        B3["editor"]
        B4["template"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Precision Tags"
        PR1["64 (pointer size)"]
        PR2["double"]
        PR3["single"]
    end
```

**Example Usage:**
```gdscript
if OS.has_feature("windows"):
    # Windows-specific code
elif OS.has_feature("linux"):
    # Linux-specific code

if OS.has_feature("x86_64"):
    # 64-bit code
```

**Internal Implementation:**
- Feature tags are lowercase for consistency
- Results are cached in `feature_cache` HashMap
- Server features can be queried via callback (`has_server_feature_callback`)
- Custom features can be defined per platform via `_check_internal_feature_support()`

**Sources:** [core/os/os.cpp:468-634](), [core/core_bind.cpp:580-589]()

### Platform Identification Table

| Platform | `get_name()` | `get_identifier()` | Feature Tag |
|----------|--------------|-------------------|-------------|
| Windows | `"Windows"` | `"windows"` | `"windows"` |
| Linux | `"Linux"` | `"linux"` | `"linux"` |
| macOS | `"macOS"` | `"macos"` | `"macos"` |
| FreeBSD | `"FreeBSD"` | `"freebsd"` | `"freebsd"` |
| Android | `"Android"` | `"android"` | `"android"` |
| iOS | `"iOS"` | `"ios"` | `"ios"` |
| Web | `"Web"` | `"web"` | `"web"` |

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:604-606](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:305-307](), [core/os/os.cpp:95-97]()

## Summary

The OS abstraction layer provides:

1. **Unified Interface**: `OS` base class with consistent API across platforms
2. **Platform Implementations**: `OS_Windows` and `OS_Unix` (with variants for macOS, BSD)
3. **Core Services**: Process management, dynamic libraries, timing, environment, I/O
4. **Script Access**: `CoreBind::OS` exposes functionality to GDScript/C#
5. **Runtime Detection**: Feature tags and system information queries

This architecture enables Godot to maintain a single codebase while supporting diverse platforms, with platform-specific optimizations and features implemented in the respective OS subclasses.32:T8a36,# Platform Services

## Purpose and Scope

This page documents the platform-specific services provided by Godot's OS abstraction layer. These services enable the engine to interact with the underlying operating system for file I/O, networking, process management, dynamic library loading, and system information queries. Each service has an abstract interface defined in the `OS` base class and platform-specific implementations in `OS_Windows`, `OS_Unix`, and other platform classes.

For information about the OS interface hierarchy and platform detection, see [OS Interface and Implementations](#8.1).

---

## Service Categories

Platform services are organized into the following categories:

| Category | Primary Classes | Purpose |
|----------|----------------|---------|
| File I/O | `FileAccess`, `DirAccess` | File and directory operations |
| Networking | `NetSocket`, `IPAddress` | Network socket operations |
| Process Management | `OS::execute()`, `OS::create_process()` | Launch and manage external processes |
| Dynamic Libraries | `OS::open_dynamic_library()` | Load shared libraries at runtime |
| System Information | `OS::get_processor_name()`, etc. | Query hardware and OS details |
| Time Services | `OS::get_ticks_usec()`, `OS::get_datetime()` | Timing and date/time operations |
| Path Services | `OS::get_user_data_dir()`, etc. | Standard system directory paths |

---

## File I/O Services

### Architecture

File and directory operations are abstracted through the `FileAccess` and `DirAccess` classes. Platform-specific implementations are registered during OS initialization.

```mermaid

    subgraph "Abstract Interface"
        FileAccess["FileAccess<br/>Virtual base class"]
        DirAccess["DirAccess<br/>Virtual base class"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Windows Implementation"

        DirAccessWindows["DirAccessWindows<br/>Windows directory ops"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Unix Implementation"
        FileAccessUnix["FileAccessUnix<br/>POSIX file I/O"]
        DirAccessUnix["DirAccessUnix<br/>POSIX directory ops"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Specialized Access"
        FileAccessPipe["FileAccessWindowsPipe<br/>FileAccessUnixPipe<br/>Pipe I/O"]
    end
    
    FileAccess --> FileAccessWindows
    FileAccess --> FileAccessUnix
    FileAccess --> FileAccessPipe
    
    DirAccess --> DirAccessWindows
    DirAccess --> DirAccessUnix
```

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:283-289](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:168-174]()

### Initialization

File access classes are registered during `OS::initialize()`:

**Windows:**
```cpp
// platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:283-289
FileAccess::make_default<FileAccessWindows>(FileAccess::ACCESS_RESOURCES);
FileAccess::make_default<FileAccessWindows>(FileAccess::ACCESS_USERDATA);
FileAccess::make_default<FileAccessWindows>(FileAccess::ACCESS_FILESYSTEM);
FileAccess::make_default<FileAccessWindowsPipe>(FileAccess::ACCESS_PIPE);
DirAccess::make_default<DirAccessWindows>(DirAccess::ACCESS_RESOURCES);
DirAccess::make_default<DirAccessWindows>(DirAccess::ACCESS_USERDATA);
DirAccess::make_default<DirAccessWindows>(DirAccess::ACCESS_FILESYSTEM);
```

**Unix:**
```cpp
// drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:168-174
FileAccess::make_default<FileAccessUnix>(FileAccess::ACCESS_RESOURCES);
FileAccess::make_default<FileAccessUnix>(FileAccess::ACCESS_USERDATA);
FileAccess::make_default<FileAccessUnix>(FileAccess::ACCESS_FILESYSTEM);
FileAccess::make_default<FileAccessUnixPipe>(FileAccess::ACCESS_PIPE);
DirAccess::make_default<DirAccessUnix>(DirAccess::ACCESS_RESOURCES);
DirAccess::make_default<DirAccessUnix>(DirAccess::ACCESS_USERDATA);
DirAccess::make_default<DirAccessUnix>(DirAccess::ACCESS_FILESYSTEM);
```

### Access Types

Three access types control file path resolution:

- `ACCESS_RESOURCES` - Accesses files relative to the project or PCK
- `ACCESS_USERDATA` - Accesses user data directory (user://)
- `ACCESS_FILESYSTEM` - Direct filesystem access with full paths
- `ACCESS_PIPE` - Special pipe-based I/O for process communication

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:270-346](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:163-183]()

## Process Management

### Process Execution Methods

The OS class provides multiple methods for process execution, each serving different use cases:

| Method | Blocking | Captures Output | Returns PID | Use Case |
|--------|----------|----------------|-------------|----------|
| `execute()` | Yes | Yes | No | Run command, capture output |
| `create_process()` | No | No | Yes | Launch independent process |
| `create_instance()` | No | No | Yes | Launch new Godot instance |
| `execute_with_pipe()` | Optional | Via pipes | Yes | Interactive I/O with process |

### Process Execution Flow

```mermaid
graph TB
    Client["Client Code"]

        execute["OS::execute()<br/>Blocking, captures stdout"]
        create_process["OS::create_process()<br/>Non-blocking, returns PID"]
        execute_with_pipe["OS::execute_with_pipe()<br/>Returns FileAccess pipes"]
        kill["OS::kill()<br/>Terminate process"]
        is_running["OS::is_process_running()"]
        get_exit_code["OS::get_process_exit_code()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Windows Implementation"
        CreateProcessW["CreateProcessW()<br/>Windows API"]
        WaitForSingleObject["WaitForSingleObject()<br/>Wait for completion"]

    end

    end
```

### Execute with Pipes

The `execute_with_pipe()` method creates bidirectional communication channels with child processes:

**Windows Implementation:**
```cpp
// Returns Dictionary with keys: "stdio", "stderr", "pid"
// Uses CreatePipe() and FILE_FLAG_OVERLAPPED for non-blocking I/O
```

**Unix Implementation:**
```cpp
// Uses pipe() and fcntl(O_NONBLOCK) for non-blocking operation
// Returns FileAccess objects wrapping pipe file descriptors
```

The method returns a Dictionary containing:
- `"stdio"` - FileAccess for stdin/stdout communication
- `"stderr"` - FileAccess for stderr (read-only)
- `"pid"` - Process ID for monitoring

## Dynamic Library Loading

### Library Loading Architecture

Dynamic library loading supports GDExtensions and other runtime-loaded code. The system handles platform-specific library formats (.dll, .so, .dylib) and provides dependency resolution.

```mermaid
    end
```

### GDExtensionData Structure

The `GDExtensionData` structure controls library loading behavior:

```cpp
// core/os/os.h:192-197
struct GDExtensionData {
    bool also_set_library_path = false;      // Add library dir to search path
    String *r_resolved_path = nullptr;       // Return actual loaded path
    bool generate_temp_files = false;        // Create temp copy for hot-reload
    PackedStringArray *library_dependencies = nullptr;
};
```

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:192-197]()

### Temporary Library Handling (Windows)

On Windows, libraries can be loaded from temporary copies to allow hot-reloading without locking the original file:

```cpp
// platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:491-515
if (p_data != nullptr && p_data->generate_temp_files) {
    // Copy the file to the same directory with a prefix
    load_path = path.get_base_dir().path_join("~" + path.get_file());
    
    // Delete any existing copy
    if (FileAccess::exists(load_path)) {
        DirAccess::remove_absolute(load_path);
    }
    
    Error copy_err = DirAccess::copy_absolute(path, load_path);
    FileAccess::set_hidden_attribute(load_path, true);
    
    // Also copy and rename the PDB file for debugging
    Error pdb_err = WindowsUtils::copy_and_rename_pdb(load_path);
}
```

Temporary libraries are tracked and cleaned up on close:

```cpp
// platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:133, 564-567
HashMap<void *, String> temp_libraries;

if (p_data != nullptr && p_data->generate_temp_files) {
    temp_libraries[p_library_handle] = load_path;
}
```

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:479-590](), [platform/windows/os_windows.h:133]()

### Dependency Checking (Windows Debug)

In debug builds on Windows, the system can check library dependencies before loading:

```cpp
// platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:531-548
#ifdef DEBUG_ENABLED
DWORD err_code = GetLastError();

HashSet<String> checked_libs;
HashSet<String> missing_libs;
debug_dynamic_library_check_dependencies(dll_path, checked_libs, missing_libs);

if (!missing_libs.is_empty()) {
    String missing;
    for (const String &E : missing_libs) {
        if (!missing.is_empty()) missing += ", ";
        missing += E;
    }
    ERR_FAIL_V_MSG(ERR_CANT_OPEN, 
        vformat("Can't open dynamic library: %s. Missing dependencies: %s. Error: %s.", 
        p_path, missing, format_error_message(err_code)));
}
#endif
```

This uses ImageHlp API to parse PE import tables and verify all dependencies are available.

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:413-476](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:531-548]()

### Memory Information Dictionary

The `get_memory_info()` method returns a Dictionary with the following keys:

| Key | Type | Description |
|-----|------|-------------|
| `"physical"` | int64 | Total physical memory in bytes |
| `"free"` | int64 | Immediately available memory |
| `"available"` | int64 | Memory available (including swap) |
| `"stack"` | int64 | Current thread stack size |

Values are -1 if unavailable on the platform.

**Windows Implementation:**
```cpp
// platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1615-1664
MEMORYSTATUSEX mem_status;
mem_status.dwLength = sizeof(MEMORYSTATUSEX);
if (GlobalMemoryStatusEx(&mem_status)) {
    meminfo["physical"] = mem_status.ullTotalPhys;
    meminfo["free"] = mem_status.ullAvailPhys;
    meminfo["available"] = mem_status.ullAvailPageFile + mem_status.ullAvailPhys;
}
```

**Unix/Linux Implementation:**
```cpp
// drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:544-569
Ref<FileAccess> f = FileAccess::open("/proc/meminfo", FileAccess::READ, &err);
while (f.is_valid() && !f->eof_reached()) {
    String s = f->get_line().strip_edges();
    if (s.begins_with("MemTotal:")) { /* parse mtotal */ }
    if (s.begins_with("MemFree:")) { /* parse mfree */ }
    if (s.begins_with("SwapFree:")) { /* parse sfree */ }
}
```

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:306](), [doc/classes/OS.xml:359-368](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1615-1664](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:403-590]()

### Random Entropy

Cryptographically secure random bytes are provided via `get_entropy()`:

**Windows:**
```cpp
// platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:406-410
Error OS_Windows::get_entropy(uint8_t *r_buffer, int p_bytes) {
    NTSTATUS status = BCryptGenRandom(nullptr, r_buffer, p_bytes, 
                                      BCRYPT_USE_SYSTEM_PREFERRED_RNG);
    ERR_FAIL_COND_V(status, FAILED);
    return OK;
}
```

**Unix:**
```cpp
// drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:279-303
#if defined(UNIX_GET_ENTROPY)
    // Use getentropy() in chunks of max 256 bytes
    int left = p_bytes;
    int ofs = 0;
    do {
        int chunk = MIN(left, 256);
        ERR_FAIL_COND_V(getentropy(r_buffer + ofs, chunk), FAILED);
        left -= chunk;
        ofs += chunk;
    } while (left > 0);
#elif !defined(NO_URANDOM)
    // Fall back to reading /dev/urandom
    int r = open("/dev/urandom", O_RDONLY);
    // ...read from file descriptor...
#endif
```

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:181](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:406-410](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:279-303]()

### Environment Variables

Environment variable access is provided through:

```cpp
// core/os/os.h:231-234
virtual bool has_environment(const String &p_var) const = 0;
virtual String get_environment(const String &p_var) const = 0;
virtual void set_environment(const String &p_var, const String &p_value) const = 0;
virtual void unset_environment(const String &p_var) const = 0;
```

**Windows Implementation:**
```cpp
// platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1448-1487
bool OS_Windows::has_environment(const String &p_var) const {
    return _wgetenv((LPCWSTR)(p_var.utf16().get_data())) != nullptr;
}

String OS_Windows::get_environment(const String &p_var) const {
    wchar_t *env = _wgetenv((LPCWSTR)(p_var.utf16().get_data()));
    if (env == nullptr) return "";
    return String::utf16((const char16_t *)env);
}

void OS_Windows::set_environment(const String &p_var, const String &p_value) const {
    _wputenv_s((LPCWSTR)(p_var.utf16().get_data()), 
               (LPCWSTR)(p_value.utf16().get_data()));
}
```

**Unix Implementation:**
```cpp
// drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:996-1024
bool OS_Unix::has_environment(const String &p_var) const {
    return getenv(p_var.utf8().get_data()) != nullptr;
}

String OS_Unix::get_environment(const String &p_var) const {
    char *env = getenv(p_var.utf8().get_data());
    if (env == nullptr) return "";
    return String::utf8(env);
}

void OS_Unix::set_environment(const String &p_var, const String &p_value) const {
    setenv(p_var.utf8().get_data(), p_value.utf8().get_data(), 1);
}
```

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:231-234](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1448-1487](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:996-1024]()

### Standard Handle Type Detection

The OS can detect whether stdin/stdout/stderr are connected to a console, file, or pipe:

```cpp
// core/os/os.h:57-63
enum StdHandleType {
    STD_HANDLE_INVALID,
    STD_HANDLE_CONSOLE,
    STD_HANDLE_FILE,
    STD_HANDLE_PIPE,
    STD_HANDLE_UNKNOWN,
};
```

**Unix Implementation:**
```cpp
// drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:216-277
OS_Unix::StdHandleType OS_Unix::get_stdin_type() const {
    int h = fileno(stdin);
    if (h == -1) return STD_HANDLE_INVALID;
    
    if (isatty(h)) return STD_HANDLE_CONSOLE;
    
    struct stat statbuf;
    if (fstat(h, &statbuf) < 0) return STD_HANDLE_UNKNOWN;
    
    if (S_ISFIFO(statbuf.st_mode)) {
        return STD_HANDLE_PIPE;
    } else if (S_ISREG(statbuf.st_mode) || S_ISLNK(statbuf.st_mode)) {
        return STD_HANDLE_FILE;
    }
    return STD_HANDLE_UNKNOWN;
}
```

This information is useful for:
- Detecting if the application is running in a CI environment
- Determining if color output is supported
- Adjusting logging behavior based on output destination

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:57-63, 177-179](), [doc/classes/OS.xml:484-497](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:216-277]()

## Time and Date Services

### High-Resolution Timing

```mermaid

    subgraph "Abstract Interface"
```

### Clock Initialization

**Windows:**
```cpp
// platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:293-311
QueryPerformanceFrequency((LARGE_INTEGER *)&ticks_per_second);
QueryPerformanceCounter((LARGE_INTEGER *)&ticks_start);

// Set minimum resolution for Sleep()
TIMECAPS time_caps;
if (timeGetDevCaps(&time_caps, sizeof(time_caps)) == MMSYSERR_NOERROR) {
    delay_resolution = time_caps.wPeriodMin * 1000;
    timeBeginPeriod(time_caps.wPeriodMin);  // Usually 1ms
}
```

**Unix (Linux):**
```cpp
// drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:127-131
static void _setup_clock() {
    struct timespec tv_now = { 0, 0 };
    ERR_FAIL_COND_MSG(clock_gettime(GODOT_CLOCK, &tv_now) != 0, 
                      "OS CLOCK IS NOT WORKING!");
    _clock_start = ((uint64_t)tv_now.tv_nsec / 1000L) + 
                   (uint64_t)tv_now.tv_sec * 1000000L;
}
```

**macOS:**
```cpp
// drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:114-120
static void _setup_clock() {
    mach_timebase_info_data_t info;
    kern_return_t ret = mach_timebase_info(&info);
    ERR_FAIL_COND_MSG(ret != 0, "OS CLOCK IS NOT WORKING!");
    _clock_scale = ((double)info.numer / (double)info.denom) / 1000.0;
    _clock_start = mach_absolute_time() * _clock_scale;
}
```

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:293-311](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:110-132]()

### Date and Time Queries

```cpp
// core/os/os.h:257-271
struct DateTime {
    int64_t year;
    Month month;
    uint8_t day;
    Weekday weekday;
    uint8_t hour;
    uint8_t minute;
    uint8_t second;
    bool dst;
};

struct TimeZoneInfo {
    int bias;      // Offset from UTC in minutes
    String name;   // Time zone name
};

virtual DateTime get_datetime(bool utc = false) const = 0;
virtual TimeZoneInfo get_time_zone_info() const = 0;
virtual double get_unix_time() const;
```

**Windows Implementation:**
```cpp
// platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:914-962
OS::DateTime OS_Windows::get_datetime(bool p_utc) const {
    SYSTEMTIME systemtime;
    if (p_utc) {
        GetSystemTime(&systemtime);
    } else {
        GetLocalTime(&systemtime);
    }
    
    TIME_ZONE_INFORMATION info;
    bool is_daylight = false;
    if (!p_utc && GetTimeZoneInformation(&info) == TIME_ZONE_ID_DAYLIGHT) {
        is_daylight = true;
    }
    
    DateTime dt;
    dt.year = systemtime.wYear;
    dt.month = Month(systemtime.wMonth);
    dt.day = systemtime.wDay;
    dt.weekday = Weekday(systemtime.wDayOfWeek);
    dt.hour = systemtime.wHour;
    dt.minute = systemtime.wMinute;
    dt.second = systemtime.wSecond;
    dt.dst = is_daylight;
    return dt;
}
```

**Unix Implementation:**
```cpp
// drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:327-349
OS::DateTime OS_Unix::get_datetime(bool p_utc) const {
    time_t t = time(nullptr);
    struct tm lt;
    if (p_utc) {
        gmtime_r(&t, &lt);
    } else {
        localtime_r(&t, &lt);
    }
    DateTime ret;
    ret.year = 1900 + lt.tm_year;
    ret.month = (Month)(lt.tm_mon + 1);
    ret.day = lt.tm_mday;
    ret.weekday = (Weekday)lt.tm_wday;
    ret.hour = lt.tm_hour;
    ret.minute = lt.tm_min;
    ret.second = lt.tm_sec;
    ret.dst = lt.tm_isdst;
    return ret;
}
```

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:257-275](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:914-962](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:327-377]()

## Path and Directory Services

### System Path Methods

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:318-341](), [doc/classes/OS.xml:179-270]()

### Windows Path Implementation

```cpp
// platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1821-1937
String OS_Windows::get_data_path() const {
    // Returns %APPDATA% (Roaming)
    PWSTR path;
    if (SHGetKnownFolderPath(FOLDERID_RoamingAppData, 0, nullptr, &path) == S_OK) {
        String ret = String::utf16((const char16_t *)path).replace_char('\\', '/');
        CoTaskMemFree(path);
        return ret;
    }
    return "C:\\Users\\Default\\AppData\\Roaming";
}

String OS_Windows::get_config_path() const {
    // Same as get_data_path() on Windows
    return get_data_path();
}

String OS_Windows::get_cache_path() const {
    // Returns %LOCALAPPDATA%
    PWSTR path;
    if (SHGetKnownFolderPath(FOLDERID_LocalAppData, 0, nullptr, &path) == S_OK) {
        String ret = String::utf16((const char16_t *)path).replace_char('\\', '/');
        CoTaskMemFree(path);
        return ret;
    }
    return get_data_path();
}

String OS_Windows::get_system_dir(SystemDir p_dir, bool p_shared_storage) const {
    // Maps SystemDir to KNOWNFOLDERID
    KNOWNFOLDERID id;
    switch (p_dir) {
        case SYSTEM_DIR_DESKTOP: id = FOLDERID_Desktop; break;
        case SYSTEM_DIR_DOCUMENTS: id = FOLDERID_Documents; break;
        case SYSTEM_DIR_DOWNLOADS: id = FOLDERID_Downloads; break;
        case SYSTEM_DIR_MOVIES: id = FOLDERID_Videos; break;
        case SYSTEM_DIR_MUSIC: id = FOLDERID_Music; break;
        case SYSTEM_DIR_PICTURES: id = FOLDERID_Pictures; break;
        // ...
    }
    // Use SHGetKnownFolderPath to retrieve
}
```

**Sources:** [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1821-1937]()

### User Data Directory

The user data directory for projects is constructed based on project settings:

```cpp
// core/os/os.cpp:339-355
String OS::get_user_data_dir() const {
    String appname = get_safe_dir_name(GLOBAL_GET("application/config/name"));
    if (!appname.is_empty()) {
        bool use_custom_dir = GLOBAL_GET("application/config/use_custom_user_dir");
        if (use_custom_dir) {
            String custom_dir = get_safe_dir_name(
                GLOBAL_GET("application/config/custom_user_dir_name"), true);
            if (custom_dir.is_empty()) {
                custom_dir = appname;
            }
            return get_user_data_dir(custom_dir);
        } else {
            return get_user_data_dir(
                get_godot_dir_name().path_join("app_userdata").path_join(appname));
        }
    } else {
        return get_user_data_dir(
            get_godot_dir_name().path_join("app_userdata").path_join("[unnamed project]"));
    }
}
```

**Windows Example:**
- Default: `C:\Users\<username>\AppData\Roaming\Godot\app_userdata\<project_name>`
- Custom: `C:\Users\<username>\AppData\Roaming\<custom_dir_name>`

**Linux Example:**
- Default: `$HOME/.local/share/godot/app_userdata/<project_name>`
- Custom: `$HOME/.local/share/<custom_dir_name>`

**Sources:** [core/os/os.cpp:335-355](), [core/os/os.h:326-327]()

### Path Sanitization

The `get_safe_dir_name()` method sanitizes directory names to be valid across platforms:

```cpp
// core/os/os.cpp:263-290
String OS::get_safe_dir_name(const String &p_dir_name, bool p_allow_paths) const {
    String safe_dir_name = p_dir_name;
    Vector<String> invalid_chars = String(": * ? \" < > |").split(" ");
    
    if (p_allow_paths) {
        // Dir separators allowed, but disallow ".."
        invalid_chars.push_back("..");
        safe_dir_name = safe_dir_name.replace_char('\\', '/').replace("//", "/").strip_edges();
    } else {
        invalid_chars.push_back("/");
        invalid_chars.push_back("\\");
        safe_dir_name = safe_dir_name.strip_edges();
        
        // These directory names are invalid
        if (safe_dir_name == ".") {
            safe_dir_name = "dot";
        } else if (safe_dir_name == "..") {
            safe_dir_name = "twodots";
        }
    }
    
    for (int i = 0; i < invalid_chars.size(); i++) {
        safe_dir_name = safe_dir_name.replace(invalid_chars[i], "-");
    }
    
    // Trim trailing periods (invalid on Windows)
    return safe_dir_name.rstrip(".");
}
```

**Sources:** [core/os/os.cpp:263-290](), [core/os/os.h:315]()

## Text Encoding Services

### Character Set Conversion

The OS provides multibyte string conversion for platform-specific text encodings:

```cpp
// core/os/os.h:297-298
virtual String multibyte_to_string(const String &p_encoding, 
                                   const PackedByteArray &p_array) const;
virtual PackedByteArray string_to_multibyte(const String &p_encoding, 
                                            const String &p_string) const;
```

**Windows Implementation:**

Windows maintains a map of encoding names to code pages:

```cpp
// platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1054-1143
void OS_Windows::_init_encodings() {
    encodings[""] = 0;
    encodings["CP_ACP"] = 0;
    encodings["CP_OEMCP"] = 1;
    encodings["IBM437"] = 437;
    encodings["IBM850"] = 850;
    encodings["WINDOWS-1252"] = 1252;
    encodings["UTF-8"] = 65001;
    // ... many more encodings
}

String OS_Windows::multibyte_to_string(const String &p_encoding, 
                                       const PackedByteArray &p_array) const {
    int codepage = encodings.get(p_encoding, 0);
    int len = MultiByteToWideChar(codepage, 0, 
                                  (LPCSTR)p_array.ptr(), p_array.size(), 
                                  nullptr, 0);
    // Allocate and convert
}

PackedByteArray OS_Windows::string_to_multibyte(const String &p_encoding, 
                                                const String &p_string) const {
    int codepage = encodings.get(p_encoding, 0);
    int len = WideCharToMultiByte(codepage, 0, 
                                  (LPCWSTR)p_string.utf16().ptr(), -1, 
                                  nullptr, 0, nullptr, nullptr);
    // Allocate and convert
}
```

**Unix Implementation:**

Unix uses iconv for character set conversion when available:

```cpp
// drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:1026-1115
String OS_Unix::multibyte_to_string(const String &p_encoding, 
                                    const PackedByteArray &p_array) const {
    if (!_iconv_ok) return String::utf8((const char *)p_array.ptr(), p_array.size());
    
    String encoding = p_encoding.is_empty() ? "UTF-8" : p_encoding;
    gd_iconv_t conv = gd_iconv_open("UTF-8", encoding.utf8().get_data());
    
    // Perform conversion using iconv
    char *in_ptr = (char *)p_array.ptr();
    size_t in_left = p_array.size();
    // ... convert to UTF-8 ...
    
    gd_iconv_close(conv);
    return result;
}
```

**Sources:** [core/os/os.h:297-298](), [platform/windows/os_windows.cpp:1054-1143, 1325-1389](), [drivers/unix/os_unix.cpp:1026-1115]()

## Purpose and Scope

The Build System handles the compilation and linking of Godot Engine across multiple platforms using SCons as the build automation tool. It manages platform detection, compiler configuration, module discovery, dependency resolution, and the generation of final binaries (editor builds and export templates).

For information about the Platform Abstraction Layer that the build system configures, see [OS Interface and Implementations](#8.1).

## Build System Architecture

The build system uses SCons (Software Construction tool) with a hierarchical structure of build scripts:


## Main Build Entry Point: SConstruct

The `SConstruct` file is the root build script that orchestrates the entire build process. It follows this execution flow:

**Sources:** [SConstruct:1-1181]()

### Platform Scanning and Detection

Platform detection occurs early in the build process:

1. **Platform Discovery** [SConstruct:77-109](): The build system scans `platform/*/` directories for `detect.py` files and imports each one to check if it can build on the current host (`detect.can_build()`).

2. **Platform Selection** [SConstruct:376-418](): If no platform is specified, the build system auto-detects based on `sys.platform`:
   - `linux*`, `freebsd*`, `openbsd*`, `netbsd*`, `dragonfly*` â†’ `linuxbsd`
   - `darwin` â†’ `macos`  
   - `win32` â†’ `windows`

3. **Option Registration** [SConstruct:420-433](): Each platform's `get_opts()` function returns platform-specific build options that are added to the global options.

**Sources:** [SConstruct:77-109](), [SConstruct:376-418](), [SConstruct:420-433]()

## Platform Detection Scripts

Each platform has a `detect.py` file that provides standardized functions:

| Function | Purpose |
|----------|---------|
| `get_name()` | Returns platform display name |
| `can_build()` | Checks if platform can be built on current host |
| `get_opts()` | Returns list of platform-specific SCons options |
| `get_flags()` | Returns default flag values for the platform |
| `configure(env)` | Configures the SCons environment for the platform |
| `get_doc_classes()` | Returns platform-specific documentation classes |

```mermaid

    subgraph "Windows Platform"
        win_detect["platform/windows/detect.py"]

        win_get_opts["get_opts()<br/>mingw_prefix, use_llvm,<br/>windows_subsystem, etc."]
        win_configure["configure(env)<br/>configure_msvc() or<br/>configure_mingw()"]
        
        win_detect --> win_can_build
        win_detect --> win_get_opts
        win_detect --> win_configure
    end
    
    subgraph "Linux/BSD Platform"
        linux_detect["platform/linuxbsd/detect.py"]
        linux_can_build["can_build()<br/>Check pkg-config exists"]
        linux_get_opts["get_opts()<br/>use_llvm, linker,<br/>use_sowrap, etc."]
        linux_configure["configure(env)<br/>Setup GCC/Clang,<br/>detect dependencies"]
        
        linux_detect --> linux_can_build
        linux_detect --> linux_get_opts
        linux_configure --> linux_configure
    end
    
    subgraph "macOS Platform"

    end
```

**Sources:** [platform/windows/detect.py:1-893](), [platform/linuxbsd/detect.py:1-558](), [platform/macos/detect.py:1-393]()

### Platform Configuration Flow

The `configure()` function in each platform's `detect.py` performs these tasks:

1. **Architecture Validation** [platform/linuxbsd/detect.py:74-77](): Validates the target architecture against supported architectures using `validate_arch()`.

2. **Compiler Detection/Selection** [platform/windows/detect.py:243-264](): Selects the appropriate compiler (MSVC, MinGW/GCC, Clang) based on availability and user options.

3. **Compiler Flags Configuration** [platform/linuxbsd/detect.py:187-215](): Sets up optimization levels, LTO (Link-Time Optimization), debug symbols, and sanitizer flags.

4. **Platform-Specific Defines** [platform/windows/detect.py:358-372](): Adds preprocessor defines like `WINDOWS_ENABLED`, `WASAPI_ENABLED`, version macros, etc.

5. **Library Dependencies** [platform/linuxbsd/detect.py:232-422](): Configures system libraries using `pkg-config` (on Linux/BSD) or manual paths (on other platforms).

**Sources:** [platform/linuxbsd/detect.py:74-558](), [platform/windows/detect.py:243-893]()

## Module Discovery and Registration

The module system allows extending Godot with optional features:

```mermaid
graph TB
    SConstruct_modules["SConstruct<br/>Detect Modules"]
    
    detect_modules["methods.detect_modules()<br/>Search for register_types.h,<br/>SCsub, config.py"]
    
    built_in["modules/ directory<br/>Built-in modules"]
    custom["custom_modules paths<br/>User-provided modules"]
    
    module_config["Module config.py<br/>is_enabled(), get_opts()"]
    
    add_options["Add module_*_enabled<br/>option for each module"]
    
    modules_scsub["modules/SCsub<br/>Process each enabled module"]
    
    gen_enabled["Generate modules_enabled.gen.h<br/>MODULE_*_ENABLED defines"]
    
    gen_register["Generate register_module_types.gen.cpp<br/>initialize/uninitialize calls"]
    
    module_scsub["module/*/SCsub<br/>Build module source files"]
    
    lib_module["libmodule_*.a<br/>Module static library"]
    
    SConstruct_modules --> detect_modules
    detect_modules --> built_in
    detect_modules --> custom
    
    built_in --> module_config
    custom --> module_config
    module_config --> add_options
    
    add_options --> modules_scsub
    modules_scsub --> gen_enabled
    modules_scsub --> gen_register
    modules_scsub --> module_scsub
    module_scsub --> lib_module
```

**Sources:** [SConstruct:435-493](), [methods.py:240-311](), [modules/SCsub:1-64]()

### Module Detection Process

The module detection algorithm [methods.py:240-311]():

1. **Directory Scanning**: Recursively or non-recursively scans directories for modules.

2. **Module Validation**: A valid module must contain:
   - `register_types.h` - Module initialization interface
   - `SCsub` - SCons build script
   - `config.py` - Module configuration

3. **Module Registry**: Discovered modules are stored in `env.modules_detected` as an `OrderedDict` mapping module names to paths.

4. **Custom Module Paths**: Custom modules can override built-in ones if they have the same name [SConstruct:461]().

**Sources:** [methods.py:240-311](), [SConstruct:435-493]()

### Module Build Integration

Each module is processed by `modules/SCsub`:

1. **Header Generation** [modules/SCsub:19-21](): Generates `modules_enabled.gen.h` with `MODULE_*_ENABLED` defines.

2. **Registration Code** [modules/SCsub:24-28](): Generates `register_module_types.gen.cpp` that includes each module's `register_types.h` and calls initialization functions.

3. **Module Compilation** [modules/SCsub:33-42](): For each enabled module, processes its `SCsub` file and builds a static library `libmodule_<name>.a`.

4. **Test Integration** [modules/SCsub:44-55](): Collects module test headers into `modules_tests.gen.h`.

**Sources:** [modules/SCsub:1-64](), [modules/modules_builders.py:1-57]()

## Build Options System

Build options are defined using SCons Variables:

| Option Category | Examples | Location |
|----------------|----------|----------|
| Target Configuration | `target`, `arch`, `optimize`, `lto` | [SConstruct:161-186]() |
| Components | `deprecated`, `minizip`, `vulkan`, `opengl3` | [SConstruct:189-224]() |
| Development | `dev_build`, `tests`, `verbose`, `warnings` | [SConstruct:227-251]() |
| Customization | `extra_suffix`, `custom_modules`, `build_profile` | [SConstruct:251-291]() |
| Third-party | `builtin_freetype`, `builtin_zlib`, etc. | [SConstruct:311-341]() |
| Compiler | `CXX`, `CC`, `LINK`, `ccflags`, `linkflags` | [SConstruct:343-360]() |

**Sources:** [SConstruct:147-360]()

### Build Profiles

Build profiles allow disabling specific features via JSON configuration [SConstruct:638-658]():

```json
{
  "disabled_classes": ["Node3D", "MeshInstance3D"],
  "disabled_build_options": {
    "disable_3d": true
  }
}
```

The profile is read and applied during environment setup, adding disabled classes to `env.disabled_classes` and setting build options.

**Sources:** [SConstruct:638-658]()

## Subsystem Build Scripts (SCsub)

Each major subsystem has an `SCsub` file that defines how it's built:

```mermaid

    subgraph "Core Subsystem"
        core_scsub["core/SCsub"]

        core_gen["Generate version files<br/>version_generated.gen.h<br/>version_hash.gen.cpp"]
        core_compile["Compile core/*.cpp"]
        core_lib["libcore.a"]
        
        core_scsub --> core_thirdparty
        core_scsub --> core_gen
        core_scsub --> core_compile
        core_thirdparty --> core_lib
        core_gen --> core_lib
        core_compile --> core_lib
    end
    
    subgraph "Modules Subsystem"
        modules_scsub["modules/SCsub"]
        modules_detect["Build modules_enabled.gen.h"]
        modules_register["Build register_module_types.gen.cpp"]
        modules_build["Build each module's SCsub<br/>â†’ libmodule_*.a"]
        modules_lib["libmodules.a"]
        
        modules_scsub --> modules_detect
        modules_scsub --> modules_register
        modules_scsub --> modules_build
        modules_register --> modules_lib
    end
    
    subgraph "Editor Subsystem"
        editor_scsub["editor/SCsub"]
        editor_docs["Generate doc_data_compressed.gen.h<br/>from XML documentation"]
        editor_trans["Generate translation files<br/>editor_translations.gen.cpp"]
        editor_exporters["Generate register_exporters.gen.cpp"]
        editor_compile["Compile editor/*.cpp"]
        editor_lib["libeditor.a"]
        
        editor_scsub --> editor_docs
        editor_scsub --> editor_trans
        editor_scsub --> editor_exporters
        editor_scsub --> editor_compile
        editor_docs --> editor_lib
        editor_trans --> editor_lib
        editor_exporters --> editor_lib

    end
    
    subgraph "Platform Subsystem"
        platform_scsub["platform/SCsub"]

        platform_apis["Generate register_platform_apis.gen.cpp"]
        platform_compile["Compile platform/*/api/*.cpp"]
        platform_lib["libplatform.a"]
        
        platform_scsub --> platform_icons
        platform_scsub --> platform_apis
        platform_scsub --> platform_compile
        platform_icons --> platform_lib
        platform_apis --> platform_lib
        platform_compile --> platform_lib
    end
```

**Sources:** [core/SCsub:1-244](), [modules/SCsub:1-64](), [editor/SCsub:1-103](), [platform/SCsub:1-31]()

### Platform-Specific Build Files

Platform-specific code is built by `platform/<platform>/SCsub` files. For example, Windows:

1. **Source Selection** [platform/windows/SCsub:15-38](): Selects common Windows sources, chooses between SEH (MSVC) or signal-based crash handlers, and includes console wrapper if GUI subsystem is used.

2. **Resource Compilation** [platform/windows/SCsub:71-82](): Compiles Windows resource files (`*.rc`) for embedding version information and icons.

3. **Binary Linking** [platform/windows/SCsub:87-93](): Links the final binary as executable, static library, or shared library based on `library_type`.

4. **D3D12 Dependencies** [platform/windows/SCsub:122-161](): Copies Agility SDK and PIX runtime DLLs to the output directory if D3D12 is enabled.

**Sources:** [platform/windows/SCsub:1-170]()

## Compilation Pipeline

The complete build process follows this pipeline:

```mermaid
graph TB
    ParseOptions["Parse Command-Line Options<br/>scons p=windows target=editor"]
    
    CreateEnv["Create Base Environment<br/>env = Environment(tools=[])"]
    
    DetectPlatform["Detect/Validate Platform<br/>Auto-detect or use p= option"]
    
    LoadDetectPy["Load platform/*/detect.py"]
    
    AddOptions["Add Platform Options<br/>detect.get_opts()"]
    
    ApplyFlags["Apply Platform Flags<br/>detect.get_flags()"]
    
    LoadTools["Load Build Tools<br/>detect.get_tools(env)<br/>msvc/mingw/clang/gcc"]
    
    Configure["Configure Environment<br/>detect.configure(env)<br/>Set compiler flags, defines, libs"]
    
    DetectModules["Detect & Configure Modules<br/>methods.detect_modules()"]
    
    GenerateHeaders["Generate Headers<br/>version_generated.gen.h<br/>modules_enabled.gen.h<br/>doc_data_compressed.gen.h"]
    
    CompileCore["Compile Core<br/>core/*.cpp â†’ libcore.a"]
    
    CompileScene["Compile Scene<br/>scene/*.cpp â†’ libscene.a"]
    
    CompileServers["Compile Servers<br/>servers/*.cpp â†’ libservers.a"]
    
    CompileModules["Compile Modules<br/>modules/*/*.cpp â†’ libmodule_*.a<br/>+ libmodules.a"]
    
    CompileEditor["Compile Editor (if target=editor)<br/>editor/*.cpp â†’ libeditor.a"]
    
    CompilePlatform["Compile Platform<br/>platform/*/*.cpp â†’ libplatform.a"]
    
    CompileMain["Compile Main<br/>main/*.cpp â†’ libmain.a"]
    
    LinkBinary["Link Final Binary<br/>godot.exe / godot<br/>Combine all .a files + platform libs"]
    
    ParseOptions --> CreateEnv
    CreateEnv --> DetectPlatform
    DetectPlatform --> LoadDetectPy
    LoadDetectPy --> AddOptions
    AddOptions --> ApplyFlags
    ApplyFlags --> LoadTools
    LoadTools --> Configure
    Configure --> DetectModules
    DetectModules --> GenerateHeaders
    GenerateHeaders --> CompileCore
    CompileCore --> CompileScene
    CompileScene --> CompileServers
    CompileServers --> CompileModules
    CompileModules --> CompileEditor
    CompileEditor --> CompilePlatform
    CompilePlatform --> CompileMain
    CompileMain --> LinkBinary
```

**Sources:** [SConstruct:1-1181]()

### Compilation Control

Key SCons environment methods added by `methods.py`:

| Method | Purpose | Location |
|--------|---------|----------|
| `add_source_files()` | Adds source files to compilation, handles SCU builds | [methods.py:80-85]() |
| `add_library()` | Creates static library with NoCache | [methods.py:595-598]() |
| `add_program()` | Creates executable with NoCache | [methods.py:601-604]() |
| `disable_warnings()` | Disables compiler warnings for thirdparty code | [methods.py:115-120]() |
| `CommandNoCache()` | Executes command without caching | [methods.py:607-610]() |

**Sources:** [methods.py:36-610]()

### Build Optimization Features

1. **SCU Builds** [SConstruct:678-690](): Single Compilation Unit builds combine multiple source files to reduce compilation time, controlled by `scu_build=yes` and `scu_limit`.

2. **Caching** [SConstruct:365-366](): SCons build cache is configured via `cache_path` option to reuse compiled objects across builds.

3. **Parallel Builds** [SConstruct:599-621](): Automatically detects CPU count and sets parallel job count (`-j`), defaulting to CPU count - 1.

4. **Fast Unsafe Mode** [SConstruct:564-571](): When `fast_unsafe=yes`, enables SCons implicit cache and max drift for faster incremental rebuilds.

**Sources:** [SConstruct:365-366](), [SConstruct:564-621](), [SConstruct:678-690]()

## Build Artifacts

The build system produces these outputs in `bin/`:

| Artifact Type | Pattern | Description |
|---------------|---------|-------------|
| Editor Binary | `godot.windows.editor.x86_64.exe` | Editor executable |
| Template Binary | `godot.windows.template_debug.x86_64.exe` | Export template (debug) |
| Template Binary | `godot.windows.template_release.x86_64.exe` | Export template (release) |
| Static Libraries | `libcore.a`, `libscene.a`, etc. | Intermediate libraries |
| Object Files | `bin/obj/**/*.o` | Compiled object files (if `redirect_build_objects=yes`) |

The naming convention includes: platform, target, architecture, and optional extra suffix [SConstruct:623-626]().

**Sources:** [SConstruct:623-626](), [methods.py:88-112]()34:T66d0,# SCons Configuration

This document describes the SCons-based build configuration system in Godot Engine, including the main build script, build options, platform detection, and compilation pipeline. For information about platform-specific build scripts and module system, see [Platform Detection and Module System](#9.2).

## Overview

Godot uses SCons (Software Construction tool) as its build system. The build configuration is centered around the **SConstruct** file, which orchestrates the entire compilation process by:

- Detecting and validating the target platform
- Configuring compiler toolchains and flags
- Discovering and enabling modules
- Managing build options and optimization levels
- Coordinating platform-specific build scripts (SCsub files)

Sources: [SConstruct:1-1181](), [methods.py:1-1450](), [platform_methods.py:1-262]()

## Build System Architecture

```mermaid
graph TB
    SConstruct["SConstruct<br/>Main Build Script"]
    methods["methods.py<br/>Build Utilities"]
    platform_methods["platform_methods.py<br/>Platform Helpers"]
    
    subgraph "Platform Detection"
        detect_py["platform/*/detect.py<br/>Platform Configuration"]
        can_build["can_build()"]
        get_opts["get_opts()"]
        get_flags["get_flags()"]
        configure["configure(env)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Build Scripts"
        core_scsub["core/SCsub"]
        editor_scsub["editor/SCsub"]
        modules_scsub["modules/SCsub"]
        platform_scsub["platform/*/SCsub"]
        main_scsub["main/SCsub"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Build Environment"
        env["Environment<br/>SCons env object"]
        opts["Variables<br/>Build options"]
        builders["Custom Builders"]
    end
    
    SConstruct -->|"imports"| methods
    SConstruct -->|"imports"| platform_methods
    SConstruct -->|"scans"| detect_py
    
    detect_py --> can_build
    detect_py --> get_opts
    detect_py --> get_flags
    detect_py --> configure
    
    SConstruct -->|"creates"| env
    SConstruct -->|"configures"| opts
    opts -->|"updates"| env
    
    detect_py -->|"configures"| env
    
    env -->|"SConscript()"| core_scsub
    env -->|"SConscript()"| editor_scsub
    env -->|"SConscript()"| modules_scsub
    env -->|"SConscript()"| platform_scsub
    env -->|"SConscript()"| main_scsub
    
    methods -->|"provides"| builders
    builders -->|"extend"| env
```

Sources: [SConstruct:1-1181](), [methods.py:1-1450](), [platform_methods.py:1-262]()

## SConstruct Main Build Script

The **SConstruct** file is the entry point for the build system. It follows a structured initialization and configuration flow:

### Initialization Phase

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["Build Start<br/>scons command"]
    Version["EnsureSConsVersion(4, 0)<br/>EnsurePythonVersion(3, 9)"]
    Helpers["_helper_module()<br/>Load helper modules"]
    PlatformScan["Platform Scanning<br/>glob('platform/*')"]
    Import["Import detect.py<br/>from each platform"]
    
    Start --> Version
    Version --> Helpers
    Helpers --> PlatformScan
    PlatformScan --> Import
    
    Import --> BuildList["platform_list<br/>platform_opts<br/>platform_flags"]
```

The build script begins by ensuring minimum tool versions and loading helper modules using the `_helper_module()` function [SConstruct:25-44](). This function explicitly resolves module paths to avoid naming conflicts.

Platform discovery occurs by scanning the `platform/` directory [SConstruct:77-109]():
- Each subdirectory with a `detect.py` file is considered a platform
- The `detect.can_build()` function determines if the platform is available
- Platform options and flags are collected into `platform_opts` and `platform_flags` dictionaries

Sources: [SConstruct:1-109](), [methods.py:1-50]()

### Environment Construction

```mermaid
graph LR
    EmptyEnv["Environment(tools=[])"]
    PrependPath["PrependENVPath('PATH')"]
    CustomMethods["Add custom methods<br/>add_source_files<br/>add_library<br/>add_program"]
    Variables["Variables(customs, ARGUMENTS)"]
    
    EmptyEnv --> PrependPath
    PrependPath --> CustomMethods
    CustomMethods --> Variables
    Variables --> UpdateEnv["opts.Update(env)"]
```

The SCons environment is created without default tools to give Godot full control [SConstruct:115]():

```python
env = Environment(tools=[])
env.PrependENVPath("PATH", os.getenv("PATH"))
```

Custom build methods are attached to the environment [SConstruct:126-139]():
- `env.add_source_files()` - Add source files with SCU build support
- `env.add_library()` / `env.add_shared_library()` / `env.add_program()` - Build artifacts
- `env.CommandNoCache()` - Execute commands without caching
- `env.disable_warnings()` - Disable compiler warnings
- `env.force_optimization_on_debug()` - Override optimization for specific files

Sources: [SConstruct:111-145](), [methods.py:36-86](), [methods.py:589-616]()

## Build Options System

Build options are defined using SCons `Variables` and organized into categories:

### Core Build Options

| Option | Type | Default | Description |
|--------|------|---------|-------------|
| `platform` | String | auto-detected | Target platform (windows, linuxbsd, macos, etc.) |
| `target` | Enum | "editor" | Build target: editor, template_release, template_debug |
| `arch` | Enum | "auto" | CPU architecture (x86_32, x86_64, arm32, arm64, etc.) |
| `dev_build` | Boolean | False | Developer build with DEV_ENABLED code |
| `optimize` | Enum | "auto" | Optimization level: none, debug, speed, speed_trace, size |
| `debug_symbols` | Boolean | False | Include debugging symbols |
| `lto` | Enum | "none" | Link-time optimization: none, auto, thin, full |

Sources: [SConstruct:161-186]()

### Component Options

| Option | Type | Default | Description |
|--------|------|---------|-------------|
| `deprecated` | Boolean | True | Enable deprecated/removed feature compatibility |
| `precision` | Enum | "single" | Floating-point precision: single, double |
| `vulkan` | Boolean | True | Enable Vulkan rendering driver |
| `opengl3` | Boolean | True | Enable OpenGL/GLES3 rendering driver |
| `d3d12` | Boolean | False | Enable Direct3D 12 rendering driver |
| `metal` | Boolean | False | Enable Metal rendering driver (Apple) |

Sources: [SConstruct:190-209]()

### Advanced Build Options

| Option | Type | Default | Description |
|--------|------|---------|-------------|
| `dev_mode` | Boolean | False | Alias for: verbose=yes warnings=extra werror=yes tests=yes |
| `ninja` | Boolean | False | Use ninja backend for faster rebuilds |
| `compiledb` | Boolean | False | Generate compile_commands.json |
| `scu_build` | Boolean | False | Use single compilation unit build |
| `verbose` | Boolean | False | Enable verbose compilation output |
| `custom_modules` | String | "" | Comma-separated paths to custom module directories |

Sources: [SConstruct:228-274]()

### Third-Party Library Options

All third-party libraries can be toggled between built-in and system versions using `builtin_<name>` options [SConstruct:312-341]():

```python
opts.Add(BoolVariable("builtin_zlib", "Use the built-in zlib library", True))
opts.Add(BoolVariable("builtin_freetype", "Use the built-in FreeType library", True))
opts.Add(BoolVariable("builtin_pcre2", "Use the built-in PCRE2 library", True))
# ... and many more
```

Sources: [SConstruct:312-341]()

## Platform Detection and Configuration

### Platform Selection Flow

```mermaid
graph TD
    CheckArg["Check 'platform' argument"]
    AutoDetect{"platform<br/>specified?"}
    DetectOS["Detect from sys.platform<br/>linuxâ†’linuxbsd<br/>darwinâ†’macos<br/>win32â†’windows"]
    
    Validate{"platform in<br/>platform_list?"}
    Error["Print error<br/>Exit(255)"]
    LoadOpts["opts.AddVariables(*platform_opts[platform])"]
    
    ApplyFlags["Apply platform_flags<br/>to env"]
    LoadDetect["Import platform detect.py"]
    GetTools["detect.get_tools(env)"]
    Configure["detect.configure(env)"]
    
    CheckArg --> AutoDetect
    AutoDetect -->|No| DetectOS
    AutoDetect -->|Yes| Validate
    DetectOS --> Validate
    
    Validate -->|No| Error
    Validate -->|Yes| LoadOpts
    LoadOpts --> ApplyFlags
    ApplyFlags --> LoadDetect
    LoadDetect --> GetTools
    GetTools --> Configure
```

Platform detection occurs in multiple stages [SConstruct:376-433]():

1. **Automatic Detection**: If no platform is specified, the script detects from `sys.platform`
2. **Alias Resolution**: Deprecated aliases like "osx" â†’ "macos" are resolved
3. **Platform Options**: Platform-specific options are added to the build configuration
4. **Platform Flags**: Default flags from `detect.get_flags()` are applied
5. **Toolchain Selection**: `detect.get_tools()` determines compiler toolchain
6. **Configuration**: `detect.configure()` sets up compiler flags and dependencies

Sources: [SConstruct:376-433](), [SConstruct:499-509](), [platform/windows/detect.py:152-161]()

### Platform detect.py Interface

Each platform provides a `detect.py` module with a standard interface:

| Function | Return Type | Purpose |
|----------|-------------|---------|
| `get_name()` | String | Platform display name |
| `can_build()` | Boolean | Check if platform can be built on current system |
| `get_opts()` | List | Platform-specific build options |
| `get_flags()` | Dict | Default platform flags (arch, supported features) |
| `get_tools(env)` | List | SCons tools to use (e.g., ["msvc", "mslink"]) |
| `configure(env)` | None | Configure environment for the platform |
| `get_doc_classes()` | List | Platform-specific documentation classes |
| `get_doc_path()` | String | Path to platform documentation |

Sources: [platform/windows/detect.py:19-241](), [platform/linuxbsd/detect.py:13-73]()

### Example: Windows Platform Configuration

The Windows platform demonstrates the full configuration flow [platform/windows/detect.py:243-519]():

```mermaid
graph TD
    configure["configure(env)"]
    DetectTool{"use_mingw or<br/>not msvc_exists()?"}
    
    MSVC["configure_msvc(env)"]
    MinGW["configure_mingw(env)"]
    
    MSVCFlags["Set MSVC flags<br/>/fp:strict, /Gd, /GR<br/>/utf-8, /bigobj"]
    MSVCLibs["Add system libraries<br/>winmm, ole32, user32, etc."]
    MSVCLto["Configure LTO<br/>/GL, /LTCG"]
    
    MinGWFlags["Set MinGW flags<br/>-ffp-contract=off<br/>-Wa,-mbig-obj"]
    MinGWTools["Set compiler tools<br/>CC=clang/gcc<br/>AR=ar/gcc-ar"]
    MinGWLto["Configure LTO<br/>-flto=thin or -flto"]
    
    configure --> DetectTool
    DetectTool -->|MinGW| MinGW
    DetectTool -->|MSVC| MSVC
    
    MSVC --> MSVCFlags
    MSVCFlags --> MSVCLibs
    MSVCLibs --> MSVCLto
    
    MinGW --> MinGWFlags
    MinGWFlags --> MinGWTools
    MinGWTools --> MinGWLto
```

Sources: [platform/windows/detect.py:243-772]()

## Module Discovery and Configuration

### Module Detection

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["Module Detection"]
    SearchPaths["module_search_paths<br/>= ['modules']"]
    CustomPaths{"custom_modules<br/>specified?"}
    AddCustom["Add custom paths<br/>to search_paths"]
    
    Detect["methods.detect_modules()<br/>for each path"]
    CheckFiles["Check for:<br/>register_types.h<br/>SCsub<br/>config.py"]
    
    AddToDict["modules_detected[name] = path"]
    LoadConfig["Import config.py"]
    AddOpts["Add module options<br/>module_<name>_enabled"]
    
    Start --> SearchPaths
    SearchPaths --> CustomPaths
    CustomPaths -->|Yes| AddCustom
    CustomPaths -->|No| Detect
    AddCustom --> Detect
    
    Detect --> CheckFiles
    CheckFiles --> AddToDict
    AddToDict --> LoadConfig
    LoadConfig --> AddOpts
```

Module discovery occurs in [SConstruct:436-492]() using `methods.detect_modules()`:

1. **Search Paths**: Start with built-in `modules/` directory
2. **Custom Modules**: Add paths from `custom_modules` option
3. **Module Validation**: Each module must have:
   - `register_types.h` - Module registration interface
   - `SCsub` - SCons build script
   - `config.py` - Module configuration

4. **Module Options**: For each detected module, create a `module_<name>_enabled` option
5. **Module-Specific Options**: Call `config.get_opts(platform)` to add module options

Sources: [SConstruct:436-492](), [methods.py:240-310]()

### Module Configuration Properties

Modules can define configuration through their `config.py`:

| Function | Purpose |
|----------|---------|
| `is_enabled()` | Return default enabled state |
| `get_opts(platform)` | Return list of module-specific build options |
| `can_build(env, platform)` | Check if module can be built for platform |
| `configure(env)` | Configure environment for the module |
| `get_doc_classes()` | Return list of documentation classes |
| `get_doc_path()` | Return path to module documentation |
| `get_icons_path()` | Return path to module icons |

Sources: [SConstruct:469-487](), [modules/SCsub:33-42]()

## Build Target Configuration

### Target Types and Defines

```mermaid
graph LR
    Target["env['target']"]
    Editor{"target == 'editor'"}
    TemplateDebug{"target == 'template_debug'"}
    TemplateRelease{"target == 'template_release'"}
    
    EditorDef["TOOLS_ENABLED<br/>DEBUG_ENABLED"]
    DebugDef["DEBUG_ENABLED"]
    ReleaseDef["NDEBUG"]
    
    Target --> Editor
    Target --> TemplateDebug
    Target --> TemplateRelease
    
    Editor --> EditorDef
    TemplateDebug --> DebugDef
    TemplateRelease --> ReleaseDef
```

Build targets determine compilation defines [SConstruct:526-556]():

- **`target=editor`**: Full editor build
  - Sets `TOOLS_ENABLED` define
  - Sets `DEBUG_ENABLED` define (debug features)
  - Sets `DEV_ENABLED` if `dev_build=yes`

- **`target=template_debug`**: Debug export template
  - Sets `DEBUG_ENABLED` define
  - Omits `TOOLS_ENABLED`

- **`target=template_release`**: Release export template
  - Sets `NDEBUG` define (disables asserts)
  - Optimized for production

Sources: [SConstruct:526-556]()

### Optimization Level Selection

```mermaid
graph TD
    OptLevel["env['optimize']"]
    Auto{"optimize == 'auto'"}
    
    DevBuild{"dev_build?"}
    DebugFeatures{"debug_features?"}
    
    SetNone["optimize = 'none'"]
    SetTrace["optimize = 'speed_trace'"]
    SetSpeed["optimize = 'speed'"]
    
    Custom["Use specified level<br/>none/debug/speed/size"]
    
    OptLevel --> Auto
    Auto -->|Yes| DevBuild
    Auto -->|No| Custom
    
    DevBuild -->|Yes| SetNone
    DevBuild -->|No| DebugFeatures
    
    DebugFeatures -->|Yes| SetTrace
    DebugFeatures -->|No| SetSpeed
```

Optimization levels are automatically selected based on build type [SConstruct:530-537]():

- `dev_build=yes` â†’ `optimize=none` (no optimization, fastest compilation)
- `debug_features=yes` â†’ `optimize=speed_trace` (optimized with profiling)
- Production â†’ `optimize=speed` (maximum performance)

Sources: [SConstruct:530-537]()

## Compiler Configuration

### Compiler Detection and Validation

The build system detects and validates compiler versions [SConstruct:704-772]():

```mermaid
graph TD
    GetVersion["methods.get_compiler_version(env)"]
    CheckVersion{"version.major != -1"}
    
    GCC{"using_gcc(env)?"}
    Clang{"using_clang(env)?"}
    MSVC{"env.msvc?"}
    
    GCCMin["Require GCC >= 9"]
    ClangMin["Require Clang >= 6<br/>or Apple Clang >= 16"]
    MSVCMin["Require VS2017 >= 15.9<br/>or VS2019 >= 16.11"]
    
    GetVersion --> CheckVersion
    CheckVersion -->|Yes| GCC
    CheckVersion -->|No| Skip["Skip validation"]
    
    GCC -->|Yes| GCCMin
    GCC -->|No| Clang
    Clang -->|Yes| ClangMin
    Clang -->|No| MSVC
    MSVC -->|Yes| MSVCMin
```

Compiler version requirements [SConstruct:704-772]():
- **GCC**: Minimum version 9 for full C++17 support
- **Clang**: Minimum version 6 (or Apple Clang 16)
- **MSVC**: VS2017 15.9+ or VS2019 16.11+ or VS2022

Sources: [SConstruct:704-772](), [methods.py:687-802]()

### Architecture-Specific Flags

```mermaid
graph TD
    Arch["env['arch']"]
    x86_64{"arch == 'x86_64'"}
    x86_32{"arch == 'x86_32'"}
    
    SSE42["Enable SSE4.2<br/>MSVC: /d2archSSE42<br/>GCC/Clang: -msse4.2 -mpopcnt"]
    SSE2["Enable SSE2<br/>MSVC: /arch:SSE2<br/>GCC/Clang: -msse2 -mfpmath=sse"]
    
    Arch --> x86_64
    Arch --> x86_32
    
    x86_64 --> SSE42
    x86_32 --> SSE2
```

CPU-specific flags are added for x86 architectures [SConstruct:775-793]():

- **x86_64**: Enable SSE4.2 and POPCNT instructions (supported since ~2009-2011 CPUs)
- **x86_32**: Enable SSE2 for more stable floating-point math vs. x87

Sources: [SConstruct:775-793]()

### Optimization and Debug Symbol Flags

Compiler flags are set based on optimization and debug settings [SConstruct:810-864]():

**MSVC**:
- Debug symbols: `/Zi /FS` + `/DEBUG:FULL`
- Speed optimization: `/O2` + `/OPT:REF`
- Size optimization: `/O1` + `/OPT:REF`

**GCC/Clang**:
- Debug symbols: `-gdwarf-4` (or `-gdwarf-5` for GCC on Windows)
- Speed optimization: Set via `$OPTIMIZELEVEL` variable
- Stripping: `-s` linker flag when not using debug symbols

Sources: [SConstruct:810-864]()

## Build Script Hierarchy

### SCsub Execution Flow

```mermaid
graph TD
    SConstruct["SConstruct<br/>Main script"]
    
    Core["core/SCsub"]
    Modules["modules/SCsub"]
    Main["main/SCsub"]
    Platform["platform/SCsub"]
    Servers["servers/SCsub"]
    Scene["scene/SCsub"]
    Editor["editor/SCsub"]
    
    ModuleSCsub["modules/*/SCsub<br/>Individual modules"]
    PlatformSCsub["platform/*/SCsub<br/>Platform-specific"]
    
    CoreLib["libcore.a"]
    ModulesLib["libmodules.a<br/>libmodule_*.a"]
    MainLib["libmain.a"]
    EditorLib["libeditor.a"]
    
    FinalLink["Final Binary<br/>godot.exe / godot"]
    
    SConstruct --> Core
    SConstruct --> Modules
    SConstruct --> Main
    SConstruct --> Platform
    SConstruct --> Servers
    SConstruct --> Scene
    SConstruct --> Editor
    
    Modules --> ModuleSCsub
    Platform --> PlatformSCsub
    
    Core --> CoreLib
    Modules --> ModulesLib
    Main --> MainLib
    Editor --> EditorLib
    
    CoreLib --> FinalLink
    ModulesLib --> FinalLink
    MainLib --> FinalLink
    EditorLib --> FinalLink
```

Each major subsystem has an SCsub file that:
1. Creates a cloned environment (`env.Clone()`)
2. Adds source files to a sources list
3. Builds a static library with `env.add_library()`
4. Prepends the library to `env.Prepend(LIBS=[])`

Sources: [core/SCsub:1-244](), [modules/SCsub:1-64](), [editor/SCsub:1-103]()

### Core Build Script Structure

The `core/SCsub` demonstrates the typical pattern [core/SCsub:1-244]():

```python
# Clone environment for thirdparty code
env_thirdparty = env.Clone()
env_thirdparty.disable_warnings()

# Build thirdparty libraries (zlib, zstd, brotli, etc.)
env_thirdparty.add_source_files(thirdparty_obj, sources)

# Build Godot core sources
env.add_source_files(env.core_sources, "*.cpp")

# Generate version files
env.CommandNoCache("version_generated.gen.h", ...)
env.CommandNoCache("version_hash.gen.cpp", ...)

# Process subdirectories
SConscript("os/SCsub")
SConscript("math/SCsub")
SConscript("io/SCsub")
# ...

# Build and register library
lib = env.add_library("core", env.core_sources)
env.Prepend(LIBS=[lib])
```

Sources: [core/SCsub:1-244]()

### Module Build Script Structure

The `modules/SCsub` coordinates module compilation [modules/SCsub:1-64]():

1. **Generate Module Headers**: Create `modules_enabled.gen.h` with `MODULE_*_ENABLED` defines
2. **Build Individual Modules**: Call `SConscript()` for each enabled module
3. **Create Module Libraries**: Each module builds `libmodule_<name>.a`
4. **Generate Registration Code**: Create `register_module_types.gen.cpp` with init/uninit functions
5. **Build Modules Library**: Create `libmodules.a` with registration code

Sources: [modules/SCsub:1-64](), [modules/modules_builders.py:1-57]()

## Build Helper Methods

### Source File Management

```mermaid
graph LR
    AddSource["env.add_source_files(sources, files)"]
    CheckSCU{"scu_build<br/>enabled?"}
    
    SCUBuild["add_source_files_scu()<br/>Use .scu/scu_*.gen.cpp"]
    RegularBuild["add_source_files_orig()<br/>Use Glob() pattern"]
    
    Object["env.Object(file)<br/>Compile to .o"]
    Append["sources.append(obj)"]
    
    AddSource --> CheckSCU
    CheckSCU -->|Yes| SCUBuild
    CheckSCU -->|No| RegularBuild
    
    SCUBuild --> Object
    RegularBuild --> Object
    Object --> Append
```

The `add_source_files()` method [methods.py:80-85]() supports:
- **Glob patterns**: `env.add_source_files(sources, "*.cpp")`
- **SCU builds**: Automatically uses pre-generated SCU files if enabled
- **Duplicate detection**: Warns if object already added

Sources: [methods.py:36-85](), [SConstruct:128]()

### Build Artifact Methods

```mermaid
graph TD
    Library["env.add_library(name, sources)"]
    SharedLib["env.add_shared_library(name, sources)"]
    Program["env.add_program(name, sources)"]
    
    Build["Build artifact"]
    NoCache["env.NoCache(artifact)"]
    Return["Return artifact"]
    
    Library --> Build
    SharedLib --> Build
    Program --> Build
    
    Build --> NoCache
    NoCache --> Return
```

Custom build methods prevent SCons from caching certain artifacts [methods.py:589-604]():

- `env.add_library()` - Build static library (`.a`)
- `env.add_shared_library()` - Build shared library (`.so`/`.dll`/`.dylib`)
- `env.add_program()` - Build executable
- `env.CommandNoCache()` - Run command without caching result

All artifacts are marked with `NoCache()` to ensure generated files are always rebuilt when needed.

Sources: [methods.py:589-616]()

### Progress and Verbosity

The build system provides progress indication [methods.py:823-1008]():

```mermaid
graph LR
    ShowProgress["show_progress(env)"]
    NodeCount["Read .scons_node_count"]
    Progress["Display 'X/Y (Z%)' progress"]
    UpdateCount["Update node count on finish"]
    
    Verbose["verbose option"]
    NoVerbose["no_verbose(env)"]
    CompactMsg["'Compiling $SOURCE ...'"]
    
    ShowProgress --> NodeCount
    NodeCount --> Progress
    Progress --> UpdateCount
    
    Verbose --> NoVerbose
    NoVerbose --> CompactMsg
```

Features:
- **Progress tracking**: Displays `[X/Y] (Z%)` during compilation
- **Colored output**: Uses ANSI colors if terminal supports it
- **Compact messages**: When `verbose=no`, shows simplified "Compiling X ..." messages

Sources: [methods.py:823-1008](), [methods.py:425-457]()

## Build Caching and Optimization

### SCons Caching

```mermaid
graph TD
    CachePath["cache_path option"]
    PrepCache["methods.prepare_cache(env)"]
    
    DirCache["CacheDir(cache_path)"]
    MaxSize["Set CACHEDIR_SIZE_MAX"]
    Atexit["Register cleanup function"]
    
    CachePath --> PrepCache
    PrepCache --> DirCache
    DirCache --> MaxSize
    MaxSize --> Atexit
```

Build caching is configured early [SConstruct:366]() via `methods.prepare_cache()`:

- **Cache directory**: Stores compiled objects for reuse across builds
- **Size limit**: Configurable via `cache_limit` option (in GiB)
- **Automatic cleanup**: Old cache entries removed when limit exceeded

Sources: [SConstruct:366](), [methods.py:1102-1233]()

### Fast Unsafe Mode

```mermaid
graph LR
    FastUnsafe["fast_unsafe=yes"]
    ImplicitCache["SetOption('implicit_cache', 1)"]
    MaxDrift["SetOption('max_drift', 60)"]
    
    FastUnsafe --> ImplicitCache
    FastUnsafe --> MaxDrift
```

The `fast_unsafe` option [SConstruct:569-571]() enables aggressive optimizations:
- **Implicit dependency cache**: Skip scanning for implicit dependencies
- **Max drift**: Allow 60-second timestamp drift before rebuild

Warning: These optimizations can cause missed rebuilds if dependencies change.

Sources: [SConstruct:564-571]()

### SCU (Single Compilation Unit) Build

When `scu_build=yes` is enabled [SConstruct:679-690]():

1. **Generate SCU files**: Create `.scu/scu_*.gen.cpp` files combining multiple sources
2. **Set include limit**: Default 8 includes per SCU (1024 for dev builds)
3. **Compile SCU files**: Compile combined files instead of individual sources

Benefits:
- Faster compilation (fewer compiler invocations)
- Better optimization opportunities

Drawbacks:
- Higher memory usage during compilation
- Can hide some include dependencies

Sources: [SConstruct:679-690](), [methods.py:55-75]()

## Compilation Database Support

```mermaid
graph TD
    Compiledb["compiledb=yes"]
    GenDB["Generate compilation_db.json"]
    Tool["SCons compilation_db tool"]
    
    CompiledbGen{"compiledb_gen_only?"}
    Exit["Exit after generation"]
    Continue["Continue with build"]
    
    Compiledb --> Tool
    Tool --> GenDB
    GenDB --> CompiledbGen
    
    CompiledbGen -->|Yes| Exit
    CompiledbGen -->|No| Continue
```

When `compiledb=yes` is specified [SConstruct:238-239]():
- Generates `compile_commands.json` for IDE integration
- Works with clangd, clang-tidy, and other tools
- Optional `compiledb_gen_only=yes` exits after generation

Sources: [SConstruct:238-239]()
