This document describes the SCons-based platform detection and module discovery system used to configure the Godot build process. It covers how platform-specific build configurations are loaded via `detect.py` scripts and how C++ modules are automatically discovered and integrated.

For information about the overall build configuration and SCons setup, see [SCons Configuration](#9.1). For platform-specific implementation details, see [Platform Abstraction Layer](#8).

---

## Overview

The build system uses a two-phase discovery mechanism:

1. **Platform Detection**: Scanning `platform/*/detect.py` files to determine available build targets and their configuration
2. **Module Discovery**: Scanning `modules/` and custom directories for C++ modules with required metadata files

Both systems follow a plugin-like architecture where discovery happens at build configuration time, and each platform/module provides standardized hooks for integration.

---

## Platform Detection System

### Platform Discovery

During SCons initialization, the build system scans all subdirectories of `platform/` looking for valid platform definitions. A valid platform must contain a `detect.py` file.

**Platform Scanning Workflow**

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["SConstruct initialization"] --> ScanPlatforms["Scan platform/*"]
    ScanPlatforms --> CheckDetect{"detect.py exists?"}
    CheckDetect -->|No| Skip["Skip directory"]
    CheckDetect -->|Yes| ImportDetect["Import detect module"]
    ImportDetect --> CanBuild{"can_build() returns True?"}
    CanBuild -->|No| Skip
    CanBuild -->|Yes| AddPlatform["Add to platform_list"]
    AddPlatform --> GetOpts["Call get_opts()"]
    GetOpts --> GetFlags["Call get_flags()"]
    GetFlags --> StoreConfig["Store in platform_opts, platform_flags"]
    Skip --> NextPlatform{"More platforms?"}
    StoreConfig --> NextPlatform
    NextPlatform -->|Yes| ScanPlatforms
    NextPlatform -->|No| End["Platform detection complete"]
```

Sources: [SConstruct:68-109]()

The scanning logic:

```python
for x in sorted(glob.glob("platform/*")):
    if not os.path.isdir(x) or not os.path.exists(x + "/detect.py"):
        continue
    tmppath = "./" + x
    
    sys.path.insert(0, tmppath)
    import detect
    
    platform_name = x[9:]  # Remove "platform/" prefix
    
    if detect.can_build():
        x = x.replace("platform/", "")
        platform_list += [x]
        platform_opts[x] = detect.get_opts()
        platform_flags[x] = detect.get_flags()
    
    sys.path.remove(tmppath)
    sys.modules.pop("detect")
```

Sources: [SConstruct:77-109]()

### The detect.py Interface

Each platform's `detect.py` must implement a standardized interface:

| Function | Purpose | Return Type |
|----------|---------|-------------|
| `get_name()` | Platform display name | `str` |
| `can_build()` | Check if platform can be built on host | `bool` |
| `get_opts()` | Platform-specific build options | `list` of SCons Variables |
| `get_flags()` | Default flag values | `dict` |
| `get_doc_classes()` | Platform-specific documentation classes | `list[str]` |
| `get_doc_path()` | Path to platform docs | `str` |
| `configure(env)` | Configure build environment | `None` |

**Example: Windows Platform Detection**

```mermaid
graph LR
    GetName["get_name()<br/>Returns 'Windows'"]
    CanBuild["can_build()<br/>Checks os.name == 'nt'<br/>or MinGW available"]
    GetOpts["get_opts()<br/>Returns mingw_prefix,<br/>msvc_version, etc."]
    GetFlags["get_flags()<br/>Returns arch, d3d12=True"]
    Configure["configure(env)<br/>Sets CC, CXX,<br/>LINKFLAGS, etc."]
    
    GetName --> CanBuild
    CanBuild --> GetOpts
    GetOpts --> GetFlags
    GetFlags --> Configure
```

Sources: [platform/windows/detect.py:19-241]()

**Platform Capability Detection**

The `can_build()` function typically checks for required toolchains or SDKs:

```python
# Windows
def can_build():
    if os.name == "nt":
        return True  # Native Windows
    if os.name == "posix":
        # Cross-compilation check
        prefix = os.getenv("MINGW_PREFIX", "")
        if try_cmd("gcc --version", prefix, "") or try_cmd("clang --version", prefix, ""):
            return True
    return False
```

Sources: [platform/windows/detect.py:49-61]()

```python
# Android
def can_build():
    return os.path.exists(get_env_android_sdk_root())
```

Sources: [platform/android/detect.py:18-19]()

```python
# Web (Emscripten)
def can_build():
    return WhereIs("emcc") is not None
```

Sources: [platform/web/detect.py:29-30]()

### Platform Options and Flags

**Build Options (`get_opts()`)**

Platform-specific build options are returned as SCons Variable objects:

```python
def get_opts():
    from SCons.Variables import BoolVariable, EnumVariable
    
    return [
        ("mingw_prefix", "MinGW prefix", mingw),
        EnumVariable("windows_subsystem", "Windows subsystem", 
                     "gui", ["gui", "console"], ignorecase=2),
        BoolVariable("use_mingw", "Use the Mingw compiler", False),
        BoolVariable("use_llvm", "Use the LLVM compiler", False),
        # ... more options
    ]
```

Sources: [platform/windows/detect.py:164-220]()

**Default Flags (`get_flags()`)**

Flags set default values that can be overridden by command-line arguments:

```python
def get_flags():
    arch = detect_build_env_arch() or detect_arch()
    
    return {
        "arch": arch,
        "d3d12": True,
        "supported": ["d3d12", "dcomp", "library", "mono", "xaudio2"],
    }
```

Sources: [platform/windows/detect.py:233-240]()

These flags are applied early in the build process:

```python
flag_list = platform_flags[env["platform"]]
for key, value in flag_list.items():
    if key not in ARGUMENTS or ARGUMENTS[key] == "auto":
        env[key] = value
```

Sources: [SConstruct:427-430]()

### Platform Configuration

The `configure(env)` function is called after all options are parsed to set up the build environment. This is where compiler detection, toolchain setup, and platform-specific compilation flags are configured.

**Configuration Stages**

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["configure(env) called"] --> ValidateArch["Validate architecture"]
    ValidateArch --> DetectCompiler["Detect/select compiler"]
    DetectCompiler --> SetupToolchain["Setup toolchain paths"]
    SetupToolchain --> CompilerFlags["Append CCFLAGS, CPPDEFINES"]
    CompilerFlags --> LinkerFlags["Append LINKFLAGS"]
    LinkerFlags --> Libraries["Configure libraries"]
    Libraries --> LTO["Configure LTO settings"]
    LTO --> End["Configuration complete"]
```

**Windows MSVC Configuration Example**

```python
def configure_msvc(env):
    # Set compiler
    if env["use_llvm"]:
        env["CC"] = "clang-cl"
        env["CXX"] = "clang-cl"
        env["LINK"] = "lld-link"
    
    # Runtime library
    if env["use_static_cpp"]:
        env.AppendUnique(CCFLAGS=["/MT"])
    else:
        env.AppendUnique(CCFLAGS=["/MD"])
    
    # Platform defines
    env.AppendUnique(CPPDEFINES=[
        "WINDOWS_ENABLED",
        "WASAPI_ENABLED",
        "WIN32",
        ("WINVER", "0x0A00"),
    ])
    
    # Libraries
    env.Append(LINKFLAGS=["winmm.lib", "dsound.lib", ...])
```

Sources: [platform/windows/detect.py:243-519]()

**Linux Dependency Detection**

```python
def configure(env):
    # pkg-config based library detection
    if not env["builtin_freetype"]:
        env.ParseConfig("pkg-config freetype2 --cflags --libs")
    
    if not env["builtin_zstd"]:
        env.ParseConfig("pkg-config libzstd --cflags --libs")
    
    # Conditional features
    if env["alsa"]:
        if os.system("pkg-config --exists alsa") == 0:
            env.ParseConfig("pkg-config alsa --cflags --libs")
            env.Append(CPPDEFINES=["ALSA_ENABLED"])
```

Sources: [platform/linuxbsd/detect.py:232-343]()

---

## Module System

### Module Discovery

Modules are C++ extensions that add functionality to Godot. The build system automatically discovers modules by scanning directories for required files.

**Module Directory Structure**

A valid module must contain:
- `register_types.h` - Module registration header
- `register_types.cpp` - Module initialization/cleanup implementation
- `config.py` - Module configuration and build options
- `SCsub` - SCons build script

**Module Detection Algorithm**

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["detect_modules(search_path, recursive)"] --> CheckIsModule{"is_module(search_path)?"}
    CheckIsModule -->|Yes| AddModule["Add search_path to modules dict"]
    CheckIsModule -->|No| CheckRecursive{"recursive?"}
    AddModule --> CheckRecursive
    CheckRecursive -->|No| GlobFiles["Glob search_path/*"]
    CheckRecursive -->|Yes| QueueSearch["Queue search_path for DFS"]
    GlobFiles --> LoopFiles{"For each file"}
    QueueSearch --> PopPath["Pop path from queue"]
    PopPath --> IsModulePath{"is_module(path)?"}
    IsModulePath -->|Yes| AddFoundModule["Add to modules dict"]
    IsModulePath -->|No| CheckDir{"Is directory?"}
    AddFoundModule --> QueueChildren["Queue children"]
    CheckDir -->|No| QueueChildren
    CheckDir -->|Yes| CheckEngine{"is_engine(path)?"}
    CheckEngine -->|Yes| QueueChildren
    CheckEngine -->|No| QueueDirs["Add to queue"]
    LoopFiles --> CheckFileEngine{"is_engine(file)?"}
    CheckFileEngine -->|Yes| LoopFiles
    CheckFileEngine -->|No| CheckFileModule{"is_module(file)?"}
    CheckFileModule -->|Yes| AddFileModule["Add to modules dict"]
    CheckFileModule -->|No| LoopFiles
    AddFileModule --> LoopFiles
    QueueChildren --> MorePaths{"More paths in queue?"}
    QueueDirs --> MorePaths
    MorePaths -->|Yes| PopPath
    MorePaths -->|No| ReturnModules["Return OrderedDict"]
    LoopFiles --> ReturnModules
```

Sources: [methods.py:240-300]()

**Module Validation (`is_module()`)**

```python
def is_module(path):
    if not os.path.isdir(path):
        return False
    must_exist = ["register_types.h", "SCsub", "config.py"]
    for f in must_exist:
        if not os.path.exists(os.path.join(path, f)):
            return False
    return True
```

Sources: [methods.py:303-310]()

### Module Search Paths

The build system searches two types of module locations:

1. **Built-in modules**: `modules/` directory (non-recursive)
2. **Custom modules**: Paths specified via `custom_modules` option (recursive if enabled)

```python
module_search_paths = ["modules"]  # Built-in path

if env["custom_modules"]:
    paths = env["custom_modules"].split(",")
    for p in paths:
        module_search_paths.append(methods.convert_custom_modules_path(p))

for path in module_search_paths:
    if path == "modules":
        # Built-in modules: non-recursive
        modules = methods.detect_modules(path, recursive=False)
    else:
        # Custom modules: recursive if enabled
        modules = methods.detect_modules(path, env["custom_modules_recursive"])
        env.Prepend(CPPPATH=[path, os.path.dirname(path)])
    
    modules_detected.update(modules)
```

Sources: [SConstruct:436-462]()

### Module Configuration Interface

Each module's `config.py` provides configuration hooks:

| Function | Purpose | Optional |
|----------|---------|----------|
| `is_enabled()` | Whether module is enabled by default | Yes |
| `get_opts(platform)` | Module-specific build options | Yes |
| `can_build(env, platform)` | Whether module can be built | Yes |
| `configure(env)` | Configure module-specific settings | Yes |
| `get_doc_classes()` | Module's documentation classes | Yes |
| `get_doc_path()` | Path to module docs | Yes |

**Module Options Registration**

```python
for name, path in modules_detected.items():
    sys.path.insert(0, path)
    import config
    
    # Determine default enabled state
    if env["modules_enabled_by_default"]:
        enabled = True
        try:
            enabled = config.is_enabled()
        except AttributeError:
            pass
    else:
        enabled = False
    
    # Add module enable/disable option
    opts.Add(BoolVariable(f"module_{name}_enabled", f"Enable module '{name}'", enabled))
    
    # Add module-specific options
    try:
        opts.AddVariables(*config.get_opts(env["platform"]))
    except AttributeError:
        pass
    
    sys.path.remove(path)
    sys.modules.pop("config")
```

Sources: [SConstruct:465-487]()

### Module Dependencies

Modules can declare dependencies on other modules:

```python
def can_build(env, platform):
    # Declare required dependencies
    env.module_add_dependencies("mymodule", ["websocket", "regex"])
    # Declare optional dependencies
    env.module_add_dependencies("mymodule", ["noise"], optional=True)
    
    # Check if dependencies are satisfied
    return env.module_check_dependencies("mymodule")
```

The dependency system ensures modules are disabled if their dependencies are missing:

```python
def module_check_dependencies(self, module):
    missing_deps = set()
    required_deps = self.module_dependencies[module][0] if module in self.module_dependencies else []
    
    for dep in required_deps:
        opt = "module_{}_enabled".format(dep)
        if opt not in self or not self[opt] or not module_check_dependencies(self, dep):
            missing_deps.add(dep)
    
    if missing_deps:
        if module not in self.disabled_modules:
            print_warning("Disabling '{}' module as the following dependencies are not satisfied: {}".format(
                module, ", ".join(missing_deps)))
            self.disabled_modules.add(module)
        return False
    return True
```

Sources: [methods.py:325-362]()

Modules are sorted topologically based on their dependencies:

```python
def sort_module_list(env):
    deps = {k: v[0] + list(filter(lambda x: x in env.module_list, v[1])) 
            for k, v in env.module_dependencies.items()}
    
    frontier = list(env.module_list.keys())
    explored = []
    
    while len(frontier):
        cur = frontier.pop()
        deps_list = deps[cur] if cur in deps else []
        if len(deps_list) and any([d not in explored for d in deps_list]):
            # Explore dependencies first
            frontier.insert(0, cur)
            continue
        explored.append(cur)
    
    for k in explored:
        env.module_list.move_to_end(k)
```

Sources: [methods.py:365-379]()

---

## Build Integration

### Platform Tools Selection

After platform detection, SCons needs to configure the build tools. The `get_tools()` function determines which SCons tools to use:

```python
tmppath = "./platform/" + env["platform"]
sys.path.insert(0, tmppath)
import detect

custom_tools = ["default"]
try:
    custom_tools = detect.get_tools(env)
except AttributeError:
    pass

for tool in custom_tools:
    env.Tool(tool)
```

Sources: [SConstruct:499-509]()

**Example: Windows Tool Selection**

```python
def get_tools(env):
    from SCons.Tool.MSCommon import msvc_exists
    
    if os.name != "nt" or env.get("use_mingw") or not msvc_exists():
        return ["mingw"]
    else:
        msvc_arch_aliases = {"x86_32": "x86", "arm32": "arm"}
        env["TARGET_ARCH"] = msvc_arch_aliases.get(env["arch"], env["arch"])
        env["MSVC_VERSION"] = env.get("msvc_version")
        return ["msvc", "mslink", "mslib"]
```

Sources: [platform/windows/detect.py:152-161]()

### Module Build Process

**Module Registration Flow**

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["modules/SCsub"] --> GenEnabled["Generate modules_enabled.gen.h"]
    GenEnabled --> GenRegister["Generate register_module_types.gen.cpp"]
    GenRegister --> ForEach["For each enabled module"]
    ForEach --> ModuleSCsub["Execute module/SCsub"]
    ModuleSCsub --> CompileSources["Compile module sources"]
    CompileSources --> CreateLib["Create libmodule_<name>.a"]
    CreateLib --> NextModule{"More modules?"}
    NextModule -->|Yes| ForEach
    NextModule -->|No| CompileRegister["Compile register_module_types.gen.cpp"]
    CompileRegister --> CreateModulesLib["Create libmodules.a"]
    CreateModulesLib --> LinkAll["Link all module libraries"]
```

Sources: [modules/SCsub:1-63]()

**Generated Module Headers**

The build system generates two important files:

1. **`modules_enabled.gen.h`**: Defines `MODULE_<NAME>_ENABLED` for each active module

```python
def modules_enabled_builder(target, source, env):
    modules = sorted(source[0].read())
    with methods.generated_wrapper(str(target[0])) as file:
        for module in modules:
            file.write(f"#define MODULE_{module.upper()}_ENABLED\n")
```

Sources: [modules/modules_builders.py:8-12]()

2. **`register_module_types.gen.cpp`**: Calls initialization/cleanup for each module

```python
def register_module_types_builder(target, source, env):
    modules = source[0].read()
    mod_inc = "\n".join([f'#include "{value}/register_types.h"' for value in modules.values()])
    mod_init = "\n".join([
        f"""#ifdef MODULE_{key.upper()}_ENABLED
    initialize_{key}_module(p_level);
#endif"""
        for key in modules.keys()
    ])
    # ... similar for mod_uninit
```

Sources: [modules/modules_builders.py:15-49]()

### Platform-Specific Build Files

Each platform provides an `SCsub` file that compiles platform-specific sources:

**Windows Platform Build**

```python
common_win = [
    "os_windows.cpp",
    "display_server_windows.cpp",
    "key_mapping_windows.cpp",
    # ... more sources
]

if env["library_type"] == "executable":
    common_win += ["godot_windows.cpp"]
else:
    common_win += ["libgodot_windows.cpp"]

env.add_source_files(sources, common_win)
sources += res_obj  # Windows resource file

prog = env.add_program("#bin/godot", sources, PROGSUFFIX=env["PROGSUFFIX"])
```

Sources: [platform/windows/SCsub:15-92]()

### Build Output Organization

The build system creates static libraries for each major subsystem:

| Library | Contents | Created By |
|---------|----------|------------|
| `libcore.a` | Core engine code | [core/SCsub:239]() |
| `libscene.a` | Scene system | Scene SCsub |
| `libservers.a` | Server implementations | Servers SCsub |
| `libmodules.a` | Module registration | [modules/SCsub:62]() |
| `libmodule_<name>.a` | Individual module | [modules/SCsub:41]() |
| `libeditor.a` | Editor code | [editor/SCsub:101]() |
| `libplatform.a` | Platform APIs | [platform/SCsub:29]() |
| `libplatform_*.a` | Platform-specific | Platform SCsub |
| `libmain.a` | Main entry point | [main/SCsub:39]() |

These are then linked into the final executable:

```python
lib = env.add_library("core", env.core_sources)
env.Prepend(LIBS=[lib])
```

Sources: [core/SCsub:239-240]()

**Final Linking**

```mermaid
graph LR
    Core["libcore.a"] --> Link["Linker"]
    Scene["libscene.a"] --> Link
    Servers["libservers.a"] --> Link
    Modules["libmodules.a"] --> Link
    ModuleLibs["libmodule_*.a"] --> Link
    Editor["libeditor.a"] --> Link
    Platform["libplatform.a"] --> Link
    PlatformSpec["libplatform_<name>.a"] --> Link
    Main["libmain.a"] --> Link
    Link --> Executable["godot.exe / godot"]
```

## Purpose and Scope

This document describes how third-party libraries are integrated into the Godot Engine codebase, including their organization, licensing, build integration, and maintenance. It covers the structure of the `thirdparty/` directory, license attribution, patch management, and common integration patterns used throughout the engine.

For information about the build system configuration that compiles these dependencies, see [Build System](#9). For details on specific subsystems that use these libraries (e.g., rendering, resource loading), see the corresponding subsystem documentation.

---

## Directory Structure and Organization

### Thirdparty Directory Layout

All external dependencies are organized in the `thirdparty/` directory at the repository root. Each library has its own subdirectory containing extracted source files, license information, and any Godot-specific modifications.

```mermaid
graph TB
    Root["Repository Root"]
    Thirdparty["thirdparty/"]
    Modules["modules/"]
    
    Root --> Thirdparty
    Root --> Modules
    
    Thirdparty --> README["README.md<br/>(Library catalog)"]
    Thirdparty --> Libs["Individual libraries<br/>(astcenc/, basis_universal/, etc.)"]
    
    Modules --> ModWrapper["Module wrappers<br/>(tinyexr/, cvtt/, etc.)"]
    
    Libs --> LibFiles["Source files"]
    Libs --> LibLicense["LICENSE files"]
    Libs --> LibPatches["patches/<br/>(optional)"]
    
    ModWrapper --> ModSCsub["SCsub<br/>(build script)"]
    ModWrapper --> ModGodot["Godot integration code"]
    ModWrapper --> ModConfig["config.py"]
    
    style README fill:#f9f9f9
    style Libs fill:#e8f4f8
    style ModWrapper fill:#f0e8f8
```

**Sources:** [thirdparty/README.md:1-1170]()

### Library Catalog

The file `thirdparty/README.md` serves as the authoritative catalog of all third-party dependencies. Each library entry documents:

- **Upstream source**: Git repository or official website URL
- **Version**: Specific version number and commit hash
- **License**: SPDX identifier or license name
- **Files extracted**: Which files from upstream are included
- **Patches applied**: List of `.patch` files with PR references

**Example entry structure:**

```markdown
## library_name

- Upstream: https://github.com/vendor/library
- Version: 1.2.3 (commit_hash, year)
- License: MIT

Files extracted from upstream source:
- `src/*.cpp` and `include/*.h`
- `LICENSE`

Patches:
- `0001-description.patch` ([GH-12345](link))
```

**Sources:** [thirdparty/README.md:8-1170]()

---

## License Management and Attribution

### COPYRIGHT.txt Structure

The `COPYRIGHT.txt` file at the repository root provides comprehensive licensing information in machine-readable debian/copyright format. It includes:

1. **Global disclaimer** for thirdparty libraries [COPYRIGHT.txt:19-37]()
2. **Per-library copyright statements** with file patterns and license identifiers
3. **Full license texts** at the end of the file

**Entry format:**

```
Files: thirdparty/library_name/*
Comment: Library Name
Copyright: year, Copyright Holder(s)
License: License-Identifier
```

**Sources:** [COPYRIGHT.txt:1-37](), [COPYRIGHT.txt:192-687]()

### License File Organization

Each third-party library directory contains its original license file(s):

| File Pattern | Purpose |
|--------------|---------|
| `LICENSE`, `LICENSE.txt`, `LICENSE.md` | Primary license text |
| `COPYING` | Alternative license file name |
| `NOTICES.txt`, `AUTHORS` | Additional attribution files |
| `LICENSE-*.txt` | Multiple license options (e.g., `LICENSE-MIT`) |

**Sources:** [thirdparty/README.md]() (various license references)

---

## Integration Patterns

### Pattern 1: Bundled Library with Module Wrapper

Many third-party libraries are wrapped by Godot modules that provide engine integration. The module acts as an adapter between the library and Godot's APIs.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Thirdparty Directory"
        TPLib["thirdparty/tinyexr/"]
        TPSrc["tinyexr.h<br/>tinyexr.cc"]
        TPLic["LICENSE"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Module Directory"
        ModDir["modules/tinyexr/"]
        SCsub["SCsub<br/>(build script)"]
        Config["config.py"]
        Loader["image_loader_tinyexr.cpp<br/>image_loader_tinyexr.h"]
        Saver["image_saver_tinyexr.cpp<br/>image_saver_tinyexr.h"]
        Register["register_types.cpp"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Build Process"
        CompileTP["Compile thirdparty library"]
        CompileMod["Compile module code"]
        Link["Link into final binary"]
    end
    
    TPLib --> TPSrc
    TPLib --> TPLic
    
    ModDir --> SCsub
    ModDir --> Config
    ModDir --> Loader
    ModDir --> Saver
    ModDir --> Register
    
    SCsub --> CompileTP
    SCsub --> CompileMod
    TPSrc --> CompileTP
    Loader --> CompileMod
    Saver --> CompileMod
    Register --> CompileMod
    
    CompileTP --> Link
    CompileMod --> Link
```

**Key components:**

- **SCsub**: Build script that compiles both thirdparty sources and module integration code [modules/tinyexr/SCsub:1-42]()
- **config.py**: Module configuration (platform support, dependencies) [modules/tinyexr/config.py:1-7]()
- **Loader/Saver classes**: Godot-facing API implementation [modules/tinyexr/image_loader_tinyexr.h:35-40]()
- **register_types.cpp**: Module registration with engine [modules/tinyexr/register_types.cpp:38-59]()

**Sources:** [modules/tinyexr/SCsub:1-42](), [modules/tinyexr/register_types.cpp:38-59](), [thirdparty/tinyexr/tinyexr.h:1-600]()

### Pattern 2: Header-Only Integration

Some libraries are integrated directly without a module wrapper, particularly header-only libraries or those used internally by servers/drivers.

**Examples:**
- `glad` (OpenGL loader) - used by rendering backends [thirdparty/glad/]()
- `doctest` (testing framework) - used by unit tests [thirdparty/doctest/doctest.h:1-50]()
- Platform headers (directx_headers, vulkan, metal-cpp)

**Sources:** [thirdparty/glad/LICENSE:1-64](), [thirdparty/doctest/doctest.h:1-100]()

### Pattern 3: Patched Libraries

Libraries requiring Godot-specific modifications include a `patches/` subdirectory with `.patch` files. Each patch is tracked in `README.md` with a GitHub PR reference.

**Patch application process:**

```mermaid
graph LR
    Upstream["Upstream release<br/>(git/tarball)"]
    Extract["Extract files<br/>(as per README.md)"]
    Apply["Apply patches/<br/>*.patch files"]
    Godot["thirdparty/<br/>library/"]
    
    Upstream --> Extract
    Extract --> Apply
    Apply --> Godot
    
    Patches["patches/<br/>0001-*.patch<br/>0002-*.patch"] -.->|git apply| Apply
```

**Common patch categories:**

| Patch Type | Example | Purpose |
|------------|---------|---------|
| Build fixes | `0001-build-fixes.patch` | Adapt to Godot build system |
| Platform support | `0001-mingw-support.patch` | Add/fix platform-specific code |
| External dependency | `0001-external-zlib.patch` | Use Godot's bundled dependency |
| Warning fixes | `0001-disable-exceptions.patch` | Suppress warnings or disable features |
| Feature customization | `0001-godot-socket.patch` | Integrate with Godot APIs |

**Sources:** [thirdparty/README.md:44-48]() (amd-fsr2 patches), [thirdparty/README.md:86-94]() (basis_universal patches), [thirdparty/README.md:257-260]() (enet patches)

---

## Common Build Integration Patterns

### SCsub Build Script Structure

Module `SCsub` files follow a standard pattern for integrating thirdparty libraries:

```python
# 1. Clone module environment
env_module = env_modules.Clone()

# 2. Define thirdparty sources
thirdparty_dir = "#thirdparty/library/"
thirdparty_sources = ["file1.cpp", "file2.cpp"]
thirdparty_sources = [thirdparty_dir + f for f in thirdparty_sources]

# 3. Configure include paths
env_module.Prepend(CPPPATH=[thirdparty_dir])

# 4. Add preprocessor defines
env_module.Append(CPPDEFINES=["LIBRARY_DEFINE"])

# 5. Compile thirdparty code (warnings disabled)
env_thirdparty = env_module.Clone()
env_thirdparty.disable_warnings()
thirdparty_obj = []
env_thirdparty.add_source_files(thirdparty_obj, thirdparty_sources)
env.modules_sources += thirdparty_obj

# 6. Compile module code
module_obj = []
env_module.add_source_files(module_obj, "*.cpp")
env.modules_sources += module_obj

# 7. Force rebuild when thirdparty changes
env.Depends(module_obj, thirdparty_obj)
```

**Sources:** [modules/tinyexr/SCsub:1-42](), [modules/cvtt/SCsub:1-45]()

### Compiler Define Configuration

Common preprocessor defines used to configure thirdparty libraries:

| Define | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| `LIBRARY_USE_MINIZ=0` | Disable bundled zlib alternative | [modules/tinyexr/SCsub:26]() |
| `LIBRARY_USE_THREAD` | Enable threading support | [modules/tinyexr/SCsub:23]() |
| `LIBRARY_IMPLEMENTATION` | Include implementation in single file | [thirdparty/tinyexr/tinyexr.cc:9]() |
| Platform-specific | Conditionally enable platform code | Various |

**Sources:** [modules/tinyexr/SCsub:20-27](), [thirdparty/tinyexr/tinyexr.cc:1-11]()

## Integration Code Patterns

### Module Registration Pattern

Modules that wrap thirdparty libraries follow a standard registration pattern to integrate with the engine's initialization system:

```mermaid
graph LR
    Init["Module Initialization<br/>(initialize_X_module)"]
    CreateLoader["Instantiate format loader<br/>Ref&lt;ImageLoaderTinyEXR&gt;"]
    Register["Register with engine<br/>ImageLoader::add_image_format_loader()"]
    SetCallback["Set callback functions<br/>Image::save_exr_func = ..."]
    
    Uninit["Module Uninitialization<br/>(uninitialize_X_module)"]
    RemoveLoader["Remove format loader<br/>ImageLoader::remove_image_format_loader()"]
    ClearCallback["Clear callbacks<br/>Image::save_exr_func = nullptr"]
    
    Init --> CreateLoader
    CreateLoader --> Register
    Register --> SetCallback
    
    Uninit --> RemoveLoader
    RemoveLoader --> ClearCallback
```

**Implementation example (TinyEXR module):**

```cpp
// Initialize function
void initialize_tinyexr_module(ModuleInitializationLevel p_level) {
    if (p_level != MODULE_INITIALIZATION_LEVEL_SCENE) {
        return;
    }
    
    image_loader_tinyexr.instantiate();
    ImageLoader::add_image_format_loader(image_loader_tinyexr);
    
    Image::save_exr_func = save_exr;
    Image::save_exr_buffer_func = save_exr_buffer;
}
```

**Sources:** [modules/tinyexr/register_types.cpp:38-59](), [modules/tinyexr/image_loader_tinyexr.h:35-40]()

### Library Initialization Pattern

When using libraries that require explicit initialization, the pattern wraps library-specific setup:

```cpp
// In module initialization
InitEXRHeader(&header);
InitEXRImage(&image);

// Use library...

// In cleanup
FreeEXRHeader(&header);
FreeEXRImage(&image);
```

**Sources:** [modules/tinyexr/image_loader_tinyexr.cpp:59-92]()

### Preprocessor Configuration Pattern

Thirdparty libraries often need configuration through preprocessor defines before including headers:

```cpp
// Configure library before including
#define TINYEXR_IMPLEMENTATION
#include "tinyexr.h"

// Or with conditional defines
#if defined(_WIN32)
#ifndef NOMINMAX
#define NOMINMAX
#endif
#endif

#include <zlib.h>  // Must come before tinyexr
#define TINYEXR_IMPLEMENTATION
#include "tinyexr.h"
```

**Sources:** [thirdparty/tinyexr/tinyexr.cc:1-11](), [modules/tinyexr/image_loader_tinyexr.cpp:31-35]()

---

## Updating Third-Party Dependencies

### Standard Update Procedure

```mermaid
graph TB
    Start["Identify library to update"]
    CheckUpstream["Check upstream for new release"]
    
    Download["Download new version<br/>(git tag/tarball)"]
    Extract["Extract files per README.md"]
    
    Patches["Apply existing patches/<br/>*.patch files"]
    TestPatch["Test if patches apply cleanly"]
    
    FixPatches{"Patches<br/>apply?"}
    UpdatePatches["Update/regenerate patches"]
    
    UpdateREADME["Update thirdparty/README.md<br/>(version, commit, year)"]
    UpdateCOPYRIGHT["Update COPYRIGHT.txt<br/>(copyright years)"]
    
    BuildTest["Build and test"]
    Success{"Tests<br/>pass?"}
    
    FixIssues["Fix integration issues"]
    NewPatches["Create new patches if needed"]
    
    PR["Create pull request"]
    
    Start --> CheckUpstream
    CheckUpstream --> Download
    Download --> Extract
    Extract --> Patches
    Patches --> TestPatch
    TestPatch --> FixPatches
    
    FixPatches -->|No| UpdatePatches
    FixPatches -->|Yes| UpdateREADME
    UpdatePatches --> UpdateREADME
    
    UpdateREADME --> UpdateCOPYRIGHT
    UpdateCOPYRIGHT --> BuildTest
    BuildTest --> Success
    
    Success -->|No| FixIssues
    FixIssues --> NewPatches
    NewPatches --> BuildTest
    
    Success -->|Yes| PR
```

### Update Checklist

When updating a library, verify the following:

**1. File extraction** [thirdparty/README.md]()
   - Extract only files listed in `README.md` entry
   - Preserve directory structure as documented
   - Keep LICENSE files

**2. Version information** [thirdparty/README.md]()
   - Update version number
   - Update commit hash
   - Update year

**3. Patch management**
   - Attempt to apply existing patches with `git apply`
   - Resolve conflicts if patches don't apply cleanly
   - Remove patches that are upstreamed
   - Regenerate patches with `git format-patch`

**4. Copyright updates** [COPYRIGHT.txt]()
   - Update copyright year ranges
   - Add new copyright holders if listed in upstream

**5. Build verification**
   - Test on multiple platforms (Linux, Windows, macOS)
   - Verify no new warnings introduced
   - Run affected subsystem tests

**6. Documentation** [thirdparty/README.md]()
   - Document any new patches with PR reference
   - Update extraction instructions if changed
   - Note any API changes in commit message

**Sources:** [thirdparty/README.md:1-1170]()

### Automated Update Scripts

Some libraries include update scripts to automate the extraction and patching process:

| Library | Script | Purpose |
|---------|--------|---------|
| `embree` | `modules/raycast/godot_update_embree.py` | Extract files and apply patches |
| `sdl` | `thirdparty/sdl/update-sdl.sh` | Extract SDL files |
| `thorvg` | `thorvg/update-thorvg.sh` | Extract ThorVG files |
| `metal-cpp` | `update-metal-cpp.sh` | Extract and patch Metal C++ headers |

**Sources:** [thirdparty/README.md:223-241]() (embree), [thirdparty/README.md:1000-1019]() (sdl), [thirdparty/README.md:1082-1098]() (thorvg), [thirdparty/README.md:706-716]() (metal-cpp)

---

## Special Cases and Considerations

### Libraries with External Dependencies

Some thirdparty libraries depend on other thirdparty libraries. These are documented in `README.md` and require careful coordination:

**Dependency chain example:**
- `tinyexr` requires `zlib` for compression [modules/tinyexr/SCsub:26]()
- `basis_universal` uses external `zstd` [thirdparty/README.md:88]()
- Module build scripts configure defines to use Godot's bundled versions

**Build configuration:**
```python
# Use Godot's zlib instead of library's bundled version
env_tinyexr.Append(CPPDEFINES=[("TINYEXR_USE_MINIZ", 0)])
```

**Sources:** [modules/tinyexr/SCsub:24-27](), [thirdparty/README.md:86-94]() (basis_universal patches)

### Platform-Specific Libraries

Some libraries are only relevant to specific platforms:

| Library | Platform(s) | Purpose |
|---------|-------------|---------|
| `directx_headers` | Windows | Direct3D 12 API |
| `d3d12ma` | Windows | D3D12 memory allocator |
| `metal-cpp` | macOS/iOS | Metal API C++ bindings |
| `angle` | Multiple | OpenGL ES on D3D11 |
| `linuxbsd_headers` | Linux/BSD | Platform headers |
| `swappy-frame-pacing` | Android | Frame pacing library |

**Sources:** [thirdparty/README.md:153-168]() (d3d12ma), [thirdparty/README.md:170-185]() (directx_headers), [thirdparty/README.md:706-716]() (metal-cpp)

### Libraries with Custom Godot Files

Some library directories contain Godot-created files alongside thirdparty sources:

**Example: mbedtls**
- `godot_core_mbedtls_platform.c` - Custom platform implementation
- `godot_core_mbedtls_config.h` - Build configuration
- `godot_module_mbedtls_config.h` - Module-specific config
- `threading_alt.h` - Custom threading implementation

**Example: enet**
- `enet_godot.cpp` - Godot socket implementation
- `enet/enet_godot.h` - Header for Godot integration
- `enet/enet_godot_ext.h` - Extension API

**Note:** These files must be preserved when updating the library.

**Sources:** [thirdparty/README.md:681-704]() (mbedtls), [thirdparty/README.md:243-263]() (enet)

### Header-Only Libraries in misc/

Single-file or small libraries are collected in `thirdparty/misc/`:

| File | Purpose | License |
|------|---------|---------|
| `bcdec.h` | BC texture decoder | MIT |
| `fastlz.{c,h}` | Fast compression | MIT |
| `FastNoiseLite.h` | Noise generation | MIT |
| `mikktspace.{c,h}` | Tangent space calculation | Zlib |
| `pcg.{cpp,h}` | Random number generation | Apache 2.0 |
| `polypartition.{cpp,h}` | Polygon triangulation | MIT |
| `smolv.{cpp,h}` | SPIR-V compression | Unlicense or MIT |
| `stb_rect_pack.h` | Rectangle packing | Public Domain/Unlicense/MIT |

**Sources:** [thirdparty/README.md:786-871]()

---

## Build System Integration Details

### Thirdparty Compilation Flags

Thirdparty code is typically compiled with warnings disabled to avoid noise from external code:

```python
env_thirdparty = env_module.Clone()
env_thirdparty.disable_warnings()
env_thirdparty.add_source_files(thirdparty_obj, thirdparty_sources)
```

**Module code** (Godot integration layer) is compiled with warnings enabled:

```python
env_module.add_source_files(module_obj, "*.cpp")
```

**Sources:** [modules/tinyexr/SCsub:28-31](), [modules/cvtt/SCsub:31-34]()

### Include Path Management

Include paths are added using `Prepend` to ensure thirdparty headers are found first:

```python
env_module.Prepend(CPPPATH=[thirdparty_dir])
```

This prevents conflicts with system-installed versions of the same library.

**Sources:** [modules/tinyexr/SCsub:20](), [modules/cvtt/SCsub:29]()

### Dependency Tracking

SCons dependency tracking ensures module code rebuilds when thirdparty sources change:

```python
env.Depends(module_obj, thirdparty_obj)
```

**Sources:** [modules/tinyexr/SCsub:41](), [modules/cvtt/SCsub:44]()

### Multi-File Libraries

Larger libraries list all source files explicitly:

```python
thirdparty_sources = [
    "file1.cpp",
    "file2.cpp",
    # ... more files
]
thirdparty_sources = [thirdparty_dir + file for file in thirdparty_sources]
```

**Sources:** [modules/cvtt/SCsub:14-26]()

---

## Summary

The Godot Engine integrates over 80 third-party libraries spanning graphics, physics, compression, networking, text rendering, and platform support. These dependencies are:

- **Centralized** in `thirdparty/` with comprehensive documentation in `README.md`
- **Licensed** and attributed in machine-readable `COPYRIGHT.txt`
- **Modified** through tracked patches in `patches/` subdirectories
- **Integrated** via module wrappers following standard SCons patterns
- **Maintained** through documented update procedures
